Nick_ebook-10










Comments on “Neurodiversity: Some Basic Terms & Definitions”

关于《神经多样性：基本术语与定义》的评论



These days the term neurodiversity is generally credited to Judy Singer, an Australian autistic sociologist who coined it in the late 1990s for a graduate thesis which was completed in 1998. However, I’ve met a couple of autistic elders who recall encountering and using the word even earlier in the 1990s, in the old email listserv discussions which were instrumental in the initial formation of autistic community. Perhaps it was just one of those ideas whose time had come, and it occurred to more than one autistic person around the same time.

如今，“神经多样性”这一术语通常归功于朱迪·辛格（Judy Singer），一位澳大利亚孤独谱系社会学家，她在 1990 年代末为 1998 年完成的研究生论文中创造了这个词。然而，我遇到过几位孤独谱系长者，他们回忆起在更早的 1990 年代，在那些对孤独谱系社群初步形成至关重要的旧邮件列表讨论中，就已接触并使用过这个词。或许这只是一个时机成熟的理念，在相近时期被不止一位孤独谱系人士独立提出。



I’m sure I’m not the only person who independently came up with neurominority and the neurodiversity paradigm in the first decade of the 21st century. Ralph Savarese and I came up with the term neurocosmopolitanism independently of one another (there’ll be more about neurocosmopolitanism later on in the book), and Athena Lynn Michaels-Dillon and I originally came up with the term neuroqueer independently of one another as well (more about that later, too). Sometimes when the time is ripe for a concept to enter the world, it enters through multiple minds at once, the way modern calculus was developed independently and concurrently by Newton and Leibniz. In any event, even if Singer wasn’t the very first to use it, I did get confirmation from her that the definition of neurodiversity I provide in “Neurodiversity: Some Basic Terms & Definitions” is consistent with her own understanding of the word.

我确信自己并非唯一在 21 世纪头十年独立提出“神经少数群体”和“神经多样性范式”的人。拉尔夫·萨瓦雷斯与我各自独立创造了“神经世界主义”一词（本书后续章节将详述该概念），而雅典娜·林恩·迈克尔斯-迪伦与我同样分别独立提出了“神经酷儿”这个术语（后续亦会展开说明）。有时当某个概念诞生的时机成熟时，它会同时涌入多个头脑，正如现代微积分由牛顿和莱布尼茨各自独立发展而成。无论如何，即便辛格并非最早使用该词的人，她已向我确认，我在《神经多样性：基本术语与定义》中提供的定义与她对该词的理解完全一致。



•



As I mentioned near the end of the definition of neurodivergent, the terms neurodivergent and neurodivergence were coined in the year 2000 by Kassiane Asasumasu. Kassiane’s a longtime friend who’s been involved in the discourse on neurodiversity even longer than I have. When I first wrote this piece, I showed it to her and she gave her seal of approval to the way I’d explained her terms. So the definitions of those two terms in “Neurodiversity: Some Basic Terms & Definitions” are creator-authorized versions, as official as definitions get. (The same can be said for the definitions of the neurodiversity paradigm and neurominority provided in this piece, since I’m the one who coined those two terms in the first place.)

正如我在“神经殊异”定义结尾处提到的，“神经殊异”和“神经殊异性”这两个术语由卡西安·阿萨苏玛苏于 2000 年创造。卡西安是我的老朋友，她参与神经多样性相关论述的时间甚至比我更久。当我最初撰写这篇文章时，曾将初稿交予她审阅，她对我阐释其术语的方式表示认可。因此，《神经多样性：基本术语与定义》中这两个术语的定义，是经创造者授权的权威版本（同理，本文中“神经多样性范式”与“神经少数群体”的定义也具有同等权威性，因为这两个术语最初正是由我本人创造的）。



Neurodivergence is a value-neutral term that encompasses any significant divergence from dominant cultural norms of neurocognitive functioning—anything from autism to dyslexia to dyspraxia to aphantasia to synesthesia to epilepsy to schizophrenia to PTSD to Williams Syndrome to the cool stuff that long-term meditation practice does to the brains of Buddhist monks. Kassiane has repeatedly stated, in public and in private, that she intended the term to be as broadly inclusive as possible.

“神经多样性”是一个价值中立的术语，涵盖了与主流文化中关于神经认知功能规范的任何显著差异——从自闭症、阅读障碍、运动协调障碍、无象性、联觉、癫痫、精神分裂症、创伤后应激障碍（PTSD）、威廉姆斯综合征，到长期冥想练习对佛教僧侣大脑产生的那些酷炫影响，无所不包。 卡西安曾多次在公开和私下场合表示，她希望这个术语能尽可能广泛地包容各种情况。



Unfortunately, as soon as the term started catching on, certain people started trying to redefine it more narrowly, in ways that directly violated Kassiane’s inclusive intent. These people would often try to claim, for instance, that the term neurodivergence only referred to forms of neurodivergence that are innate genetic neurodevelopmental variants like autism.

遗憾的是，就在这个术语开始流行之际，某些人便试图对其进行更狭隘的重新定义，这种做法直接违背了卡西安（Kassiane）所倡导的包容性初衷。例如，这些人常常声称，“神经多样性”这一术语仅指像自闭症那样先天性的、由基因决定的神经发育变异。



It struck me that the main reason people were trying to distort the meaning of the word neurodivergence in this exclusionary way was because they were trying to talk about neurominority groups but they didn’t have the word neurominority. So I coined the term neurominority in 2004 partly so that I’d have a term to use when I wanted to talk specifically about groups of people who all share similar forms of innate developmental neurodivergence for which they might encounter discrimination (e.g., autistic or dyslexic people), and partly so that other people would have a term for that purpose—and would thus, I hoped, stop misusing Kassiane’s term.

我意识到，人们之所以试图以这种排他性的方式曲解“神经多样性”一词的含义，主要是因为他们想讨论“神经少数群体”，却没有“神经少数群体”这个词。 因此，我在 2004 年创造了“神经少数群体”这一术语，一方面是为了在需要具体讨论那些因具有相似形式的先天性发育性神经多样性而可能遭受歧视的人群（例如自闭症或阅读障碍者）时，能有一个专用的术语；另一方面也是为了让其他人也能拥有一个用于此目的的术语——从而， ——我希望——不再误用卡西安（Kassiane）的术语。



Two decades later, I still encounter people who are trying to make the definitions of neurodivergent and neurodivergence narrower and less inclusive, or who have been taught an incorrect and exclusionary definition. As long as they’re the sort of people who are open to learning (rather than the sort whose egos are so invested in being right that they aggressively double down on their errors), I sometimes find the problem can often be solved just by introducing them to the term neurominority, and explaining the distinction between neurominority and neurodivergent.

二十年过去了，我仍会遇到一些人试图让“神经殊异”和“神经殊异性”的定义变得更狭隘、更缺乏包容性，或是被灌输了一种错误且排他性的定义。只要他们是那种愿意学习的人（而非那种自我意识过于强烈、固执己见、加倍坚持错误的人），我有时发现，只需向他们介绍“神经少数群体”这一术语，并解释“神经少数群体”与“神经殊异”之间的区别，问题往往就能迎刃而解。



I’ll say this one more time, because so many folks seem to have trouble grasping it: neurodivergent is not a euphemism for autistic, or for “autistic and/or ADHD,” or anything along those lines. If you mean autistic, say autistic. If you mean “autistic and/or ADHD,” say “autistic and/or ADHD.” There are myriad possible ways to be neurodivergent, and many of them bear no resemblance whatsoever to autism or ADHD.

我再强调一次，因为很多人似乎难以理解这一点：“神经殊异”并非“孤独谱系”的委婉说法，也不是“孤独谱系和/或注意力缺陷多动障碍”之类的代称。如果你指的是孤独谱系，就请直接说孤独谱系；如果你指的是“孤独谱系和/或注意力缺陷多动障碍”，就请直接说“孤独谱系和/或注意力缺陷多动障碍”。成为神经殊异的方式有无数种，其中许多与孤独谱系或注意力缺陷多动障碍毫无相似之处。



•



The single most common language error that people make, in writing or speaking about neurodiversity-related matters, is still the misuse of the word neurodiverse to mean neurodivergent. I already discuss particular error at length in the “Terms & Definitions” piece itself. For the benefit anyone who’s still confused about this particular issue, please allow me to boil it all down to three clear and simple rules:

在撰写或谈论与神经多样性相关的话题时，人们最常犯的语言错误，仍然是误用"神经多元"一词来指代"神经殊异"。我已在《术语与定义》一文中详细讨论过这一特定错误。为了帮助仍对此问题感到困惑的朋友，请允许我将要点归纳为三条清晰简单的规则：




Never, ever refer to yourself or any other individual as “neurodiverse.” There is no such thing as a “neurodiverse person.” The word you’re looking for is neurodivergent.

永远不要用"神经多元"来指代自己或任何个体。根本不存在所谓的"神经多元的人"。你真正想用的词是"神经殊异"。



Never, ever describe neurodivergent people or neurominority members collectively as “neurodiverse people.”

永远不要将神经殊异群体或神经少数群体成员统称为"神经多元的人"。



Never, ever misuse “diverse” as a synonym or euphemism for “member of a marginalized or oppressed group,” whether you’re talking about neurodiversity, ethnic diversity, or any other form of diversity.

永远不要将"多元"误用作"边缘化或受压迫群体成员"的同义词或委婉语——无论你谈论的是神经多样性、种族多样性，还是其他任何形式的多样性。




One thing I’ve learned about the error of misusing neurodiverse to mean neurodivergent is that it’s an absolutely reliable indicator that the person making the error is a person whose thinking is still rooted in the pathology paradigm on some level, and who has simply misappropriated some neurodiversity-related terminology without actually bothering to study the neurodiversity paradigm or the work of the (mostly autistic) scholars and thinkers who developed the neurodiversity paradigm. It doesn’t matter how well-known the person in question is, or what sort of credentials they boast; if they haven’t learned words like neurodivergent and neurominority, and they’re misusing the word neurodiverse instead, you can be 100% sure that you’re looking at a person who hasn’t done their homework well enough to really know what they’re talking about.

关于将“神经多样性”（neurodiverse）误用为“神经差异性”（neurodivergent）这一错误，我领悟到的一点是：这绝对是一个可靠的指标，表明犯此错误的人在某种程度上思维仍根植于病理学范式，他们只是擅自挪用了某些与神经多样性相关的术语，却从未真正去研究神经多样性范式，也未曾深入了解那些（多为自闭症人士）建立该范式的学者和思想家的研究成果。 无论此人名气多大，或拥有何等资历；如果他们连“神经多样性群体”和“神经少数群体”这样的词汇都不了解，却错误地使用“神经多样性”一词，那么你可以百分之百确信，眼前这个人并没有做好功课，根本不知道自己在谈论什么。



•



Finally, it’s of the utmost importance to remember that the pathology paradigm and the neurodiversity paradigm are ways of understanding and relating to the phenomenon of human neurodiversity, and are foundations for practice—i.e., for how one treats one’s fellow humans. The vocabulary that expresses the conceptual basis of a paradigm is an essential aspect of that paradigm, but the vocabulary itself is not the paradigm. Adopting the language of the neurodiversity paradigm isn’t the same as actually making a meaningful shift in one’s consciousness and one’s practices.

最后，必须牢记的是，病理学范式和神经多样性范式都是理解和看待人类神经多样性现象的方式，也是实践的基础——即决定我们如何对待他人的基础。表达范式概念基础的术语是该范式不可或缺的组成部分，但术语本身并非范式。 采用神经多样性范式的语言，并不等同于在意识和实践中真正实现有意义的转变。



I’ve found that the people who haven’t truly made an internal shift to the neurodiversity paradigm, and are just appropriating the terminology of the neurodiversity paradigm while still operating based on the pathology paradigm, tend to use the terminology badly because they don’t understand what it really means. But even if someone seems to be using the vocabulary of the neurodiversity paradigm well, that’s no guarantee that they’ve made an authentic shift in their consciousness. If a person is talking about “overcoming neurodivergence,” or is subjecting autistic children to “behavioral therapy” in order to make them act more like neurotypical children, they’re still clearly operating based on the pathology paradigm regardless of what words they’ve adopted to disguise it.

我发现，那些尚未真正从内心转变为神经多样性范式，只是借用了神经多样性范式的术语，却仍基于病理学范式行事的人，往往会错误地使用这些术语，因为他们并不理解其真正的含义。但即使有人看似很好地运用了神经多样性范式的词汇，也并不能保证他们的意识已经发生了真正的转变。 如果有人谈论“克服神经多样性”，或者为了让自闭症儿童的行为更像神经典型儿童而对他们施以“行为疗法”，那么无论他们采用何种词汇来掩饰，显然仍是在病理范式下行事。



•



The definitions I provide in “Neurodiversity: Some Basic Terms & Definitions,” while still accurate, are simplified for the sake of brevity. Nowadays I feel that certain terms, like neurodiversity and neurotypical, require more nuanced explanation in order to adequately convey the complexity of the concepts and in order to discourage overly reductionist interpretations. I’ve attempted to convey these more nuanced understandings in the two chapters that follow this one.

我在《神经多样性：一些基本术语与定义》中提供的定义虽然仍然准确，但为了简洁而进行了简化。如今我认为某些术语（如神经多样性和神经典型）需要更细致的解释，才能充分传达这些概念的复杂性，并避免过于简化的解读。在接下来的两章中，我尝试传达了这些更细致的理解。







---


Nick_ebook-11










Defining Neurodiversity

定义神经多样性



This brief essay is a new one, written especially for this book in the Summer of 2021. It started out as one of my comments on “Throw Away the Master’s Tools,” but it got long enough that I decided to give it its own chapter.

这篇短文是 2021 年夏季专为本书撰写的新作。最初它只是我对《抛弃主人的工具》一文的一条评论，但篇幅渐长后，我决定将其独立成章。



Neurodiversity is the variation among minds.

神经多样性是指心智之间的差异。



Each human being differs to some extent from every other human being, with respect to their neurocognitive functioning—how they think, perceive, know, and develop, how their minds process information and interact with the world. Neurodiversity is the name for this phenomenon.

每个人类个体在神经认知功能方面——即思考、感知、认知、发展的方式，以及心智处理信息、与世界互动的方式——都与其他个体存在不同程度的差异。神经多样性正是这一现象的命名。



Neurodiversity is an intrinsic characteristic of the human species. It is a diversity produced by a combination of multiple interacting factors, including the myriad possible permutations of genetics, the influence of developmental environments on genetic expression, and the infinite variety of ways in which each individual mind is shaped by culture, activity, environment, and experience throughout the lifespan.

神经多样性是人类物种固有的特征。这种多样性由多种相互作用因素共同产生，包括基因的无数可能组合、发育环境对基因表达的影响，以及每个个体心智在生命历程中通过文化、活动、环境和经验塑造的无限方式。



In speaking of neurodiversity as the diversity among minds, I use the word mind in the broadest possible sense, to encompass the totality of every aspect of perception, cognition, emotion, memory, psyche, and consciousness.

在将神经多样性视为心智之间的多样性时，我以最广义的方式使用"心智"一词，涵盖感知、认知、情感、记忆、心理和意识等所有方面的整体。



Mind is an embodied phenomenon. The activity and development of the mind has a physical component in the form of electrochemical activity in the brain; the mind is encoded in the brain as ever-changing webs of neural connectivity. Changes in the brain create changes in the mind, and changes in the mind—new experiences, new mental activity—create changes in the brain. The brain, meanwhile, is not separate from the rest of the body; the body is a system of which the brain is one part, intricately interconnected with the rest by a vast network of nerves and blood vessels. The brain directs bodily activity and at the same time is continually affected and shaped by bodily activity and experience.

心灵是一种具身现象。心灵的活动与发展具有物理基础，表现为大脑中的电化学活动；心灵以不断变化的神经连接网络形式编码于大脑中。大脑的变化引发心灵的变化，而心灵的变化——新的体验、新的心理活动——又反过来重塑大脑。与此同时，大脑并非独立于身体其他部分存在；身体是一个系统，大脑是其中一部分，通过庞大的神经网络和血管系统与身体其他部分紧密相连。大脑指挥着身体活动，同时也不断受到身体活动与体验的影响与塑造。



Mind is inextricably entwined with brain, and brain with body; thus, mind is inextricably entwined with body in a single complex system and in a continuous dance of mutual shaping. We’re not minds riding around in vehicles of flesh and bone; we’re bodyminds, bodies that think and perceive. Experience, awareness, sense of self, psychological development, and capacities for feeling, knowing, cognition, connection, and action are all entwined with—and shape, and are shaped by—habits of bodily usage, including habits of movement, posture, breath, contact, consumption, tension and relaxation, gaze, gesture, and expression.

心灵与大脑密不可分，大脑与身体亦如此；因此，心灵与身体在一个复杂的系统中相互交织，持续进行着相互塑造的舞蹈。我们并非乘坐血肉之躯的载具四处游荡的心灵；我们是身心合一的存在，是能够思考与感知的身体。体验、意识、自我感、心理发展，以及感受、认知、理解、联结和行动的能力，都与身体的使用习惯——包括运动、姿势、呼吸、接触、消耗、紧张与放松、凝视、手势和表达的习惯——相互交织，并彼此塑造。



If mind is an embodied phenomenon, it follows that the diversity of minds must also be a diversity of embodiments. Variations in neurocognitive functioning are entwined with variations in embodiment; autism, for example, involves distinctive modes of physicality and sensorimotor experience that are intimately connected with autistic modes of cognition. So when I say that neurodiversity is the diversity among minds, I’m really saying that it’s the diversity among bodyminds.

如果心灵是一种具身现象，那么心灵的多样性必然也是具身方式的多样性。神经认知功能的差异与身体形态的差异相互交织；例如，孤独谱系涉及独特的身体性和感觉运动模式，这些模式与孤独谱系的认知方式密切相关。因此，当我提到神经多样性是心灵的多样性时，实际上是在说它是身心整体的多样性。



It used to be commonplace for people to speak of neurodiversity as diversity among brains, and there are still people who speak about it that way. I think this is a mistake, an overly reductionist and essentialist definition that’s decades behind present-day understandings of how human bodyminds work.

过去人们常将神经多样性描述为大脑的多样性，至今仍有人沿用这种说法。我认为这是一种错误，是过于简化且本质主义的定义，落后于当代对人类身心运作机制的理解数十年之久。



The persistence of this reductionist interpretation of neurodiversity is no doubt at least partly due to the fact that when most people see the prefix neuro-, they translate it as brain. But neuro- doesn’t mean brain, it means nerve. In my view, the neuro- in neurodiversity is most usefully understood as referring not just to the brain but to the entire nervous system—and, by extension, to the full complexity of human cognition and the central role the nervous system plays in the embodied dance of consciousness.

这种对神经多样性的简化解读之所以持续存在，无疑部分源于大多数人看到前缀"神经-"时，会将其直接理解为"大脑"。但"神经-"的本意并非大脑，而是指神经。在我看来，神经多样性中的"神经-"前缀最有益的理解方式，不应局限于大脑，而应涵盖整个神经系统——进而延伸至人类认知的完整复杂性，以及神经系统在意识具身舞蹈中所扮演的核心角色。







---


Nick_ebook-12










Defining Neurotypicality &

Neurodivergence

定义神经典型性与神经殊异性



Like the previous essay, this is a new one written in the Summer of 2021—another piece that started out as a comment on “Throw Away the Master’s Tools” and then grew into its own chapter.

与前一篇论文类似，这篇也是 2021 年夏季新写的——另一篇最初是作为对“扔掉主人的工具”的评论，后来发展成独立章节的文章。



The term neurotypical has been around since at least the early 1990s. It’s a term that’s widely misunderstood, and widely objected to by the people who misunderstand it. The standard objection goes something like this: “No one is neurotypical because everyone’s brain is unique!” But in fact, the concept of neurotypicality is in no way incompatible with recognizing the uniqueness of every brain and every mind, and this argument against the term neurotypical is based in an inaccurate understanding of what the term means.

“神经典型性”一词至少自 20 世纪 90 年代初就已存在。这是一个被广泛误解的术语，而误解它的人往往对其持反对态度。典型的反对意见大致如下：“没有人是神经典型的，因为每个人的大脑都是独一无二的！”但事实上，神经典型性的概念与承认每个大脑和每个心灵的独特性丝毫不矛盾，这种反对该术语的论点建立在对该词含义的误解之上。



The false assumption underlying the “no one is neurotypical” argument is the assumption that neurotypical is just a synonym for normal. It’s not. The neurodiversity paradigm rejects the whole idea that there’s such a thing as a “normal brain” or a “normal mind.” Belief in “normal” minds and brains is the hallmark of the pathology paradigm, so it would make no sense at all for the vocabulary of the neurodiversity paradigm to include a term that meant “having a normal mind or brain.”

“没有人是神经典型者”这一论点背后隐藏的错误假设，是将“神经典型”等同于“正常”。但事实并非如此。神经多样性范式彻底否定了存在所谓“正常大脑”或“正常心智”的概念。相信存在“正常”心智与大脑，正是病理范式的核心特征——因此，神经多样性范式的词汇体系中，绝不可能包含一个意为“拥有正常心智或大脑”的术语。



To understand what we do mean by neurotypical, let’s draw an analogy between neurodiversity and the diversity of gender and sexuality. The pathology paradigm’s construction and idealization of normativity pervades the dominant culture—which means that the majority of people in the world still behave as if there’s such a thing as a normal brain or mind, in much the same way that the majority of people in the world still behave as if culturally constructed heteronormative gender roles are “normal” and “natural.”

要理解我们所说的“神经典型”究竟指什么，不妨将神经多样性与性别及性取向的多样性进行类比。病理范式对规范性的建构与理想化，深深渗透于主流文化之中——这意味着世界上大多数人仍表现得仿佛存在所谓“正常大脑”或“正常心智”，正如世界上大多数人仍将文化建构的异性恋规范性别角色视为“正常”与“自然”一般。



From earliest childhood, people are trained and pressured into the performance of heteronormativity—the performance of a restrictive binary heterosexual masculine or feminine gender role assigned to them at birth based on the shape of their genitalia. By the same token, people are trained and pressured from earliest childhood into the performance of neuronormativity—the performance of the local dominant culture’s current prevailing images of how a so-called “normal” person with a so-called “normal” mind thinks and looks and behaves.

从童年早期开始，人们就被训练和施压去表演异性恋规范——即基于出生时生殖器形态被赋予的、限制性的二元异性恋男性或女性性别角色表演。同样地，从童年早期开始，人们也被训练和施压去表演神经规范——即表演当地主流文化当前盛行的、关于所谓"正常"心智的"正常"人如何思考、外表和行为的标准形象。



If you can perform your assigned heteronormative gender role convincingly enough throughout your life, and if staying within the boundaries of that performance is actually sustainable and bearable for you, and if you choose to stay within those boundaries and comply with the demands of heteronormativity, then the dominant culture judges your gender and sexuality to be “normal” and rewards you with cisgender privilege and straight privilege—in other words, the reward for your constant and convincing compliance with dominant standards of heteronormativity is that members and institutions of the dominant culture don’t discriminate against you for being queer.

如果你能在整个生命历程中足够令人信服地扮演好被指定的异性恋规范性别角色，并且这种角色扮演的边界对你而言确实可持续且可承受，同时你选择停留在这些边界内并服从异性恋规范的要求，那么主流文化就会判定你的性别与性取向为"正常"，并赋予你顺性别特权与异性恋特权——换言之，你持续且令人信服地服从主流异性恋规范所获得的奖赏，就是主流文化的成员与机构不会因你属于酷儿群体而对你进行歧视。



By the same token, if the functioning of your bodymind is such that it’s possible and bearable for you convincingly maintain the performance of neuronormativity throughout your life, and if you choose to maintain that performance and comply with the dominant culture’s standards of neuronormativity, then the dominant culture judges your mind to be “normal” and rewards you with neurotypical privilege—in other words, the reward for your constant and convincing compliance with dominant standards of neuronormativity is that members and institutions of the dominant culture don’t discriminate against you for being “abnormal.” This is what it means to be neurotypical.

同理，如果你的身心运作方式使你能够且忍受终身令人信服地维持神经规范性的表演，并且你选择维持这种表演、遵从主流文化的神经规范性标准，那么主流文化就会判定你的心智"正常"，并赋予你神经典型特权——换言之，你持续且令人信服地遵从主流神经规范性标准所获得的回报，就是主流文化的成员和机构不会因你"异常"而歧视你。这就是成为神经典型者的含义。



So when we say someone is neurotypical, we don’t mean they were born with a specific type of brain, and that the type of brain they were born with is the “normal” type—because that’s just nonsense. There’s no such thing as a normal brain or a normal “type of brain.” In fact, while it can be useful to consider certain bodyminds in terms of categorizations like autistic or dyslexic, and while the bodyminds that fit into those categories often do appear to share certain distinguishing neurobiological characteristics, the whole idea of “types of brains” is ultimately rather dubious, or, at the very least, overly reductionist.

因此，当我们说某人属于神经典型者时，并非指他们天生拥有特定类型的大脑，且这种大脑类型属于"正常"范畴——因为这种说法毫无意义。根本不存在所谓正常的大脑或正常的"大脑类型"。事实上，虽然将某些身心状态归类为孤独谱系或阅读障碍等类别可能具有参考价值，且符合这些类别的身心状态确实常表现出某些独特的神经生物学特征，但"大脑类型"这一整体概念终究值得商榷，至少是过度简化了。



When we say someone is neurotypical, what we mean is that they live, act, and experience the world in a way that consistently falls within the boundaries of neuronormativity—i.e., within the boundaries of what the prevailing culture imagines a person with a “normal mind” to be like. That’s quite different from saying that a person actually has a normal mind or a normal brain.

当我们说某人属于神经典型者时，实际含义是：他们的生活方式、行为模式及对世界的体验始终符合神经规范性标准——即符合主流文化对"正常心智"者的想象。这与声称某人确实拥有正常心智或正常大脑是截然不同的概念。



This queer-theory-informed understanding of the culturally constructed and situated nature of neurotypicality also enables us to better understand the meaning of the terms neurodivergent and neurodivergence. These terms, like the term neurotypical, are often objected to by well-intentioned people who don’t fully understand their meanings. The usual objection is something along the lines of, “Calling a mind divergent implies that the mind diverges from normal, and I don’t believe there’s such a thing as a normal mind.”

这种基于酷儿理论的理解，揭示了神经典型性在文化建构与情境中的本质，也让我们更清晰地把握“神经殊异”与“神经殊异性”这两个术语的含义。如同“神经典型性”一词，这些术语常遭到善意却未完全理解其内涵者的质疑。常见的反对意见大致是：“将某种心智称为‘殊异’，意味着它偏离了‘正常’，而我认为根本不存在所谓‘正常的心智’。”



As already noted, though, the neurodiversity paradigm also rejects the idea that there’s such a thing as a normal mind. When we call someone neurodivergent we don’t mean that they aren’t “normal,” we mean that they aren’t neurotypical.

但如前所述，神经多样性范式同样否定“正常心智”的存在。当我们称某人为“神经殊异者”时，并非指其“不正常”，而是指其“非神经典型”。



In other words, what a neurodivergent person diverges from are the prevailing culturally constructed standards and culturally mandated performance of neuronormativity. Neurodivergence is divergence not from some “objective” state of normality (which, again, doesn’t exist), but rather from whatever constructed image and performance of normality the prevailing culture currently seeks to impose.

换言之，神经殊异者所偏离的，是主流文化建构的神经规范性标准及其强制要求的行为表现。神经殊异性并非偏离某种“客观”的正常状态（这种状态本不存在），而是偏离主流文化当前试图强加的那种被建构的“正常”形象与行为模式。







---


Nick_ebook-13










Neurodivergence & Disability

神经殊异性与残障



Another chapter written especially for this book in 2021.

2021 年专为本书撰写的另一章。



In many years of teaching college courses on autism and the neurodiversity paradigm, not to mention incorporating material on autism and other forms of neurodivergence into various psychology courses, a troubling issue I’ve consistently encountered is that the vast majority of my students—even at the graduate level—arrive in my classroom entirely unfamiliar with the social model of disability. Since I’m planning to use this book as a textbook in at least one of my courses, I figure this is my chance to save myself from having to explain Disability Theory 101 all over again every semester. I can just write the explanation into the textbook, with particular focus on how it applies to the experience of autistic people and members of other pathologized neurominority groups.

在多年教授关于孤独谱系与神经多样性范式的大学课程中，更不用说将孤独谱系及其他神经殊异性相关内容融入各类心理学课程时，我始终遇到一个令人困扰的问题：绝大多数学生——甚至研究生阶段——进入我的课堂时，对残障的社会模式完全陌生。既然我计划将本书用作至少一门课程的教材，我认为这是让自己免于每学期都要重新解释一遍残障理论 101 的机会。我只需将解释写入教材，特别聚焦于该理论如何适用于孤独谱系群体及其他被病理化的神经少数群体的经历。



The Medical Model vs the Social Model

医疗模式与社会模式



There are two distinct models for understanding disability. One model is generally referred to, in the field of Disability Studies, as the medical model of disability (or sometimes, in the UK, the individual model of disability). The other model is generally referred to as the social model of disability. They’re not the only possible models, but at present nearly all disability-related theory and praxis is based in one or the other of these two models.

理解残障有两种不同的模式。在残障研究领域，一种模式通常被称为残障的医疗模式（有时在英国也被称为残障的个人模式）。另一种模式通常被称为残障的社会模式。它们并非唯一可能的模式，但目前几乎所有与残障相关的理论和实践都基于这两种模式之一。



In the medical model, the term disability refers to an impairment or defect which is seen as being located in the body and/or mind of an individual. Through the lens of the medical model, in other words, a person is seen as “having” a disability. The medical model is currently the prevailing model in the modern world, and has been for quite some time, which means it’s the understanding of disability that most people have picked up by default unless they’ve actively looked for an alternative and/or done some serious critical thinking on the subject. The medical model is highly compatible with capitalism and other related aspects of the prevailing culture. When it comes to the discourse on autism and various other marginalized neurocognitive styles, the medical model is deeply entwined with the pathology paradigm.

在医疗模式中，"残障"一词指的是被视为存在于个体身体和/或心智中的损伤或缺陷。换言之，通过医疗模式的视角，一个人被视为"拥有"某种残障。医疗模式是当今世界的主流模式，且已持续相当长的时间，这意味着除非人们主动寻找替代观点或对此进行严肃的批判性思考，否则大多数人默认接受的便是这种对残障的理解。医疗模式与资本主义及主流文化的其他相关方面高度契合。在涉及孤独谱系及其他被边缘化的神经认知风格的讨论中，医疗模式与病理学范式紧密交织。



The social model of disability emerged within the disability rights movement and remains a cornerstone of disability rights activism, as well as being a foundational concept in the field of Disability Studies. When it comes to the discourse on autism and various other marginalized neurocognitive styles, the social model is deeply entwined with the neurodiversity paradigm and the neurodiversity movement. In the social model, disabled is understood as the opposite of enabled. Society is set up to meet the needs of people with a specific set of traits, needs, and abilities. Those privileged people are abled, or enabled—in other words, society is set up to enable their participation.

残障的社会模式源于残障权利运动，至今仍是残障权利行动的核心支柱，也是残障研究领域的基础概念。在涉及孤独谱系及各类边缘化神经认知风格的讨论中，社会模式与神经多样性范式及神经多样性运动紧密交织。在社会模式中，"残障"被理解为"赋能"的反面。社会体系是为满足特定特质、需求与能力的人群而构建的。这些享有特权的人被称为"健全者"或"被赋能者"——换言之，社会体系的构建旨在保障他们的参与。



Within the social model of disability, when we say that a person is disabled, we mean that society isn’t properly set up to enable their participation, and instead is often set up in a way that creates barriers to their participation (e.g., building staircases without ramps or good working elevators is a barrier to wheelchair users; the expectation of eye contact in job interviews is a barrier to autistic people). Thus, those people whose needs differ significantly from those of the dominant majority are disabled by society rather than enabled.

在残障的社会模式下，当我们说一个人是残障人士时，意味着社会并未妥善设置以促进其参与，反而常常以制造参与障碍的方式运作（例如，建造楼梯而不设坡道或良好运行的电梯，对轮椅使用者构成障碍；面试中期待眼神交流，对孤独谱系群体构成障碍）。因此，那些需求与主流多数群体显著不同的人，被社会致残而非赋能。



Where the medical model is reductionist, the social model is far more complex and nuanced because disability is understood as always being contingent upon the context in which the individual is currently operating. In other words, disability is not a static condition located within the individual (as per the medical model) but instead is a phenomenon that manifests in varying ways and varying degrees depending upon the nature and degree of the mismatch between the individual’s needs and the way those needs are accommodated in the context of a given situation or societal surround.

医疗模式是还原论的，而社会模式则远为复杂且微妙，因为残障始终被理解为取决于个体当前所处的情境。换言之，残障并非个体内部的静态状况（如医疗模式所认为），而是一种现象，其表现形式和程度因个体需求与特定情境或社会环境对其需求的适配程度之间的不匹配性质与程度而异。



Unlike the medical model, the social model makes a crucial distinction between disability and impairment. An impairment is when an individual lacks some specific capacity that the majority of individuals possess. In the medical model disability and impairment are viewed as effectively synonymous. In the social model, however, an impairment creates an atypical set of access needs, and disability is what happens when those needs aren’t sufficiently accommodated. You’re disabled to whatever degree your participation isn’t properly enabled within a given setting.

与医疗模式不同，社会模式对残障和损伤做出了关键区分。损伤是指个体缺乏大多数人所具备的某种特定能力。在医疗模式中，残障和损伤被视为实质上同义的概念。然而在社会模式中，损伤会带来一套非典型的无障碍需求，而残障则是在这些需求未能得到充分满足时发生的情况。当你在特定环境中无法获得适当参与条件时，你就在相应程度上处于残障状态。



Understood through the lens of the social model, then, disability (or disablement) is a form of marginalization. This is why the phrase person with a disability is part of the language of the medical model: it’s a phrase that implies that the disability is located entirely within the bodymind of the person, rather than in the way the external environment fails to meet the person’s access needs.

通过社会模式的视角来理解，残障（或致残）是一种边缘化形式。这就是为什么"残障人士"这一表述属于医疗模式的语言范畴：这种说法暗示残障完全存在于个体的身心之中，而非源于外部环境未能满足该个体的无障碍需求。



In the social model, people don’t have disabilities; people are disabled. In the social model, a phrase like person with a disability is nonsensical; it’s like saying person with a marginalization or person with an oppression. And that disgusting ableist euphemism differently abled is even more ridiculous; it’s like describing members of an oppressed group as differently privileged.

在社会模式中，人们并非“拥有残障”，而是“被致残”。在社会模式中，像“残障人士”这样的说法毫无意义，就如同说“被边缘化的人”或“受压迫的人”一样。而那个令人作呕的、能力主义者的委婉说法“能力不同者”则更加荒谬，这就像把受压迫群体的成员描述为“特权不同者”一样。



A Few Examples

几个例子



Let’s start with a relatively simple example to help make the social model of disability more clear: if you can’t walk, that’s what’s known as a mobility impairment. Are you disabled? Yes, but here’s the crucial piece that the social model highlights: the precise degree to which you’re disabled depends on how well your access needs are accommodated.

让我们从一个相对简单的例子开始，以帮助更清晰地理解残障的社会模式：如果你无法行走，这被称为行动损伤。你算残障吗？是的，但社会模式强调的关键在于：你被致残的具体程度，取决于你的无障碍需求得到满足的程度。



If you can’t walk, a wheelchair is an invaluable accommodation. If you live in a society that hasn’t invented wheelchairs or only has the clunkiest of old-fashioned wheelchairs, you’re going to be more disabled than if you live in a society that provides all its mobility-impaired citizens with high-quality electric wheelchairs. If you live in a town where most of the buildings (and public transit stations and other structures) have stairs but no ramps or elevators, and where most of the doorways are absurdly narrow, then you’re going to be much more disabled than you would be if you lived in a town in which all of the structures are built with wheelchair access in mind.

如果你无法行走，轮椅便是一种极为宝贵的辅助工具。如果你生活在一个尚未发明轮椅、或只有最笨重的老式轮椅的社会，那么你面临的障碍将比生活在为所有行动不便的公民提供高质量电动轮椅的社会中更为严重。如果你居住的城镇中，大多数建筑（包括公共交通站点和其他设施）只有楼梯而没有坡道或电梯，且大部分门道窄得离谱，那么你面临的障碍将远比生活在所有建筑都考虑轮椅通行设计的城镇中更为严重。



Note also that social attitudes are a key component in the dynamics of enablement and disablement: an office building might have state-of-the-art ramps and elevators and wide automatic doors, but none of that will matter much if the people who work in the building are unwilling to hire a wheelchair user.

同时请注意，社会态度也是赋能与致残动态中的关键组成部分：一栋办公楼可能配备了最先进的坡道、电梯和宽敞的自动门，但如果楼内的工作人员不愿雇用轮椅使用者，那么这些设施便毫无意义。



Moving on to an example that’s specifically neurodivergence-related: in the dyslexic bodymind, the impairment is in the capacity to process visual detail in a linear two-dimensional fashion, which of course affects the ability to read and spell. This impairment seems to be just an inconvenient side effect of a neurocognitive processing style that also comes with significant strengths in areas like 3-D spatial processing and nonlinear big-picture thinking. And here’s where it gets interesting, from a social model of disability perspective: it’s a side effect that only becomes a significant inconvenience in cultures and contexts in which it’s important to be able to read.

接下来看一个与神经殊异性相关的例子：在阅读障碍者的身心系统中，损伤体现在以线性二维方式处理视觉细节的能力上，这自然会影响阅读和拼写能力。这种损伤似乎只是某种神经认知处理模式带来的不便副作用，而这种模式在三维空间处理和非线性全局思维等领域也具备显著优势。从社会残障模型的角度来看，有趣之处在于：这种副作用只有在重视阅读能力的文化背景和情境中才会成为显著障碍。



Dyslexia, like autism and various other forms of innate neurodivergence, has likely existed within the human species for a very long time, probably since our prehistoric hunter-gatherer days. For most of that vast span of time, societal participation and the meeting of societal demands haven’t required the ability to quickly and accurately process a lot of linear strings of written or typed letters and words on flat surfaces—which means that for most of the time dyslexia has been around, being dyslexic hasn’t meant being disabled at all. And within the next few centuries, it’s possible that dyslexic people will go back to not being disabled at all, either because massive societal collapse makes literacy less relevant, or because massive technological advancement brings us to a stage where the reading and writing of linear text is largely supplanted by engagement with information in multisensory 3-D virtual interfaces. Dyslexia thus serves as a particularly clear illustration of the context-dependent nature of disability.

阅读障碍，如同孤独谱系及其他多种先天神经殊异性特征，很可能在人类物种中存在了极其漫长的岁月，或许可追溯至史前狩猎采集时代。在这段浩瀚时光中，社会参与及满足社会需求并不要求人们具备快速准确处理平面线性文字符号的能力——这意味着在阅读障碍存在的绝大部分时间里，阅读障碍者根本不被视为残障。而在未来几个世纪内，阅读障碍者可能重新回归非残障状态，这要么源于社会体系大规模崩溃导致读写能力失去价值，要么源于科技巨变使线性文本读写被多感官三维虚拟界面交互所取代。阅读障碍由此成为揭示残障情境依赖性的绝佳例证。



And with dyslexia, again, attitudes are part of the social context that enables or disables. A dyslexic child is far more disabled by a school environment in which they’re shamed and written off as “stupid” for their reading difficulties, than by a school environment that responds to those same difficulties by immediately providing accommodations, taking a strengths-based approach to the child’s development, teaching the child what dyslexia is in a non-stigmatizing way, and providing the child with examples of positive dyslexic role models. When proponents of the reductionist medical model describe a dyslexic child as “having a learning disability,” they promote ableism by framing the disability as a defect located within the child (i.e., as something the child “has”), and by thus directing attention away from the child’s environment and the ways in which the local education system might be functioning to disable the child rather than enable them.

再以阅读障碍为例，态度同样是构成社会情境中"赋能"或"致残"的关键因素。一个患有阅读障碍的儿童，若身处因阅读困难而被羞辱、被贴上"愚蠢"标签的学校环境，其遭受的残障程度远甚于另一种学校环境——后者能针对同样的困难立即提供合理便利，以优势视角促进儿童发展，用去污名化的方式向儿童解释何为阅读障碍，并为其提供积极的阅读障碍榜样案例。当还原论医疗模式的支持者将阅读障碍儿童描述为"有学习障碍"时，他们通过将残障框定为儿童内在的缺陷（即儿童"拥有"的某种东西），从而将注意力从儿童所处的环境以及当地教育系统可能正在致残而非赋能儿童的方式上转移开，这实际上是在助长能力主义。



Finally, let’s consider the example of a hypothetical autistic individual who has no significant difficulty with motor coordination, can readily handle any sensory experiences they’re likely to encounter in day-to-day life in the modern world, and is cognitively capable of executing all the tasks that are assigned in whatever school or professional environment they find themselves in. Now let’s also say that this autistic person’s physical mannerisms are quite visibly autistic: rocking back and forth; no eye contact or imitation of neurotypical expressions; distinctively autistic hand and head motions (you’ll know what I’m talking about if you’ve hung out with enough autistic folks who haven’t been forced to suppress their natural embodiment styles). And add to this a distinctively autistic communication style (statements, questions, and answers that are direct, blunt, truthful, and literal).

最后，让我们设想一个假设的孤独谱系个体案例：此人运动协调能力无显著障碍，能自如应对现代日常生活中的各类感官体验，且认知能力足以完成所处学校或职场环境中的所有指定任务。但与此同时，这位孤独谱系人士的肢体语言明显带有孤独谱系特征：前后摇晃身体；避免眼神接触或模仿神经典型人群的表情；具有独特性的手部与头部动作（若你接触过足够多未被强制压抑自然表达方式的孤独谱系人士，便会明白我所指为何）。此外还伴有独特的孤独谱系沟通风格（陈述、提问与回答均直截了当、不加修饰、真实且字面化）。



In the context of the prevailing social milieu, this person is going to be disabled, because their autistic style of embodiment and communication will result in social rejection, discrimination, misunderstanding, disrespect, exclusion, and abuse by the majority of non-autistic people they encounter. A multitude of doors will be closed to them; they’ll have undue difficulty getting or keeping jobs (or other useful things, like apartments); their performance at school and work will be seriously impacted by the hostility of peers and authority figures; they’ll have a hard time getting any assistance they need from others (including those whose jobs are supposed to involve protecting people from abuse and discrimination). All this adds up to some pretty significant disablement.

在当前主流社会环境下，这个人将会处于失能状态，因为其孤独谱系特有的具身化与沟通方式，会导致他们遭遇多数非孤独谱系群体的社会排斥、歧视、误解、不尊重、排挤乃至虐待。无数机会之门将对他们关闭；他们获取或维持工作（以及其他生活必需品如公寓）将异常艰难；其学业与职场表现会因同伴与权威人物的敌意而严重受损；他们难以获得所需的任何援助（包括那些本应保护人们免受虐待与歧视的岗位人员）。这一切累积起来，构成了相当严重的失能状态。



What makes this particular example such an interesting study in the social model of disability and the dynamics of disablement is that this person’s styles of embodiment and communication aren’t actual functional impairments in any objective sense. The autistic person in this example is disabled entirely as a result of societal attitudes—specifically, the prevailing culture’s intolerance for divergence from the dominant norms of neurotypical social performance. The accommodations this person needs in order to enable their full societal access and participation consist entirely of changes to social attitudes.

这个特定案例之所以成为研究残障社会模型和致残动态的有趣范例，在于该个体的具身化风格与沟通方式在客观意义上并非真正的功能性损伤。此例中的孤独谱系者完全因社会态度——具体而言，是主流文化对偏离神经典型社会表现规范的不容忍——而陷入残障状态。该个体为获得充分的社会参与和准入所需的支持，完全取决于社会态度的转变。



(Note that a great many autistic people do also have specific impairments that require more material accommodation—for instance, non-speaking autistics who need access to assistive communication technologies, or autistics with the sort of sensory sensitivities that are best accommodated through adjustments to physical environments. But autistics like the one in the preceding example, who don’t have such impairments and whose disablement could be alleviated entirely through shifts in social attitudes without any substantial material or logistical accommodation, also exist, and I’ve chosen to focus the preceding example on such a person for purposes of more clearly illustrating one particular aspect of the social dynamics of disablement.)

（请注意，许多孤独谱系群体确实存在需要更多物质性便利的特定损伤——例如，需要辅助沟通技术的非口语孤独谱系者，或对感官敏感度较高、需通过调整物理环境来适应的孤独谱系者。但像前例中那样没有此类损伤、仅通过社会态度转变即可完全缓解其残障状态、无需实质性物质或后勤便利的孤独谱系者同样存在。我选择以前例中的这类人为焦点，是为了更清晰地阐明残障社会动态的某一特定方面。）



Autism & Disability

孤独症与残障



In the interest of clearing up a common misconception, I want to address a couple of specific points regarding the disablement of autistic people. Some people, working from incomplete and inaccurate understandings of the neurodiversity paradigm, somehow arrive at the false impression that the neurodiversity paradigm implies that autistic people aren’t disabled. This is a gross misinterpretation.

为澄清常见误解，我想就孤独谱系群体的残障问题谈几点具体内容。有些人基于对神经多样性范式不完整且不准确的理解，竟错误地认为该范式暗示孤独谱系者并非残障人士。这实属严重曲解。



Recall that the fundamental principles of the neurodiversity paradigm are that neurodiversity is one form of human diversity; that there’s no one “right” or “normal” type of mind; and that the social dynamics that manifest in regard to neurodiversity are similar to the social dynamics that manifest in regard to other forms of human diversity. None of these principles in any way contradicts or precludes the idea that some neurodivergent people might be disabled.

回顾神经多样性范式的核心原则：神经多样性是人类多样性的一种形式；不存在唯一“正确”或“正常”的心智类型；围绕神经多样性所呈现的社会动态，与其他形式人类多样性所呈现的社会动态相似。这些原则中没有任何一条与“某些神经殊异者可能属于残障人士”这一观点相矛盾或相排斥。



And in fact, modern society—a society which by and large is designed exclusively around neurotypical needs and expectations, and is unrelentingly hostile to deviation from neurotypical norms—systematically disables a great many neurodivergent people, autistic people included. Within the present social milieu, autistic people are almost always disabled to at least some degree.

事实上，现代社会——一个基本上完全围绕神经典型者的需求和期望来设计，且对偏离神经典型规范的行为毫不留情的社会——系统性地使大量神经殊异者（包括孤独谱系群体）陷入残障状态。在当下的社会环境中，孤独谱系群体几乎总是至少在一定程度上处于残障状态。



The reason that so many autistic rights activists and other folks interested in fostering autistic well-being have embraced the neurodiversity paradigm, and are opposed to framing autism as a pathology (e.g., a “disorder” or “condition”), isn’t that we’re pretending autistic people aren’t disabled. Rather, it’s that we’ve observed that the pathology paradigm serves to exacerbate rather than mitigate autistic disablement.

那么多孤独谱系权利活动家以及其他关心孤独谱系群体福祉的人之所以接受神经多样性范式，并反对将孤独谱系视为病理（例如“障碍”或“状况”），并不是因为我们假装孤独谱系群体没有残疾。相反，是因为我们观察到病理范式反而加剧而非减轻了孤独谱系群体的失能状况。



The assumption that autism is intrinsically pathological, intrinsically a problem or form of wrongness, leads inevitably to the assumption that the well-being of any given autistic person hinges on that autistic person somehow becoming less autistic. This in turn has the effect of keeping discourse and praxis focused on eliminating or “treating” autism—using methods that are consistently harmful to autistic people, such as abusive behaviorist approaches or pseudo-biomedical quackery—at the expense of any substantial focus on actions that would actually improve autistic people’s quality of life.

认为孤独谱系本质上是病理性的、本质上是一种问题或错误形式的假设，必然导致另一个假设：任何孤独谱系个体的福祉都取决于该个体以某种方式变得不那么孤独谱系。这反过来又使得话语和实践始终聚焦于消除或“治疗”孤独谱系——采用那些一贯对孤独谱系群体有害的方法，例如虐待性的行为主义方法或伪生物医学骗术——而牺牲了对真正能改善孤独谱系群体生活质量的行动的任何实质性关注。



The framework of the neurodiversity paradigm, on the other hand, supports approaches based in the social model of disability. If we start by recognizing autistic people as a marginalized group, we can see that their disablement is part of their marginalization; i.e., part of how autistics are marginalized within the present social milieu is that their access needs aren’t properly accommodated. We can also see that the pathology paradigm itself is one of the factors that contributes to autistic disablement—for instance, framing autism as a pathology fosters a societal mindset in which autistic modes of embodiment, expression, and communication are stigmatized as pathological symptoms rather than accommodated.

另一方面，神经多样性范式的框架支持基于残障社会模型的方法。如果我们首先承认孤独谱系群体是一个被边缘化的群体，就能发现他们的残障状态正是其边缘化的一部分——也就是说，在当前社会环境中，孤独谱系群体被边缘化的部分原因在于他们的无障碍需求未能得到妥善满足。我们同样可以看到，病理学范式本身就是导致孤独谱系群体残障化的因素之一——例如，将孤独谱系定义为病理现象会催生一种社会心态，使得孤独谱系群体的具身化、表达和沟通模式被污名化为病态症状，而非得到合理接纳。



The neurodiversity paradigm, properly understood and applied in conjunction with the social model of disability, thus suggests an approach to autistic well-being based in de-pathologizing autism, accepting autistic people as autistic people, and actively working to enable the full societal inclusion of autistic people by finding better ways to accommodate their access needs. Enablement as the solution to disablement.

因此，当正确理解神经多样性范式并将其与残障社会模型结合运用时，它便为促进孤独谱系群体的福祉提供了新思路：基于去病理化孤独谱系、承认孤独谱系群体作为独立个体的存在价值，并通过更有效地满足其无障碍需求来积极推动孤独谱系群体全面融入社会。以赋能作为解决残障化问题的根本途径。



This is why if you ask me whether autism is a disability, I’ll say no, but if you ask me whether autistic people are disabled, I’ll say yes. To people who don’t understand the distinction between the medical model of disability and the social model of disability, “autism is a disability” and “autistic people are disabled” might seem like they mean the same thing. But the implications of these two phrases are actually quite different. “Autism is a disability” essentially means “autism is a pathology or deficit,” whereas “autistic people are disabled” essentially means “autistic people’s needs are not properly accommodated by the world around them in a way that enables their societal participation.”

这就是为什么如果你问我孤独症是否是一种残障，我会说不；但如果你问我孤独谱系群体是否处于残障状态，我会说是。对于不了解残障医疗模式与残障社会模式区别的人来说，“孤独症是一种残障”和“孤独谱系群体处于残障状态”似乎表达的是同一回事。但这两句话的实际含义其实大相径庭。“孤独症是一种残障”本质上意味着“孤独症是一种病理或缺陷”，而“孤独谱系群体处于残障状态”本质上意味着“孤独谱系群体的需求未能被周围世界以促进其社会参与的方式妥善接纳”。



To say “autism is a disability” is to perpetuate the frameworks of the pathology paradigm and the medical model of disability, by framing autism as a problem located within the autistic individual. To say “autistic people are disabled,” by contrast, embraces the frameworks of the neurodiversity paradigm and the social model of disability—and opens the door to better approaches to autistic well-being—by framing autistic disablement as being the result of correctible mismatches between autistic needs and societal accommodations.

说“孤独症是一种残障”，就是延续病理学范式和医疗模式残障观的框架，将孤独症视为孤独谱系个体内在的问题。相比之下，说“孤独谱系群体是残障人士”，则拥抱了神经多样性范式和社会模式残障观——通过将孤独谱系群体的失能状态归因于孤独谱系需求与社会支持之间可修正的错配，为改善孤独谱系群体的福祉开辟了更优路径。



Not All Neurodivergent People Are Disabled

并非所有神经殊异者都是残障人士



In wrapping up this discussion of neurodivergence and disability, I want clarify one final point: not all neurodivergent people are disabled.

在结束关于神经殊异与残障的讨论前，我想澄清最后一点：并非所有神经殊异者都是残障人士。



Neurodivergence is a broadly inclusive term that means any significant divergence from dominant cultural norms of neurocognitive functioning. Kassiane Asasumasu, who coined the terms neurodivergence and neurodivergent way back in the year 2000, has consistently emphasized that she intended the terms to be interpreted as inclusively as possible—i.e., that when she says any significant divergence from dominant cultural norms of neurocognitive functioning, she means any significant divergence. In all the time I’ve known her and followed her writings, Kassiane has never once said, “Oh, wait, I only mean the forms of divergence that are pathologized,” or “Oh, wait, when I said that neurodivergent people are people whose neurocognitive functioning diverges from dominant norms, I only meant the disabled ones.”

神经殊异性是一个广泛包容的术语，意指任何与主流文化神经认知功能规范显著偏离的情况。早在 2000 年，创造"神经殊异性"和"神经殊异"这两个术语的卡西安·阿萨苏马苏便始终强调，她希望这些术语能被尽可能包容地解读——即，当她提到"任何与主流文化神经认知功能规范显著偏离的情况"时，她指的是任何显著的偏离。在我认识她并关注她著作的这些年里，卡西安从未说过"哦，等等，我指的只是那些被病理化的偏离形式"，或"哦，等等，当我说神经殊异人群是神经认知功能偏离主流规范的人时，我指的只是那些残障人士"。



Any significant divergence. That includes both innate forms of divergence (e.g., autism, dyslexia, aphantasia, Down Syndrome) and forms of divergence that can be acquired during the lifespan (e.g., the lasting neurocognitive effects of various sorts of trauma and/or extensive drug use).

任何显著的偏离。这既包括先天性的偏离形式（例如孤独症、阅读障碍、心盲症、唐氏综合征），也包括后天获得的偏离形式（例如各类创伤和/或长期药物使用对神经认知产生的持久影响）。



There are innate forms of neurodivergence that don’t involve any sort of disablement. Many forms of synesthesia, for example. While it’s possible to have levels of synesthesia so intense as to result in atypical access needs which require accommodation, the majority of people who experience synesthesia aren’t impaired by it in any significant way, and thus require no special accommodation for it, and thus aren’t disabled by the absence of such accommodation.

存在一些先天性的神经殊异性形式，并不涉及任何功能障碍。例如，多种形式的联觉。虽然有些人可能因联觉程度过强而产生非典型的无障碍需求，需要特殊便利措施，但大多数有联觉体验的人并未因此受到显著损害，因此无需为此提供特殊便利，也不会因缺乏此类便利而成为残障人士。



As for acquired forms of neurodivergence that don’t involve disablement, the wonders of human neuroplasticity make it possible for people to alter their neurocognitive functioning in all sorts of interesting ways, some of which are both long-lasting and clearly divergent from dominant norms. I know a number of people who’ve permanently altered their neurocognitive functioning through the use of psychedelic drugs, without becoming disabled (i.e., they’re still able to fully access, participate in, and thrive within the systems, structures, and institutions of the dominant culture).

至于后天获得且不涉及功能障碍的神经殊异性形式，人类神经可塑性的奇妙之处在于，人们能够以各种有趣的方式改变自身的神经认知功能，其中一些改变既持久又明显偏离主流规范。我认识一些人，他们通过使用迷幻药物永久性地改变了神经认知功能，却并未因此成为残障人士（即他们仍能充分接触、参与主流文化的系统、结构和机构，并在此中蓬勃发展）。



A few of the old friends I used to take LSD with, for instance, have reported that some of the visual effects of that marvelous drug never entirely went away for them; decades later, they still see trails and auras, and still find that every blank wall they look at morphs into a writhing tapestry of color. This hasn’t impaired them in any way or necessitated any accommodations, but it’s obviously not “normal” by the standards of conventional society. (I can’t say for sure whether my own youthful LSD use had any such lasting sensory effect, because trails and auras and writhing surfaces and other such visual embellishments have been part of my autistic sensory reality since I was born.)

例如，我曾一起服用 LSD 的几位老友报告说，那种神奇药物的某些视觉效果从未完全消失；几十年后，他们仍能看到拖影和光晕，每面空白的墙壁在他们眼中都会变幻成色彩翻涌的织锦。这并未对他们造成任何损害，也无需任何特殊安排，但显然不符合传统社会的"正常"标准。（我无法确定自己年轻时服用 LSD 是否留下了类似的持久感官影响，因为拖影、光晕、翻涌的表面以及其他这类视觉修饰，自出生起就是我孤独谱系感官现实的一部分。）



Another example would be the neurocognitive effects of long-term meditation practice. Neuroimaging studies on Buddhist monks have demonstrated that extensive engagement in meditation practices over a long period of time results not only in lasting alterations to consciousness and neurocognitive functioning, but also in significant and measurable changes to the thickness of the prefrontal cortex. So experienced Buddhist monks and other lifelong meditation practitioners come to diverge from neurotypical norms on a neurobiological level and certainly on a cognitive level (anyone who’s spent time with a zen master can tell you that they think very differently from just about anyone else). And yet, meditation clearly doesn’t lead to disablement; in fact, many long-term meditation practitioners, myself included, have found that meditation-induced neurodivergences can actually be quite helpful in navigating modern life and can even help to mitigate the challenges posed by some other forms of neurodivergence.

另一个例子是长期冥想练习对神经认知的影响。针对佛教僧侣的神经影像学研究表明，长期大量进行冥想练习不仅会导致意识和神经认知功能的持久改变，还会使前额叶皮层厚度发生显著且可测量的变化。因此，经验丰富的佛教僧侣和其他终身冥想修行者在神经生物学层面——当然也包括认知层面——会逐渐偏离神经典型性规范（任何与禅宗大师相处过的人都能告诉你，他们的思维方式与常人截然不同）。然而，冥想显然不会导致失能；事实上，包括我在内的许多长期冥想修行者发现，冥想引发的神经殊异性实际上有助于应对现代生活，甚至能缓解其他形式的神经殊异性所带来的挑战。



So please recognize that a great many neurodivergent people are disabled. Please learn to see how societal prejudices and failures of accommodation serve to create this disablement, and please look for ways in which you can help to challenge these prejudices and remedy these failures of accommodation. But also, please respect the inclusive intentions of the person who gave us the word neurodivergence; please don’t attempt to redefine the word in ways that exclude non-disabled neurodivergent people.

因此，请认识到大量神经殊异人士是残障者。请学会观察社会偏见与包容性缺失如何共同制造这种残障，并积极寻找途径帮助挑战这些偏见、弥补包容性缺失。但同时也请尊重赋予我们"神经殊异性"一词之人的包容初衷；请不要试图以排斥非残障神经殊异人士的方式重新定义这个词。







---


Nick_ebook-14










Reflections on

Neurocosmopolitanism

关于神经宇宙主义的思考



And let’s wrap up Part I of this book with one more new piece written in 2021...

让我们用一篇 2021 年创作的新作来为本书的第一部分画上句号……



I’ve been involved in the neurodiversity movement since it was just a ragtag scattering of scrappy autistic activists connecting with one another on early internet platforms, and I’ve been involved in laying the foundations of the field of Neurodiversity Studies since long before anyone was calling it a field. Through it all, a central aim of my work has been to help bring about a paradigm shift in how the prevailing culture understands and engages with human neurodiversity—a shift away from the currently-dominant pathology paradigm, toward what I’ve long referred to as the neurodiversity paradigm.

我参与神经多样性运动时，它不过是早期互联网平台上零星散落的孤独谱系活动家们相互联络的松散群体；而在"神经多样性研究"被正式称为一个学科领域之前很久，我就已投身于该领域的基础建设。贯穿始终，我工作的核心目标始终是推动主流文化在理解与应对人类神经多样性方面实现范式转变——从当前主导的病理学范式，转向我长期称之为"神经多样性范式"的新方向。



To create a better future, one must first be able to imagine a better future. Working to eliminate specific problems is often necessary but ultimately insufficient; it’s essential to also have some positive guiding vision of what one is working toward. When working to bring about transformation on any scale from the personal to the global, it’s vital to ask oneself what it might look like if one’s work were to someday succeed in the fullest possible way. Those of us engaged in the work of fostering a cultural shift from the pathology paradigm to the neurodiversity paradigm would thus do well to reflect upon two questions:

要创造更美好的未来，首先必须能够想象一个更美好的未来。致力于消除具体问题往往是必要的，但最终仍显不足；关键还在于要有一个积极的前瞻性愿景，明确自己努力的方向。当我们在从个人到全球的各个层面推动变革时，必须自问：如果我们的工作有朝一日能以最圆满的方式成功，那会是什么样子？因此，我们这些致力于推动文化从病理范式转向神经多样性范式的人，最好认真思考两个问题：




What sort of attitude or approach toward neurodiversity might one find in individuals who have truly comprehended, embraced, and integrated the neurodiversity paradigm?

真正理解、接纳并内化了神经多样性范式的个体，会对神经多样性持有什么样的态度或方式？



What sort of attitude or approach toward neurodiversity might one find in a society that has fully embraced and been transformed by the neurodiversity paradigm?

一个完全接纳神经多样性范式并因此发生转变的社会，会对神经多样性持有什么样的态度或方式？




My own answer, in both cases, is encapsulated in the term neurocosmopolitanism (a term coined by my fellow neurodiversity scholar Ralph Savarese and myself, independently of one another and more or less concurrently). An individual who has truly comprehended, embraced, and integrated the neurodiversity paradigm is likely to exhibit neurocosmopolitan attitudes, and a society that has fully embraced and been transformed by the neurodiversity paradigm would be a neurocosmopolitan society. So, what does that mean? What is neurocosmopolitanism?

我个人的答案，在两种情况下都浓缩在"神经世界主义"（neurocosmopolitanism）一词中（这个词由我和神经多样性学者拉尔夫·萨瓦雷斯各自独立提出，时间大致相同）。一个真正理解、接纳并内化了神经多样性范式的人，很可能展现出神经世界主义的态度；而一个完全接纳神经多样性范式并为之改变的社会，将是一个神经世界主义的社会。那么，这意味着什么？什么是神经世界主义？



Cosmopolitanism is the open-minded embracing of human diversity. The term is traditionally used in regard to the diversity of cultures, ethnicities, and nationalities; cosmopolite literally translates as citizen of the world. The cosmopolite regards all humanity as ultimately part of a single global community—an essential unity which is in no way invalidated by the differences among us, and which in fact has the potential to be greatly enriched by those differences when we engage with them in a spirit of humility, respect, and openness to learning.

世界主义是以开放心态拥抱人类多样性。这个词传统上用于指代文化、种族和国籍的多样性；"世界公民"的字面意思是"世界的公民"。世界主义者认为全人类最终都属于同一个全球共同体——这种本质上的统一性绝不会因我们之间的差异而失效，事实上，当我们以谦逊、尊重和开放学习的态度面对这些差异时，它们反而有可能极大地丰富这个共同体。



Neurocosmopolitanism consists of approaching neurodiversity in the same spirit in which the cosmopolite approaches cultural diversity. To embrace the neurodiversity paradigm is to refuse to pathologize neurocognitive styles and experiences that differ from our own, and to accept neurodiversity as a natural, healthy, and important form of human biodiversity—a fundamental and vital characteristic of the human species, a crucial source of evolutionary and creative potential. Neurocosmopolitanism goes beyond this baseline of acceptance, though, just as cosmopolitanism goes beyond mere tolerance of cultural differences. The neurocosmopolitan seeks to actively engage with and preserve human neurodiversity, and to honor, explore, and cultivate its creative potentials, in a spirit of humility, respect, and continual openness to learning and transformation.

神经世界主义是指以世界主义者对待文化多样性的同样精神来对待神经多样性。接受神经多样性范式意味着拒绝将不同于我们自身的神经认知风格和体验病理化，并承认神经多样性是人类生物多样性中一种自然、健康且重要的形式——它是人类物种的基本且至关重要的特征，是进化与创造潜力的关键源泉。然而，神经世界主义超越了这种基础的接纳，正如世界主义超越了单纯对文化差异的容忍。神经世界主义者寻求以谦逊、尊重以及持续开放学习与转变的精神，积极接触并保护人类的神经多样性，同时尊重、探索并培育其创造潜力。



Cosmopolitanism’s opposite is provincialism. In the context of the diversity of cultures and nationalities, provincialism boils down to viewing one’s own native culture and people as the default “normal” culture and people, and other cultures and peoples as exotic, inferior, threatening, inhuman, and/or just plain “wrong” to whatever extent they differ from one’s own. One might say, then, that the pathology paradigm, with its privileging of particular bodyminds and particular modes of cognition and behavior as “normal” and implicitly superior, is a form of neuroprovincialism.

世界主义的对立面是地方主义。在文化与民族多样性的语境下，地方主义本质上将自身所属的本土文化与族群视为默认的"正常"标准，而其他文化与族群只要与自身存在差异，就会被视为异域风情、低等、具有威胁性、非人性化，甚至纯粹是"错误的"。由此可以说，病理范式将特定身心状态、认知模式和行为方式奉为"正常"并暗含优越性，本质上就是一种神经地方主义。



A neurocosmopolitan perspective, by contrast, privileges no bodymind as the “natural” default way of being, nor as more “normal” or intrinsically correct than any other, just as a hallmark of cosmopolitanism is the recognition that no one culture is more intrinsically correct, natural, or “normal” than any other. The neurocosmopolite welcomes and appreciates the differences among bodyminds—all the manifold variations in perception, cognition, embodiment, experience, needs, and styles of communication and interaction—in the same open-minded and profoundly egalitarian spirit with which the true cosmopolite greets cultural differences.

相比之下，神经世界主义视角不将任何身心形态视为“天然”的默认存在方式，也不认为其比其它形态更“正常”或本质上更正确——正如世界主义的标志性特征在于承认没有哪种文化本质上比其它文化更正确、更自然或更“正常”。神经世界主义者以真正世界主义者对待文化差异时那种开放包容、彻底平等的精神，欢迎并欣赏不同身心形态之间的差异——包括感知、认知、具身化、体验、需求、沟通与互动风格等所有层面的多样性。



The development of a truly cosmopolitan spirit necessarily involves transcending racism, nationalism, and delusions of cultural supremacy. A racist cosmopolite would be a contradiction in terms, at least by any definition of cosmopolitanism I’d consider worthy of the name. And yet, while transcendence of these various ugly manifestations of provincialism is obviously a fundamental prerequisite for cosmopolitanism, their mere absence does not in itself constitute cosmopolitanism. There are various understandings of cosmopolitanism, but the versions of cosmopolitan thought toward which I lean go far beyond mere tolerance and acceptance of human diversity. In the forms of cosmopolitanism that serve as models for how I envision neurocosmopolitanism, the cosmopolite actively welcomes, celebrates, and engages with the differences among us as sources of learning, growth, and mutual aesthetic, intellectual, cultural, and creative enrichment.

真正世界主义精神的培育必然需要超越种族主义、民族主义和文化优越论的迷思。种族主义的世界主义者本身就是矛盾的表述——至少就我所认可的世界主义定义而言。然而，尽管超越这些狭隘主义的丑陋表现显然是世界主义的基本前提，但仅仅消除这些表现本身并不构成世界主义。人们对世界主义有着不同的理解，但我所倾向的世界主义思想版本远不止于对人类多样性的简单容忍与接纳。在我构想神经世界主义所参照的世界主义范式中，世界主义者会主动欢迎、颂扬并参与我们之间的差异，将其视为学习、成长以及彼此在审美、智识、文化和创造力上相互丰富的源泉。



The same can be said in regard to neurocosmopolitanism. The cultivation of a neurocosmopolitan attitude necessarily involves unlearning and transcending the neuroprovincialist mindset of the pathology paradigm—in other words, making the shift to the neurodiversity paradigm. This paradigm shift is as much an essential prerequisite for the emergence of neurocosmopolitanism as the unlearning of racism, nationalism, and cultural chauvinism are prerequisites for cosmopolitanism. To view the bodyminds of neurominority members through the lens of pathology—e.g., to frame autism and other minority modes of neurocognitive functioning as “conditions,” or to rank the functioning of human bodyminds as “high” or “low” based on the degree to which they conform to some particular set of cultural norms of performance—is fundamentally incompatible with the neurocosmopolitan spirit in the same way that the framing of certain ethnic groups as “superior” or “inferior” is incompatible with cosmopolitanism.

同样适用于神经世界主义。培养神经世界主义态度必然需要摒弃并超越病理学范式的神经地方主义思维——换言之，即转向神经多样性范式。这种范式转变是神经世界主义产生的必要前提，正如摒弃种族主义、民族主义和文化沙文主义是世界主义的前提条件。通过病理学视角看待神经少数群体的身心状态——例如将孤独症及其他少数神经认知功能模式定义为"病症"，或根据人类身心功能符合特定文化表现规范的程度将其划分为"高功能"或"低功能"——本质上与神经世界主义精神背道而驰，正如将某些族群定义为"优越"或"低劣"与世界主义精神相悖。



At the same time, the neurodiversity paradigm is by no means synonymous with neurocosmopolitanism. The shift from the pathology paradigm to the neurodiversity paradigm doesn’t lead inevitably to the emergence of full-blown neurocosmopolitanism, it’s just an essential first step. True neurocosmopolitanism goes further, as Ralph Savarese implied when he gave one of his essays on neurocosmopolitanism the subtitle “Beyond Mere Acceptance and Inclusion.” True neurocosmopolitanism, like true cosmopolitanism, extends beyond the mere acceptance and accommodation of the differences among us, to an active embracing of and engagement with those differences as potential sources of growth, enrichment, and creative synergy.

与此同时，神经多样性范式绝不等于神经世界主义。从病理范式转向神经多样性范式并不会必然催生成熟的神经世界主义，这只是必要的第一步。真正的神经世界主义走得更远，正如拉尔夫·萨瓦雷塞在为其神经世界主义论文所加副标题"超越单纯的接纳与包容"中所暗示的那样。真正的神经世界主义如同真正的世界主义，不仅止于接纳和包容我们之间的差异，更要主动拥抱并参与这些差异，将其视为成长、丰富与创造性协同的潜在源泉。



The mere presence of neurodivergent individuals cannot serve on its own to augment the creative power of a group or organization or society, if having a real voice within that group or society is contingent upon acting neurotypical and upon only making the sort of social contributions that don’t trouble the collective trance of neuronormativity. The true creative potentials of neurodiversity can be realized, within any given environment, only to the extent that people are empowered to participate in the ongoing collective co-creation and shaping of that environment while openly acting in ways that violate the constraints of neuronormative performance.

仅凭神经殊异个体的存在，并不能自动增强某个群体、组织或社会的创造力——如果在该群体或社会中拥有真正的话语权，必须以表现神经典型行为为前提，且只能做出那些不扰乱神经规范集体迷思的社会贡献。神经多样性的真正创造潜能，在任何特定环境中都只能通过以下方式实现：人们被赋予权力，能够以公开违反神经规范表演约束的方式行事，并持续参与该环境的集体共创与塑造。



Although we live in a world in which the prevailing attitudes toward cultural, ethnic, and national differences are often far from cosmopolitan, individual cosmopolites nonetheless abound. By the same token, any individual who’s learned to see beyond the narrow distorting lens of the pathology paradigm can cultivate a neurocosmopolitan approach to life.

尽管我们生活的世界对文化、种族和民族差异的主流态度往往远非世界主义，但个体层面的世界主义者依然比比皆是。同理，任何学会超越病理范式狭隘扭曲视角的人，都能培养出面向生活的神经世界主义态度。



My hope is that some readers will be inspired not only to begin generating their own visions of a neurocosmopolitan future, but also to share and discuss those emerging visions in a variety of contexts—and thus to inspire others toward their own neurocosmopolitan futurist imaginings and toward participation in further dialogues about those imaginings, so that collective and collaborative visions of possible neurocosmopolitan futures can eventually emerge to provide a greater sense of direction for the work of the neurodiversity movement and the field of Neurodiversity Studies.

我希望，一些读者不仅能受到启发，开始构想自己心中的神经多元未来图景，还能在各种场合分享和讨论这些正在形成的愿景——从而激励他人展开自己的神经多元未来主义想象，并参与关于这些想象的进一步对话。这样，关于可能的神经多元未来的集体协作愿景终将浮现，为神经多样性运动及神经多样性研究领域的工作提供更明确的方向。



I’ve found the thought experiment of imagining a neurocosmopolitan future to be both consistently productive and inspiring, and consistently challenging. Challenging, because the pathology paradigm is so deeply and pervasively ingrained in present-day society that it currently shapes even the neurodiversity movement itself, along with most neurodiversity scholarship. Having emerged in opposition to the abuse, stigmatization, and marginalization of neurominorities that are the inevitable consequences of the pathology paradigm, the neurodiversity movement—and much of the existing neurodiversity scholarship so far—has been largely defined by that quite necessary opposition. Part of the challenge of imagining a truly neurocosmopolitan future is that it means imagining not merely a future in which the neurodiversity movement has made substantial progress in its goals, but a future in which those goals may have been so well achieved as to render the movement obsolete.

我发现，想象一个神经世界主义未来的思想实验既始终富有成效、鼓舞人心，又始终充满挑战。之所以充满挑战，是因为病理学范式在当今社会中根深蒂固、无处不在，以至于它目前甚至塑造了神经多样性运动本身，以及大多数神经多样性学术研究。神经多样性运动——以及迄今为止的大部分神经多样性学术研究——是在反对病理学范式所必然导致的神经少数群体遭受虐待、污名化和边缘化的过程中兴起的，因此很大程度上是由这种必要的对立所定义的。想象一个真正神经世界主义未来的挑战之一在于，这意味着不仅要想象一个神经多样性运动在其目标上取得重大进展的未来，还要想象一个这些目标可能已充分实现，以至于该运动变得过时的未来。



I offer the following questions to spark reflection and imagination. This short list of questions is obviously far from comprehensive; I mean them as “sample questions,” intended not only to inspire thoughts about possible neurocosmopolitan futures but also to inspire the formulation of further questions along similar lines:

我提出以下问题，旨在激发反思与想象。这份简短的问题清单显然远非全面；我将其视为“示例问题”，不仅意在启发对神经多元共融未来的思考，也旨在激发沿着类似思路提出更多问题：



What might education look like in a system in which the acceptance, inclusion, and accommodation of every sort of bodymind represents an unquestioned baseline? What if “acceptance and inclusion” didn’t mean neurodivergent students being accepted and included under neurotypical supervision within educational environments created by and for neurotypicals, but instead meant a system which has itself been shaped through the collaboration of a wide diversity of minds—a system sufficiently neurocosmopolitan as to place all students on equal footing and render the concepts of “typical” and “divergent” effectively irrelevant? What might classroom education look like at various levels from preschool through grad school, in the context of a neurocosmopolitan approach to education in which it’s built into the curriculum that every person in the class, teachers and students alike, works at learning to comprehend and accommodate the neurocognitive styles and communication needs of every other person in the class as best they can? What if both the education of youth and adults, and the training of educators, included the explicit understanding that no neurocognitive style is more “correct” or “normal” than any other, and that the work of mutual accommodation is both an essential part of a proper education and an essential preparation for being a participating citizen in a civilized society?

在一个将各种身心形态的接纳、包容与适配视为不容置疑的基准的体系中，教育会呈现何种面貌？倘若"接纳与包容"并非指神经殊异的学生在神经典型人士的监管下，被纳入由神经典型者创造并服务于神经典型者的教育环境，而是指一个由多元心智协作塑造的体系——一个具备充分神经世界主义特质、能让所有学生处于平等地位、并使"典型"与"殊异"概念实质上失去意义的体系，那又会怎样？从学前到研究生院的各级课堂教育，在神经世界主义教育理念的语境下——即课程本身已内建这样的机制：课堂中的每个人，无论师生，都致力于学习理解并尽可能适配其他每个人的神经认知风格与沟通需求——又会呈现出何种面貌？ 如果对青少年和成人的教育，以及对教育工作者的培训，都明确包含这样一种理解：没有任何一种神经认知风格比另一种更“正确”或“正常”，而相互适应的过程既是恰当教育的重要组成部分，也是成为文明社会中参与型公民的必要准备，那会怎样？



What might the results be if it were standard practice for organizations to actively seek to cultivate neurodiversity within their ranks at every level, including the highest levels of leadership and policy-making? What might organizations and social institutions look like, if conformity to some particular set of neurocognitive norms was not in any way—officially or unofficially—an advantage in attaining entry, employment, inclusion, advancement, or positions of leadership? What if cultivation of neurodiversity within organizational ranks didn’t consist merely of neurodivergent individuals being brought into neurotypical-run organizational environments under neurotypical supervision, but instead occurred in the context of neurocosmopolitan organizational environments in which the systems, structures, and policies were created collaboratively under the leadership of a wide diversity of minds—with no one sort of mind privileged over others or considered the default norm?

如果各类组织积极在各个层级（包括最高领导层和政策制定层）培养神经多样性成为标准实践，结果会如何？如果遵循某种特定的神经认知规范——无论正式或非正式——不再成为进入、受雇、融入、晋升或担任领导职位的优势，组织和社会机构又会呈现何种面貌？如果组织内部培养神经多样性，并非仅仅是将神经殊异个体带入由神经典型人士主导、受其监管的环境，而是在神经多元共融的组织环境中进行——在这种环境中，系统、结构和政策由多元思维在广泛协作下共同制定，没有任何一种思维模式被赋予特权或被视为默认标准——那又会怎样？



Cosmopolitanism has historically functioned as a source of cultural enrichment and creative innovation by creating opportunities for the process of mutual adaptation and transformative fusion known as hybridization. When cross-cultural interactions are navigated with in a cosmopolitan spirit, rather than with provincial prejudices or colonialist agendas of domination, it fosters mutually beneficial cultural exchanges and the creative hybridizations and synergies which have in myriad ways shaped music, art, language, literature, spirituality, philosophy, aesthetics, science, and technology throughout history and into the present day. How much more of what the philosopher Edgar Morin calls “the genius of diversity” might be awakened in a society that was not only truly cosmopolitan in its engagement with cultural diversity, but also truly neurocosmopolitan in its engagement with neurodiversity? What new confluences, creative hybridizations, and transformative synergies might emerge, on every scale in every realm of society and culture, and what might the results look like?

世界主义在历史上一直是文化丰富和创造性创新的源泉，它为被称为“杂交化”的相互适应与变革性融合过程创造了机会。当跨文化互动以世界主义精神进行，而非带有地方偏见或殖民主义的支配议程时，它促进了互利的文化交流，以及创造性的杂交与协同效应——这些效应以无数方式塑造了音乐、艺术、语言、文学、精神性、哲学、美学、科学和技术，贯穿历史直至今日。在一个不仅真正以世界主义精神参与文化多样性，而且真正以神经世界主义精神参与神经多样性的社会中，哲学家埃德加·莫兰所称的“多样性的天才”还能被唤醒多少？在社会和文化的各个领域、各个层面，可能会出现哪些新的融合、创造性的杂交和变革性的协同效应，其结果又会是什么样子？



We’re a long ways from a neurocosmopolitan society, but it’s a goal worth working toward and a vision that serves to guide and inspire much of my work. Perhaps it will guide and inspire you as well. And while we work toward this perhaps distant goal, each one of us can cultivate the neurocosmopolitan spirit in our own minds and in our own lives, right here and right now.

我们距离一个神经多元共融的社会还很遥远，但这是一个值得为之奋斗的目标，也是指引并激励我大部分工作的愿景。或许它也能指引并激励你。在朝着这个或许遥远的目标努力的同时，我们每个人都可以在此刻、在此地，在自己的思想和生活中培育神经多元共融的精神。







---


Nick_ebook-15










PART II:

AUTISTIC EMPOWERMENT

第二部分：孤独谱系赋权



“Our essential task in life is to awaken to the way that the eternal would speak through us, to learn to live out our intended personality and the inner weirdness that makes us a unique torchbearer of the flame of life.”

“我们在生命中的根本任务，是觉醒于永恒之道如何通过我们言说，学会活出我们被赋予的独特人格，以及那份使我们成为生命火焰独特火炬手的内在奇异。”



Michael Meade

迈克尔·米德







---


Nick_ebook-16










The Story Behind

“What Is Autism?”

《“什么是孤独症？”背后的故事》



From 2012 to 2018, I worked with the Multidisciplinary Association for Psychedelic Studies (MAPS) as a consultant on a groundbreaking research study which we eventually published in the journal Psychopharmacology (vol. 235, no. 11, June 2018) under the accurate but cumbersome title “Reduction in Social Anxiety After MDMA-Assisted Psychotherapy with Autistic Adults: A Randomized, Double-Blind, Placebo-Controlled Pilot Study.”

2012 年至 2018 年间，我与多学科迷幻研究协会（MAPS）合作，担任一项开创性研究的顾问。这项研究最终于 2018 年 6 月发表在《精神药理学》期刊（第 235 卷，第 11 期）上，标题准确却略显冗长：“MDMA 辅助心理治疗对成年孤独谱系个体社交焦虑的缓解效果：一项随机、双盲、安慰剂对照的初步研究”。



This was the first formal psychopharmacological study of autistic subjects to be grounded in the neurodiversity paradigm rather than the pathology paradigm. There was nothing in the study that pathologized autistic people for being autistic, or that framed autism as inferior to neurotypicality. It wasn’t in any way about “treating autism” (a concept as innately oppressive as the concept of “treating homosexuality”). It was about treating social anxiety in consenting adult autistics who wanted to stop experiencing social anxiety.

这是首个基于神经多样性范式而非病理学范式对孤独谱系受试者进行的正式精神药理学研究。该研究既未将孤独谱系群体因自身特质而病理化，也未将孤独谱系视为低于神经典型状态的缺陷。它绝非关于“治疗孤独症”（这一概念与“治疗同性恋”同样具有本质上的压迫性），而是关于帮助那些希望摆脱社交焦虑的、自愿参与的成年孤独谱系个体缓解社交焦虑。



We did the whole study and subsequent journal article without using the language of the pathology paradigm. Where researchers mired in the pathology paradigm might have framed social anxiety as a “symptom” of autism or a “comorbid condition” (thus implicitly framing autism as a pathological “condition”), we explicitly acknowledged that social anxiety in the autistic population was a symptom of the extensive social trauma neurotypical society inflicts upon autistics from childhood—in other words, that what we sought to treat was a symptom not of autism but of traumatic oppression.

我们完成了整个研究及后续的期刊文章，全程未使用病理范式的语言。当深陷病理范式的研究者可能将社交焦虑描述为孤独谱系的“症状”或“共病状况”（从而隐含地将孤独谱系视为一种病态的“状况”）时，我们明确承认孤独谱系人群中的社交焦虑，是神经典型社会从童年起对孤独谱系者施加的广泛社会创伤的症状——换言之，我们寻求治疗的不是孤独谱系的症状，而是创伤性压迫的症状。



My friend and colleague Alicia Danforth, one of the lead researchers on the study, did a brief interview with me about it via email for the Spring 2014 issue of the MAPS Bulletin. The study was still in the proposal stage at that time, and the MAPS audience on the whole wasn’t any more knowledgeable about autism than the rest of the general public, so the idea behind the interview was to help this audience understand the important distinction between “treating autism” (ugh) and treating a trauma-related anxiety issue for which a significant number of autistic folks wanted an effective treatment.

我的朋友兼同事艾丽西亚·丹福思是该研究的主要研究者之一，她通过电子邮件就此事对我进行了一次简短采访，发表于 2014 年春季的《MAPS 公报》。当时该研究仍处于提案阶段，而《MAPS》的读者群体整体上对孤独谱系的了解并不比普通公众更多，因此这次采访的初衷是帮助读者理解“治疗孤独谱系”（唉）与治疗创伤相关焦虑问题之间的重要区别——后者正是许多孤独谱系人士迫切希望获得有效治疗的领域。



Alicia’s first question to me in the interview was “What is your definition of autism?” When I’d typed out my response, I realized I’d created something which up until that point hadn’t existed and was badly needed: a clear, concise, accessible explanation of autism which was based in the neurodiversity paradigm rather than the pathology paradigm. In March of 2014, weeks before that interview appeared in the MAPS Bulletin, I published my explanation of autism on my website under the title “What Is Autism?” I included this introduction:

艾丽西亚在采访中问我的第一个问题是：“你如何定义孤独症？”当我打出回答时，我意识到自己创造了一个此前不存在且极为需要的东西：一个基于神经多样性范式而非病理学范式、清晰、简洁且易于理解的孤独症解释。2014 年 3 月，就在那篇采访刊登于《MAPS 公报》的几周前，我在个人网站上以“什么是孤独症？”为题发布了这份解释。我附上了这样的引言：



How many websites are there that have a page called something like “What Is Autism?” or “About Autism”? How often do organizations, professionals, scholars, and others need to include a few paragraphs of basic introductory “What Is Autism?” text in a website, brochure, presentation, or academic paper?

有多少网站设有名为“什么是孤独症？”或“关于孤独症”的页面？又有多少组织、专业人士、学者及其他人在网站、宣传册、演示文稿或学术论文中需要包含几段基础性的“什么是孤独症？”介绍文字？



I’ve seen so many versions of that obligatory “What Is Autism” or “About Autism” text. And they’re almost all terrible. For starters, almost all of them—even the versions written by people who claim to be in favor of “autism acceptance” or to support the neurodiversity paradigm—use the language of the pathology paradigm, which intrinsically contributes to the oppression of autistics.

我见过太多那种千篇一律的“什么是孤独症”或“关于孤独症”的文本。它们几乎都糟糕透顶。首先，几乎所有这类文本——即便是那些声称支持“孤独症接纳”或拥护神经多样性范式的人所写的版本——都使用了病理范式的语言，这本质上加剧了对孤独症群体的压迫。



On top of that, most of these descriptions of autism – even many of the descriptions written by autistics – propagate inaccurate information and false stereotypes. Some are so bad that they actually quote the DSM.

更糟糕的是，大多数关于孤独症的描述——甚至包括许多孤独症人士自己写的描述——都在传播不准确的信息和虚假的刻板印象。有些文本糟糕到直接引用《精神障碍诊断与统计手册》（DSM）的程度。



Of course, there are also a few really good pieces of “What Is Autism” text out there. But for the most part, they’re rather personal pieces, about the authors’ own unique experiences of autism, rather than general introductory definitions. What is needed is some good basic introductory “What Is Autism” text that is:

当然，市面上确实也有少数几篇优秀的“什么是孤独症”文本。但总体而言，它们更像是个人化的随笔，描述作者自身独特的孤独症体验，而非通用的入门定义。我们真正需要的是这样一篇基础性的“什么是孤独症”入门文本：




consistent with current evidence;

符合当前科学证据；



not based in the pathology paradigm;

不基于病理学范式；



concise, simple, and accessible;

简洁、简单且易于理解；



formal enough for professional and academic use.

足够正式，适用于专业和学术用途。




Since I couldn’t find such a piece of text elsewhere, I wrote one. And here it is. I hereby give everyone permission to reprint the text below, in whole or in part, whenever you need a piece of basic “What Is Autism” or “About Autism” text. Please do credit me for writing it. But really, as long as credit is given, anyone can go ahead and use this text for free.

由于我在别处找不到这样的文本，于是自己写了一篇。这就是它。我在此授权所有人，在需要一段基础的“什么是孤独症”或“关于孤独谱系”的文本时，可以自由转载以下全文或部分内容。请注明我的作者身份。但真的，只要注明出处，任何人都可以免费使用这段文字。



A lot of folks have taken me up on that invitation. Where “Neurodiversity: Some Basic Terms & Definitions” is the piece of my writing that’s been most widely cited in other people’s writing so far, “What Is Autism?” is the piece that’s been most widely reprinted, quoted, adapted, and translated. As of this writing in 2021, there are translations of “What Is Autism?” available online in Spanish, Portuguese, Russian, German, Swedish, Czech, Slovene, and Estonian.

很多人响应了我的邀请。在《神经多样性：基本术语与定义》是我被他人引用最广泛的作品之后，《什么是孤独谱系？》则是我被转载、引用、改编和翻译最多的文章。截至 2021 年撰写本文时，《什么是孤独谱系？》已有西班牙语、葡萄牙语、俄语、德语、瑞典语、捷克语、斯洛文尼亚语和爱沙尼亚语的在线译本。



The MAPS study was a great success, by the way. Our study participants did indeed show statistically significant long-term reductions in social anxiety symptoms in the wake of their MDMA-assisted psychotherapy sessions. We also showed that it was possible to get federal approval for a research study with autistic participants (one currently needs approval from both the FDA and the DEA to use a controlled substance like MDMA in a research study), and possible to subsequently get the results of that study published in a prestigious scientific journal, without once disrespecting the autistic participants by using the language of the pathology paradigm.

顺便一提，MAPS 研究取得了巨大成功。我们的研究参与者在接受 MDMA 辅助心理治疗后，社交焦虑症状确实在统计学上显示出长期显著改善。我们还证明，获得联邦批准开展涉及孤独谱系参与者的研究（目前使用 MDMA 等管制物质进行研究需同时获得 FDA 和 DEA 批准），并随后将研究成果发表在权威科学期刊上是可行的——全程无需使用病理范式的语言来贬低孤独谱系参与者。







---


Nick_ebook-17










What Is Autism?

什么是孤独谱系？



Autism is a genetically-based human neurological variant. The complex set of interrelated characteristics that distinguish autistic neurology from non-autistic neurology is not yet fully understood, but current evidence indicates that the central distinction is that autistic brains are characterized by particularly high levels of synaptic connectivity and responsiveness. This tends to make the autistic individual’s subjective experience more intense and chaotic than that of non-autistic individuals: on both the sensorimotor and cognitive levels, the autistic mind tends to register more information, and the impact of each bit of information tends to be both stronger and less predictable.

孤独谱系是一种基于基因的人类神经学变异。目前尚未完全理解区分孤独谱系神经学与非孤独谱系神经学的那一系列复杂且相互关联的特征，但现有证据表明，核心区别在于孤独谱系大脑以特别高的突触连接性和反应性为特征。这往往使得孤独谱系个体的主观体验比非孤独谱系个体更强烈、更混乱：在感觉运动与认知层面，孤独谱系思维倾向于记录更多信息，且每条信息的影响往往既更强又更不可预测。



Autism is a developmental phenomenon, meaning that it begins in utero and has a pervasive influence on development, on multiple levels, throughout the lifespan. Autism produces distinctive, atypical ways of thinking, moving, interaction, and sensory and cognitive processing. One analogy that has often been made is that autistic individuals have a different neurological “operating system” than non-autistic individuals.

孤独谱系是一种发展性现象，意味着它始于子宫内，并在整个生命周期中对多个层面的发展产生普遍影响。孤独谱系会产生独特、非典型的思维、运动、互动以及感官与认知处理方式。一个常被引用的类比是：孤独谱系个体拥有与非孤独谱系个体不同的神经学“操作系统”。



According to current estimates, somewhere between one percent and two percent of the world’s population is autistic. While the number of individuals diagnosed as autistic has increased continually over the past few decades, evidence suggests that this increase in diagnosis is the result of increased public and professional awareness, rather than an actual increase in the prevalence of autism.

根据目前的估计，全球约有百分之一到百分之二的人口属于孤独谱系。尽管过去几十年中被诊断为孤独症的人数持续增加，但证据表明，这一诊断数量的增长源于公众和专业认知的提升，而非孤独症实际患病率的上升。



Despite underlying neurological commonalities, autistic individuals are vastly different from one another. Some autistic individuals exhibit exceptional cognitive talents.
