However, in the context of a society designed around the sensory, cognitive, developmental, and social needs of non-autistic individuals, autistic individuals are almost always disabled to some degree—sometimes quite obviously, and sometimes more subtly.

尽管存在共同的神经学基础，但孤独谱系个体之间差异巨大。部分孤独谱系者展现出非凡的认知天赋。然而，在一个围绕非孤独谱系者的感官、认知、发展及社交需求而设计的社会中，孤独谱系者几乎总会面临不同程度的障碍——有时表现明显，有时则更为隐蔽。



The realm of social interaction is one context in which autistic individuals tend to consistently be disabled. An autistic child’s sensory experience of the world is more intense and chaotic than that of a non-autistic child, and the ongoing task of navigating and integrating that experience thus occupies more of the autistic child’s attention and energy. This means the autistic child has less attention and energy available to focus on the subtleties of social interaction. Difficulty meeting the social expectations of non-autistics often results in social rejection, which further compounds social difficulties and impedes social development. For this reason, autism has been frequently misconstrued as being essentially a set of “social and communication deficits,” by those who are unaware that the social challenges faced by autistic individuals are just by-products of the intense and chaotic nature of autistic sensory and cognitive experience.

社交互动领域是孤独谱系个体常常面临障碍的一个情境。孤独谱系儿童对世界的感官体验比非孤独谱系儿童更强烈、更混乱，因此处理并整合这些体验的持续任务占据了他们更多的注意力和精力。这意味着孤独谱系儿童用于关注社交互动微妙之处的注意力和精力更少。难以满足非孤独谱系者的社交期望往往导致社交排斥，这进一步加剧了社交困难并阻碍了社交发展。正因如此，孤独谱系常被不了解情况的人误解为本质上是一组"社交与沟通缺陷"，而他们并未意识到孤独谱系个体面临的社交挑战，仅仅是其强烈而混乱的感官与认知体验的副产品。



Autism is still widely regarded as a “disorder,” but this view has been challenged in recent years by proponents of the neurodiversity model, which holds that autism and other neurocognitive variants are simply part of the natural spectrum of human biodiversity, like variations in ethnicity or sexual orientation (which have also been pathologized in the past). Ultimately, to describe autism as a disorder represents a value judgment rather than a scientific fact.

孤独症仍被广泛视为一种“障碍”，但近年来这一观点已受到神经多样性模型支持者的挑战。该模型认为，孤独谱系及其他神经认知变异只是人类生物多样性自然光谱的一部分，如同种族或性取向的差异（这些差异在过去也曾被病理化）。归根结底，将孤独症描述为一种障碍是一种价值判断，而非科学事实。







---


Nick_ebook-18










Autism and Social Trauma

孤独症与社会创伤



As previously noted, my “What Is Autism?” piece was originally written as an answer to a question in Alicia Danforth’s interview with me for the MAPS Bulletin in 2014. Later on in that same interview, in answer to a question about the rationale behind studying ways to treat social anxiety in the autistic population, I shared a few thoughts that I figure might be worth sharing again here...

如前所述，我的《什么是孤独症？》一文最初是为 2014 年《MAPS 公报》中艾丽西亚·丹福思对我的采访所写的回答。在那次采访的后续部分，当被问及研究孤独谱系群体社交焦虑治疗方法的理论依据时，我分享了一些想法——这些想法或许值得在此再次提及……



Many autistics suffer from some degree of social anxiety—a fear and anxiety response around social interaction. The crucial thing to understand is that social anxiety is not intrinsic to autism. Intense and atypical sensory experiences, and atypical styles of physical movement, are innate to autistic neurocognitive processing; if one is autistic, such experiences are going to be part of one’s reality to some degree. But that’s not necessarily the case with social anxiety.

许多孤独谱系个体都遭受着不同程度的社交焦虑——一种围绕社交互动产生的恐惧与焦虑反应。关键在于要理解：社交焦虑并非孤独谱系的内在特质。强烈而非典型的感官体验，以及非典型的身体运动方式，是孤独谱系神经认知处理过程所固有的；如果一个人属于孤独谱系，这类体验在某种程度上必然是其现实的一部分。但社交焦虑却未必如此。



To non-autistics, autistic people almost always come across as socially “odd” in some way—sometimes very much so. Indeed, as already noted, it’s become a widespread error in the field of psychology to misconstrue autism as being primarily a set of “social and communication deficits.”

对于非孤独谱系人群而言，孤独谱系个体几乎总会以某种方式显得社交上“古怪”——有时甚至非常明显。事实上，如前所述，心理学领域已普遍存在一个错误认知，即将孤独谱系曲解为主要表现为一系列“社交与沟通缺陷”。



A more accurate and less biased way of looking at it is that the communication difficulties between autistics and non-autistics run both ways: autistics have trouble understanding and communicating with non-autistics, and non-autistics have trouble understanding and communicating with autistics. This makes perfect sense: of course it’s challenging to understand someone whose mind works very differently from one’s own.

更准确且更少偏见的看法是，孤独谱系者与非孤独谱系者之间的沟通困难是双向的：孤独谱系者难以理解与非孤独谱系者交流，而非孤独谱系者也难以理解与孤独谱系者沟通。这完全合理：当然，理解一个思维方式与自己截然不同的人会充满挑战。



But because autistics are very much in the minority and hold less power in society, communication difficulties between an autistic and a non-autistic are always attributed to a deficit on the part of an autistic person. One rarely hears it pointed out that a non-autistic person suffers from an impaired ability to understand autistics. As the political scientist Karl Deutsch once noted, power is “the ability not to have to learn.”

但由于孤独谱系者属于少数群体，在社会中权力较小，孤独谱系者与非孤独谱系者之间的沟通困难，总是被归咎于孤独谱系者自身的缺陷。很少有人会指出，非孤独谱系者同样存在理解孤独谱系者的能力缺陷。正如政治学家卡尔·多伊奇曾指出的那样，权力就是“不必学习的能力”。



The upshot of all this is that the vast majority of autistic people experience frequent social rejection and hostility, beginning in very early childhood. Most autistics today constantly receive the message—again, starting in very early childhood—that the ways they naturally think, feel, move, and communicate are all wrong; that who they are is wrong.

这一切的最终结果是，绝大多数孤独谱系群体从幼年时期起就频繁经历社交排斥与敌意。如今大多数孤独谱系人士自童年早期便不断接收到这样的信息——他们与生俱来的思考、感受、行动和沟通方式都是错误的；他们本身的存在就是错误的。



This constant social rejection is deeply painful and traumatic. When such experiences are the norm in a person’s vulnerable formative years, of course that person is going to come to see social interaction as a venture into a minefield, a miserable and frightening experience likely to erupt without warning into yet another experience of pain, failure, and humiliation. Unfortunately, this often becomes a self-fulfilling prophecy, since no one is at their best socially when they’re experiencing overwhelming fear and anxiety. So the early history of social rejection causes social anxiety, which impairs social performance, resulting in further negative social experiences that reinforce the trauma.

这种持续性的社交排斥带来深重的痛苦与创伤。当这些经历成为一个人脆弱成长期的常态时，他自然会将社交互动视为踏入雷区的冒险——一种充满痛苦、失败与羞辱的可怕体验，随时可能毫无预兆地爆发。不幸的是，这往往演变为自我实现的预言：当人处于极度恐惧与焦虑时，根本无法展现最佳社交状态。于是早期社交排斥史催生社交焦虑，进而损害社交表现，导致更多负面社交体验，最终形成创伤的恶性循环。



Therein lies the key point, and the cause for hope and optimism: the social anxiety that afflicts so many autistics isn’t inherent to autism—it is, instead, a symptom of trauma. And trauma can be healed.

关键点及希望与乐观的根源在于：困扰众多孤独谱系人士的社交焦虑并非孤独谱系本身所固有，而是创伤的症状。而创伤是可以被治愈的。







---


Nick_ebook-19










Person-First Language Is the

Language of Autistiphobic Bigots

人先语言是孤独症恐惧偏执者的语言



This piece is a new one, written in 2021. A number of autistic authors have written critiques of person-first language in the past, beginning with Jim Sinclair’s “Why I Dislike Person First Language” in 1999. While these previous critiques have articulated excellent points with which I’m largely in agreement, I haven’t been entirely satisfied with them; I’ve yet to encounter one that offers sufficient critical analysis of the purposes and rationales behind person-first language. So I wrote my own, and here it is.

本文写于 2021 年，是一篇新作。过去已有不少孤独谱系作者对人先语言提出批评，最早可追溯至吉姆·辛克莱 1999 年发表的《为何我反感人先语言》。尽管这些批评文章提出了许多精辟观点，我大体上也表示赞同，但始终觉得不够尽善尽美——我尚未读到一篇能对人先语言背后的目的与逻辑进行充分批判性分析的文章。于是，我决定亲自撰写一篇，便是此文。



If you have even the slightest familiarity with the societal discourse on autism—whether you’ve learned about autism in an academic or professional setting, or just been exposed to discussions about it in the mass media—you’ve almost certainly encountered person-first language. That’s where instead of simply referring to autistic people as autistic people, folks use grotesque and needlessly cumbersome phrases like people with autism, children who have autism, individuals experiencing autism, or adults living with autism.

但凡你对孤独症的社会讨论稍有了解——无论你是在学术或专业场合学习过孤独症知识，还是仅通过大众媒体接触过相关讨论——你几乎必定遇到过人先语言。这种语言不会直接称孤独谱系群体为孤独谱系群体，而是使用诸如"患有孤独症的人"、"有孤独症的儿童"、"经历孤独症的个体"或"与孤独症共存的成年人"这类怪异且累赘的表述。



Person-first language is rooted in autistiphobia and anti-autistic bigotry, and its use is widely recognized by most of the autistic community as being a reliable indicator of autistiphobic attitudes. The reason that person-first language is so prevalent in our society’s discourses on autism is that those discourses have always been dominated by the voices and viewpoints of autistiphobic bigots. From the 1930s through the present day, the vast majority of the non-autistic people who’ve written about autism or done any sort of autism-related work have held deeply ingrained autistiphobic attitudes. The language used in their work reflects those attitudes.

以人为先的语言根植于孤独恐惧症和反孤独谱系的偏见，其使用已被大多数孤独谱系群体广泛视为孤独恐惧症态度的可靠指标。这种语言在我们的社会关于孤独症的讨论中如此普遍，原因在于这些讨论历来被孤独恐惧症偏见者的声音和观点所主导。从 20 世纪 30 年代至今，绝大多数撰写关于孤独症或从事任何与孤独症相关工作的非孤独谱系人士，都持有根深蒂固的孤独恐惧症态度。他们作品中所使用的语言反映了这些态度。



The use of person-first language when talking about autistic people is so prevalent and so widely accepted that most non-autistic folks don’t think twice about it and don’t even recognize it as the language of bigotry and stigma. The autistiphobic bigotry inherent in person-first language doesn’t become obvious until you listen to how it sounds when you use that same sort of language to talk about members of other historically oppressed and marginalized groups.

在谈论孤独谱系群体时使用以人为先的语言如此普遍且被广泛接受，以至于大多数非孤独谱系人士对此不假思索，甚至未能认识到这是偏见与污名化的语言。以人为先的语言中固有的孤独恐惧症偏见，只有当你用同样的语言谈论其他历史上受压迫和边缘化的群体成员时，才会变得显而易见。



Here, give it a try: People with homosexuality? Children who have Jewishness? Adults experiencing femaleness? Ooh, how about individuals living with Blackness? Are you comfortable with those phrases? If you read an article in which the author consistently referred to gay people as people with homosexuality, adults who have homosexuality, and individuals living with homosexuality, what would be your impression of that author’s attitude toward being gay?

来试试看：有同性恋倾向的人？有犹太特质的儿童？经历女性特质的成年人？哦，那"生活在黑人性中的人"呢？你对这些说法感到自在吗？如果你读到一篇文章，作者始终将同性恋者称为"有同性恋倾向的人"、"拥有同性恋特质的成年人"和"生活在同性恋性中的人"，你会对作者对待同性恋的态度产生什么印象？



•



There are only two kinds of people who use person-first language when talking about autistics:

在谈论孤独谱系人士时，只有两种人会使用"人先语言"：




Autistiphobic bigots. In other words, people who believe that there’s something wrong with being autistic—that being autistic is in some way a bad thing or a shameful thing.

孤独症恐惧偏执者。换句话说，就是那些认为成为孤独谱系人士本身有问题的人——认为孤独谱系在某种程度上是坏事或可耻的事。



People who don’t know any better. In other words, people who picked up the habit of using person-first language because it’s so ubiquitous in the discourse on autism (thanks to the influence of autistiphobic bigots), and who’ve just never really thought enough about the implications of person-first language to recognize its intrinsically autistiphobic nature.

不明就里的人。换句话说，就是那些养成使用"人先语言"习惯的人——因为这种说法在关于孤独谱系的讨论中太普遍了（受孤独症恐惧偏执者的影响），而他们从未真正深入思考过"人先语言"的隐含意义，未能认识到其本质上的孤独症恐惧偏见。




It’s generally a waste of time to argue with bigots, whether it’s about autistiphobic language or any other issue, because bigots don’t argue in good faith. Since they’re driven by fear and hatred of difference rather than by reason, they’ll just double down and keep repeating the same spurious arguments—or resort to personal attacks, condescension, tone policing, or whatever other derailing tactic they can come up with—rather than acknowledge a valid counterargument.

与偏执者争论通常是浪费时间，无论是关于仇视自闭症的语言还是其他问题，因为偏执者并非出于善意进行辩论。他们被对差异的恐惧和仇恨所驱使，而非理性，因此只会固执己见，不断重复同样的虚假论点——或者诉诸人身攻击、居高临下的态度、语气指责，或任何其他能想到的转移话题策略——而不会承认有效的反驳。



So I’m writing this essay primarily for the benefit of those who fall into the second category: those who don’t know any better, or at least didn’t know any better up until now. If you were honestly unaware that person-first language is autistiphobic and that the majority of autistic people these days consider it objectionable—well, that’s nothing to be ashamed of. Given the sheer pervasiveness of autistiphobic attitudes and autistiphobic language in the world today, and given that person-first language is even taught in college classrooms and professional training programs, you can hardly be blamed for having accepted and adopted such language without realizing that it’s autistiphobic and disrespectful of autistic people. You’re not a bad person for not having known any better than what you were taught. And now that you do know better, you can do better. You can stop using person-first language and just call autistic people autistic, instead of continuing to inadvertently disrespect and stigmatize us.

所以我写这篇文章，主要是为了那些属于第二类的人：那些不明就里，或者至少直到现在还不明就里的人。如果你确实不知道“人先语言”是反孤独谱系的，并且如今大多数孤独谱系群体都认为这种说法令人反感——嗯，这没什么可羞愧的。鉴于当今世界反孤独谱系的态度和语言如此普遍，而且“人先语言”甚至在大学课堂和专业培训项目中都有教授，你因接受并采用这种语言而未能意识到它是对孤独谱系群体的不尊重和歧视，这几乎不能怪你。你并非因为不知道比你所学的更好的东西就是个坏人。而现在你知道了更好的做法，就可以做得更好。你可以停止使用“人先语言”，直接称呼孤独谱系群体为孤独谱系，而不是继续无意中不尊重和污名化我们。



The big lie that autistiphobic bigots tell about person-first language is that person-first language is the “respectful” way to talk about autistic people. There’s a specific set of spurious arguments that autistiphobic bigots use to support this lie, or to justify their continued use of person-first language when autistic people and our allies object to it. If you were taught to use person-first language when talking about autistic people, chances are that you were also taught to accept these arguments. You may have heard these arguments from people in positions of authority, or from people who supposedly had some sort of expertise on the topic—and as a result, you might have accepted them without giving them the necessary critical scrutiny. So let’s do that critical scrutiny right here and now. Let’s look at the three most common arguments for person-first language, one by one, and debunk them.

反孤独症偏执者关于“人先语言”的最大谎言，是声称这种表述是谈论孤独谱系群体时“尊重”的方式。当孤独谱系群体及其盟友反对时，反孤独症偏执者会搬出一套特定的虚假论据来支撑这个谎言，或为其继续使用“人先语言”辩护。如果你曾被教导在谈论孤独谱系群体时要使用“人先语言”，那么你很可能也接受了这些论据。你可能从权威人士或所谓“专家”那里听到过这些论据——因此，你或许未经必要的批判性审视就全盘接受了它们。那么，我们现在就来展开批判性审视。让我们逐一剖析支持“人先语言”的三个最常见论据，并揭穿其谬误。



•



Spurious Argument #1: “Person-first language is more respectful because it separates the person from the autism.”

虚假论据一：“人先语言更尊重，因为它将人与孤独症区分开来。”



No. This is exactly why person-first language is disrespectful of autistic people.

不。这正是“人先语言”对孤独谱系群体不尊重的原因所在。



Who would want to “separate the person from the autism”? Only someone who believes, deep down, that there’s something wrong with being autistic—someone who believes that being autistic in some way a bad thing or a shameful thing. And anyone who believes that it’s bad or shameful to be autistic is, by definition, an autistiphobic bigot (just like anyone who believes that it’s bad or shameful to be gay is a homophobic bigot, and anyone who believes that it’s bad or shameful to be Black is a racist bigot).

谁会想要“把人与孤独症分开”？只有那些内心深处认为成为孤独谱系群体有问题的人——那些认为成为孤独谱系群体是坏事或可耻之事的人。而任何认为成为孤独谱系群体是坏事或可耻的人，按定义就是孤独谱系恐惧的偏执者（就像任何认为同性恋是坏事或可耻的人是恐同偏执者，任何认为身为黑人是坏事或可耻的人是种族主义偏执者一样）。



Autism doesn’t exist separately from autistic people. It’s not actually a thing that a person can “have.” It isn’t a disease, like a tumor or a virus. You can’t cut an autism out of a person and preserve it in a bottle. You can’t isolate autism in a laboratory and have a little test tube or petri dish full of autism. Being autistic informs every facet of a person’s development, embodiment, cognition, and experience, in ways that are pervasive and inseparable from the person’s overall being. So the autistic person can’t be separated from the autism, and the autism can’t be separated from the autistic person.

孤独谱系并非独立于孤独谱系群体而存在。它实际上不是一个人可以“拥有”的东西。它不是像肿瘤或病毒那样的疾病。你无法从一个人身上切除孤独谱系并将其保存在瓶子里。你无法在实验室中分离出孤独谱系，并拥有装满孤独谱系的小试管或培养皿。成为孤独谱系群体影响着一个人发展的方方面面——包括成长、具身化、认知和体验——这些影响无处不在，且与人的整体存在密不可分。因此，孤独谱系群体无法与孤独谱系分离，孤独谱系也无法与孤独谱系群体分离。



The idea that an autistic person can be somehow “separated from the autism” is an autistiphobic fantasy. It’s a fantasy that appeals to those whose autistiphobia runs so deep that on some level they see being autistic as incompatible with being fully human, and therefore can only see an autistic person as human by pretending that there’s a non-autistic version of the person somehow hidden under the autism. Thus, person-first language is born of a fundamental inability or unwillingness to accept autistic people as they are. There’s nothing respectful about that.

认为孤独谱系个体可以某种方式“与孤独谱系分离”的想法，是一种孤独恐惧症的幻想。这种幻想吸引着那些孤独恐惧症根深蒂固的人——他们在某种程度上将孤独谱系视为与完整人性不相容的存在，因此只能通过假装孤独谱系之下隐藏着一个非孤独谱系的版本，才能将孤独谱系者视为人类。由此，以人为先的语言诞生于根本无力或不愿接纳孤独谱系群体本真状态的困境。这毫无尊重可言。



In fact, person-first language was originally developed by autistiphobic parents of autistic children, and has largely been propagated and insisted upon by such parents—parents who hold the autistiphobic belief that autism is some sort of horrible tragic disorder, and that this disorder functions as a sort of shell under which their imagined “real” (i.e., non-autistic) children are hiding.

事实上，以人为先的语言最初由孤独谱系儿童的孤独恐惧症父母所创，并主要由这类父母传播和坚持——这些父母持有孤独恐惧症的信念，认为孤独谱系是某种可怕悲惨的障碍，而这种障碍如同外壳，其下隐藏着他们想象中的“真实”（即非孤独谱系）孩子。



These parents are so intensely autistiphobic that they refuse to accept and love the autistic children they actually have, and instead they’ve constructed a twisted fantasy world in which the terrible disorder of autism has stolen their “real” children from them. According to this fantasy, if parents fight hard enough against autism and steadfastly refuse to accept their autistic children as they are, they might someday magically remove the autism from their children and thus “recover” the non-autistic children that they’ve wished for all along.

这些父母对孤独谱系有着极度的恐惧，以至于他们拒绝接受和爱自己真实的孤独谱系孩子，反而构建了一个扭曲的幻想世界——在这个世界里，可怕的孤独症障碍偷走了他们“真正”的孩子。按照这种幻想，如果父母与孤独症抗争到底，坚决拒绝接受孩子本来的样子，或许有朝一日能神奇地消除孩子的孤独谱系，从而“找回”他们一直渴望的非孤独谱系孩子。



Person-first language was expressly intended to promote and reinforce this sick autistiphobic fantasy, and that’s still the primary purpose that person-first language ultimately serves. There are multi-billion-dollar industries today that have been created specifically to exploit this fantasy for profit. These industries include the “autism charity” industry (comprised of money-grubbing “charitable” organizations that raise funds by portraying the existence of autistic children as a heart-rending tragedy), the “behavioral therapy” industry (comprised of providers of bogus “therapies” like ABA, in which autistic children are abused, coerced, and traumatized into imitating the outward behavior of neurotypical children, at the expense of their long-term psychological well-being), and the vast industry of quack pseudo-medical “autism cures” (many of which cause lasting physical and psychological harm, sometimes fatal harm, to the children on which they’re inflicted). These industries all harm autistic people and defraud the families of autistic people, while encouraging the “recovery” fantasy and fanning the flames of autistiphobia.

人本语言明确旨在推广并强化这种病态的孤独恐惧幻想，而这正是人本语言最终服务的首要目的。如今存在价值数十亿美元的产业，专门利用这种幻想牟利。这些产业包括"孤独症慈善"产业（由唯利是图的"慈善"组织构成，它们通过将孤独谱系儿童的存在描绘成令人心碎的悲剧来筹集资金）、"行为治疗"产业（由提供 ABA 等虚假"疗法"的机构组成，这些疗法通过虐待、胁迫和创伤手段迫使孤独谱系儿童模仿神经典型儿童的外在行为，牺牲其长期心理健康），以及庞大的伪医学"孤独症疗法"产业（其中许多疗法对接受治疗的儿童造成持久的身心伤害，有时甚至是致命伤害）。这些产业都在伤害孤独谱系群体、欺诈孤独谱系家庭的同时，助长"康复"幻想并煽动孤独恐惧情绪。



Every time you use person-first language, you’re complicit in all of this. I’m sure that’s not your intention, but actual impact matters more than naïve good intentions. Every time you use person-first language, you’re helping to promote and reinforce a twisted and hateful autistiphobic fantasy. Every time you use person-first language, you’re helping to legitimize the industries which profit by exploiting that fantasy—and thus you’re complicit in the harm that these industries do to autistic people.

每次你使用“人先语言”（person-first language），你都在助长这一切。我确信这并非你的本意，但实际影响远比天真的善意更重要。每次你使用“人先语言”，你都在帮助推广和强化一种扭曲且充满仇恨的孤独谱系恐惧幻想。每次你使用“人先语言”，你都在帮助那些利用这种幻想牟利的行业获得合法性——因此，你对这些行业对孤独谱系群体造成的伤害负有共谋责任。



And there’s definitely nothing respectful about that.

这绝对谈不上任何尊重。



•



Spurious Argument #2: “We have to put the person first to show that they’re people first and that autism doesn’t define them.”

谬论之二：“我们必须把人放在第一位，以表明他们首先是‘人’，而孤独症不能定义他们。”



This is just straight-up nonsense. The whole debate about whether to say “autistic person” or (ugh) “person with autism” originated in English-speaking countries and has continued to rage primarily in English-speaking countries. And in the English language, it’s standard grammar to place the adjective before the noun.

这纯粹是无稽之谈。关于该说“孤独谱系人士”还是（唉）“患有孤独症的人”的争论，最初源于英语国家，并主要在这些国家持续激烈。而在英语中，标准语法是将形容词置于名词之前。



Anyone fluent in the English language implicitly understands that the noun is primary regardless of where it’s placed in relation to the adjective. It’s understood that any adjectives placed before the noun merely serve to provide further information about the noun. When I write about a blue Norwegian parrot, for instance, anyone fluent in English understands that it’s first and foremost a parrot, and that its color and nationality are secondary to its parrotness.

任何精通英语的人都会本能地理解，无论形容词置于名词之前还是之后，名词始终是核心。置于名词前的形容词仅用于提供关于该名词的补充信息。例如，当我描述一只"蓝色的挪威鹦鹉"时，所有英语使用者都明白它首先是一只鹦鹉，而它的颜色和国籍属性都从属于其"鹦鹉本质"。



Anyone fluent the English language also understands that adjectives aren’t exclusive—in other words, the presence of a given adjective before a noun doesn’t imply that it’s the one adjective that entirely and exclusively defines that noun. When I refer to a parrot as “the blue parrot,” everyone understands that I’m not in any way implying that the parrot is entirely and exclusively defined by its blueness. Everyone understands that the parrot can be blue and also Norwegian, male, large, resting, and all manner of other things at the same time.

任何精通英语的人同样明白，形容词并非排他性修饰——换言之，名词前出现某个形容词，并不意味着该形容词能完全且唯一地定义这个名词。当我称一只鹦鹉为"那只蓝色的鹦鹉"时，所有人都明白我绝无暗示这只鹦鹉仅由"蓝色"这一属性定义。大家理解这只鹦鹉可以同时是蓝色的、挪威的、雄性的、体型庞大的、正在休息的，以及具备其他各种属性。



The autistiphobic bigots who react to the phrase “autistic people” with indignant shouts of “Their autism doesn’t define them!” are perfectly aware of how adjectives work in English. When you say “six-year-old children,” these bigots never jump in with shouts of “Their age doesn’t define them!” When you say “tall people” they never jump in with “Their height doesn’t define them!” They don’t demand that you say “children who are six years old,” or “people living with tallness.” So the argument that we have to use person-first language in order to affirm that autistic people are “people first” and that “autism doesn’t define them” is not only downright ridiculous, it’s also disingenuous.

那些对“孤独谱系群体”这一表述愤然抗议“他们的孤独症不能定义他们！”的孤独症恐惧偏执者，其实完全清楚英语中形容词的用法。当你说“六岁儿童”时，这些偏执者从不会跳出来大喊“他们的年龄不能定义他们！”；当你说“高个子人群”时，他们也从不会插嘴“他们的身高不能定义他们！”他们不会要求你必须说“年龄为六岁的儿童”或“患有身高症的人群”。因此，所谓必须使用“人本优先语言”来确认孤独谱系群体“首先是人类”且“孤独症不能定义他们”的论点，不仅荒谬至极，更是虚伪透顶。



The real reason these people insist on person-first language, and the real reason they freak out when people use the adjective “autistic” the same way one would use any other adjective, is autistiphobia. Deep down, because of their own unresolved psychological issues, they fear and despise autistic people. But because they need to convince themselves of their own goodness, they can’t admit to themselves that they feel such fear and hatred toward a group of people—especially not a group which, in the case of many autistiphobes, might include their own children.

这些人坚持使用“人先语言”的真正原因，以及当人们像使用其他形容词一样使用“孤独谱系”这个形容词时他们抓狂的真正原因，是孤独恐惧症。在内心深处，由于他们自身未解决的心理问题，他们害怕并厌恶孤独谱系群体。但因为他们需要说服自己相信自己的善良，他们无法承认自己对某一群体怀有如此恐惧和憎恨——尤其是当这个群体，在许多孤独恐惧症患者的情况下，可能包括他们自己的孩子时。



So instead, they buy into the autistiphobic fantasy already discussed: the fantasy that the autism can somehow be separated from the person. This enables them to pretend that it’s only some horrid “disorder” or “condition” called autism toward which they feel aversion, rather than actual autistic human beings. It’s exactly the same strategy of self-deception that homophobic right-wing Christian bigots use when they pretend that they don’t hate gay people and instead just hate “the sin of homosexuality.”

因此，他们转而相信之前讨论过的孤独恐惧症幻想：即孤独症可以以某种方式与人分离的幻想。这使他们能够假装自己厌恶的只是某种可怕的“障碍”或“状况”，即所谓的孤独症，而不是真实的孤独谱系人类个体。这与恐同的右翼基督教偏执者使用的自我欺骗策略完全相同——他们假装自己不憎恨同性恋者，而只是憎恨“同性恋之罪”。



When a person relies on denial and fantasy to protect their own psyche from deeply uncomfortable truths, the arrangement is fragile. Anything that contradicts the fantasy threatens to bring the whole thing crashing down, and threatens to bring the person face to face with the realities they’re so desperately hiding from themselves. If they were to accept even for a moment that the autism can’t ever be separated from the autistic person, they’d have to face an overwhelming flood of deeply uncomfortable repressed feelings and repressed truths (including, in the case of many autistiphobic parents, the truth that they’ve been unable to accept and love the person their autistic child actually is).

当一个人依赖否认和幻想来保护自己的心理免受深层不安真相的冲击时，这种心理结构是脆弱的。任何与幻想相矛盾的事物都可能使整个体系崩塌，迫使他们直面自己拼命逃避的现实。哪怕只是短暂地承认孤独谱系无法与孤独谱系者分离，他们就必须面对汹涌而来的、被压抑的不安感受与真相（包括许多仇视孤独谱系者的父母所不愿面对的真相——他们始终无法接纳和爱自己孤独谱系孩子的真实模样）。



This is why so many autistiphobes don’t just insist on using person-first language, but also aggressively insist that everyone else should use person-first language, too. The fantasy is so fragile, and their need to keep hiding reality from themselves is so strong, that even hearing the phrase “autistic person” feels like an existential threat to them on some visceral unconscious level.

正因如此，许多仇视孤独谱系者不仅坚持使用"人先语言"，还咄咄逼人地要求所有人都必须如此措辞。这种幻想如此脆弱，他们隐藏现实的需求如此强烈，以至于听到"孤独谱系者"这个短语，都会在某种本能的无意识层面，让他们感受到存在性的威胁。



They can’t look at where their strong feelings and reactions are truly coming from (since that would involve looking at their own denial), so instead they come up with desperate rationalizations to justify those feelings and reactions. And that’s how they end up making such a patently absurd argument as “We have to put the person first to show that they’re people first and that autism doesn’t define them”—an argument which, as we’ve now seen, makes no sense, given how adjectives actually work in the English language.

他们无法正视自己强烈情绪和反应的真正来源（因为那将意味着审视自身的否认心理），于是便拼命寻找牵强的理由来合理化这些感受和反应。正因如此，他们才会提出如此荒谬的论点：“我们必须把人放在首位，以表明他们首先是‘人’，而孤独症不能定义他们”——正如我们所见，这个论点在英语形容词的实际用法中根本站不住脚。



So once again, we find that person-first language has nothing to do with being respectful of autistic people. As previously noted, the fantasy that person-first language serves to promote—the fantasy that autism can be separated from an autistic person—is a fantasy that exists for the comfort of autistiphobes, and has dire consequences for autistic people. So using person-first language is in fact grossly disrespectful of autistic people, because it prioritizes the fantasies and fragilities of autistiphobes over autistic well-being.

因此我们再次发现，所谓“人先语言”与尊重孤独谱系群体毫无关系。如前所述，“人先语言”所宣扬的幻想——即孤独症可以与孤独谱系个体分离——是一种为满足孤独症恐惧者舒适感而存在的幻想，对孤独谱系群体造成了严重后果。使用“人先语言”实际上是对孤独谱系群体的极大不敬，因为它将孤独症恐惧者的幻想与脆弱置于孤独谱系群体的福祉之上。



•



Spurious Argument #3: “I’m a trained professional [or I’ve listened to professionals] and person-first language is what I was taught to use; it’s standard in the field.”

谬误之三：“我是受过训练的专业人士（或我听从过专业人士的意见），而‘人先语言’是我被教导使用的，也是该领域的标准。”



We live in a profoundly autistiphobic society in which the discourses on autism, including the academic and professional discourses, have been dominated from the beginning by autistiphobic voices and viewpoints. The reason that person-first language is the standard in whatever academic or professional fields you’re involved in (or in the academic and professional fields of whatever non-autistic “experts” you’ve learned about autism from) is that autistiphobia is deeply ingrained in the history, literature, conventions, and practices of those fields. This applies to fields as disparate as psychology, medicine, education, social work, journalism, and neurobiology (and if you think a physical science like biology can’t have bigotry ingrained in it, go look up “scientific racism”).

我们生活在一个极度仇视孤独谱系的社会中，关于孤独谱系的论述——包括学术和专业领域的论述——从一开始就被仇视孤独谱系的声音和观点所主导。无论你身处哪个学术或专业领域（或你从哪些非孤独谱系的“专家”那里了解孤独谱系），‘人先语言’之所以成为该领域的标准，正是因为仇视孤独谱系已深深植根于这些领域的历史、文献、惯例和实践中。这适用于心理学、医学、教育学、社会工作、新闻学和神经生物学等截然不同的领域（如果你认为像生物学这样的自然科学不可能根植偏见，不妨去查查“科学种族主义”）。



The professors, professionals, and other “experts” who taught you to use person-first language were either autistiphobic bigots themselves, or else were well-intentioned but ill-informed people who learned from the work of autistiphobic bigots and passed the autistiphobic language and lessons along to the next generation without recognizing them as harmful.

那些教导你使用“人先语言”的教授、专业人士及其他“专家”，要么本身就是厌恶自闭症者的偏执狂，要么就是心怀善意但信息闭塞的人——他们从厌恶自闭症者的偏执狂的著作中习得这套理论，并将这些带有歧视性的语言和观念传递给下一代，却未能意识到其危害性。



So please, never say anything like “Person-first language is what I was taught to use,” unless it’s the first half of a sentence and the second half is something along the lines of “but now I know better and will never use it again.” Believe me, autistic people already know quite well that person-first language is what you were taught to use. We already know that you learned about autism from autistiphobic bigots, or from people who uncritically passed along the harmful lessons of autistiphobic bigots. We already know that autistiphobic bigotry is deeply ingrained in whatever academic or professional fields you’ve turned to for knowledge in the past. You don’t need to remind us of any of this. We don’t want to hear your attempts to justify your use of autistiphobic language. We’re not asking you to explain yourself, we’re asking you to start doing better.

所以，请永远不要说“我学到的就是使用人先语言”这种话，除非这句话的前半句之后紧跟着“但现在我明白了，再也不会这样用了”。相信我，孤独谱系群体早已清楚人先语言是你们被教导使用的。我们明白你们是从仇视孤独症的偏执者那里，或是从盲目传播这种有害观念的人那里了解孤独症的。我们也知道，在你们过去寻求知识的学术或专业领域里，仇视孤独症的偏见早已根深蒂固。你们无需提醒我们这些。我们不想听你们为使用仇视孤独症的语言辩解。我们不是在要求你们解释，而是在要求你们开始做得更好。



Your society is autistiphobic. Your field is autistiphobic. Your “experts” are autistiphobic. Your teachers were autistiphobic. We’re asking you to be better and to do better. Doing better means recognizing that many things you were taught about autistic people were just plain wrong, and that much of the language that you were taught was acceptable or preferable to use when speaking about us—including person-first language—is actually stigmatizing, insulting, and harmful to us. Doing better means refusing to perpetuate the autistiphobic language, beliefs, and practices that you were taught, even when that refusal puts you at odds with the authorities and traditions from which you’ve previously learned.

你的社会患有孤独症恐惧症。你的领域患有孤独症恐惧症。你的“专家”患有孤独症恐惧症。你的老师患有孤独症恐惧症。我们要求你变得更好，做得更好。做得更好意味着认识到，你被教导的关于孤独谱系群体的许多事情完全是错误的，而且你被教导在谈论我们时可以使用或更倾向于使用的许多语言——包括人本语言——实际上是在污名化、侮辱和伤害我们。做得更好意味着拒绝延续你被教导的那些带有孤独症恐惧症色彩的语言、信念和做法，即使这种拒绝会让你与之前所学习的权威和传统产生冲突。



•



Every autistic person who spends any significant length of time working to combat autistiphobia within public, academic, or professional spheres—especially if any of their work takes place on social media—eventually learns an ironic truth: the non-autistics who are most insistent on using person-first language when talking about us, the ones who most loudly declare that person-first language is more “respectful” because “it puts the person first,” always turn out to be the ones who have the least respect for us and who don’t really see us as people at all.

每一个在公共、学术或专业领域——尤其是那些在社交媒体上开展工作的——长期致力于对抗孤独谱系恐惧症的孤独谱系人士，最终都会领悟到一个讽刺的真相：那些在谈论我们时最坚持使用“人先语言”（person-first language）的非孤独谱系人士，那些最响亮地宣称“人先语言”更“尊重人”因为“它把人放在第一位”的人，往往正是最不尊重我们、根本不把我们视为真正人类的人。



In two decades of autism-related advocacy, teaching, and scholarship, I’ve found this correlation between autistiphobic bigotry and person-first language to be a 100 percent reliable constant. It’s a truth widely recognized within the autistic community these days. Most of us know that we can never trust a person-firster, and those who don’t learn this lesson through observation or by listening to fellow autistics end up learning the hard way sooner or later.

在二十年的孤独症相关倡导、教学和学术研究中，我发现这种孤独谱系恐惧症偏见与人先语言之间的关联是百分之百可靠的常数。如今，这在孤独谱系社群中已是广为人知的真相。我们大多数人都知道，永远不能信任一个坚持使用人先语言的人；而那些未能通过观察或倾听其他孤独谱系人士学到这一教训的人，迟早会以惨痛的方式领悟。



A lot of autistiphobes who’ve been called out for using person-first language have tried to dodge the whole issue by using euphemisms like “on the spectrum” as another way to avoid saying “autistic.” Guess what? We autistics see exactly what you’re doing. We’re notoriously good at pattern recognition. Whether it’s person-first language or euphemisms, we can tell when someone is trying desperately to avoid just calling us autistic. And we know that the refusal to just call autistic people autistic is the universally reliable number one sign that someone is an autistiphobic bigot.

许多被指责使用“人先语言”的孤独症恐惧者，试图用“在谱系上”这类委婉说法来回避直接说“孤独谱系”。猜怎么着？我们孤独谱系群体完全看穿了你们的把戏。我们以模式识别能力著称。无论是“人先语言”还是委婉说法，我们都能分辨出有人正拼命避免直接称呼我们为孤独谱系。而我们知道，拒绝直接称呼孤独谱系群体为孤独谱系，是判断某人是否患有孤独症恐惧偏执的普遍可靠的首要标志。



As I explained earlier in this essay, the refusal to call autistic people autistic is often a sign that a person’s autistiphobia is so intense that they’ve sought refuge in the desperate fantasy that the autism can be separated from the person. And of course, calling an autistic person autistic is an acknowledgement of reality that threatens to bring this whole pathetic fragile fantasy crashing down.

正如本文前文所述，拒绝称呼孤独谱系群体为孤独谱系，往往表明一个人的孤独症恐惧症已严重到让他们躲进一种绝望的幻想中——认为孤独谱系可以与个体分离。当然，称呼孤独谱系者为孤独谱系，是对现实的承认，这足以撼动这个可悲脆弱的幻想。



Any doubts I may have had about the accuracy of this explanation have been dispelled by the results of an experiment that I like to perform when I give trainings on autism to groups of psychotherapists, social workers, special ed teachers, or other professionals. The experiment is simple: one by one, I have each participant look me in the eyes and say to me, “You are autistic.”

我曾对这个解释的准确性存有疑虑，但当我为心理治疗师、社会工作者、特殊教育教师及其他专业人士进行孤独症培训时，我常做的一个实验的结果打消了这些疑虑。这个实验很简单：我让每位参与者逐一看着我的眼睛，对我说：“你是孤独谱系人士。”



I’m not a big fan of eye contact, but in this case it’s worth it. The autistiphobia of many of the participants is instantly exposed, and it also becomes quite evident just how desperately they’re clinging to their pitiful autistiphobic fantasy that we’re “people with autism” rather than autistic people.

我并不热衷于眼神接触，但在这个情境下，这很值得。许多参与者对孤独谱系的恐惧瞬间暴露无遗，同时也很明显，他们多么拼命地 clinging 着那个可悲的、恐惧孤独谱系的幻想——认为我们是“患有孤独症的人”，而不是孤独谱系人士。



You see, it turns out that when I ask these adult professionals to look me in the eye and acknowledge out loud that I’m autistic, many of them just can’t do it. They squirm. They look down and avoid my gaze. They argue and bargain and complain. Some of them shut down completely. Some of them fly into indignant rages and storm out of the room. A lot of them cry. One time, one of them threw up. Autistiphobia runs deep, and its connection to the terms people use to talk about us should not be underestimated.

你看，结果发现，当我要求这些成年专业人士看着我的眼睛，并大声承认我是孤独谱系人士时，他们中的许多人就是做不到。他们局促不安，低头避开我的目光，争辩、讨价还价、抱怨。有些人完全僵住，有些人愤怒地冲出房间，很多人哭了。有一次，还有人吐了。对孤独谱系的恐惧根深蒂固，而它与人们用来谈论我们的术语之间的联系，绝不应被低估。



A person who can’t just call autistic people autistic is a person autistic people can’t trust, and a person who should never ever be permitted to be in a position of any authority over autistic people or to work with autistic people in any professional capacity.

一个连直接称呼孤独谱系群体为“孤独谱系”都做不到的人，是孤独谱系群体无法信任的人，也是绝不应被允许在任何权威岗位上管理孤独谱系群体、或以任何专业身份与孤独谱系群体共事的人。



If you’re a non-autistic person who’s accustomed to using person-first language or euphemisms, put yourself to the test. Start calling autistic people autistic. If it’s easy for you to make the switch to calling us autistic, that’s excellent. You’re now one more voice refusing to perpetuate autistiphobic language and the autistiphobic attitudes and fantasies associated with such language. Thank you.

如果你是非孤独谱系人士，且习惯使用“人先语言”或委婉说法，请对自己做个测试。开始直接称呼我们为“孤独谱系”吧。如果这对你来说很容易做到，那太好了——你已成为拒绝延续反孤独谱系语言、以及与之相关的偏见态度与幻想的一份子。谢谢你。



And if it’s hard for you to discard the person-first language and the evasive euphemisms? If it’s hard for you to start calling us autistic? If you find yourself resisting the change, making excuses, having trouble just saying or writing the phrase “autistic people”? Well, now you’ve learned something important about yourself, and you have some work to do.

但如果抛弃“人先语言”和回避性委婉说法对你来说很困难？如果直接称呼我们为“孤独谱系”让你感到艰难？如果你发现自己抗拒改变、寻找借口、甚至难以说出或写下“孤独谱系群体”这个短语？那么，你已从中认识到自身的重要问题，并且需要做出改变。







---

About the Author

关于作者



Nick Walker is a queer, transgender, flamingly autistic writer and educator best known for her foundational work on the neurodiversity paradigm, her development of the term neuroqueer and the concept of neuroqueering, and her contributions to fostering the emergent genre of neuroqueer speculative fiction. She is a professor of psychology at California Institute of Integral Studies, and senior instructor at the Aiki Arts Center in Berkeley.

尼克·沃克是一位酷儿、跨性别、热情洋溢的孤独谱系作家和教育家，以其在神经多样性范式方面的奠基性工作、对“神经酷儿”这一术语及“神经酷儿化”概念的提出，以及为培育新兴的神经酷儿思辨小说类型所做的贡献而闻名。她是加州整合研究学院的心理学教授，也是伯克利合气道艺术中心的高级讲师。



Dr. Walker is co-founder and Managing Editor of the worker-owned indie publishing house Autonomous Press, and has co-edited and contributed to multiple volumes of the annual Spoon Knife neuroqueer lit anthology published by Autonomous Press’ NeuroQueer Books imprint.

沃克博士是工人所有的独立出版社 Autonomous Press 的联合创始人兼执行编辑，并共同编辑和参与了该出版社旗下 NeuroQueer Books 品牌出版的年度《Spoon Knife》神经酷儿文学选集的多卷内容。



Along with her co-writer Andrew M. Reichart and artist Mike Bennewitz, Dr. Walker is part of the creative team behind the urban fantasy webcomic Weird Luck.

沃克博士与合著者安德鲁·M·赖卡特及艺术家迈克·本尼维茨共同组成了都市奇幻网络漫画《Weird Luck》的创作团队。



Website: neuroqueer.com

网站：neuroqueer.com



Webcomic: weirdluck.net

网络漫画：weirdluck.net

On the Practice of Stimming

关于自我刺激行为的实践



When I was writing my doctoral dissertation, I needed to include a definition of stimming. I couldn’t find one that satisfied me, so I wrote my own from scratch. In case anyone else also has use for a good definition of stimming, here it is. I wrote the original dissertation version of this piece sometime in 2018. The version I’m sharing here has been newly revised to enable it to better stand on its own and to make it a bit more readable.

在撰写博士论文时，我需要为"自我刺激行为"下一个定义。但始终找不到令我满意的现成定义，于是便从零开始自行撰写。若有人也需要一个精准的自我刺激行为定义，以下便是我的成果。这篇文字的原始版本写于 2018 年博士论文期间，如今分享的版本经过全新修订，使其更独立完整且更具可读性。



A major defining feature of autistic embodiment is the tendency to engage in repetitive physical movements or other actions that provide specific forms of sensory stimulation. In conventional disciplinary discourses on autism based in the pathology paradigm, such actions have traditionally been referred to as stereotypy or self-stimulatory behavior, and are regarded as pathological symptoms that are best eliminated. In a crucial step toward taking back ownership of narratives about autistic embodiment, autistics transformed the pathologizing and rather ungainly term self-stimulatory behavior into the more graceful and less medical-sounding term stimming. The root word stim functions as both a verb and a noun: “I stim by rocking back and forth; rocking back and forth is my favorite stim.”

孤独谱系具身化的一个主要特征，是倾向于重复进行特定的身体动作或其他行为，以获取特定形式的感官刺激。在基于病理范式的传统孤独症学科话语中，这类行为通常被称为刻板行为或自我刺激行为，被视为需要消除的病理症状。在夺回孤独谱系具身化叙事主导权的关键一步中，孤独谱系群体将带有病理化色彩且颇为笨拙的术语"自我刺激行为"，改造成了更优雅、更少医学色彩的"刺激行为"（stimming）。词根"刺激"（stim）兼具动词和名词功能："我通过前后摇晃来进行刺激行为；前后摇晃是我最喜欢的刺激方式。"



The infinite possible varieties of stimming include, but are certainly not limited to:

刺激行为的形式无穷无尽，但至少包括：




proprioceptive or kinesthetic (e.g., rocking, pacing, waving or flapping one’s hands, seeking physical pressure or impact);

本体感觉或动觉刺激（例如摇晃、踱步、挥手或拍手、寻求身体压力或冲击）；



tactile (e.g., touching objects and surfaces with appealing textures, stroking one’s own skin);

触觉刺激（例如触摸具有诱人质感的物体表面、抚摸自己的皮肤）；



vestibular (e.g., spinning or swinging);

前庭刺激（如旋转或荡秋千）；



visual (e.g., gazing at running water or rising smoke);

视觉刺激（如凝视流水或升腾的烟雾）；



auditory (e.g., listening to running water or loud music);

听觉刺激（如聆听流水声或大声播放音乐）；



olfactory or gustatory (e.g., sniffing or tasting things);

嗅觉或味觉刺激（如嗅闻或品尝物品）；



verbal (e.g., repetition of particular words or phrases);

言语方面（例如重复特定词语或短语）；



any combination of the above (e.g., drumming, which combines the kinesthetic, the tactile, and the auditory).

上述任意组合（例如敲击动作，它融合了动觉、触觉与听觉）。




Pathology-oriented discourse around autism has tended to frame stimming as dysfunctional compulsive or automatic behavior that serves no purpose other than to detract from an autistic person’s performance of normativity—the performance of normativity being, from the perspective of those operating within the pathology paradigm, the goal toward which all autistics should be relentlessly pushed regardless of their own needs or wishes. The majority of autistics, on the other hand, along with a growing number of non-autistic thinkers who’ve come to view autism and autistics from perspectives less bound by the assumptions of the pathology paradigm, recognize stimming as serving vital functions in autistic consciousness.

围绕孤独谱系的病理导向论述，往往将自我刺激行为视为功能失调的强迫性或自动性行为，认为其除了削弱孤独谱系个体表现规范性之外毫无意义——在病理范式视角下，规范性表现正是所有孤独谱系个体应被持续推向的目标，无论其自身需求或意愿如何。而另一方面，多数孤独谱系个体，以及越来越多摆脱病理范式假设束缚的非孤独谱系思考者，都认识到自我刺激行为在孤独谱系意识中发挥着至关重要的功能。



Among those researchers and professionals who recognize that it has value and purpose, stimming is most commonly understood as serving essential functions of self-regulation and integration—that is, as being a means by which autistics are able to regulate their chaotic experience to avoid being overwhelmed by it, and by which they are able to better integrate that experience in order to bring increased coherence and navigability to their perceptual worlds. Non-autistic infants in what Jean Piaget called the sensorimotor stage of development, immersed in the developmental task of parsing the blooming, buzzing confusion of the sensory field into coherence, are constantly engaged in stimming, even though it’s not commonly referred to as stimming when non-autistic infants do it. Given the central role of stimming in the developmental task of parsing and integrating the sensory field, and given that parsing and integrating the sensory field tends to be more of an ongoing lifelong activity for autistics rather than just an early developmental stage, it makes sense that stimming would also be a lifelong activity for autistics.

在那些承认刻板行为具有价值和意义的研究者与专业人士看来，这种行为最常被理解为承担着自我调节与整合的关键功能——即孤独谱系者借此调节混乱的体验以避免被其淹没，同时通过这种方式更好地整合体验，从而为自身的感知世界带来更强的连贯性与可导航性。非孤独谱系婴儿在让·皮亚杰所称的感觉运动发展阶段中，沉浸于将感官领域那纷繁嘈杂的混乱解析为连贯性的发展任务时，会持续进行刻板行为——尽管当非孤独谱系婴儿这样做时，通常不被称为刻板行为。鉴于刻板行为在解析与整合感官领域这一发展任务中的核心作用，且对于孤独谱系者而言，解析与整合感官领域往往更像是一项持续终身的活动而非仅限早期发展阶段，那么刻板行为成为孤独谱系者终身活动的现象也就合乎逻辑了。



While stimming does indeed serve these vital regulatory and integrative functions for autistics, an understanding of stimming that looks no further than those particular functions is woefully incomplete. Such an understanding is of course a vast improvement over the conventional view of stimming as a purposeless and pathological symptom to be eradicated—but it is nonetheless a limited understanding, and I suspect the limitations derive from the same paternalistic attitudes and implicit assumptions of neurotypical superiority that lie at the root of the pathology paradigm.

虽然自我刺激行为确实为自闭症患者提供了这些重要的调节和整合功能，但仅停留在这些特定功能层面的理解是极其不完整的。这种理解固然比将自我刺激视为无意义且需要消除的病态症状的传统观点有了巨大进步——但这仍然是一种局限的理解，我怀疑这种局限性源于与病理学范式根源相同的家长式态度和神经典型优越性的隐性假设。



When stimming is understood as only a coping strategy or accommodation that enables autistics to compensate for their alleged neurobiological or sensorimotor “defects,” the underlying narrative is still a narrative in which autistics are defective—a narrative which implicitly assumes that the only worthwhile potential of autistics is their potential to compensate for their putative defects well enough to fit into neurotypical society and be almost-normal, and a narrative that thus implicitly dismisses the possibility that there are autistic capacities and potentials worth exploring that have nothing to do with aspiring to normativity or with mere compensation.

当自我刺激行为仅被理解为一种应对策略或适应手段，用以帮助孤独谱系者弥补其所谓的神经生物学或感觉运动"缺陷"时，其背后的叙事逻辑依然将孤独谱系者视为有缺陷的存在——这种叙事暗含的假设是，孤独谱系者唯一有价值的发展潜力，就是充分弥补其所谓缺陷以融入神经典型社会、成为"近乎正常"的人。这种叙事因此也隐晦地否定了另一种可能性：孤独谱系者所拥有的能力与潜能，或许与追求正常化或单纯补偿毫无关联，本身就值得深入探索。



Discussions of stimming in the first-hand accounts of autistics offer a striking contrast to this reductionist narrative. In some first-person accounts of autistic experience (particularly among autistics who have liberated themselves from disempowering narratives of pathology), stimming is revealed to be a highly complex and sophisticated body of intuitive sensorimotor practices. In addition to serving to regulate and integrate sensory, perceptual, cognitive, and emotional experience, stimming can also function as a way of exploring and relating to the sensory world, and as a means of accessing not only a wide range of cognitive and emotional capacities but also exceptional human capacities such as flow states or experiences of profound communion and ego transcendence.

在孤独谱系人士的第一手叙述中，关于刻板行为的讨论与这种简化论叙事形成了鲜明对比。在一些孤独谱系体验的第一人称描述中（尤其是那些已从病态化叙事的弱势框架中解放出来的孤独谱系人士），刻板行为被揭示为一套高度复杂且精妙的直觉性感觉运动实践体系。除了调节与整合感官、知觉、认知及情感体验外，刻板行为还能作为探索和联结感官世界的方式，不仅能够调动广泛的认知与情感能力，更能触及人类非凡的潜能——例如心流状态，或深层的共融体验与自我超越。



It’s worth noting here that the act of stimulating one’s own senses in specific ways in order to access certain states, feelings, or capacities is hardly unique to autistics. Everyone does this to some degree, in some way or other. Every day, millions of neurotypical individuals engage in such behaviors as pacing back and forth because it helps them think, drumming their fingers on a desk or table, pausing to deeply inhale a pleasing scent, letting themselves be soothed and entranced by the sound of rain on the roof or the sight of flickering flames in a fireplace, stroking a pet or the hair or skin of a lover because it feels good, or spontaneously moving their bodies as they get into the groove of a piece of music. One could therefore argue that everybody stims, and that autistics, because stimming is such an essential practice for the regulation and navigation of autistic sensory and cognitive experience, simply tend to stim more than non-autistics.

值得在此指出的是，通过特定方式刺激自身感官以进入某种状态、感受或能力的行为，并非孤独谱系人士所独有。每个人都在某种程度上以某种方式进行着这种行为。每天，数百万神经典型个体会做出诸如来回踱步（因为这有助于思考）、用手指敲击桌面、停下来深吸一口令人愉悦的气味、让自己沉浸在屋顶雨声或壁炉跳动的火焰中而获得抚慰与陶醉、抚摸宠物或爱人的头发与肌肤以获得愉悦感，或随着音乐节奏不自觉地摆动身体等行为。因此可以说，每个人都会进行自我刺激行为，而孤独谱系人士由于自我刺激行为对其感官与认知体验的调节与导航至关重要，往往比非孤独谱系人士更频繁地进行这种行为。



Based on the origins and common usage of the term stim, however, I would argue that the sort of activities described in the previous paragraph, as ordinarily performed by neurotypical individuals, are properly excluded from the category of stimming by virtue of the very fact that they fall within the commonly accepted neurotypical norms of behavior and embodiment. Such activities, when engaged in by neurotypical individuals, are not commonly regarded as symptoms of any dire pathology, nor assigned such labels such as “self-stimulatory behavior,” because they fall within the bounds of dominant cultural standards of neuronormativity. I would argue that in some way and at least to some small degree, an action must necessarily fall outside the bounds of neuronormative performance in order to qualify as stimming.

然而，根据"刺激"一词的起源和常见用法，我认为前文所述的那些由神经典型个体常规进行的活动，恰恰因其符合神经典型行为与具身化的普遍规范，应当被排除在"刺激行为"范畴之外。当神经典型个体进行这类活动时，既不会被视作某种可怕病理的症状，也不会被贴上"自我刺激行为"之类的标签——因为它们完全处于神经规范主导文化标准的界限之内。我认为，某种行为必须在一定程度上、至少是轻微地超出神经规范表现的边界，才能被界定为刺激行为。



With all this in mind, I offer the following as a working definition: To stim is to engage in any action that falls outside the boundaries of the social performance of normativity, and that provides some form of sensory stimulation in order to facilitate, intentionally or otherwise, some particular cognitive or sensorimotor process, or access to some particular state or capacity of consciousness or sensorimotor experience.

基于以上考虑，我提出以下工作定义：自我刺激行为是指任何超出规范性社会表现边界的行为，通过提供某种形式的感官刺激，有意或无意地促进特定的认知或感觉运动过程，或进入某种特定的意识状态、能力状态或感觉运动体验。







---


Nick_ebook-21










The Story Behind “This Is Autism”

“这就是孤独症”背后的故事



On November 11th, 2013, a large and well-funded anti-autistic hate group—an organization ironically named “Autism Speaks,” which boasts an extensive history of promoting the stigmatization, silencing, disenfranchisement, abuse, murder, and eugenic extermination of autistic people—released a “call for action” authored by one of its founders.

2013 年 11 月 11 日，一个资金雄厚的大型反孤独谱系仇恨组织——这个讽刺地名为“孤独症之声”的机构，长期致力于污名化、噤声、剥夺权利、虐待、谋杀以及优生灭绝孤独谱系群体——发布了由其创始人之一撰写的“行动号召”。



Like much of the previous anti-autistic hate speech produced by Autism Speaks, this “call for action” characterized the very existence of autistic children as a “monumental health crisis” a “national emergency,” and a terrible, life-destroying tragedy visited upon the families of these children. As is usual in the rhetoric of Autism Speaks, the existence of millions of autistic adults was not mentioned at all; acknowledging our existence would make it hard for them to keep selling the lie that autism is a growing “epidemic” rather than a manifestation of human biodiversity which serves an evolutionary purpose and has most likely been present in the species since our hunter-gatherer origins.

与“孤独症之声”此前大量反孤独谱系仇恨言论如出一辙，这份“行动号召”将孤独谱系儿童的存在本身描述为“巨大的健康危机”“国家紧急状态”，以及降临在这些儿童家庭身上的可怕毁灭性悲剧。正如该组织惯用的修辞手法，文中完全未提及数百万成年孤独谱系个体的存在；承认我们的存在，将使他们难以继续兜售“孤独症是日益蔓延的‘流行病’”这一谎言——而事实上，孤独谱系是人类生物多样性的体现，具有进化意义，且自人类狩猎采集时代起便很可能已存在于物种之中。



Written in the tone of over-the-top alarmism characteristic of the rhetoric of hate groups everywhere, this hand-wringing “call for action” featured melodramatic descriptions of the daily horrors allegedly faced by parents of autistic children. Three times, in the course of this list of horrors, the author repeated the sentence “This is autism” in bold lettering for extra dramatic effect.

以仇恨团体特有的危言耸听口吻写就，这篇焦虑不安的“行动呼吁”用夸张笔触描绘了孤独症儿童家长据称每日面对的恐怖场景。在这份恐怖清单中，作者三次用加粗字体重复“这就是孤独谱系”这句话，以增强戏剧效果。



Unsurprisingly, the autistic community took issue with this. A week later, on November 18th, an autistic blogger named Cynthia Kim organized a flash blog as a creative pushback. A flash blog is when a whole bunch of people all make blog posts on a single topic on the same day; I don’t know whether this is still a thing that anyone does, but it was a thing people did back in 2013. An impressive number of autistics and allies wrote things for the flash blog, and the piece that follows, predictably entitled “This Is Autism,” was my contribution. Its original 2013 publication date makes it one of the oldest pieces in this book; the only one that predates it is “Throw Away the Master’s Tools.”

不出所料，孤独谱系社群对此提出异议。一周后的 11 月 18 日，一位名叫辛西娅·金的孤独谱系博主发起了一场闪电博客作为创造性反击。闪电博客是指一大群人在同一天就同一主题发表博客文章——我不知道现在是否还有人这么做，但在 2013 年这确实是人们会做的事。数量可观的孤独谱系人士及其盟友为这场闪电博客撰写了文章，而接下来这篇题为《这就是孤独谱系》的文章便是我的投稿。其 2013 年的原始发表日期使其成为本书最古老的文章之一；唯一比它更早的是《扔掉大师的工具》。



Since the original piece of Autism Speaks hate speech that inspired the flash blog featured a series of brief melodramatic depictions of the horrors of living with autistic children, I figured I’d make my piece a series of brief accurate depictions of my experiences being autistic and meeting up with other autistic folks.

由于那篇引发闪博的“自闭症之声”仇恨言论原文，以一系列简短夸张的戏剧化描述，渲染了与孤独谱系儿童共同生活的种种恐怖，我决定将自己的文章写成一系列简短而真实的描述，记录我作为孤独谱系人士的经历，以及与其他孤独谱系人士相遇的体验。



The version of “This Is Autism” that appears here has been edited a bit from the original. In the original version, I spoofed the melodramatic Autism Speaks “call for action” piece by putting the sentence “This is autism” in bold lettering in between scenes, just like the Autism Speaks founder had done. I took it out in this version because I think my piece reads better without it; the satirical boldface “This is autism” refrain only made sense in the piece’s original context. I also cut out a couple of scenes that just don’t work as well for me anymore, for one reason or another.

此处呈现的《这就是孤独谱系》版本，相较原文略有编辑。在原始版本中，我模仿了“自闭症之声”那篇戏剧化的“行动呼吁”文章，像其创始人那样，在场景之间用粗体字写上“这就是孤独谱系”这句话。在这个版本中，我删除了它，因为我认为没有它，我的文章读起来更流畅；那讽刺性的粗体“这就是孤独谱系”重复句，只有在原文的语境中才有意义。我还删除了几个场景，这些场景如今出于种种原因，对我来说已不再那么奏效。



The Autism Speaks co-founder who wrote the original “call for action” died in 2016. As soon as she was gone, Autism Speaks began a major rebranding. They continued supporting the disenfranchisement, abuse, murder, and eugenic extermination of autistic people, but they toned down their rhetoric to make their agenda a good deal less obvious to the uninformed observer. Autistic activist efforts like that flash blog had started to put a dent in their popularity and their bottom line—a small dent, but apparently enough to make them realize that times were a-changin’ and that it would be better for business if they made an effort to look and sound like something other than the hate group they are. As part of their rebranding, they took down that melodramatic “call for action” hate piece by their departed co-founder. So my “This Is Autism” piece has long outlasted the dreadful bit of garbage that first inspired it.

撰写《行动呼吁》的“自闭症之声”联合创始人于 2016 年去世。她离世后，“自闭症之声”立即启动了大规模品牌重塑。他们继续支持对孤独谱系群体的剥夺权利、虐待、谋杀和优生灭绝，但调整了措辞，使不明真相的观察者更难察觉其真实意图。孤独谱系活动人士发起的“闪博”等行动已开始削弱该组织的公众形象和盈利能力——虽然影响有限，但足以让他们意识到时代正在改变，为了商业利益，他们必须伪装成与仇恨组织不同的形象。作为品牌重塑的一部分，他们撤下了那位已故联合创始人撰写的煽动性《行动呼吁》仇恨文章。因此，我那篇《这就是孤独症》的回应文章，比最初激发它的那篇可憎垃圾文字存活得更久。







---


Nick_ebook-22










This Is Autism

这就是孤独症



It’s a bright cool Sunday in Berkeley, and when I step into my aikido dojo the sun is singing through the skylights, suffusing the big airy space and making shiny hot pools of white on the rich vibrant blue of the mat. That vibrant expanse of blue makes a low soft thrumming and gives me a feeling of warm wide open spaces behind me and in the lower part of my lungs. The sunlight sounds like a choir of angels, and together with the pleasantly humming mint-flavored whiteness of walls it makes my skin tingle and opens a luminous sky in my chest and all around my head. I inhale into that space and the cool air fills my head with exhilarating white-blue and brings new, higher harmonies into the choir.

在伯克利一个晴朗凉爽的周日，当我踏入合气道道场时，阳光透过天窗吟唱，充盈着宽敞通透的空间，在生机勃勃的深蓝色垫子上洒下耀眼的白热光斑。那片充满活力的蓝色发出低沉柔和的嗡鸣，让我感到身后和肺腑深处涌起温暖开阔的空间。阳光听起来像天使合唱团，与墙壁令人愉悦的薄荷白嗡鸣交织，令我的皮肤微微发麻，在胸腔和头颅四周点亮一片澄澈的天空。我向那片空间深深吸气，清凉的空气让我的脑海充满令人振奋的白蓝色，并为合唱团增添了新的、更高亢的和声。



There’s a moment of silence waiting for me at the top of the inhale, and just as I reach it I realize that another sound is happening, too, a grey-brown sound that rolls and tumbles like an otter in the blue-white river of sensation. This sound is incongruous and merits investigation, so as I begin to breathe out I do that trick that I learned to do when I was a real tiny kid, the trick that no one ever talked about and that I could never explain to anyone because, as I eventually learned long after I grew up, for most people it’s not a trick that they have to do, it’s just the way they are all the time. The trick where I filter and sort and separate the currents of the river until they resolve themselves into a world of discrete objects with names and meanings.

吸气到达顶点时，有一瞬静默在等我。就在触及那刻，我意识到还有另一种声响——灰褐色的声音，在蓝白交织的感知河流中翻滚腾跃，像只水獭。这声音格格不入，值得探究。于是呼气时，我使出了幼时学会的把戏——那个从未有人提及、我也始终无法向任何人解释的把戏。因为直到长大很久以后我才明白，对大多数人而言，这根本算不上什么把戏，不过是他们与生俱来的常态。这个把戏就是：将河流的湍流过滤、分类、分离，直到它们化作一个由名称与意义构成的离散世界。



Dojo, walls, blue mat on blonde wood floor. Seven of my aikido students in white gi, early arrivals for class, on the mat, stretching. The choir is still singing blue-white, the walls still have that minty tingle. Interpreting some of the currents and eddies of the river as discrete objects with names doesn’t make the river stop. The flow is always happening. The world of discrete objects and names is a part of the river, too, and it’s the part where most other people live by default. Me, I’m just visiting.

道场，墙壁，金色木地板上铺着蓝色垫子。我的七名合气道学生穿着白色道服，提前到达上课，正在垫子上拉伸。合唱团仍在唱着蓝白色的歌，墙壁仍带着那股薄荷般的刺痛感。将河流中的某些水流和漩涡解读为有名字的独立物体，并不会让河流停止流动。流动始终在发生。独立物体和名字的世界也是河流的一部分，而那是大多数其他人默认生活的地方。至于我，我只是个过客。



Once I’ve made the necessary shift in consciousness, it becomes clear to me that the grey-brown tumbling otter sound that got my attention was someone talking to me. A greeting, I think, from one of the students on the mat. Yes, he’s looking at me.

一旦我完成了必要的意识转换，我就明白了，那个引起我注意的灰褐色翻滚水獭般的声音，是有人在跟我说话。我想，是垫子上某个学生的问候。是的，他正看着我。



Quick mental checklist, made quicker by the fact that I don’t think in words and thus don’t have to go through it in a linear fashion. If it were a literal checklist, though, written out in words, it would go something like this:

快速的心理检查清单，因为我不以语言思考，所以不必线性地逐一检查，这使过程更快。但如果真要用文字写出来，这份清单大概会是这样：



Does his greeting call for a response on my part? Yes, definitely.

他的问候需要我回应吗？是的，毫无疑问。



Is he smiling? Yes.

他在微笑吗？是的。



Should I smile back? Yes.

我该回以微笑吗？是的。



Do I already happen to be smiling? Yes. How convenient!

我是否恰好已经在微笑了？是的。真巧！



Does this exchange of greetings also require speech on my part? Most likely.

这场问候的交换是否也需要我开口说话？极有可能。



Have I now taken so long to respond that there may be some potential social awkwardness to navigate? Probably not. In terms of clock time it’s only been a couple of seconds. A slightly longer pause than is usual for the ordinary rhythms of social conversation, but my students are quite accustomed to my pauses by now.

我是否已经拖延了太久才回应，以至于可能产生一些社交上的尴尬需要应对？大概不会。按时钟时间算，其实只过了几秒钟。比起日常社交对话的普通节奏，这停顿稍长了一些，但我的学生们早已习惯我的停顿了。



“Good Morning,” I say, smiling.

“早上好，”我微笑着说道。



I bow, because I’m entering the dojo, and one bows when one enters the dojo.

我鞠了一躬，因为我正走进道场，而进入道场时理应鞠躬。



It’s past noon by the clock, but I say Good Morning because I always say Good Morning. Yet another quirk to which my students are well accustomed.

时钟显示已过正午，但我依然说“早上好”，因为我总是说“早上好”。这不过是我的又一个怪癖，学生们对此也早已习以为常。



I like to remember that it’s always morning somewhere.

我喜欢提醒自己，总有一个地方正值清晨。



•



Julia and Zoe come to town. We meet on the porch of a Thai restaurant near my apartment in North Berkeley. Julia is taller than I expected. It is my intention to have Thai food for lunch, but Julia has not experienced Thai food and is reluctant to do so at this time.

朱莉娅和佐伊来到镇上。我们在北伯克利公寓附近一家泰国餐厅的门廊碰面。朱莉娅比我想象中更高。我本打算午餐吃泰国菜，但朱莉娅没尝过泰国菜，此刻对此有些犹豫。



There was a long period in my adolescence and young adulthood when I would have regarded Julia’s reluctance to eat Thai food as something that I should help her to overcome, by badgering her in the manner that I learned as a child from Sam I Am in Dr. Seuss’ Green Eggs and Ham. “Would you eat them in a box? Would you eat them with a fox?”

在我青春期和青年时期很长一段时间里，我会把朱莉娅对泰国菜的犹豫视为需要帮助她克服的障碍——就像我童年时从苏斯博士《绿鸡蛋和火腿》中山姆·艾姆学来的方式那样纠缠她：“你会不会在盒子里吃？你会不会和狐狸一起吃？”



Now, though, my years of immersion in the emergent autistic culture have deeply inculcated in me a rule that I think of as the Golden Rule of Neurodiversity: Respect the bodily, sensory, and cognitive needs of others as you would want your own to be respected, whether or not you understand the reasons for those needs.

然而如今，多年沉浸在新兴的孤独谱系文化中，我深深内化了一条准则——我称之为神经多样性的黄金法则：尊重他人的身体、感官和认知需求，如同你希望自己的需求被尊重一样，无论你是否理解这些需求背后的原因。



So I suggest an establishment across the street, that serves good cuisine of a more Euro-American variety. A place where Julia and Zoe can have pancakes with whipped cream for lunch, while I can have a large salad with some sort of spicy ginger dressing that satisfies my own sensory preferences. The noise and bad acoustics inside this establishment are unpleasant for all three of us, so we elect to sit at a table out on the sidewalk. Julia has found a small purplish flower somewhere, and she twirls, twirls, twirls it between her thumb and forefinger while we wait for our food. We all watch the flower, watch it spin, spin, spin.

于是我提议去街对面那家餐厅，那里提供更偏欧美风味的精致菜肴。朱莉娅和佐伊可以点浇着奶油的煎饼当午餐，而我则能享用一份配着辛辣姜汁酱料的大沙拉——这正合我的感官偏好。店内嘈杂的声响和糟糕的声学环境让我们三人都感到不适，于是我们选择坐在人行道边的餐桌旁。朱莉娅不知从哪儿捡到一朵淡紫色小花，等餐时她一直用拇指和食指捻着它旋转、旋转、旋转。我们全都盯着那朵花，看它转啊转啊转。



•



Kassiane comes to town. We lunch on delicious Thai food, on the porch of a Thai restaurant near my apartment in North Berkeley.

卡西安来到城里。我们在北伯克利公寓附近一家泰国餐厅的露台上，享用了美味的泰式午餐。



I’ve been reading Kassiane’s activist writings online for more than a dozen years. Her writing is fiery and powerful, the writing of someone who has learned well and truly that the consequences of standing up and pushing back hard against the forces of oppression are never as bad as the consequences of not pushing back. I know a lot of people who are scared of her. I regard her as a hero.

我在网上阅读卡西安的激进主义文章已有十多年。她的文字炽烈而有力，出自一个深谙真理之人——她真正明白，挺身反抗压迫势力的后果，永远比不反抗的后果要好。我知道很多人怕她。而我视她为英雄。



In person, Kassiane is smaller that I expected, and she has a white cat named Purkinje who rides on her shoulder. She looks ten years younger than her age, and her voice is soft and light, easy on the ears. She loves the color purple. I’ve seen photos of her with purple hair, but today it’s brown. She might or might not be wearing purple. I can’t tell. It doesn’t matter. Because everything she does is a beautiful bright purple. My brain processes her voice as purple, her movements as purple. She’s warm and friendly, and when she hugs me, she means it, and I feel like I’ve been enveloped by a purple glow.

见到卡西安本人时，她比我想象中娇小，肩上趴着一只名叫普尔金耶的白猫。她看起来比实际年龄年轻十岁，声音轻柔悦耳。她钟爱紫色。我看过她染紫发的照片，但今天她留着棕色头发。她或许穿着紫色，或许没有。我分辨不清。但这并不重要。因为她所做的一切都闪耀着美丽的亮紫色。我的大脑将她的声音感知为紫色，将她的动作感知为紫色。她温暖而友善，拥抱我时充满真诚，让我感觉自己被紫色的光芒包裹。



•



Riki comes to town. She knows the species, traits, and potential uses of every plant in the neighborhood. She smells of patchouli and walks with a cane, and my daughter loves her.

瑞奇来到镇上。她认得街坊邻里每一株植物的种类、特性与用途。身上散发着广藿香的气息，拄着手杖行走，我的女儿很喜欢她。



Riki spends hours fixing my out-of-commission electric scooter, taking it apart and putting it back together. It seems to me that she’s doing me a great favor working on my scooter, but from Riki’s perspective, I’m doing her a favor because she’s never had the opportunity to take this sort of scooter apart before. The whole time she works on the scooter, she talks to it like she’s a friendly veterinarian talking to an animal. She refuses to take a break to eat.

Riki 花了几个小时修理我那辆坏掉的电动滑板车，拆了又装。在我看来，她帮我修车是帮了我一个大忙，但从 Riki 的角度看，我反而帮了她——因为她以前从没机会拆开这种滑板车。整个修车过程中，她一直对着滑板车说话，就像友善的兽医在跟动物聊天。她不肯停下来吃饭。



Afterward, I take her out for Thai food.

之后，我带她去吃了泰国菜。



•



The youngest and most enthusiastic student in my aikido dojo, the girl is five years old and so small that even the smallest size of gi is adorably large on her.

我合气道道场里最年轻、最热情的学生是个五岁的小女孩，个子小到连最小号的道服穿在她身上都显得可爱地宽大。



She loves aikido. Like me, when I started my own aikido training at the age of twelve, she has a hard time learning the moves, but she keeps on working at it because she gets what the art is about, she appreciates its sublime beauty in a way that most people, so far as I can tell, don’t arrive at until they’ve been training for ten or twenty or thirty years.

她热爱合气道。就像我十二岁刚开始练习合气道时一样，她学动作很吃力，但她一直坚持练习，因为她理解这门武道的精髓——她能感受到它那超凡的美感，而据我所知，大多数人要练上十年、二十年甚至三十年才能领悟到这种境界。



That’s my secret, really. The secret to how I ended up as the senior instructor of a thriving aikido dojo. Most people assume that I had some sort of natural physical talent for it, but nothing could be further from the truth. The secret was that the beauty of the art touched me, that I could see from the beginning that its dance contained all the sublime subtle grace that I saw and loved in the flight of birds and the movement of the ocean’s waves. And even though I had no talent for the art at all, I wanted so much to feel what it was like to embody that grace, that I was willing to put in as much work as I had to in order to get there.

这就是我的秘密，真的。我之所以能成为一所蓬勃发展的合气道道场的高级教练，秘诀就在于此。大多数人以为我天生就有这方面的运动天赋，但事实恰恰相反。秘密在于，这门艺术的优美触动了我——从一开始，我就看出它的舞蹈中蕴含着那种我在鸟儿的飞翔和海洋波浪的律动中所看见并深爱的、崇高而微妙的优雅。尽管我毫无天赋，但我如此渴望去感受那种优雅化为自身一部分的滋味，以至于我愿意付出一切努力去达到那个境界。



More than three decades later, I’m still at it; I’ve gotten far enough now that I’ve had some first tastes of that grace, now and then in recent years, and it’s just served to whet my appetite.

三十多年过去了，我依然在坚持；如今我已走得足够远，在近些年里偶尔初尝了那种优雅的滋味，而这反而更激起了我的渴望。



This little girl can see the beauty, too. And today, before class starts, she can barely wait to talk to me. But she still remembers to stop and bow when she enters the dojo.

这个小女孩也能看见那份美。今天，在课程开始前，她几乎等不及要和我说话。但她依然记得在进入道场时停下来鞠躬。



After her bow, she comes bounding across the mat to me.

鞠躬之后，她蹦蹦跳跳地穿过垫子向我跑来。



“Hello, Sensei,” she says.

“你好，老师。”她说。



“Good Morning,” I say.

“早上好。”我回应道。



“Today is a special class!” She informs me, looking somewhere past my left shoulder. “Today is my fifty-third aikido class!”

“今天可是节特别的课！”她告诉我，目光越过我的左肩望向某处。“今天是我第五十三节合气道课！”



“Ah,” I say. I think for just a moment, then it comes to me. “That’s a prime, isn’t it?”

“啊，”我说。我略作思索，随即明白了。“那是个质数，对吧？”



“Yes!” she laughs, and bounds away across the blue mat, hands flapping.

“没错！”她笑着，双手拍打着，蹦跳着穿过蓝色垫子。







---


Nick_ebook-23










Comments on “This Is Autism”

关于《这就是孤独症》的评论



In 2012, while researching the massive tome that he would publish in 2015 under the title NeuroTribes, my friend Steve Silberman visited my dojo and watched me teach an aikido class. After the class was over, Steve interviewed me over dinner at the same Thai restaurant that’s featured in “This Is Autism.”

2012 年，我的朋友史蒂夫·西尔伯曼正在为他 2015 年出版的巨著《神经部落》做调研。期间他来到我的道场，观摩了我教授的一节合气道课程。课后，我们在《这就是孤独症》中提及的那家泰国餐厅共进晚餐，史蒂夫对我进行了采访。



At one point during out conversation, he remarked, “I think the way you do aikido has got to be the most sophisticated form of stimming I’ve ever seen.”

交谈中他说道："我认为你练习合气道的方式，是我见过最高级的自我刺激行为。"



“Exactly what I’ve been going for,” I said.

"这正是我追求的境界。"我回应道。



•



The Julia who appears in “This Is Autism” is the same one who put together the Loud Hands anthology for which I wrote the first version of “Throw Away the Master’s Tools.” In fact, the meeting described in “This Is Autism” was the 2011 meeting at which we discussed Loud Hands and I agreed to write something about the neurodiversity paradigm for it.

出现在《这就是孤独症》中的朱莉娅，正是那位编纂《响亮的手》文集的同一个人，我为该文集撰写了《扔掉主人的工具》的初版。事实上，《这就是孤独症》中描述的会议正是 2011 年那次讨论《响亮的手》的会议，当时我同意为文集撰写一篇关于神经多样性范式的文章。



•



The Kassiane who appears in “This Is Autism” is, of course, Kassiane Asasumasu, who’s mentioned a few times in this book because she coined the terms neurodivergent and neurodivergence. The moment described here was our first in-person meeting but not our last. She remains a friend, and dear to my heart. Sometime after “This Is Autism” was written, Kassiane began training an aikido dojo in her own hometown, joining the distinguished ranks of autistic aikido practitioners.

出现在《这就是孤独症》中的卡西安，自然就是卡西安·阿萨苏马苏。本书中多次提及她，因为她创造了"神经殊异"和"神经殊异性"这两个术语。文中描述的场景是我们首次见面，但绝非最后一次。她至今仍是我的挚友。在《这就是孤独症》成文后不久，卡西安开始在家乡开办合气道道场，加入了杰出的孤独谱系合气道练习者行列。



•



The Riki who appears in “This Is Autism” is my friend Riki Sarah Dennis. We’re both transgender autistic women and we went through the Transformative Studies doctoral program at California Institute of Integral Studies together. At the time of the visit recounted in “This Is Autism,” she’d only recently figured out she was autistic and I hadn’t yet figured out I was a woman. I supported her as best I could through her process of coming out as autistic, and a few years later she supported me as best she could through my process of coming out as transgender.

《这就是孤独症》中出现的里基是我的朋友里基·莎拉·丹尼斯。我们都是跨性别孤独谱系女性，曾一起在加州整合学院攻读转化研究博士项目。在《这就是孤独症》记述的那次拜访时，她刚意识到自己是孤独谱系不久，而我尚未意识到自己是女性。我竭尽全力支持她完成孤独谱系身份的自我认同过程，几年后她也同样全力支持我完成跨性别身份的自我认同过程。



•



These days my wife Azzia runs the youth program at our aikido dojo, and we both teach the adults. In both the youth classes and the adult classes, the majority of our students aren’t autistic, though at any given time we have at least a couple who are.

如今我的妻子阿齐亚在我们合气道道场负责青少年课程，我们共同教授成人班。无论是青少年班还是成人班，大部分学员并非孤独谱系，但任何时候都至少有两三位是孤独谱系者。



Which brings me to this word of advice I’d like to offer to parents of autistic kids, or any other adults with autistic kids in their care, who are considering aikido training or training in some other martial art as a way to support the kids’ long-term empowerment and well-being: please note that absolutely none of my aikido training has occurred in the context of any sort of “special” program or class designed specifically with autistics in mind. I began my aikido training in classes in which I was the only autistic participant. All of my training since then has occurred in settings that were not in an way designed for autistics, and in which either I was the only autistic or in which there were a couple of other autistics but we were still considerably in the minority.

这让我想给孤独谱系孩子的父母，或其他照顾孤独谱系孩子的成年人一句建议——如果你们正考虑让孩子学习合气道或其他武术，以此支持他们长期的成长与福祉：请注意，我所有的合气道训练经历，从未在任何专门为孤独谱系人士设计的“特殊”课程或班级中进行。我最初学习合气道时，是班上唯一的孤独谱系学员。此后的所有训练，也都在并非为孤独谱系人士设计的场合中进行——要么我是唯一的孤独谱系学员，要么虽有其他几位孤独谱系同伴，但我们始终是明显的少数群体。



I wouldn’t have had it any other way. From everything I’ve seen, programs of activity designed specially for autistics (at least when non-autistics have a hand in their design or implementation) seem to inevitably tend toward the paternalistic, toward condescension and lowered expectations, and toward incorporating and insidiously prioritizing agendas of normativity. There has been no time in my life at which I would have voluntarily subjected myself to the indignity of such a program; had I been forced to participate in one in my youth, my energies would have been focused entirely on resisting it and seeking to extricate myself. If my exposure to aikido had occurred in the context of such a program, instead of among non-autistic fellow students in a traditional dojo environment with the traditional goals, expectations, and teaching methodology, I wouldn’t have stuck with aikido and it’s unlikely that I’d be thriving as I am today.

我绝不会选择其他方式。根据我所见，专为孤独谱系人士设计的活动项目（至少当非孤独谱系人士参与设计或实施时）似乎不可避免地走向家长式作风，充满居高临下的态度和降低的期望，并暗中将规范化的议程置于优先地位。我一生中从未自愿屈尊参与过此类项目；若年少时被迫参加，我的全部精力都会用于反抗并设法脱身。如果我对合气道的接触发生在这样的项目中，而非在传统道场环境里与普通学员共同遵循传统目标、期望和教学法，我绝不会坚持练习合气道，更不可能像今天这样蓬勃发展。



When it comes to fostering autistic well-being through practices like martial arts, dance, theater, or what-have-you, the best long-term outcomes for autistics are achieved not through putting them in segregated “special” programs (ugh), but through their voluntary participation in systems and communities of practice in which they work side-by-side with their non-autistic fellow practitioners with no agenda except to work toward mastery of the practice for its own sake. That’s how I did my training, and that’s how we do it in my dojo today.

当通过武术、舞蹈、戏剧或其他实践来促进孤独谱系者的福祉时，最佳长期效果并非来自将他们安置在隔离的"特殊"项目（唉），而是通过他们自愿参与那些与非孤独谱系同伴并肩协作的实践体系与社群——在这里，唯一的目标就是为技艺本身而精进。这正是我当年接受训练的方式，也是如今我们道场遵循的准则。







---


Nick_ebook-24










For Parents of Autistic Children

给孤独谱系儿童家长的建议



This one was originally written in 2015 as the foreword to a book of short writings by autistic authors, compiled for parents of autistic children. That book is out of print now, and my foreword seems worth re-publishing here. It’s a nice little beginner-friendly piece and it’s one of the few things I’ve written so far that’s specifically addressed to non-autistic parents of autistic children.

本文最初写于 2015 年，是一本由孤独谱系作者撰写的短文集的前言，该书专为孤独谱系儿童的家长编纂。如今该书已绝版，但我的前言似乎值得在此重新发布。这是一篇适合初学者的温馨短文，也是我迄今为数不多的、专门写给孤独谱系儿童的非孤独谱系家长的作品之一。



Every good and loving parent in the world faces the same question every day: How do I help my child to thrive?

世上每一位充满爱与责任心的父母，每天都要面对同一个问题：我该如何帮助孩子茁壮成长？



Every time a truly good and loving parent makes any sort of parenting choice, however big or small—whether it’s choosing a school or choosing a bedtime story, choosing when to put a toddler down for a nap or choosing what rules and advice to give a teen about dating—that is the question we must answer as best we can, the question that guides our decisions, even if we never put it into words. How do I help my child to thrive?

每当一位真正充满爱与责任心的父母做出任何育儿选择时——无论大小，无论是选择学校还是选择睡前故事，是决定何时让幼儿小睡，还是为青少年提供关于约会的规则与建议——我们都必须尽力回答这个问题。这个问题指引着我们的每一个决定，即便我们从未将其诉诸言语。我该如何帮助孩子茁壮成长？



Any good parent can tell you that this question is endlessly challenging. No matter how many times we grapple with it and find what we hope is a good answer, a new situation is guaranteed to come along soon that requires us to grapple with it yet again and to find yet another answer. And sometimes we have to wait months or years or even decades to find out how good our answers were.

任何称职的父母都能告诉你，这个问题极具挑战性。无论我们多少次绞尽脑汁找到自以为满意的答案，新的状况总会接踵而至，迫使我们再次面对它，寻找新的解答。有时我们甚至要等待数月、数年乃至数十年，才能验证当初的答案是否足够好。



If your child is autistic, and you’re not autistic yourself, the question of how to help your child to thrive becomes a hundred times harder. But this is not because being autistic is in any way incompatible with thriving. Rest assured that autistic people can thrive, and do thrive. Autistic people, including your child, can have good lives full of joy and love and meaningful connection and creative fulfillment.

如果你的孩子是孤独谱系，而你自己并非孤独谱系，那么"如何帮助孩子茁壮成长"这个问题会变得难上百倍。但这绝非因为孤独谱系与幸福生活存在任何矛盾。请放心，孤独谱系群体完全可以——也确实正在——活出精彩人生。包括你的孩子在内的所有孤独谱系群体，都能拥有充满喜悦、爱意、真挚联结与创造性成就的美好人生。



So why is it so hard to determine how to help your autistic child to thrive? Most of the difficulty can be traced to three factors. The first factor is that your child’s sensory experience of the world is fundamentally different from yours, and the way your child’s mind works is fundamentally different from yours. So different that it may be nigh-impossible for you to imagine what your child experiences, senses, thinks, knows, or feels, or what your child is trying to communicate, or why your child is doing some particular thing . And this, of course, can make it quite difficult to figure out what your child needs. Fortunately, the insights of autistic adults can be of great help in this regard. Autistic adults have been there. They have insider knowledge.

那么，为何帮助你的孤独谱系孩子茁壮成长如此困难？大部分困难可归结为三个因素。第一个因素是：你孩子对世界的感官体验与你截然不同，其思维运作方式也与你迥异。这种差异之大，以至于你几乎无法想象孩子所经历、感知、思考、认知或感受的一切，无法理解孩子试图表达的内容，也无法明白孩子为何做出某些特定行为。这自然使得判断孩子的需求变得异常艰难。幸运的是，成年孤独谱系个体的见解在这方面能提供巨大帮助。他们曾身处其中，拥有来自内部的认知。



The second factor is that there’s so much misinformation and bad advice about autism out there. Many of the standard “expert” or “professional” approaches to autism are badly misguided and rooted in ignorance. For instance, there are certain “therapies” that are widely recommended for autistic children but that are actually harmful and traumatizing. When so many of the “experts” are so utterly wrong and so confident in their prejudices and misinformation, it’s hard to know who to listen to. Here, again, the insights and insider knowledge of autistic adults are invaluable.

第二个因素是，关于孤独谱系存在大量错误信息和糟糕建议。许多所谓的"专家"或"专业"方法对孤独谱系的理解严重偏离正轨，且根植于无知。例如，某些被广泛推荐给孤独谱系儿童的"疗法"实际上具有伤害性并会造成心理创伤。当如此多的"专家"完全错误，却又对自己的偏见和错误信息深信不疑时，人们很难知道该听信谁。在此，成年孤独谱系个体的洞察与内行知识再次显得弥足珍贵。



The third factor is that because the minds, interests, experiences, abilities, and needs of autistic people are different from those of non-autistic people, thriving also looks different in autistic people than it does in non-autistic people. Health, happiness, success, personal fulfillment, good relationships, psychological well-being, a high quality of life—all of these things are possible for autistic people, including your child, but the autistic versions of these things are often quite different from the non-autistic versions.

第三个因素是，由于孤独谱系群体的思维、兴趣、经历、能力和需求与非孤独谱系个体存在差异，他们实现蓬勃发展的方式也与非孤独谱系个体截然不同。健康、幸福、成功、个人成就感、良好的人际关系、心理健康、高品质生活——所有这些对孤独谱系群体（包括您的孩子）而言都是可能实现的，但属于孤独谱系版本的这些事物往往与非孤独谱系版本大相径庭。



When you’re trying to help a “typical” child to thrive, the society in which you live provides you with many models of what a thriving child looks like, and many models of successful, thriving adulthood. These models provide some idea of what you’re aiming for, some idea of what you want to help your child to become. But parents rarely have access to models of what a thriving autistic child looks like, or a successful, thriving autistic adult. So how do you know if your autistic child is on the right track, developmentally, when the “right track” for your child might be vastly different from the established societal standards of what the right track looks like?

当你试图帮助一个“典型”儿童茁壮成长时，你所处的社会会提供许多关于茁壮成长儿童的模样，以及成功、茁壮成长的成年人的范例。这些范例让你对目标有所认知，也让你明白希望帮助孩子成为什么样的人。但父母很少能接触到关于茁壮成长的孤独谱系儿童或成功、茁壮成长的孤独谱系成年人的范例。那么，当你的孤独谱系孩子的发展“正确轨道”可能与既定的社会标准大相径庭时，你又如何判断孩子是否走在正确的发展轨道上呢？



Most non-autistic “experts” are unhelpful about this sort of thing, because they regard autism as intrinsically unhealthy, intrinsically a “wrong track.” Most non-autistic “experts” think that key to helping an autistic person thrive is to try to make them non-autistic, or to try to make them as indistinguishable from a non-autistic person as possible. Making an autistic person into a non-autistic person simply can’t be done (though sadly, many parents fall prey to unscrupulous quacks and cultish organizations selling phony and expensive “treatments” for autism). And trying to make an autistic person outwardly indistinguishable from a non-autistic person ultimately does the autistic person far more harm than good.

大多数非孤独谱系的“专家”对此类问题毫无助益，因为他们将孤独谱系视为本质上不健康、本质上是“错误轨道”的存在。这些非孤独谱系“专家”认为，帮助孤独谱系者茁壮成长的关键在于试图让他们变得非孤独谱系，或尽可能让他们与非孤独谱系者毫无区别。将孤独谱系者变成非孤独谱系者根本不可能实现（遗憾的是，许多家长仍会落入兜售虚假昂贵“疗法”的无良庸医和邪教组织的陷阱）。而试图让孤独谱系者在外表上与非孤独谱系者毫无区别，最终对孤独谱系者造成的伤害远大于益处。



So when it comes to the question of what the path to a good life might look like for your autistic child, autistic adults can yet again offer crucial insight, and can also serve as examples of what’s possible. Most of us had a hard time getting to the point where we were thriving, and many of us are still recovering from the hard times we had. We want the next generation of autistic children, including your child, to have an easier time. Like you, we want your child to thrive.

因此，当谈及你的孤独谱系孩子通往美好生活的道路可能是什么样子时，成年孤独谱系个体再次提供了关键见解，并可作为可能性范本。我们中的大多数人都曾历经艰难才达到茁壮成长的状态，许多人至今仍在从过往的困境中恢复。我们希望包括你的孩子在内的下一代孤独谱系儿童能拥有更顺遂的成长历程。与你一样，我们也期盼你的孩子能够蓬勃发展。







---


Nick_ebook-25










Autism and the

Pathology Paradigm

孤独症与病理学范式



This little essay started out as an excerpt from my doctoral dissertation proposal. In 2016 I revised it so that it would stand well enough on its own, and posted it on the Neurocosmopolitanism website. It’s written in formal enough language that quotes from it can fit nicely into academic papers, so it’s one of those pieces that a lot of students and academic-types have found useful.

这篇短文最初是我博士论文提案中的一段摘录。2016 年我对其进行了修订，使其能够独立成篇，并发布在神经世界主义网站上。文章采用了足够正式的语言，其中的引文可以很好地融入学术论文中，因此成为许多学生和学术研究者觉得有用的作品之一。



Discourse and education on autism, in the academic and professional realms, has thus far been dominated by what I have termed the pathology paradigm. At the root of the pathology paradigm is the assumption that there is one “right” style of human neurocognitive functioning. Variations in neurocognitive functioning that diverge substantially from socially constructed standards of “normal”—including the variations that constitute autism—are framed within this paradigm as medical pathologies, as deficits, damage, or “disorders.”

迄今为止，在学术和专业领域，关于孤独症的论述和教育一直被我称之为"病理学范式"所主导。病理学范式的根源在于假设存在一种"正确"的人类神经认知功能模式。那些与社会建构的"正常"标准存在显著差异的神经认知功能变异——包括构成孤独谱系的变异——在此范式下被框定为医学病理、缺陷、损伤或"障碍"。



In recent years a new paradigm has begun to emerge, which I refer to as the neurodiversity paradigm. The term neurodiversity, coined in the 1990s, refers to the diversity of human minds—the variations in neurocognitive functioning that manifest within the human species.
