Within the neurodiversity paradigm, neurodiversity is understood to be a form of human diversity that is subject to social dynamics—including the dynamics of oppression and systemic social power inequalities—similar to those dynamics that commonly occur around other forms of human diversity such as racial diversity or diversity of gender and sexual orientation.

近年来，一种新的范式开始浮现，我称之为神经多样性范式。神经多样性这一术语诞生于 20 世纪 90 年代，指的是人类心智的多样性——即人类物种内部神经认知功能的变异。在神经多样性范式下，神经多样性被视为人类多样性的一种形式，它受到社会动态的影响——包括压迫动态和系统性社会权力不平等——类似于围绕种族多样性、性别与性取向多样性等其他人类多样性形式常见的动态。



Through the lens of the neurodiversity paradigm, the pathology paradigm’s medicalized framing of autism and various other constellations of neurological, cognitive, and behavioral characteristics as “disorders” or “conditions” can be seen for what it is: a social construction rooted in cultural norms and social power inequalities, rather than a “scientifically objective” description of reality.

通过神经多样性范式的视角，病理学范式将孤独谱系及各种神经、认知和行为特征集合医学化为“障碍”或“病症”的做法，其本质便昭然若揭：这是一种植根于文化规范和社会权力不平等的社会建构，而非对现实的“科学客观”描述。



The choice to frame the minds, bodies, and lives of autistic people (or any other neurological minority group) in terms of pathology does not represent an inevitable and objective scientific conclusion, but is merely a cultural value judgment. Similar pathologizing frameworks have been used time and again to lend an aura of scientific legitimacy to all manner of other bigotry, and to the oppression of women, indigenous peoples, people of color, and queer people, among others. The framing of autism and other minority neurological configurations as disorders or medical conditions begins to lose its aura of scientific authority and “objectivity” when viewed in this historical context—when one remembers, for instance, that homosexuality was classified as a mental disorder in the American Psychiatric Association’s Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders (DSM) well into the 1970s; or that in the Southern United States, for some years prior to the American Civil War, the desire of slaves to escape from slavery was diagnosed by some white Southern physicians as a medical “disorder” called drapetomania.

将孤独谱系群体（或任何其他神经少数群体）的心灵、身体与生活框定为病理现象，并非不可避免的客观科学结论，而仅仅是一种文化价值判断。类似的病理化框架曾反复被用来为各种偏见披上科学合法性的外衣，并用于压迫女性、原住民、有色人种及性少数群体等。当我们将孤独症及其他少数神经构造被定义为障碍或医学状况的框架置于历史语境中审视时——例如，美国精神病学会《精神障碍诊断与统计手册》（DSM）直至 20 世纪 70 年代仍将同性恋列为精神障碍；或美国内战前数年，美国南部一些白人医生将奴隶逃离奴役的愿望诊断为名为"漂泊癖"的医学"障碍"——这种框架的"科学权威"与"客观性"光环便开始褪色。



At this time, sadly, the pathologization of autistic minds, bodies, and lives still has not been widely recognized—especially not within the academic and professional mainstream—as being yet another manifestation of this all-too-familiar form of institutionalized oppression and othering. The academic and professional discourse on autism, and the miseducation on autism given to each new generation of professionals, remain uncritically mired in the assumptions of the pathology paradigm. And since bad assumptions and unexamined prejudices inevitably become self-reinforcing when mistaken for facts, this entrenchment in the pathology paradigm has kept autism-related theory, praxis, and education stuck in a self-perpetuating cycle of ignorance and bigotry.

遗憾的是，时至今日，将孤独谱系者的心智、身体与生活病理化的做法，仍未得到广泛认知——尤其在学术与专业主流领域——这不过是这种司空见惯的制度化压迫与异化现象的又一体现。关于孤独谱系的学术与专业论述，以及向每一代新晋专业人士灌输的关于孤独谱系的错误教育，仍不加批判地深陷于病理范式的假设之中。由于错误的假设与未经审视的偏见一旦被误认为事实，便会不可避免地自我强化，这种对病理范式的固守，使得与孤独谱系相关的理论、实践与教育，始终困于无知与偏见的自我循环之中。



A proper accounting of the devastating consequences of this ignorance and bigotry, both for autistic persons and for society, would fill many pages and would be beyond the intended scope of this brief essay. However, for the benefit of those readers less familiar with the realm of autism-related professional and institutional praxis, a brief summary of the general shape of the situation is in order. The crux of the matter is that the neurodiversity paradigm is fundamentally in alignment with the social model of disability (disability understood as the result of failures of accommodation, societal attitudes, and systemic barriers, which conflict with the needs, traits, and abilities of specific groups and individuals); whereas the pathology paradigm is inextricably entwined with the medical model of disability (disability attributed exclusively to medicalized defects located within the disabled individual, with the implicit assumption that status quo societal norms are more or less “right” and “natural” and that having traits and needs that are incompatible with those norms constitutes a personal deficiency).

要完整记录这种无知与偏见对孤独谱系人士及社会造成的毁灭性后果，需要大量篇幅，远超这篇简短文章的范围。不过，为了让那些不太熟悉孤独症相关专业及机构实践的读者了解情况，有必要简要概述当前局势的总体面貌。问题的核心在于：神经多样性范式从根本上与社会残障模式（将残障理解为环境适应失败、社会态度及系统性障碍与特定群体及个体的需求、特质及能力相冲突的结果）保持一致；而病理范式则与医疗残障模式（将残障完全归因于残障个体内部的医学化缺陷，隐含假设现状社会规范或多或少是"正确"和"自然"的，而拥有与这些规范不相容的特质和需求则构成个人缺陷）密不可分。



The near-total dominance of the pathology paradigm (and thus of the medical model of disability) in the discourse on autism means that autism-related professional and institutional praxis is overwhelmingly dominated by a focus on “fixing” autistic persons—i.e., trying to make them non-autistic—at the expense of any significant focus on societal acceptance of autism, accommodation of autistic needs, removal of systemic barriers to access and inclusion, or supporting autistic persons in thriving as autistic persons. Further, since it is not actually possible to make an autistic person into a non-autistic person, the focus on this goal has inevitably served to generate nothing but absurd pseudoscience, quackery, and horrifying abuses.

病理学范式（以及残障的医疗模式）在关于孤独谱系的论述中几乎占据绝对主导地位，这意味着与孤独谱系相关的专业和机构实践压倒性地聚焦于"修复"孤独谱系个体——即试图让他们变得非孤独谱系——而严重忽视了社会对孤独谱系的接纳、满足孤独谱系需求、消除获取资源和融入社会的系统性障碍，或支持孤独谱系个体作为孤独谱系者茁壮成长。此外，由于实际上不可能将孤独谱系个体转变为非孤独谱系个体，这种目标导向的实践不可避免地只会催生荒谬的伪科学、江湖骗术和骇人听闻的虐待行为。



The worst and most widespread abuses have been those perpetrated under the guise of “behavioral therapies” (e.g., Applied Behavior Analysis, or ABA), which have been used to torture and traumatize two generations of autistic children, and which remain popular with parents and professionals despite the warnings of autistic adult survivors. The popularity of these abusive “behavioral therapies” can be traced directly to the focus on the impossible goal of making autistic persons into non-autistic persons, a goal implicitly mandated by the pathology paradigm. Behaviorism circumvents the impossibility of this goal by pretending that superficial outward compliance with specified non-autistic behavioral norms is the same thing as “recovery from autism,” while ignoring the long-term psychological costs of such compliance and of the abusive methods used to attain it.

最严重且最普遍的虐待行为，是那些打着“行为疗法”（例如应用行为分析，即 ABA）旗号所实施的。这些疗法已被用于折磨并创伤两代孤独谱系儿童，尽管成年孤独谱系幸存者不断发出警告，却仍深受家长和专业人士的青睐。这些虐待性“行为疗法”之所以流行，直接源于其聚焦于一个不可能实现的目标——将孤独谱系者转变为非孤独谱系者，而这一目标正是病理范式所隐含的强制要求。行为主义通过假装表面上的、符合特定非孤独谱系行为规范的外在顺从等同于“从孤独症中康复”，从而回避了这一目标的不可能性，同时却忽视了这种顺从以及为达成顺从所采用的虐待性方法所带来的长期心理代价。



The dominance of the pathology paradigm makes the proliferation of such abuses inevitable. Only a fundamental shift in the discourse—a shift from the pathology paradigm to the neurodiversity paradigm—is likely to create any substantial improvement in the realm of autism-related praxis.

病理范式的统治地位使得此类虐待行为的泛滥不可避免。唯有在话语层面实现根本性转变——从病理范式转向神经多样性范式——才有可能在孤独谱系相关实践领域带来实质性的改善。







---


Nick_ebook-26










Making the Shift to the

Neurodiversity Paradigm

转向神经多样性范式



In 2020, my esteemed friend and colleague Dora M. Raymaker conducted an extensive interview with me via email which was eventually published in the academic journal Autism in Adulthood (vol. 3, no. 1) in March of 2021 under the title, “Toward a Neuroqueer Future: An Interview with Nick Walker.” This piece is a revised version of one brief passage from that interview.

2020 年，我尊敬的友人与同事多拉·M·雷梅克通过电子邮件对我进行了深度访谈，该访谈最终于 2021 年 3 月发表在学术期刊《成年孤独症》（第 3 卷第 1 期）上，题为《迈向神经酷儿未来：尼克·沃克访谈录》。本文即是对该访谈中一段简短内容的修订版本。



As I see it, the long-term aim of our work is a cultural paradigm shift: a widespread supplanting of the pathology paradigm by the neurodiversity paradigm. For those who want to be a part of making this happen, there’s a set of practices we’ll need to cultivate rigorously in the years to come.

在我看来，我们工作的长期目标是实现文化范式的转变：让神经多样性范式广泛取代病理学范式。对于希望参与推动这一变革的人们而言，未来数年我们需要严格践行一系列实践准则。



First, we’ll need to be absolutely clear—in our own minds and in our written and spoken discourse—that the pathology paradigm is nothing more than institutionalized bigotry masquerading as science, and that it’s illegitimate and harmful in the same sort of ways as racism, misogyny, and other forms of bigotry that have also historically masqueraded as science.

首先，我们必须彻底认清——无论在我们自己的认知中，还是在书面与口头论述中——病理学范式不过是披着科学外衣的制度化偏见，其危害性与非法性堪比种族主义、厌女症及其他历史上同样曾伪装成科学的偏见形式。



Second, we’ll need to train ourselves to recognize the pathology paradigm in all its myriad manifestations. The nature of any culture’s dominant paradigms is that they’re so pervasive that they become normalized to the point of invisibility for anyone raised within that culture. This is why so many people fail to recognize sexism or racism when it’s happening right in front of them. Waking up and learning to see the pathology paradigm is like waking up and learning to see any other form of systemic oppression. When we hear someone refer to autism as a “disorder” or “condition,” it should instantly set off the same sort of alarm bells in our minds as hearing someone refer to homosexuality as a “disorder” or refer to a member of some specific ethnic group as “inferior.” A pathology paradigm phrase like “individuals with autism” should register with us as inappropriate in the same way that we intuitively recognize that there’s something wrong with the phrase “individuals with homosexuality.”

其次，我们需要训练自己识别病理学范式及其无数表现形式。任何文化的主流范式都具有这样的特性：它们无处不在，以至于在该文化中成长的人将其视为常态，甚至难以察觉。这就是为什么许多人在性别歧视或种族主义发生在眼前时却视而不见。觉醒并学会识别病理学范式，就像觉醒并学会识别其他形式的系统性压迫一样。当我们听到有人将孤独症称为"障碍"或"病症"时，这应该立即在我们脑海中触发与听到有人将同性恋称为"障碍"或将某个特定族裔成员称为"低等"时同样的警报。像"孤独症患者"这样的病理学范式用语，应该让我们意识到其不当性，就像我们直觉上能识别出"同性恋患者"这种说法有问题一样。



Third, we’ll need to get a lot better about holding the boundary that the pathology paradigm is every bit as unacceptable as any other form of bigotry. And yes, this means rejecting almost all autism-related discourse and research produced over the past 90 years or so. I’m all for that. Up until the 1970s, nearly all scholarship pertaining to homosexuality framed it as a mental disorder, and professional practice was geared toward figuring out its causes, treating it, and/or preventing it. Sound familiar? In 1960, it would’ve been unthinkable to most psychologists to throw out every bit of scholarship and practice that stigmatized homosexuality and treated it as a pathology. And yet, over the past few decades, the academic and professional mainstream has done exactly that—and the results have been entirely beneficial.

第三，我们需要更严格地守住底线：病理学范式与其他任何形式的偏见一样不可接受。是的，这意味着要摒弃过去约 90 年间几乎所有与孤独症相关的论述和研究。我完全支持这一点。直到 20 世纪 70 年代，几乎所有关于同性恋的学术研究都将其视为精神障碍，专业实践也致力于探究其成因、治疗和/或预防。听起来很熟悉吧？在 1960 年，大多数心理学家根本无法想象要抛弃所有将同性恋污名化、视为病理的学术成果与实践。然而在过去几十年里，学术界和专业主流恰恰做到了这一点——而结果完全是积极的。



Today, if a psychology professor at a major university gave a lecture that advocated “curing homosexuality,” there’d be an outcry and likely an administrative reprimand. If a researcher wrote an article framing homosexuality as a medical pathology and advocating for gay conversion therapy, and submitted it to a journal dedicated to queer studies or LGBTQ health, it would be sternly rejected. And yet, even universities that put on a public show of embracing neurodiversity are still willing to employ faculty who speak of autistic people in pathologizing terms and advocate subjecting autistic children to abusive conversion therapy techniques like Applied Behavior Analysis—and that same sort of bigotry is still blithely published by academic journals and academic publishing imprints.

如今，若某知名大学的心理学教授在讲座中鼓吹"治愈同性恋"，必将引发强烈抗议，甚至可能受到行政处分。若某研究者撰写论文将同性恋定义为医学病理并主张进行扭转治疗，投稿至酷儿研究或 LGBTQ 健康领域的期刊，定会遭到严词拒稿。然而，即便是那些公开标榜拥抱神经多样性的大学，仍会聘用那些以病理化语言描述孤独谱系群体、主张对孤独谱系儿童实施应用行为分析等虐待性扭转疗法的教职人员——而学术期刊与出版社竟仍对这类偏见言论照单全收。



This sort of thing will continue as long as we allow it to continue—and we don’t have to allow it to continue. Overt homophobia and racism are becoming increasingly unacceptable and difficult to get away with in mainstream academic discourse these days, and that’s a positive development which began with relatively small groups of people in academia deciding that they weren’t going to silently accept that sort of thing anymore. Challenging oppressive discourses is an uphill battle at first, but I take heart when I look at how much the academic discourse on homosexuality has shifted during my own lifetime. We can do this.

只要我们允许这种情况继续存在，它就会持续下去——而我们不必容忍它继续存在。如今，公开的恐同和种族主义在主流学术话语中正变得越来越不可接受，也越来越难以蒙混过关，这是一个积极的进展，始于学术界中相对小规模的一群人决定不再默默忍受这类现象。挑战压迫性话语起初是一场艰苦的战斗，但当我看到在我有生之年，关于同性恋的学术话语发生了多么巨大的转变时，我备受鼓舞。我们能做到。







---


Nick_ebook-27










The Story Behind

“Neurotypical Psychotherapists & Autistic Clients”

“神经典型心理治疗师与孤独谱系来访者”背后的故事



Since 2010, I’ve been a faculty member at California Institute of Integral Studies, a school known for its excellent Counseling Psychotherapy graduate programs. Most of the grad students in my classes are in training to become psychotherapists, and many of the students in my undergraduate classes are also headed in that direction.

自 2010 年起，我一直在加州整合研究学院任教，这所学校以其卓越的心理咨询与治疗研究生项目而闻名。我课堂上的大多数研究生都在接受心理治疗师的培训，而本科班上的许多学生也正朝着这个方向发展。



By 2014, largely as a result of the essays on my website getting shared and discussed on social media, interest in my work had expanded beyond the autistic community and I was getting requests for consultation from psychotherapists and other professionals. I occupied an unusual niche, as someone who was both autistic and knowledgeable in the ways of psychotherapy (there are more people sharing that niche with me these days then there were back then, but not as many as I hope to see eventually). Some of the professionals who contacted me encouraged me to write up some guidelines for working with autistic clients.

到 2014 年，由于我网站上的文章在社交媒体上被广泛分享和讨论，人们对我的工作的兴趣已超越孤独谱系社群，我开始收到心理治疗师及其他专业人士的咨询请求。我占据了一个独特的位置——既是孤独谱系人士，又精通心理治疗之道（如今与我共享这一位置的人比当年更多，但尚未达到我期望的规模）。一些联系我的专业人士鼓励我撰写一些与孤独谱系来访者工作的指导原则。



What finally helped me get around to writing such a thing was an email from Sarah Coenen and Helen Cha-Choe, a pair of Counseling Psychotherapy grad students at California Institute of Integral Studies. I’d never met them, but Sarah and Helen were taking a Research Methods course taught by my friend and colleague Eri Çela. As their final project for that class, they wanted to research the attitudes of neurotypical psychotherapists toward autistic clients, and how those attitudes affected the quality of their work with those clients. Eri pointed them in my direction. They went to my website and read “Throw Away the Master’s Tools” and “Neurodiversity: Some Basic Terms & Definitions,” then contacted me with some follow-up questions.

最终促使我着手撰写这样一篇文章的，是来自加州整合研究院心理咨询与治疗专业的两位研究生——莎拉·科南和海伦·查乔——的一封邮件。我从未见过她们，但莎拉和海伦正在修读我朋友兼同事埃里·切拉教授的研究方法课程。作为该课程的期末项目，她们希望研究神经典型心理治疗师对孤独谱系来访者的态度，以及这些态度如何影响其与来访者的工作质量。埃里建议她们联系我。她们访问了我的网站，阅读了《扔掉大师的工具》和《神经多样性：基本术语与定义》两篇文章，随后联系我提出了一些后续问题。



I was delighted to learn that their project was grounded in the neurodiversity paradigm. Sarah and Helen recognized that the capacity of non-autistic professionals to work well with autistic clients was a form of cultural competency, and that the pathology paradigm constituted an obstacle to such competency and engendered condescending and unempathic attitudes toward autistic clients. Their clear understanding of the topic, and their excellent questions, inspired me to answer them at length. Having done so, I realized I’d finally managed to write the sort of advice to professionals that folks had been asking me to write. So in December of 2014 I put my answers to Sarah and Helen’s questions up on my website, and now I’m reprinting it here.

我很高兴得知他们的项目基于神经多样性范式。莎拉和海伦认识到，非孤独谱系专业人士与孤独谱系客户良好合作的能力是一种文化能力，而病理范式则构成了这种能力的障碍，并导致对孤独谱系客户产生居高临下和缺乏共情的态度。他们对这一主题的清晰理解以及提出的出色问题，促使我详细作答。在完成回答后，我意识到自己终于写出了人们一直要求我撰写的那种给专业人士的建议。于是，2014 年 12 月，我将对莎拉和海伦问题的回答发布在我的网站上，现在在此重新刊印。



In my answer to the second question, there’s a bit where I say “Listen to autistic people, and read what we write,” and then I list a few essential readings. I’ve edited the online version a few times over the years to update the list of readings I recommend, because new stuff keeps coming along that’s better than the old stuff. Unfortunately, I won’t be able to do that with the list in this version of the piece, because, well, it’s printed in a book. The small handful of readings I’ve recommended in this version are so good that I’m confident they’ll remain relevant for a long time, but I’m also confident that more great material that I want to recommend to psychotherapists working with autistic clients will come along in the years after this book is published.

在回答第二个问题时，我提到"请倾听孤独谱系群体的声音，阅读我们的文字"，随后列举了几篇必读文献。多年来我多次修订网络版中的推荐书单，因为不断有更优质的新作涌现。遗憾的是，本书印刷版中的书单无法同步更新——毕竟它已付梓成书。虽然当前版本推荐的少量文献质量上乘，足以经得起时间考验，但我确信在本书出版后的岁月里，还会有更多值得推荐给从事孤独谱系来访者心理治疗工作的优秀作品问世。







---


Nick_ebook-28










Neurotypical Psychotherapists & Autistic Clients

神经典型心理治疗师与孤独谱系来访者



Q: How would you address empathy deficits and poor communication skills in neurotypical people working with autistic clients?

问：您如何看待与孤独谱系来访者共事时，神经典型人群在共情缺陷和沟通技巧不足方面的问题？



The 20th Century political scientist Karl Deutsch said, “Power is the ability not to have to learn.”

20 世纪政治学家卡尔·多伊奇曾言："权力就是不必学习的特权。"



I quote this statement often, because I think it’s one of the most important truths ever articulated about privilege, oppression, and social power relations.

我常引用这句话，因为它揭示了关于特权、压迫与社会权力关系的最重要真理之一。



When a social system is set up such that one particular group is almost always in a position of social power or privilege over another group, the members of the privileged group never truly need to learn or practice empathy or understanding for the members of the disempowered, oppressed group. Nor do the members of the privileged group need to learn to adapt to the communication style of the oppressed group.

当一个社会系统的构建使得某一特定群体几乎总是处于对另一群体的社会权力或特权地位时，特权群体的成员永远不需要真正学习或实践对弱势、受压迫群体的同理心或理解。特权群体的成员也无需学习适应受压迫群体的沟通方式。



Neurotypical privilege means that neurotypical people interacting with autistic people—particularly when the neurotypical people in question are in positions of professional authority—have the luxury of never having to address or even acknowledge their own empathy deficits or poor communication skills, because they can blame all failures of empathy, understanding, and communication on the alleged deficits of the autistic people.

神经典型特权意味着，神经典型人士在与孤独谱系群体互动时——尤其是当这些神经典型人士处于专业权威地位时——他们享有永远不必正视甚至承认自身同理心缺陷或沟通能力不足的奢侈，因为他们可以将所有同理心、理解和沟通的失败归咎于孤独谱系群体所谓的缺陷。



Anthropologist Mary Catherine Bateson, writing about learning and power relations in colonialism, observed that “People who don’t wear shoes learn the languages of people who do, not vice versa.”

人类学家玛丽·凯瑟琳·贝特森在论述殖民主义中的学习与权力关系时指出："不穿鞋的人会学习穿鞋者的语言，反之则不然。"



Bateson’s wording of this insight is especially resonant for the autistic community: when autistic activists object to the pathologization and abuse of autistic children by neurotypical parents and professionals, or the murder of autistic children by neurotypical parents, neurotypicals often attempt to silence us by condescendingly admonishing us to “put ourselves in the shoes” of the perpetrators. Yet as neurodiversity activist Kassiane Asasumasu has pointed out, not only do these same neurotypical parents and professionals never seriously attempt to put themselves in the shoes of autistic people, they do not even “acknowledge that we have shoes,” metaphorically speaking.

贝特森对这一洞见的表述对孤独谱系群体尤为共鸣：当孤独谱系活动家反对神经典型父母和专业人士对孤独谱系儿童的病理化与虐待，或反对神经典型父母杀害孤独谱系儿童时，神经典型者常以居高临下的姿态告诫我们要"设身处地"为施害者着想，试图以此让我们噤声。然而正如神经多样性活动家卡西安娜·阿萨苏马苏所指出的，这些神经典型父母和专业人士不仅从未认真尝试设身处地理解孤独谱系群体，甚至隐喻性地"连我们是否有鞋穿都不予承认"。



Power—or privilege, as we now more commonly call the particular kind of power to which Deutsch was referring—is the ability not to have to learn. There’s a phrase, “check your privilege,” that’s often repeated but is rarely understood or heeded by those privileged persons at whom it is directed. If we start from Deutsch’s definition of power or privilege as the ability not to have to learn, we can understand “check your privilege” to mean, at least in part, “Learn! Be quiet, pay attention, and learn. Learn, even though the learning process, and the level of profound humility it requires, is going to be uncomfortable. Learn even though, because of your privilege, this sort of learning and humility is a discomfort that you have the luxury of being able to avoid—a luxury that we didn’t have, when we had to learn your ways. Learn even though you don’t have to.”

权力——或者用我们现在更常说的“特权”，即多伊奇所指的那种特殊权力——就是不必学习的特权。有句常被提及却鲜少被特权者理解或遵循的话：“审视你的特权”。若从多伊奇对权力或特权的定义出发，将其理解为不必学习的特权，那么“审视你的特权”至少部分意味着：“去学习！保持安静，专注倾听，去学习。即便学习过程及其所需的深切谦卑令人不适，也要学习。即便因你的特权，这种学习与谦卑带来的不适是你本可回避的奢侈——这种奢侈是我们当初学习你们的方式时不曾拥有的——也要学习。即便你本不必如此，也要学习。”



Unfortunately, as members of all oppressed groups discover, most privileged people just won’t do that. The states of profound mindfulness, humility, openness to correction, and tolerance for uncertainty that such learning demands are too far outside of most people’s comfort zones. Most human beings simply won’t go that far outside of their comfort zones if they don’t have to. And privilege means they don’t have to.

不幸的是，正如所有受压迫群体成员所发现的那样，大多数特权人士根本不会这样做。这种学习所需的深度正念、谦逊、对纠正的开放态度以及对不确定性的容忍，远远超出了大多数人的舒适区。如果不必如此，大多数人根本不会走出舒适区这么远。而特权意味着他们不必这样做。



The system is currently set up so that when neurotypical professionals work with autistic individuals, the neurotypical professional is always in the role of greater authority: neurotypical therapist and autistic client; neurotypical doctor and autistic patient; neurotypical educator and autistic student; neurotypical researcher and autistic subject.

当前系统的设置是，当神经典型专业人士与孤独谱系个体合作时，神经典型专业人士始终处于更高权威的角色：神经典型治疗师与孤独谱系来访者；神经典型医生与孤独谱系患者；神经典型教育者与孤独谱系学生；神经典型研究者与孤独谱系研究对象。



As long as this is the case, as long as neurotypical professionals only have regular, close contact with autistic individuals in situations that are set up such that the neurotypical professionals hold greater authority and power, the neurotypical professionals will never have to subject themselves to the uncomfortable humility of checking their privilege, will never have to learn real empathy and understanding for the autistic, and will never have to learn to understand and adapt to autistic forms of communication.

只要情况如此——只要神经典型专业人士仅在自身拥有更高权威和权力的情境下，与孤独谱系个体保持规律性密切接触——他们就永远无需承受审视自身特权的谦卑不适，永远无法真正学会对孤独谱系者的共情与理解，也永远无法习得适应孤独谱系沟通方式的能力。



And if they don’t have to, most of them won’t.

而若无需如此，他们中的大多数便不会主动为之。



A related consideration is that when a person’s entire experience of an oppressed group consists of situations in which the members of that group are in “inferior” roles, it inevitably shapes that person’s perspective on the group in question. Just look at the Stanford Prison Experiment, for a glimpse of how quickly and powerfully this effect kicks in.

另一个相关考量是：当一个人对某个受压迫群体的全部认知，都源于该群体成员处于"低等"角色的情境时，这种经历必然塑造其对该群体的看法。只需看看斯坦福监狱实验，便能窥见这种效应以何等迅疾而强大的方式发挥作用。



Anyone who understands this phenomenon will be unsurprised to learn that in my experience, the people who have the least empathy for autistic persons, the least ability to communicate respectfully with autistic persons, and the least genuine openness to learning from autistic persons, are the neurotypical professionals who have spent their careers working with autistic persons, in situations in which the professional always holds the authority and the autistic persons are always in the role of the patient, student, research subject, or “recipient of services.”

任何理解这一现象的人都不会感到惊讶：根据我的经验，对孤独谱系人士最缺乏同理心、最不善于以尊重的方式与他们沟通、最缺乏真诚开放态度向他们学习的人，正是那些职业生涯中始终与孤独谱系人士打交道的神经典型专业人士——在这些情境中，专业人士始终掌握权威，而孤独谱系人士永远处于患者、学生、研究对象或"服务接受者"的角色。



It’s nearly impossible for professionals of that sort to make the shift to the neurodiversity paradigm, to learn to check their neurotypical privilege, or to start respectfully listening to and learning from autistic perspectives. They’ve simply become too entrenched in the habit of not seeing autistic persons as equals.

这类专业人士几乎不可能转向神经多样性范式，学会审视自身的神经典型特权，或开始以尊重态度倾听并学习孤独谱系视角。他们早已深陷于不将孤独谱系人士视为平等个体的惯性思维中。



So my answer to the question of how to address empathy deficits and poor communication skills in neurotypical people working with autistic populations? Change the system, such that no neurotypical professional is permitted to work with autistic populations unless all of the following conditions are met:

那么，对于如何解决与孤独谱系群体共事的神经典型人士存在的同理心缺失和沟通能力不足问题，我的答案是：改革现有体系，规定任何神经典型专业人士必须满足以下所有条件，方可获准与孤独谱系群体共事——




The neurotypical professional must have received extensive training from autistic teachers, using curricula designed or approved by autistic experts. The autistic teachers and etxperts in question must themselves be well-versed in the neurodiversity paradigm—and in realms of critical and liberatory theory like Critical Psychology, Liberation Psychology, Disability Studies, Critical Autism Studies, and Queer Studies—rather than tame, token autistic persons (like Temple Grandin) who have themselves internalized and accepted the language of the pathology paradigm and the ableism of the dominant culture.

典型神经发育的专业人士必须接受过孤独谱系教师的广泛培训，并使用由孤独谱系专家设计或批准的课程。这些孤独谱系教师和专家本身必须精通神经多样性范式——以及批判心理学、解放心理学、残障研究、批判孤独谱系研究和酷儿研究等批判性与解放性理论领域——而不是像坦普尔·葛兰汀那样被驯服、象征性的孤独谱系人士，他们自身已内化并接受了病理学范式的语言以及主流文化中的能力主义。



The neurotypical professional must be licensed to work with autistic populations, by a licensing board composed primarily of autistic persons well-versed in the neurodiversity paradigm.

典型神经发育的专业人士必须获得由主要精通神经多样性范式的孤独谱系人士组成的认证委员会的许可，才能与孤独谱系群体合作。



The work of the neurotypical professional must be subject to supervision, input, and audit by autistic representatives of the aforementioned licensing board, who have the authority to make recommendations to the board regarding the status of the neurotypical professional’s license.

典型神经发育专业人士的工作必须接受前述认证委员会中孤独谱系代表的监督、意见和审计，这些代表有权就专业人士的执照状态向委员会提出建议。




None of these suggestions are likely to be implemented in the society in which we currently live, of course. But it’s a solution to the problems mentioned in your question—one of the only solutions to those problems that, if it were someday implemented, would actually work. And even when such solutions seem a long way off, one must dare to dream.

当然，这些建议在当前我们所处的社会中，都不太可能被付诸实施。但这是对你问题中提到的那些问题的一种解决方案——是少数几种如果某天得以实施，就确实能奏效的方案之一。即便这类解决方案看似遥不可及，人也必须敢于梦想。



Q: What advice and or suggestions can you offer psychotherapists working with autistic clients?

问：对于与孤独谱系来访者工作的心理治疗师，您能提供哪些建议或意见？



Check your privilege.

审视你的特权。



Empty your cup, as the Zen Buddhists say.

正如禅宗所言，倒空你的杯子。



Make the shift to the neurodiversity paradigm, completely. Throw out everything you’ve learned that’s in any way based in the pathology paradigm, all the messages about autism that you’ve been fed by the dominant culture. Be ferociously, eternally diligent about this: sociocultural programming is a constantly ongoing process, so breaking your sociocultural programming must also be a constantly ongoing process, and you’ll be swimming against the current. And it’s harder for members of privileged groups than members of oppressed groups: the status quo works in your favor, makes you the authority, lets you stay in your comfort zone, so it requires enormous ongoing commitment to stay mindful of the insidious and pervasive influence of the dominant paradigm, and to go against it.

彻底转向神经多样性范式。抛弃所有基于病理范式的认知，以及主流文化灌输给你的关于孤独谱系的一切信息。对此必须保持凶猛而永恒的警觉：社会文化编程是一个持续不断的过程，因此打破你的社会文化编程也必须是一个持续不断的过程，而且你将逆流而上。对于特权群体成员而言，这比受压迫群体成员更加困难：现状对你有利，赋予你权威，让你留在舒适区，因此需要巨大的持续投入，才能保持对主流范式阴险而普遍影响的警觉，并与之对抗。



The master’s tools will never dismantle the master’s house, but throwing away the master’s tools is hard—and it’s ten times harder if, within the current status quo, you’re one of the masters.

主人的工具永远无法拆除主人的房子，但扔掉主人的工具是困难的——如果你在当前的现状中是主人之一，那难度还要增加十倍。



Recognize that nearly everything written or taught about neurodivergence by neurotypical “experts” is just plain wrong, and is harmful to your autistic clients. The dominant culture’s stereotypes about any oppressed group are not more true just because you read them in a book or article written by an “expert.” Remember that there has been plenty of work published in the past by “experts”—including psychologists—that promoted sexist and racist stereotypes under the guise of “science.”

认识到几乎所有由神经典型“专家”撰写或教授的关于神经殊异性的内容都是完全错误的，并且对你的孤独谱系来访者有害。主流文化对任何受压迫群体的刻板印象，并不会因为你从“专家”写的书或文章中读到就变得更真实。记住，过去已有大量由“专家”（包括心理学家）发表的著作，以“科学”为幌子宣扬性别歧视和种族歧视的刻板印象。



Remember that an author, teacher, researcher, or other “expert” who refers to autism, for instance, as a “disorder,” is no more of a trustworthy, unbiased, “objective” authority than an “expert” who refers to homosexuality as a “disorder,” or than the “experts” who used to describe non-white peoples as “savage.”

记住，一位作者、教师、研究员或其他“专家”若将孤独谱系称为“障碍”，其可信度、客观性与公正性并不比将同性恋称为“障碍”的“专家”更高，也不比那些曾将非白人描述为“野蛮”的“专家”更高。



Remember that if you use the language of the pathology paradigm, you are reinforcing a social paradigm that harms your clients, and thus you are working against your clients’ interests.

记住，如果你使用病理学范式的语言，你就是在强化一种伤害你来访者的社会范式，从而违背了你来访者的利益。



Seek out autistic teachers, supervisors, and consultants who are well-versed in the neurodiversity paradigm. And pay them for their work. It’s remarkable how many neurotypical professionals and organizations are happy to pay neurotypical “experts” to talk about autistic people, but balk at paying the same rates for the harder-earned expertise of actual autistic people.

寻找精通神经多样性范式的孤独谱系教师、督导和顾问，并为他们付出的劳动支付报酬。令人惊讶的是，许多神经典型专业人士和组织乐于花钱请神经典型的"专家"谈论孤独谱系群体，却对以同等报酬聘请真正孤独谱系群体更来之不易的专业知识犹豫不决。



Listen to autistic people, and read what we write. Read autistic scholars and activists like Remi Yergeau, Kassiane Asasumasu, Amy Sequenzia, and myself. Read Yergeau’s book Authoring Autism and their article “Clinically Significant Disturbance.” Read Finn V. Gratton’s Supporting Transgender Autistic Youth and Adults. Read Michael Scott Monje’s Defiant. Read neuroqueer speculative fiction by autistic authors like Dora M. Raymaker and Ada Hoffmann.

倾听孤独谱系群体的声音，阅读我们的文字。阅读孤独谱系学者和活动家如雷米·耶尔戈、卡西安·阿萨苏马苏、艾米·塞肯齐亚以及我的作品。阅读耶尔戈的著作《书写孤独症》及其文章《临床意义上的显著困扰》。阅读芬恩·V·格拉顿的《支持跨性别孤独谱系青少年与成人》。阅读迈克尔·斯科特·蒙热的《反抗》。阅读孤独谱系作家如多拉·M·雷梅克和艾达·霍夫曼创作的神经酷儿思辨小说。



Never attempt to cure your client of being autistic. When you have an autistic client suffering from anxiety and depression, for instance, remember that your job is to treat the client for anxiety and depression, not for autism. Professionals who truly understand the neurodiversity paradigm would no sooner attempt to “treat” a client’s autism than attempt to “treat” a client’s homosexuality, or attempt to “treat” a client’s ethnicity.

永远不要试图“治愈”你的来访者的孤独谱系特质。例如，当你有一位患有焦虑和抑郁的孤独谱系来访者时，请记住你的工作是治疗焦虑和抑郁，而不是孤独谱系。真正理解神经多样性范式的专业人士，绝不会试图“治疗”来访者的孤独谱系，就像不会试图“治疗”来访者的同性恋或种族身份一样。



Familiarize yourself with the field of Liberation Psychology, and be continually aware that many of the psychological issues with which your autistic clients struggle will be issues created by social injustice and oppression, rather than by the client’s innate qualities. And remember that a good treatment plan is likely to include helping a client recognize this fact—helping the client understand their own oppression, both external and internalized, as a primary cause of their suffering.

请熟悉解放心理学领域，并时刻意识到你的孤独谱系来访者所面临的许多心理问题，往往源于社会不公与压迫，而非来访者与生俱来的特质。同时请记住，一个有效的治疗方案很可能包括帮助来访者认识到这一事实——帮助他们理解自己所遭受的外部压迫与内化压迫，正是其痛苦的主要根源。



Indeed, remember that your client may have completely bought into the pathology paradigm and may be ignorant of and even resistant to the neurodiversity paradigm. In which case, in order to support your client’s psychological well-being and liberation, it may be your duty as a therapist to introduce your client to the neurodiversity paradigm, and to educate your client by pointing them to writings like the ones mentioned above.

确实，请记住，你的来访者可能完全认同病理学范式，对神经多样性范式一无所知甚至抵触。在这种情况下，为了支持来访者的心理健康与解放，作为治疗师，你有责任向其介绍神经多样性范式，并通过推荐上述著作等资料来引导他们学习。



And above all, check your privilege.

最重要的是，审视你的特权。



Q: How does your training in somatics (both as a therapeutic orientation and your aikido background) factor into your work in the Neurodiversity Movement?

问：你在身心学方面的训练（既作为治疗取向，也包含你的合气道背景）如何影响你在神经多样性运动中的工作？



I see cognitive liberty as a core value of the Neurodiversity Movement.

我将认知自由视为神经多样性运动的核心价值。



The term cognitive liberty was coined by Wrye Sententia and Richard Glen Boire, the founders of the Center for Cognitive Liberty and Ethics. Cognitive liberty as an ethical value boils down to the idea that individuals have the right to absolute sovereignty over their own brains and their own cognitive processes. Advocates of cognitive liberty often break this idea down into two fundamental guiding ethical principles (originally inspired by the two “commandments” offered by Timothy Leary in The Politics of Ecstasy):

“认知自由”这一术语由“认知自由与伦理中心”的创始人怀尔·森滕蒂亚和理查德·格伦·博伊尔提出。作为一种伦理价值，认知自由的核心观点是：个体拥有对其自身大脑及认知过程的绝对主权。认知自由的倡导者常将此理念分解为两项基本指导伦理原则（最初受蒂莫西·利里在《迷幻政治学》中提出的两条“戒律”启发）：




Individuals have the right to not have their brains and cognitive processes tampered with non-consensually.

个体有权拒绝其大脑及认知过程在未经同意的情况下被干预。



Individuals have the right to tamper with their own brains and cognitive processes, or to voluntarily have them tampered with, in any way they choose.

个体有权以任何自选方式干预自身大脑及认知过程，或自愿允许他人对其进行干预。




Those of us who are deeply involved in transformative somatic practices or in the field of Somatic Psychology understand that the psyche is somatically organized, which means that each individual’s distinctive neurocognitive processes are intimately entwined with that individual’s style of movement and embodiment. Changes in movement and embodiment create changes in cognition.

深度参与转化性身体实践或躯体心理学领域的人士都明白，心理活动是以躯体方式组织的——这意味着每个人独特的神经认知过程与其运动模式和具身化风格紧密交织。运动与具身化的改变会引发认知的变化。



This means that to tamper with a person’s unique individual style of movement and embodiment (for instance, through the behaviorist techniques that are frequently used to make autistic children suppress the outward signs of autism) is to tamper with that person’s cognition, and thus to violate their cognitive liberty.

这意味着，干涉一个人独特的个体运动与具身风格（例如，通过行为主义技术频繁地让孤独谱系儿童抑制孤独谱系的外在表现），就是干涉这个人的认知，从而侵犯其认知自由。



In other words, freedom of embodiment—that is, the freedom to indulge, adopt, and/or experiment with any styles or quirks of movement and embodiment, whether they come naturally to one or whether one chooses them—is an essential element of cognitive liberty, and thus an essential area of focus for the Neurodiversity Movement. The freedom to be autistic necessarily includes the freedom to give bodily expression to one’s neurodivergence.

换言之，具身自由——即沉浸、采纳和/或尝试任何运动与具身风格或特质的自由，无论这些风格是自然流露还是主动选择——是认知自由的基本要素，因此也是神经多样性运动的关键关注领域。成为孤独谱系者的自由，必然包括通过身体表达自身神经殊异性的自由。



For somatically-oriented psychotherapists, one important implication of all this is that autistic clients will often have acquired habitual unconscious tensions (what Wilhelm Reich referred to as character armor) that prevent them from giving full expression to the movement style that is natural and optimal for them. These tensions will tend to be especially severe and deep-rooted in clients who, in childhood, were frequently shamed or otherwise abused for their physical expressions of neurodivergence, or who were subjected to behaviorist “therapies” or other forms of coerced physical conformity.

对于以躯体为导向的心理治疗师而言，这一切的一个重要启示在于：孤独谱系来访者往往已形成习惯性的无意识紧张（威廉·赖希称之为“性格盔甲”），这种紧张阻碍了他们充分展现自身自然且最优的运动风格。这些紧张在童年时期因神经殊异性的身体表达而频繁遭受羞辱或其他虐待的来访者中尤为严重且根深蒂固，同样的情况也出现在那些曾被迫接受行为主义“疗法”或其他形式强制身体服从的来访者身上。



An integration of the neurodiversity paradigm into the field of Somatic Psychology would include the recognition of these habitual tensions as somatic manifestations of internalized oppression. And it seems to me that somatically-oriented psychotherapists, once they have embraced the neurodiversity paradigm, are uniquely qualified to assist autistic clients in the task of liberating themselves from the bonds of such tensions, and thus recovering their capacity for giving full expression to their unique potentials.

将神经多样性范式融入躯体心理学领域，需要将这些习惯性紧张视为内化压迫的躯体表现。在我看来，一旦躯体导向的心理治疗师接纳了神经多样性范式，他们便具备独特的能力，能够帮助孤独谱系来访者摆脱这些紧张的束缚，从而恢复充分展现其独特潜能的自由。







---


Nick_ebook-29










Guiding Principles for a

Course on Autism

孤独症课程指导原则



In 2014, I was invited to create and teach a course called Critical Perspectives on Autism and Neurodiversity in the undergraduate Interdisciplinary Studies program at California Institute of Integral Studies. I taught that course a couple of times, and in 2016 I wrote this piece inspired by the experience. In 2018, I was invited to create and teach an updated version of the course for the school’s new undergraduate Psychology program. As of this writing in 2021, that course has evolved into Introduction to Neurodiversity Studies, and is part of the undergraduate Psychology program’s core curriculum. In fact, one of the reasons I’m writing this book now is so I can use it as one of the textbooks for the course.

2014 年，我受邀在加州整合研究学院（California Institute of Integral Studies）的本科跨学科研究项目中，创建并教授一门名为《孤独症与神经多样性批判性视角》的课程。我教授该课程数次后，于 2016 年基于这段经历撰写了本文。2018 年，我再次受邀为该校新设的本科心理学项目创建并教授该课程的更新版本。截至 2021 年撰写本文时，该课程已演变为《神经多样性研究导论》，并成为本科心理学项目核心课程的一部分。事实上，我撰写本书的原因之一，正是为了将其用作该课程的教材。



I originally published this piece on my Neurocosmopolitanism website in July of 2016. It was the final essay that I wrote for that site, before turning my attention to other sorts of writing in other venues. The quality of thought and writing in this piece strikes me as a significant step up from my earlier essays. It’s got a distinctly neuroqueer vibe, at least to my eye, which might have something to do with the fact that I wrote it while I was just beginning to come to terms with being transgender. I think it makes for a good conclusion to this part of the book, and a good segue into the material that’s more directly focused on neuroqueering.

我最初于 2016 年 7 月在 Neurocosmopolitanism 网站上发表了这篇文章。这是我为那个网站撰写的最后一篇随笔，之后便将注意力转向了其他平台的其他写作形式。在我看来，这篇文章的思想深度与写作质量较之前的随笔有了显著提升。它带有鲜明的神经酷儿气质——至少在我看来如此——这或许与我写作时刚刚开始接纳自己的跨性别身份有关。我认为这篇文章能为本书这一部分画上圆满的句号，并自然过渡到更直接聚焦神经酷儿实践的内容。



“The classroom remains the most radical space of possibility in the academy.” —bell hooks

“教室依然是学术领域中最具可能性的激进空间。”——贝尔·胡克斯



Early on in the process of designing my Critical Perspectives on Autism and Neurodiversity course for the undergraduate program at California Institute of Integral Studies, I asked myself the question, “What are the most essential and indispensable guiding principles any course on autism must follow, in order to ensure that the course truly remains grounded in the neurodiversity paradigm and avoids inadvertently reinforcing the attitudes of the pathology paradigm on any level?” I eventually developed a list of seven such guiding principles, which have served me quite well and which are here enumerated in the hope that they will be useful to others in creating similar courses.

在为我为加州整合研究学院本科课程设计《孤独症与神经多样性批判视角》课程的过程中，我早期曾自问：“任何关于孤独症的课程，若要确保真正立足于神经多样性范式，并避免在无意中强化病理范式的态度，必须遵循哪些最根本且不可或缺的指导原则？”最终，我总结出七项原则，它们在实践中效果显著，现列举于此，希望能为他人设计类似课程提供参考。



1. To Hell with “Balance”

1. 去他的“平衡”



A good course on autism (or, for that matter, a good piece of writing on autism, or good education or journalism on autism in any medium) should not attempt to strike any sort of “balance” between the neurodiversity paradigm and the pathology paradigm. The pathology paradigm is simply an outgrowth of cultural ableism and bigotry. Work based in the pathology paradigm has no more scholarly or “scientific” validity than work based in cultural paradigms of racism, misogyny, or homophobia. Like racism, misogyny, and homophobia, the pathology paradigm is just plain wrong. The fact that at this point in history nearly all mainstream academic and professional writing on autism is based in the pathology paradigm doesn’t make it any less wrong. There was a time that nearly all mainstream academic and professional writing on race was racist, and that didn’t make racism valid or right.

一门优秀的孤独症课程（或一篇优秀的孤独症文章、任何媒介中关于孤独症的优质教育或新闻报道）不应试图在神经多样性范式与病理学范式之间寻求任何形式的"平衡"。病理学范式不过是文化能力主义与偏见的产物。基于病理学范式的研究，其学术或"科学"有效性并不比基于种族主义、厌女症或恐同症等文化范式的研究更高。与种族主义、厌女症和恐同症一样，病理学范式本身就是完全错误的。即便在当下历史节点，几乎所有主流学术和专业文献都基于病理学范式来论述孤独症，这丝毫不能减轻其错误性。正如曾经几乎所有关于种族的主流学术和专业文献都带有种族主义色彩，但这并不能使种族主义变得合理或正确。



A good educator should seek to expose students to good information while steering them away from ignorance and bigotry. A “balance” between right and wrong isn’t right; a “balance” between good information and ignorant bigotry isn’t superior to good information. So, to hell with “balance.” If you were teaching an African-American Studies course, would you insist that half of the assigned readings consist of racist literature by white supremacists, in the interest of “balance”? I certainly hope not.

优秀的教育者应当引导学生接触优质信息，同时引导他们远离无知与偏见。正确与错误之间的"平衡"并非正确；优质信息与无知偏见之间的"平衡"并不优于优质信息。所以，让"平衡"见鬼去吧。如果你在教授非裔美国人研究课程，你会为了"平衡"而坚持让一半的指定阅读材料包含白人至上主义者的种族主义文献吗？我当然希望你不会。



Consider also that the pathology paradigm is so dominant and pervasive in academia and in society as a whole that all students in any course on autism have grown up thoroughly steeped in the assumptions of the pathology paradigm, and it’s likely that nearly everything they’ve been taught about autism has been based in the pathology paradigm. Students come into a class on autism already heavily biased toward the pathology paradigm and with heads already full of the bigoted misconceptions about autism engendered by the pathology paradigm, and outside of the class they’ll continue to dwell in a world in which the pathology paradigm is constantly reinforced. Thus, even if “balance” were our priority, courses that are entirely and intentionally weighted toward the neurodiversity paradigm are merely a small step toward restoring balance in a world that’s overwhelmingly biased toward the pathology paradigm.

同时要考虑到，病理学范式在学术界和整个社会中如此根深蒂固且无处不在，以至于任何孤独谱系课程的学生都在成长过程中深受其假设的影响，他们所学到的关于孤独谱系的一切几乎都基于病理学范式。学生在进入孤独谱系课堂时，已经对病理学范式抱有强烈偏见，脑海中充斥着该范式所催生的关于孤独谱系的偏执误解，而在课堂之外，他们仍将生活在一个不断强化病理学范式的世界里。因此，即便"平衡"是我们的优先考量，在这个严重偏向病理学范式的世界中，那些完全且有意倾向于神经多样性范式的课程，也不过是恢复平衡的一小步。



So a good course on autism should actively and uncompromisingly promote the neurodiversity paradigm, just as a good African-American Studies course is actively and uncompromisingly anti-racist. Work based in the pathology paradigm, if it’s assigned at all, should be assigned only so that the instructor and students can critique it in order to hone the students’ skills at recognizing and critiquing such work.

因此，一门优秀的孤独症课程应当积极且毫不妥协地推广神经多样性范式，正如一门优秀的非裔美国人研究课程会积极且毫不妥协地反对种族主义。基于病理范式的研究，即便被列入课程，也仅应作为师生批判的对象，以培养学生识别和批判此类研究的能力。



2. The Instructor Must Be Autistic

2. 授课教师必须是孤独谱系人士



The instructor must be autistic. Imagine the outcry that would (rightly) ensue if a college’s courses in Women’s Studies were primarily taught by men, or if a college’s courses on African-American Studies were primarily taught by white people! The fact that it’s still widely regarded as acceptable for courses on autism to be mostly taught by non-autistic people is an indicator of just how deeply the pathology paradigm pervades the mindset of our society. Regardless of the curriculum, every course on autism that isn’t taught by an autistic instructor implicitly reinforces the pathology paradigm and the ableist assumption that non-autistic persons are better qualified to speak for and about autistic persons than autistic persons themselves. There are enough out-of-the-closet autistics in academia these days that any college should be able to find one to teach a course on autism. And given how heavily most hiring processes discriminate against autistics, the autistic academics could certainly use the work.

授课者必须是孤独谱系人士。试想，如果大学里的女性研究课程主要由男性教授，或者非裔美国人研究课程主要由白人教授，那将会引发何等（理所当然的）抗议！然而，人们至今仍普遍认为，由非孤独谱系人士来教授孤独症相关课程是可以接受的——这一事实恰恰表明，病理学范式对我们的社会心态渗透得有多深。无论课程大纲如何，任何一门由非孤独谱系人士讲授的孤独症课程，都在无形中强化了病理学范式，以及那种能力主义假设：即非孤独谱系人士比孤独谱系人士更有资格代表他们发言、谈论他们。如今学术界已有足够多的公开身份的孤独谱系人士，任何大学都应该能找到一位来教授孤独症课程。而且，考虑到大多数招聘流程对孤独谱系群体的严重歧视，这些孤独谱系学者们确实需要这样的工作机会。



3. The Instructor Must Be a Participant in Autistic Culture, Community, and Resistance

3. 授课者必须是孤独谱系文化、社群及抗争的参与者



When academic institutions do invite an autistic person to have any sort of significant voice in their curriculum on autism, the autistic person in question is nearly always chosen from a short list of well-known autistics whom I have come to think of as the tame autistics. The tame autistics all have certain traits in common: they are white; they are heterosexual, asexual, and/or fairly closeted about their sexuality; they grew up fairly affluent and have never faced extreme poverty or homelessness; they are highly capable of oral speech; they are ableist, and have no problem with pathologizing non-speaking autistics or other autistics who are significantly more disabled than themselves; they regard disability as shameful and tend to avoid describing themselves as disabled; they rarely contradict non-autistic “autism experts” or ableist autism organizations run by non-autistic people; they have few (if any) close autistic friends and have never been deeply involved in the radical activist autistic culture and communities from which the Neurodiversity Movement emerged; they have appropriated the term “neurodiversity” now that it’s becoming a well-known buzzword, but their thinking remains rooted in the pathology paradigm. Temple Grandin and John Elder Robison are probably the best-known of these tame autistics at the time that I write this, but there are many others—in fact, there are a couple of publishing companies, specializing in autism-related books based in the pathology paradigm, that actively seek the work of tame autistic authors.

当学术机构邀请孤独谱系人士在孤独症相关课程中拥有重要发言权时，被选中的孤独谱系人士几乎总是来自一份我称之为"驯化型孤独谱系者"的短名单。 被驯化的孤独谱系群体都有某些共同特征：他们是白人；他们是异性恋、无性恋，或对自己的性取向相当隐秘；他们成长于相当富裕的环境，从未经历过极端贫困或无家可归；他们高度擅长口语表达；他们持有能力主义偏见，对非口语孤独谱系者或比自己残障程度更重的孤独谱系者毫无顾忌地进行病理化标签；他们将残障视为羞耻，倾向于避免将自己描述为残障者；他们很少反驳非孤独谱系的"孤独症专家"或由非孤独谱系者运营的能力主义孤独症组织；他们几乎没有（或完全没有）亲密的孤独谱系朋友，也从未深度参与催生神经多样性运动的激进行动主义孤独谱系文化与社群；如今"神经多样性"成为流行热词后，他们盗用了这个术语，但其思维仍根植于病理学范式。 坦普尔·葛兰汀和约翰·埃尔德·罗宾逊在我写下这些文字时，可能是这些“驯化型孤独谱系人士”中最知名的两位，但还有许多人——事实上，有几家专门出版基于病理学范式的孤独症相关书籍的出版公司，正在积极寻找驯化型孤独谱系作者的作品。



Autistic though they may be, none of these tame autistics would be equipped to create or teach a curriculum that poses real critical challenges to the pathology paradigm and to the bigotry of the dominant cultural narratives around autism. For a course to be effective in serving those goals, it’s not enough for the instructor to be autistic; the instructor must be an autistic with a substantial history of active participation in autistic culture and community, including autistic rights activism, resistance to oppressive cultural and professional practices based in the pathology paradigm, and celebration of autistic pride.

尽管他们可能属于孤独谱系，但这些驯化型孤独谱系人士中，没有谁能够创建或教授一门真正对病理学范式以及围绕孤独症的主流文化叙事中的偏见提出批判性挑战的课程。要使一门课程有效服务于这些目标，仅仅让教师是孤独谱系人士是不够的；教师必须是一位在孤独谱系文化和社群中有着大量积极参与历史的孤独谱系人士，包括孤独谱系权利倡导、抵制基于病理学范式的压迫性文化和专业实践，以及颂扬孤独谱系自豪感。



4. Autistic Voices Must Be Central

4. 孤独谱系的声音必须居于核心地位



The writings and perspectives of actual autistic persons must be central, not peripheral, to the curriculum. At least 80% of the assigned readings should be by autistic authors. Tame autistics don’t count—not that the course can’t include any material by tame autistics, but such material should be approached with the explicit intent of critiquing the internalized oppression of the authors, and the way that the work of such authors tends to perpetuate the pathologizing narratives that the authors have been taught to impose on their lives. A course in which most of the readings by autistics are by tame autistics is a course that reinforces dominant cultural narratives rather than challenging them.

实际孤独谱系人士的著作与观点必须成为课程的核心，而非边缘内容。指定阅读材料中至少 80%应来自孤独谱系作者。驯化的孤独谱系人士不算在内——并非课程完全不能包含这类作者的材料，但应以明确批判其内化压迫的意图来对待这些材料，并揭示这类作者的作品如何延续他们被教导强加于自身生活的病态化叙事。若课程中孤独谱系作者的阅读材料大多来自驯化者，这样的课程只会强化主流文化叙事，而非挑战它们。



5. Truth Is Where It Is

5. 真理所在之处



In the realm of conventional academic literature (e.g., peer-reviewed journals and books from mainstream academic presses) the discourse on autism is dominated by the voices of non-autistic writers whose work is based in the pathology paradigm. Autistic voices and narratives that pose critical challenges to this dominant discourse, and to the host of beliefs and practices around autism that are rooted in the pathology paradigm, are systematically marginalized in this literature—excluded, silenced, disingenuously misinterpreted, or condescendingly dismissed.

在传统学术文献领域（例如同行评审期刊和主流学术出版社出版的书籍），关于孤独谱系的论述主要由基于病理学范式的非孤独谱系作者的声音主导。那些对主流论述以及围绕孤独谱系、根植于病理学范式的一系列信念与实践提出批判性挑战的孤独谱系声音与叙事，在此类文献中系统性地被边缘化——或被排除、被压制、被虚伪地曲解，或被居高临下地否定。



To find the autistic voices that challenge the assumptions and practices of the dominant paradigm through various combinations of personal testimony and direct critique, one must generally look outside the well-guarded walls of mainstream academic literature. Until quite recently, nearly all of the most important work by non-tame autistic authors could only be found on the internet. While autistic work based in the neurodiversity paradigm is now beginning to gain footholds in academia—particularly with the recent emergence of the fields of Neurodiversity Studies and Critical Autism Studies—the leading edges of liberatory autistic thought still tend to initially emerge online or through the efforts of independent publishing houses like Autonomous Press that specifically seek to amplify marginalized voices. Given this state of affairs, the list of assigned readings for a course on autism based in the neurodiversity paradigm rather than the pathology paradigm must necessarily consist to a significant degree of materials drawn from sources outside of the realm of conventional academic publishing.

要寻找那些通过个人证言与直接批判相结合的方式挑战主流范式假设与实践的孤独谱系声音，通常需要将目光投向主流学术文献高墙之外。直到最近，几乎所有非驯化型孤独谱系作者最重要的作品都只能在互联网上找到。尽管基于神经多样性范式的孤独谱系研究如今开始进入学术界——特别是随着神经多样性研究与批判性孤独谱系研究领域的兴起——但解放性孤独谱系思想的前沿阵地仍倾向于首先在网络上涌现，或通过像 Autonomous Press 这样专门放大边缘声音的独立出版社的努力而传播。鉴于这种现状，基于神经多样性范式而非病理范式设计的孤独谱系课程必读书目，必然在很大程度上需要从传统学术出版领域之外的资源中选取。



The instructor ought to make a point of explaining all of this on the first day of class, and perhaps also articulate it in the syllabus. It’s good for students to understand the rationale behind an unorthodox reading list; it’s also good for students to understand how the gatekeeping systems of conventional academic literature resist incursions by marginalized voices that pose radical challenges to dominant paradigms—and how such challenges, as a result, tend to emerge outside the borders of mainstream academia and only gradually fight their way inward.

教师应在第一天的课堂上明确解释所有这些内容，或许也应在课程大纲中加以阐述。让学生理解非传统阅读清单背后的逻辑是有益的；同样，让学生明白传统学术文献的守门机制如何抵制那些对主流范式构成根本挑战的边缘化声音的介入——以及这些挑战因此往往在主流学术界之外涌现，并逐步向内渗透——也是有益的。



6. The Instructor Must Model the Accommodation of

6. 教师必须示范如何适应

Neurodivergence

神经殊异性



Most academic settings reflect the ableist and neuronormative values of the dominant culture. Students are expected to conform to the dominant neuronormative conventions of learning and participation, and students whose learning and access needs conflict with those conventions are heavily discriminated against in most educational institutions. The instructor must openly and explicitly declare the class a zone of freedom from this sort of discrimination and compulsory neuronormativity, and must clearly and consistently demonstrate the creative accommodation of neurodivergence and individual access needs in her conduct of the class.

大多数学术环境都反映了主流文化中存在的体能健全主义与神经规范主义价值观。学生被要求遵循主流神经规范主义的学习与参与惯例，而在大多数教育机构中，那些学习与参与需求与这些惯例相冲突的学生会遭受严重歧视。教师必须公开明确地宣布课堂为免于此类歧视和强制性神经规范主义的自由区域，并在教学过程中清晰且持续地展现对神经殊异性及个体无障碍需求的创造性适应。



An instructor may assign a superb list of readings on the neurodiversity paradigm, and may speak eloquently on the importance of embracing neurodiversity and accommodating the access needs of neurodivergent persons—but if the instructor does not model this embracing and accommodation of neurodivergence in how she actually conducts the class and deals with the students, then the instructor’s hypocrisy will ultimately undermine her message and the course will be a hollow sham. One cannot convincingly challenge a paradigm of compulsory neuronormativity while remaining complicit in the institutionalized enforcement of that same neuronormativity. In the immortal words of Audre Lorde, the master’s tools will never dismantle the master’s house.

一位教师可能会布置一份关于神经多样性范式的优秀阅读清单，并慷慨陈词地论述拥抱神经多样性和满足神经殊异者无障碍需求的重要性——但如果这位教师在课堂实际运作和与学生互动中，并未亲身示范如何接纳和包容神经殊异性，那么她的虚伪最终会削弱其传达的信息，课程也将沦为空洞的幌子。一个人若仍默许制度化的强制性神经典型规范，就无法令人信服地挑战这一范式。正如奥德丽·洛德那句不朽箴言：主人的工具永远无法拆毁主人的房屋。



It is not sufficient for the instructor to only grant students the accommodations that are mandated for them by the college’s Disability Services department. This is merely compliance with the law (although many instructors and many institutions resist even doing that much). Disability Services departments in the world of higher education reinforce the pathology paradigm by demanding that neurodivergent students subject themselves to the process of being professionally diagnosed, and of having their divergences from neuronormativity pathologized as “disorders,” before accommodations are granted. Thus, any instructor who provides accommodations only when required by the Disability Services department is also implicitly reinforcing and condoning the pathology paradigm.

仅仅按照大学残障服务部门的规定为学生提供便利措施是不够的，这不过是遵守法律而已（尽管许多教师和机构连这一点都抗拒执行）。高等教育界的残障服务部门要求神经殊异学生接受专业诊断流程，将其偏离神经规范的特质病理化为"障碍"后才给予便利措施，这种做法强化了病理学范式。因此，任何仅在残障服务部门要求时才提供便利措施的教师，实际上也在默许并强化这种病理学范式。



Instead, on the first day of class, the instructor should explicitly point out the above dynamics, and should invite all students to publicly or privately speak up about any access needs they have that they’re aware of or that they might become aware of during the course of the term. The instructor should do her best to work with the students to accommodate their needs. If there are accommodations that neither the instructor nor the student can provide, and Disability Services and/or other institutional departments must be involved, then the instructor should advocate for the student with those departments if such advocacy can help to expedite the provision of the needed accommodations.

相反，在开课第一天，教师应明确指出上述动态，并邀请所有学生公开或私下提出他们在学期中已知或可能意识到的任何无障碍需求。教师应尽力与学生合作，满足他们的需求。如果有些需求教师和学生都无法满足，必须涉及残障服务部门和/或其他机构部门，那么教师应在这些部门为学生争取权益——若此类倡导有助于加快所需无障碍支持的落实。



Conflicts between the access needs of different individuals should be negotiated in class as part of the learning process. For instance, I often get students who need to take notes on laptops, tablets, or other electronic devices, because they need the notes in order to retain information but they can’t write quickly enough by hand. Personally, I can’t focus on speaking and listening to the class while someone next to me is noisily tap-tap-tapping away at a keyboard. So, right at the beginning of the first day of class (when I’m teaching in person rather than online), I tell students that they’re welcome to type during class as long as they don’t sit too close to me—there’s a “no typing zone” around the front of the room where I’m positioned, and a “typing zone” across the room from me. This works for everyone—and more importantly, it immediately provides students with an example of what access needs are and how they can be civilly negotiated.

不同个体的无障碍需求冲突应在课堂上作为学习过程的一部分进行协商。例如，我经常遇到需要借助笔记本电脑、平板电脑或其他电子设备做笔记的学生，因为他们需要笔记来记忆信息，但手写速度又不够快。就我个人而言，当邻座同学噼里啪啦敲击键盘时，我无法专注于课堂的口语表达和听力。因此，在每学期第一堂课（线下授课而非线上教学时）开始前，我会明确告知学生：只要不坐得离我太近，欢迎他们在课堂上使用键盘——教室前方我所在区域划为"禁敲区"，而教室远端则设为"敲击区"。这个方案既满足了所有人的需求，更重要的是，它立即向学生展示了什么是无障碍需求，以及如何通过文明协商达成共识。



7. The Instructor Must Model and Invite the Embodied

7. 教师必须示范并邀请具身化

Expression of Neurodivergence

神经殊异性的表达



In the classroom, students must be free to be neurodivergent, to act neurodivergent, to look and sound neurodivergent. Each student must be free to openly engage in whatever forms and styles of embodiment and movement come naturally to them, or meet their (physical, cognitive, and/or emotional) needs, or emerge as spontaneous responses to external or internal circumstances. The classroom must be declared a zone of freedom from the dominant culture’s pervasive requirement that everyone strive to constantly perform neuronormativity. Students must instead be invited to drop the performance of neuronormativity and to freely explore and indulge in the embodied performance of neurodivergence.

在课堂上，学生必须能够自由地展现神经殊异，以神经殊异的方式行动、呈现和发声。每个学生都应自由地以任何自然流露的形态与动作进行表达，或满足其（生理、认知及/或情感）需求，或作为对外部/内部环境的自发反应。课堂必须被宣告为摆脱主流文化普遍要求的自由区域——那种要求所有人持续表演神经规范性的桎梏。相反，应邀请学生放下神经规范性的表演，自由探索并沉浸于神经殊异性的具身化表达之中。



It is not sufficient for the instructor to merely tell students that in this class it’s okay for them to give expression to their neurodivergence. Sociocultural pressures to perform neuronormativity are lifelong, pervasive, and insidious. By the time people are old enough to end up in a college classroom, they have almost always internalized these pressures to the point where they habitually police themselves and engage in the performance of neuronormativity even in situations in which it isn’t explicitly required of them by any external authority. That’s how enculturation works, and how internalized oppression works on an embodied level. Internalized normativity is a powerful force, especially when engrained into habits of embodied performance.

仅仅告诉学生在这门课上可以表达他们的神经殊异性是不够的。社会文化要求人们表现神经规范的压力是终身、普遍且潜移默化的。当人们到了进入大学课堂的年龄时，几乎总是已经将这些压力内化到习惯性地自我约束的程度，即使在没有任何外部权威明确要求的情况下，也会进行神经规范的表现。这就是文化适应运作的方式，也是内化压迫在身体层面发挥作用的方式。内化的规范性是一股强大的力量，尤其是当它根植于身体表现的习性之中时。



Thus, in order for the classroom to actually function as any sort of zone of liberation from compulsory neuronormativity, it is necessary for the instructor to explain all of this—to explain how the dominant culture entrains us all toward the performance of normativity, and how this performance becomes internalized and habituated on a bodily level, and how breaking out of that shell of normative performance is an essential component of self-liberation. It is necessary for the instructor to explicitly declare the classroom a zone for free experimentation with shedding habits of normative performance and actively exploring, practicing, reclaiming, and cultivating non-normative modes of embodiment. And it is necessary for the instructor to personally practice what she preaches: to personally, physically model the embodied expression of neurodivergence. The autistic instructor must move like an autistic person, must freely and visibly follow her natural movement impulses in the classroom. Most students simply will not dare to engage in such exploration in the classroom unless the instructor leads the way. And this means, of course, that in order to be qualified to teach in a way that liberates others, the instructor must do the work of self-liberation on a bodily level.

因此，为了让课堂真正成为摆脱强制性神经规范性的解放空间，教师必须阐明这一切——解释主流文化如何训练我们所有人去表演规范性，这种表演如何在身体层面被内化和习惯化，以及打破这种规范性表演的桎梏如何成为自我解放的关键组成部分。教师必须明确宣告课堂是一个自由实验的场所，在这里可以摆脱规范性表演的习惯，积极探索、实践、重拾并培育非规范性的具身模式。同时，教师必须亲身践行自己的主张：在身体层面示范神经殊异性的具身表达。孤独谱系教师应当以孤独谱系者的方式行动，在课堂上自由而可见地遵循自身的自然运动冲动。除非教师率先垂范，否则大多数学生根本不敢在课堂上进行此类探索。 当然，这意味着，若要以解放他人的方式进行教学，教师必须在身体层面完成自我解放的工作。



Conducting the class in this manner is obviously both liberatory and educational (it’s fascinating and edifying to observe the many different forms and styles of movement that gradually emerge in the classroom). What may be less obvious is that this is as much about access as about liberation. To whatever extent they think about access needs in the classroom at all, most people tend to think in terms of eliminating physical barriers (e.g., by providing wheelchair access, captioned videos, or lighting that doesn’t trigger seizures), or accommodating atypical learning styles (e.g., by giving dyslexic students extra time on quizzes). Both of these, of course, are essential forms of accommodation. But freedom of embodiment is also an access need. A student who must constantly exert her energy and attention toward passing for “normal”—i.e., performing neuronormativity rather than allowing their natural neurodivergent styles of movement and embodiment to come to the surface—is a student who has less energy and attention available for the tasks of learning and creative participation. Students can be better students when they’re given the space to move in the ways that are optimal for the functioning of their particular neurologies, rather than the ways that are required for the performance of normativity.

以这种方式授课显然既具有解放性又具有教育意义（观察课堂上逐渐涌现出的各种不同形式和风格的动作，既引人入胜又富有启发性）。可能不那么明显的是，这既关乎解放，也关乎无障碍。大多数人在思考课堂上的无障碍需求时，往往只想到消除物理障碍（例如提供轮椅通道、带字幕的视频或不会引发癫痫的照明），或适应非典型学习风格（例如给阅读障碍学生更多测验时间）。当然，这两种都是必要的辅助形式。但身体表达的自由同样是一种无障碍需求。一个必须不断耗费精力与注意力来伪装成"正常"——即表演神经常态性，而非让自身天然的神经殊异动作与身体表达方式自然流露——的学生，能够用于学习和创造性参与的能量与注意力就会减少。 当学生被允许以最适合其特定神经系统运作的方式活动，而非为了表现"正常"而被迫遵循特定行为模式时，他们能成为更好的学生。



Here, again, conflicting access needs can be openly negotiated in class as part of the learning experience. If one student needs to drum her fingers on the desktop and another needs quiet, then perhaps the drummer can place a folded scarf or other article of clothing on the desktop to create a quieter drumming surface. If one student needs to stand up and make dance-like full-body movements, and others find this visually distracting, perhaps a corner of the room that’s outside of the visual field of the seated students can become the designated dancing space.

在此，课堂上同样可以将相互冲突的便利需求作为学习体验的一部分进行公开协商。若某位学生需要用手指敲击桌面，而另一位需要安静环境，那么敲击者或许可以在桌面上垫一条折叠的围巾或其他衣物，以降低敲击声。若某位学生需要站立并做出类似舞蹈的全身动作，而其他人觉得这分散视觉注意力，或许可以在教室角落划出一个位于就座学生视野之外的区域，作为专属的舞蹈空间。



Just as intentionally liberating oneself from the culturally ingrained and enforced performance of heteronormativity is sometimes referred to as queering, intentionally liberating oneself from the culturally ingrained and enforced performance of neuronormativity can be thought of as neuroqueering. To invite the embodied expression of neurodivergence in the classroom is a way of neuroqueering the classroom space, and an invitation to students to engage in the practice of neuroqueering. The concept of neuroqueering represents a rich and important intersection of the fields of Neurodiversity Studies and Queer Theory, and, on top of its other benefits, introducing the practice of neuroqueering embodiment into the classroom is an excellent way to introduce neuroqueering as a concept.

正如有意将自己从文化中根深蒂固且被强制执行的异性恋规范表演中解放出来有时被称为“酷儿化”，有意将自己从文化中根深蒂固且被强制执行的神经规范表演中解放出来，可以被视为“神经酷儿化”。在课堂上邀请神经殊异性的具身表达，是一种对课堂空间进行神经酷儿化的方式，也是邀请学生参与神经酷儿化实践的方式。神经酷儿化的概念代表了神经多样性研究与酷儿理论领域之间一个丰富且重要的交叉点，除了其诸多益处之外，将神经酷儿化具身实践引入课堂，也是介绍神经酷儿化这一概念的绝佳途径。



In Conclusion

结语



The present state of autism-related discourse, theory, and praxis in the academic and professional spheres is deplorable. The discourse and theory reflect a level of ignorance and bigotry that would be regarded as scandalous in most academic circles today if it involved any other historically oppressed group. The praxis generated by this shoddy discourse and theory consistently makes life worse for autistic persons and their families; the situation is so bad that harm, degradation, and trauma suffered at the hands of therapists, educators, and other professionals has become one of the most consistent and pervasive themes in the writings of autistics. This whole sorry state of affairs can be traced directly to the dominance of the pathology paradigm, which assumes as a starting premise that autistic minds and lives are intrinsically defective and inferior. There is simply no way to generate good theory and praxis by clinging to unsound and bigoted assumptions.

当前学术界与专业领域中，与孤独谱系相关的论述、理论及实践状况令人堪忧。这些论述与理论所反映的无知与偏见程度，若涉及其他历史上受压迫群体，在当今大多数学术圈中早已被视为丑闻。由这种拙劣论述与理论催生的实践，持续恶化着孤独谱系人士及其家庭的生活质量；其恶劣程度已使治疗师、教育工作者及其他专业人士造成的伤害、贬抑与创伤，成为孤独谱系群体书写中最普遍且最持久的主题之一。这一可悲局面的根源，可直接追溯至病理范式的统治地位——该范式将孤独谱系者的心智与生活本质上有缺陷且低劣作为基本前提。固守错误且充满偏见的假设，绝无可能催生优质的理论与实践。



Substantial change for the better will only come from abandoning the pathology paradigm and making the shift to the neurodiversity paradigm. For such a shift to happen, the next generation of professionals must be educated on autism from a perspective based solidly in the neurodiversity paradigm, and must be inoculated against the pathology paradigm by being trained to recognize and critique it as a manifestation of cultural prejudice possessing no more scientific validity than any other form of bigotry.

真正意义上的积极变革，唯有摒弃病理学范式、转向神经多样性范式才能实现。要实现这一转变，下一代专业人士必须接受基于神经多样性范式的孤独症教育，并通过训练识别和批判病理学范式——这种文化偏见与任何其他形式的偏执一样缺乏科学依据——来建立对病理学范式的免疫力。



The seven principles I’ve delineated are intended to serve as a foundational set of guidelines for creating college courses that provide this sort of critical education on autism. It is my hope that sharing these ideas will encourage the creation of many other courses in other schools, built upon similar principles and with the same intent to prepare new generations of students to be active participants in creating the much-needed shift from the pathology paradigm to the neurodiversity paradigm in the academic and professional discourse on autism.

我所阐述的七项原则，旨在为开设此类批判性孤独症教育的大学课程提供基础性指导框架。希望这些理念的分享能激励其他院校创建更多遵循相似原则的课程，以培养新一代学生成为推动学术与专业领域从病理学范式向神经多样性范式转变的积极参与者。







---


Nick_ebook-30










PART III:

POSTNORMAL POSSIBILITIES

第三部分：后常态的可能性



“‘Queer,’ in any case, does not designate a class of already objectified pathologies or perversions; rather, it describes a horizon of possibility whose precise extent and heterogeneous scope cannot in principle be delimited in advance.”

“无论如何，‘酷儿’并非指代一类已被物化的病理或变态；相反，它描述了一种可能性的地平线，其精确范围和异质性广度在原则上无法预先界定。”



David M. Halperin

大卫·M·哈尔珀林







---


Nick_ebook-31










Neuroqueer: An Introduction

神经酷儿：引言



I originally wrote this piece and published it on my website on May 2, 2015. As the concept of neuroqueer(ing) has caught on and sparked imaginations, it’s become one of my more frequently cited writings.

本文最初于 2015 年 5 月 2 日发布在我的网站上。随着神经酷儿（化）这一概念逐渐流行并激发人们的想象力，它已成为我引用频率最高的作品之一。



I coined the term neuroqueer in a paper I wrote for a grad school class in the Spring of 2008. Over the next several years, I played with it in further grad school papers, in private conversations, and in the ongoing development of my own thoughts and practices. The concept of neuroqueer, or of neuroqueering (I’ve always seen it as a verb first and an adjective second), increasingly came to inform my thinking, my embodiment, and my approach to life.

2008 年春季，我在为研究生课程撰写的一篇论文中首次创造了"神经酷儿"这个术语。在随后的几年里，我通过更多研究生论文、私人对话以及自身思想与实践的持续发展，不断探索这个概念。神经酷儿或神经酷儿化（我始终视其为动词优先于形容词）的概念，日益深刻地影响着我的思维方式、身体实践以及生活态度。



When I first started publishing pieces of my writing on neurodiversity in 2012, I wasn’t ready to put the term neuroqueer out into the world yet. I wanted more time to let it simmer, to think and feel my way into its nuances and implications. In early 2014, though, I mentioned it in in a small private Facebook group for autistic bloggers, and discovered that my friend and colleague Athena Lynn Michaels-Dillon had also come up with the term independently and had also been playing around with it, letting it simmer, and thinking about putting it into publication eventually. Another dear friend and colleague, Remi Yergeau, who was also in that discussion, revealed that although the term neuroqueer was new for them, they’d been thinking along quite similar and compatible lines in playing with the concept of “neurological queerness.”

2012 年我开始陆续发表关于神经多样性的文章时，尚未准备好将"神经酷儿"这个术语公之于众。我想多花些时间让它沉淀，通过思考与感受来探索其细微差别与深层含义。然而在 2014 年初，我在一个孤独谱系博主的小型私人脸书群组中提及了这个词，发现我的朋友兼同事雅典娜·林恩·迈克尔斯-狄龙也独立提出了相同的术语，并且同样在反复推敲、沉淀酝酿，计划最终将其发表。另一位挚友兼同事雷米·耶尔戈也在那次讨论中坦言，虽然"神经酷儿"对他们而言是个新词，但他们一直在沿着高度相似且兼容的思路，探索"神经酷儿性"这一概念。



The three of us—Athena, Remi, and I—emerged from that conversation freshly inspired to begin introducing the term, and the set of concepts and practices it describes, into our public work and into our communities and the broader culture. Athena and I, along with our friend B. Martin Allen and others, founded the independent worker-owned publishing house Autonomous Press, and its imprint NeuroQueer Books, to publish books with neuroqueer themes (including the annual Spoon Knife multi-genre neuroqueer lit anthology).

我们三人——雅典娜、雷米和我——在那次对话后深受启发，开始将这个词及其所描述的概念与实践体系引入我们的公共工作、社群及更广泛的文化中。雅典娜、我与友人 B·马丁·艾伦等人共同创立了独立员工所有制出版社"自主出版社"及其旗下品牌"神经酷儿书系"，专门出版神经酷儿主题的书籍（包括年度多体裁神经酷儿文学选集《勺子刀》）。



Meanwhile, a couple of other members of that little Facebook group, who were involved in the discussion where Athena and Remi and I first discovered we’d each been playing with the same concept, became so excited about this new term that they immediately ran out and started spreading it around on various social media platforms. The word caught on like wildfire, much faster than its creators had imagined and much faster than we could keep up with. Soon it was showing up not only all over queer and neurodivergent social media spaces, but also in academic papers and conference presentations by people we’d never heard of.

与此同时，那个小型脸书群组中参与讨论的另外几位成员——正是我们三人首次发现彼此都在探索相同概念的讨论参与者——对这个新术语兴奋不已，立即开始在各种社交媒体平台上传播。这个词如野火般迅速蔓延，其传播速度远超创造者的想象，也快得让我们难以跟上。很快，它不仅出现在酷儿与神经殊异社群的社交媒体空间，还出现在我们素未谋面之人的学术论文和会议报告中。



(The day before I wrote this piece, I was at California Institute of Integral Studies teaching a new course on neurodiversity. I was introducing my students to basic neurodiversity-related terminology like neurotypical and neurodivergent, when a young undergraduate excitedly asked me, “Have you ever heard of the term neuroqueer?”)

（在我写这篇文章的前一天，我正在加州整合研究学院教授一门关于神经多样性的新课程。当时我正在向学生们介绍与神经多样性相关的基础术语，比如神经典型和神经殊异，这时一位年轻的本科生兴奋地问我：“你听说过‘神经酷儿’这个词吗？”）



It was nice to see it catch on like that. There’s a special kind of joy in bringing something new into the world and seeing it become meaningful to a lot of other people whom one hasn’t even met. On the downside, the word was almost instantly appropriated by people whose understanding of it was far more narrow and simplistic than its creators had intended. I’ve seen a lot of interpretations of neuroqueer and attempts at definition from folks who’ve adopted the term, and sometimes those interpretations miss the point in ways that are truly facepalm-worthy. Other interpretations are a bit more on-point but overly narrow, and I find myself responding with, “Yeah, well, I suppose that’s part of what we were getting at…”

看到这个词如此受欢迎，真是令人欣慰。将某种新事物带入世界，并看到它成为许多素未谋面的人心中有意义的存在，这是一种特别的喜悦。但另一方面，这个词几乎立刻就被那些对其理解远比创造者意图更狭隘、更简单化的人所挪用。我见过许多人对“神经酷儿”的解读和定义尝试，有时这些解读完全偏离了重点，令人无语。其他一些解读则稍微切中要害，但过于狭隘，以至于我不得不回应说：“嗯，我想那只是我们想表达的一部分……”



So what were we getting at? What is neuroqueer (or neuroqueerness, or neuroqueering)?

那么，我们到底想表达什么呢？什么是神经酷儿（或神经酷儿性，或神经酷儿化）？



I should first of all acknowledge that any effort to establish an “authoritative” definition of neuroqueer is in some sense inherently doomed and ridiculous, simply because the sort of people who identify as neuroqueer and engage in neuroqueering tend to be the sort of people who delight in subverting definitions, concepts, and authority.

首先必须承认，任何试图为"神经酷儿"确立"权威"定义的努力，本质上都注定是徒劳且荒谬的——因为那些自认神经酷儿并践行神经酷儿化的人，往往正是热衷于颠覆定义、概念与权威的那类人。



That said, the eight-point definition that follows is the closest thing to an “authoritative”  (or at least creator-authorized) definition as is ever likely to exist. I wrote it with the input and approval of the other originators of the concept—so it’s the one definition out there that all of the originators have agreed is not only accurate, but also inclusive of all of the various practices and ways-of-being that any of the three of us intended the word to encompass.

话虽如此，以下八点定义仍是目前最接近"权威"（或至少经创作者授权）的版本。我在其他两位概念创始人的参与和认可下撰写此定义——这是所有创始人一致认同的版本，不仅准确无误，更包容了我们三人各自期望该词涵盖的所有实践方式与存在形态。



I originally conceived of neuroqueer as a verb: neuroqueering as the practice of queering (subverting, defying, disrupting, liberating oneself from) neuronormativity and heteronormativity simultaneously. It was an extension of the way queer is used as a verb in Queer Theory; I was expanding the Queer Theory conceptualization of queering to encompass the queering of neurocognitive norms as well as gender norms—and, in the process, I was examining how socially-imposed neuronormativity and socially-imposed heteronormativity were entwined with one another, and how the queering of either of those two forms of normativity entwined with and blended into the queering of the other one.

我最初将神经酷儿构想为一个动词：神经酷儿化是指同时酷儿化（颠覆、反抗、瓦解、解放自身于）神经规范性和异性恋规范性的实践。这是对酷儿理论中"酷儿"作为动词用法的延伸——我将酷儿理论中"酷儿化"的概念范畴扩展至涵盖对神经认知规范与性别规范的酷儿化。在此过程中，我审视了社会强加的神经规范性与社会强加的异性恋规范性如何相互交织，以及这两种规范性中任何一种的酷儿化如何与另一种的酷儿化相互缠绕、彼此交融。



So neuroqueer was a verb first, and then, like its root word queer, it was also an adjective. Even in that first paper in which I used the term in 2008, I used it as both a verb and an adjective. As a verb, it refers to a broad range of interrelated practices. As an adjective, it describes things that are associated with those practices or that result from those practices: neuroqueer theory, neuroqueer perspectives, neuroqueer embodiments, neuroqueer narratives, neuroqueer literature, neuroqueer art, neuroqueer culture, neuroqueer spaces.

因此，“神经酷儿”最初是一个动词，随后像其词根“酷儿”一样，也成为了形容词。即便在 2008 年首次使用该术语的论文中，我也同时将其用作动词和形容词。作为动词，它指代一系列相互关联的实践；作为形容词，它描述与这些实践相关或由此产生的事物：神经酷儿理论、神经酷儿视角、神经酷儿具身化、神经酷儿叙事、神经酷儿文学、神经酷儿艺术、神经酷儿文化、神经酷儿空间。



And, just like queer, the adjective form of neuroqueer can also serve as a label of social identity. One can neuroqueer, and one can be neuroqueer. A neuroqueer individual is any individual whose identity, selfhood, gender performance, and/or neurocognitive style have in some way been shaped by their engagement in practices of neuroqueering, regardless of what gender, sexual orientation, or style of neurocognitive functioning they may have been born with.

正如“酷儿”一词，神经酷儿的形容词形式也可作为社会身份标签。一个人可以“进行神经酷儿实践”，也可以“成为神经酷儿”。神经酷儿个体是指其身份、自我认知、性别表现和/或神经认知风格在某种程度上因参与神经酷儿实践而塑造的人，无论其天生性别、性取向或神经认知功能模式如何。



Or, to put it more concisely (but perhaps more confusingly): you’re neuroqueer if you neuroqueer.

或者更简洁（但可能更令人困惑）地说：如果你进行神经酷儿实践，你就是神经酷儿。



So what does it mean to neuroqueer, as a verb? What are the various practices that fall within the definition of neuroqueering?

那么，作为动词的“神经酷儿化”意味着什么？哪些实践属于神经酷儿化的范畴？




Being both neurodivergent and queer, with some degree of conscious awareness and/or active exploration around how these two aspects of one’s being entwine and interact (or are, perhaps, mutually constitutive and inseparable).

既具有神经殊异性又具有酷儿身份，同时在一定程度上自觉意识到和/或主动探索自身这两个方面如何交织互动（或可能相互构成、不可分割）。



Embodying and expressing one’s neurodivergence in ways that also queer one’s performance of gender, sexuality, ethnicity, and/or other aspects of one’s identity.

以同时酷儿化自身性别、性取向、族裔及其他身份面向的方式，具身化并表达自身的神经殊异性。



Engaging in practices intended to undo and subvert one’s own cultural conditioning and one’s ingrained habits of neuronormative and heteronormative performance, with the aim of reclaiming one’s capacity to give more full expression to one’s uniquely weird potentials and inclinations.

参与旨在解构和颠覆自身文化规训、以及内化的神经规范与异性恋规范表演习惯的实践，以重新获得更充分表达自身独特怪异潜能与倾向的能力。



Engaging in the queering of one’s own neurocognitive processes (and one’s outward embodiment and expression of those processes) by intentionally altering them in ways that create significant and lasting increase in one’s divergence from prevailing cultural standards of neuronormativity and heteronormativity.

通过有意改变自身的神经认知过程（以及这些过程的外在体现与表达），使其与主流文化标准中的神经常态与异性恋常态产生显著且持久的偏离，从而对自身的神经认知过程进行酷儿化改造。



Approaching, embodying, and/or experiencing one’s neurodivergence as a form of queerness (e.g., in ways that are inspired by, or similar to, the ways in which queerness is understood and approached in Queer Theory, Gender Studies, and/or queer activism).

将自身的神经殊异性视为一种酷儿形态来接近、体现和/或体验（例如，借鉴或类似酷儿理论、性别研究和/或酷儿行动主义中理解与对待酷儿的方式）。



Producing literature, art, scholarship, and/or other cultural artifacts that foreground neuroqueer experiences, perspectives, and voices.

创作以神经酷儿经历、视角和声音为核心的文学、艺术、学术研究和/或其他文化作品。



Producing critical responses to literature and/or other cultural artifacts, focusing on intentional or unintentional characterizations of neuroqueerness and how those characterizations illuminate and/or are illuminated by actual neuroqueer lives and experiences.

对文学和/或其他文化作品进行批判性回应，聚焦于其中有意或无意对神经酷儿特质的刻画，并探讨这些刻画如何揭示或被真实的神经酷儿生活与经历所揭示。



Working to transform social and cultural environments in order to create spaces and communities—and ultimately a society—in which engagement in any or all of the above practices is permitted, accepted, supported, and encouraged.

致力于改造社会和文化环境，以创造空间和社群——最终构建一个社会——在其中，参与上述任何一种或全部实践的行为，都能得到允许、接纳、支持和鼓励。




So there you have it, from the people who brought you the term. This definition is, again, not an authoritative “last word” on the subject, because that would be a silly thing to attempt. Rather, I hope this will be taken as a “first word”—a broad “working definition” from which further theory, practice, and play will proceed.

以上就是来自提出该术语的人们给出的定义。再次强调，这并非关于该主题的权威“最终定论”，因为试图给出那样的定论是愚蠢的。相反，我希望这能被视作一个“初步定义”——一个宽泛的“工作定义”，由此展开进一步的理论、实践与探索。



Happy neuroqueering!

祝神经酷儿化愉快！







---


Nick_ebook-32










Comments on “Neuroqueer:

An Introduction”

关于《神经酷儿：导论》的评论



Around the same time “Neuroqueer: An Introduction” appeared on my Neurocosmopolitanism website, Autonomous Press published the first edition of Athena Lynn Michaels-Dillon’s semi-autobiographical neuroqueer novella Defiant (written under the pen name Michael Scott Monje). The word neuroqueer didn’t appear in the text of Defiant, but its appearance on the back cover marked the word’s first time in print.

大约在《神经酷儿：导论》发表于我的 Neurocosmopolitanism 网站的同时，Autonomous Press 出版了 Athena Lynn Michaels-Dillon（笔名 Michael Scott Monje）的半自传体神经酷儿中篇小说《反抗》。虽然"神经酷儿"一词并未出现在《反抗》的正文中，但该词首次以印刷形式出现是在其封底上。



Remi Yergeau, who at the time of our first discussion of neuroqueer(ing) had been playing around with the concept of autism as “neurological queerness” in the book they were working on, integrated the term neuroqueer into their manuscript, citing and quoting “Neuroqueer: An Introduction.” Remi’s book was published by Duke University Press in 2018 under the title Authoring Autism: On Rhetoric and Neurological Queerness; as of this writing, it remains the single best and most comprehensive critique of the rhetoric of the pathology paradigm and how the pathology paradigm informs (or rather, deforms) the discourse on autism and autistics.

Remi Yergeau 在我们首次讨论神经酷儿（化）概念时，正在其著作中探索将孤独症视为"神经酷儿性"的理念。她将"神经酷儿"一词整合进手稿，并引用《神经酷儿：导论》的内容。Remi 的著作于 2018 年由杜克大学出版社出版，书名为《书写孤独症：论修辞与神经酷儿性》；截至本文撰写时，该书仍是对病理范式修辞及其如何影响（更确切地说是扭曲）关于孤独症与孤独症人士论述的最佳且最全面的批判性著作。



My own work has been focused primarily on two aspects of neuroqueer(ing). The first aspect is neuroqueering as embodied practice—playing with the synthesis of the neurodiversity paradigm, queer theory, the field of somatic psychology, and transformative movement practices like aikido and physical theater. Neuroqueering as somatic praxis has been central to my conception of neuroqueer from the start. The 2008 grad school paper in which I first coined the term neuroqueer was written for the magnificent Dr. Ian J.
