Grand’s magnificent Psychodynamics course in the Somatic Psychology program at California Institute of Integral Studies. Ian Grand shuffled off this mortal coil in 2017, and as of 2021 I’m teaching that same Psychodynamics course myself—doing my best to make the classroom a queerly creative space, or perhaps a creatively queer space, just like Ian made his classroom the sort of creative space into which a concept like neuroqueer could be born.

我个人的研究主要聚焦于神经酷儿（化）的两个方面。第一个方面是将神经酷儿化作为具身实践——融合神经多样性范式、酷儿理论、躯体心理学领域，以及合气道、形体戏剧等变革性运动实践。从最初构想神经酷儿概念时，神经酷儿化作为躯体实践就始终处于核心位置。2008 年我在研究生课程论文中首次提出"神经酷儿"这一术语，正是为加州整合研究学院躯体心理学项目中伊恩·J·格兰德博士那门精彩的《心理动力学》课程所撰写。伊恩·格兰德于 2017 年离世，而到 2021 年，我已亲自教授同一门《心理动力学》课程——竭尽全力将课堂打造成酷儿化的创意空间，或者说创意性的酷儿空间，正如伊恩当年将他的课堂塑造成能让神经酷儿这类概念诞生的创意场域。



The second aspect of neuroqueer(ing) on which I’ve been focused is the fostering of neuroqueer literature. In my role as Managing Editor at Autonomous Press, especially through my involvement in our annual Spoon Knife literary anthology, I’ve done my best to contribute in any way I can to the development of an explicitly neuroqueer literature, particularly what I see as an emerging genre of neuroqueer speculative fiction.

我关注的神经酷儿（化）的第二个方面，是培育神经酷儿文学。作为 Autonomous Press 的执行编辑，特别是通过参与年度文学选集《Spoon Knife》，我尽己所能为发展明确的神经酷儿文学贡献力量，尤其是我认为正在兴起的神经酷儿思辨小说流派。



•



The use of the adjective neuroqueer as a label of social identity, like gay or trans or Asian-American, wasn’t part of my original conception of the word back in 2008. My background in transformative practices like aikido and zazen inclines me to focus more on practice than on fixed identity categories, and defining the sort of work I wanted to do was far more interesting to me than defining myself.

将形容词"神经酷儿"用作社会身份标签（如同"同性恋"、"跨性别"或"亚裔美国人"），并非我 2008 年最初构想的词义。我在合气道、坐禅等转化性实践中的背景，使我更关注实践而非固定的身份类别——定义我想从事的工作，远比定义自我更令我感兴趣。



Six years later, though, as I discussed neuroqueer(ing) with Athena Lynn Michaels-Dillon and Remi Yergeau for the first time, we recognized that if we put this word out into the world and it caught on, some folks probably were going to adopt it as an identity label. We were okay with that possibility. We figured that if identifying as neuroqueer helped anyone to understand and define themselves—or, better still, to transform and create themselves—in a way that was liberating and empowering for them, then yay, we were all for it.

然而，六年后，当我首次与雅典娜·林恩·迈克尔斯-迪伦和雷米·耶尔戈讨论“神经酷儿（化）”时，我们意识到，如果我们将这个词公之于众并流行起来，有些人可能会将其用作身份标签。我们对此持开放态度。我们想，如果认同为神经酷儿能帮助任何人以解放和赋权的方式理解并定义自己——甚至更好地改造和创造自己——那么，太好了，我们全力支持。



And that is, in fact, what’s been happening. While a growing number of people use neuroqueer as the dual-purpose verb/adjective I originally intended it to be, many have also found it meaningful and empowering as a term of identity. I hear from them sometimes, or meet them, or see them talk about it online. It’s made a positive difference for some folks to be able to describe themselves as neuroqueer, and this makes me happy just like it makes me happy when someone tells me that their lives have been changed for the better by my teaching or my writing. I’m glad to have offered something that makes a difference to someone.

而事实上，这正是正在发生的事。尽管越来越多的人将“神经酷儿”作为我最初设想的双功能动词/形容词使用，但许多人发现它作为身份术语同样富有意义且具有赋权作用。我偶尔会收到他们的来信，或与他们相遇，或在网上看到他们讨论这个词。对一些人来说，能够将自己描述为神经酷儿带来了积极改变，这让我感到欣慰——就像有人告诉我，我的教学或写作让他们的生活变得更好时一样快乐。我很高兴能提供一些对他人有所影响的东西。



What doesn’t make me so happy, though, is that some of the people who’ve adopted neuroqueer as a term of identity have also tried to redefine the term in a narrow and exclusionary way, and have appointed themselves the arbiters of who gets call themselves neuroqueer.

不过，让我不太高兴的是，有些将“神经酷儿”作为身份标签的人，试图以狭隘排他的方式重新定义这个词，并自封为评判谁能自称神经酷儿的仲裁者。



So, let me make this clear: the essay “Neuroqueer: An Introduction” contains an intentionally broad list of practices that fall within the definition of neuroqueering. Anyone who engages in any of those practices can call themselves neuroqueer anytime they damn well want to. Anyone who says otherwise is misappropriating a concept intended to be liberatory, and turning it into just another excuse to form a special little club that they can exclude other people from to make themselves feel more important. Anyone trying to police other people’s self-identities is just another tedious cop, and a cop is pretty much the most un-queer, non-liberatory thing a person can be.

所以，让我把话说清楚：《神经酷儿：导论》一文中列举的神经酷儿实践清单本就是有意宽泛的。任何人只要从事其中任何一项实践，随时都可以自称神经酷儿。若有人对此说三道四，那便是盗用了一个本应具有解放意义的概念，将其变成又一种借口——组建一个排他性小团体，通过排斥他人来彰显自身重要性。任何试图干涉他人自我认同的人，不过是又一个令人厌烦的“警察”，而“警察”恰恰是最不酷儿、最不具解放性的存在。



It doesn’t matter whether a person was born autistic, or born neurodivergent in any way. It doesn’t matter what their gender or sexual orientation is. If they engage in neuroqueering, and they want to call themselves neuroqueer, they’re welcome to, and it’s no one else’s business. A person who starts out neurotypical and heterosexual and cisgender, and chooses to intentionally engage in neuroqueering by creatively altering their own consciousness in ways that simultaneously queer their gender performance, has just as valid a claim to considering themselves neuroqueer as someone who was born autistic and gay.

一个人是天生的孤独谱系，还是以任何方式天生神经殊异，这并不重要。他们的性别或性取向是什么，也不重要。如果他们从事神经酷儿化实践，并且希望称自己为神经酷儿，他们完全有权利这样做，这不关任何人的事。一个原本神经典型、异性恋且顺性别的人，如果选择通过创造性地改变自身意识来刻意参与神经酷儿化，同时以此方式酷儿化其性别表现，那么他们与天生是孤独谱系且同性恋的人一样，有充分理由将自己视为神经酷儿。



If you see anyone trying to narrow the definition of neuroqueer and trying to police who gets to use the term, feel free to tell them that I said to stop acting like a fucking cop. The world needs more queering and fewer cops.

如果你看到有人试图窄化神经酷儿的定义，并试图管控谁可以使用这个词，请尽管告诉他们，我说过别他妈像个警察一样行事。这个世界需要更多的酷儿化，而不是更多的警察。







---


Nick_ebook-33










A Horizon of Possibility: Some Notes on Neuroqueer Theory

可能性的地平线：关于神经酷儿理论的一些笔记



I’m typing these words on a cool foggy morning in Berkeley, California, in the Summer of 2021, and trying to wrap my brain around the fact that it’s been fifteen years since I coined the term neuroqueer, seven years since the term leaked out into the sphere of public discourse via social media and began catching on considerably faster than I’d expected, and six years since I first published a brief working definition in the essay “Neuroqueer: An Introduction.”

2021 年夏天，我在加州伯克利一个凉爽多雾的早晨敲下这些文字，努力让自己接受一个事实：距离我创造"神经酷儿"这个术语已经过去十五年，距离它通过社交媒体渗入公共话语领域并开始以远超预期的速度流行起来已有七年，距离我首次在论文《神经酷儿：导论》中发表简短的工作定义也已六年。



The concept of neuroqueer was born shortly after my daughter, and like my daughter it has a life of its own now and gets involved in all sorts of mischief that I don’t find out about until well after it’s happened. A lot of folks—most of whom I’ve never had any direct personal contact with—have adopted the term, used it in all manner of interesting ways in a variety of interesting contexts, and explored various aspects of its implications and potentials. I think this is fabulous.

神经酷儿这个概念诞生于我女儿出生后不久，如今它和我女儿一样拥有了自己的生命，在我毫不知情的情况下卷入各种奇遇，直到事后很久我才知晓。许多人——其中绝大多数我从未有过直接接触——采纳了这个术语，在各种有趣的语境中以各种有趣的方式使用它，并探索了其内涵与潜能的诸多面向。我认为这简直妙不可言。



For my own part, while my life and work have been increasingly informed by neuroqueer principles and practices—and while I’ve been closely involved in the emerging field of neuroqueer speculative fiction as both an author and an editor—apart from that little “Neuroqueer: An Introduction” essay I somehow haven’t gotten around to writing up and publishing anything substantial about my own take on the meaning of neuroqueer or about the vistas of theory, praxis, and possibility toward which I’ve always intended the term to point. So this is where I finally get around to it.

就我个人而言，尽管我的生活与工作日益受到神经酷儿原则与实践的启发——且作为作者和编辑，我一直深度参与新兴的神经酷儿思辨小说领域——但除了那篇简短的《神经酷儿：导论》文章外，我竟始终未能抽身撰写并发表任何关于我对神经酷儿内涵的见解，或是我始终希望该术语指向的理论、实践与可能性图景的实质性内容。因此，此刻我终于着手完成此事。



The conceptualization of Neuroqueer Theory I’m presenting here is essentially the same as what I had in mind when I first came up with the term neuroqueer in 2008—though after a decade and a half of putting the theory into practice, and of refining both my ideas and my dubious writing skills, I can now articulate these concepts somewhat more clearly than I ever managed to do in my original awkward (and thankfully unpublished) grad school papers.

我在此呈现的神经酷儿理论概念化，本质上与 2008 年我首次提出"神经酷儿"一词时的构想一致——尽管经过十五年将理论付诸实践，并不断打磨我的观点与拙劣的写作技巧后，如今我能比当初那些笨拙（且幸未发表的）研究生论文更清晰地阐述这些概念。



Four Realizations

四大领悟



The majority of people grow up believing their culture’s socially-constructed gender norms to be “natural,” and believing their socially-assigned gender roles and acquired habits of heteronormative gender performance to be innate and predetermined by biology. Queer Theory offers a different perspective, a perspective which recognizes the myriad ways in which the prevailing culture and its institutions work continually to impose heteronormative gender roles on each and every person, and to ingrain and enforce the performance of these roles—and a perspective which recognizes, also, that it is the sheer pervasiveness of this ongoing process which creates the compelling illusion that heteronormative gender roles are innate and natural. (Note that gender, as I’m using the term here, includes sexuality and sexual orientation, since heteronormative sexual behavior is part of the culturally-mandated performance of heteronormative gender roles.)

大多数人从小便相信，其文化中社会建构的性别规范是“自然的”，并认为社会赋予的性别角色以及后天习得的异性恋规范性别表现，是与生俱来且由生物性决定的。酷儿理论提供了另一种视角——它揭示了主流文化及其制度如何持续不断地将异性恋规范性别角色强加于每个人，并深化与固化这些角色的表演；同时，这一视角也认识到，正是这种无处不在的持续过程，才制造出异性恋规范性别角色与生俱来且自然的令人信服的幻觉。（需注意，此处使用的“性别”概念包含性欲与性取向，因为异性恋规范性行为本身即是文化所规定的异性恋规范性别角色表演的一部分。）



A central concept in Queer Theory, perhaps best articulated by Judith Butler in Gender Trouble, is that one’s gender is constituted by one’s ongoing performance of culturally conditioned habits of embodiment and activity. One’s gender, in other words, is first and foremost something that one does—and therein lies the possibility of liberation from the confines of normativity. If gender is maintained through the habitual performance of specific actions, then heteronormativity and heteronormative gender roles can be subverted, transformed, modified, loosened, escaped from, and/or rendered more fluid, through engagement in practices that creatively deviate from and fuck with heteronormative performance. To engage in such practices is commonly referred to as queering.

酷儿理论中的一个核心概念（或许由朱迪斯·巴特勒在《性别麻烦》中阐述得最为透彻）是：一个人的性别是由其持续表演文化制约下的身体习惯与行为模式所构成的。换言之，一个人的性别首先且最重要的是其"所做之事"——而解放的可能性正蕴含于此。如果性别是通过特定行为的习惯性表演来维持的，那么通过参与那些创造性偏离并颠覆异性恋规范表演的实践，异性恋规范及其性别角色就能被颠覆、转化、修正、松动、逃离，和/或变得更加流动。从事此类实践的行为通常被称为"酷儿化"。



The concept of neuroqueering came to me in 2008 when I was a grad student majoring in somatic psychology, a field which among other things studies how the organization and functioning of the psyche are entwined with the organization and usage of the body. I was writing a paper about how it harms autistic people to suppress their distinctively autistic modes of movement and embodiment in the interest of passing for neurotypical. Since the degree program I was in encouraged introspection and self-awareness, the paper included discussion of my own experience of masking my autistic modes of embodiment in order to survive my brutal childhood and young adulthood—and my subsequent process of learning to unmask and recover those autistic modes of embodiment (a project I was only just beginning to explore at that time, which eventually proved to be life-changing and which is still ongoing). As I worked on the paper, four realizations struck me in rapid succession:

神经酷儿化这一概念诞生于 2008 年，当时我正攻读躯体心理学研究生课程。这个领域研究心理的组织与运作如何与身体的组织与使用相互交织。当时我正在撰写一篇论文，探讨为了伪装成神经典型者而压抑孤独谱系群体特有的运动与具身模式会对其造成怎样的伤害。由于就读的学位课程鼓励内省与自我觉察，论文中包含了我在残酷的童年与青年时期为求生存而伪装孤独谱系具身模式的亲身经历——以及随后学习卸下伪装、重新找回这些孤独谱系具身模式的历程（这个当时才刚开始探索的项目，最终证明彻底改变了我的人生，至今仍在持续进行）。在撰写论文的过程中，四个顿悟接连击中了我：




The process of suppressing my visible expressions of autistic embodiment and trying to pass for neurotypical for the sake of survival in my younger years seemed remarkably similar to the process of suppressing my femininity and trying to pass as a cisgender heterosexual male for the sake of survival in my younger years.

为了在年轻时生存而压抑自己孤独谱系特质的可见表达、试图伪装成神经典型者的过程，与我为了在年轻时生存而压抑自己的女性气质、试图伪装成顺性别异性恋男性的过程，惊人地相似。



If the process of liberating myself from my acquired habits of masculine gender performance and letting myself embody more fluid and feminine gender expressions could be described as a process of queering heteronormativity, then perhaps the process of liberating myself from my acquired habits of neurotypical performance and letting myself embody my neurodivergence could be described as queering neuronormativity.

如果说，将自己从后天习得的男性性别表演习惯中解放出来、允许自己展现更流动和女性化的性别表达的过程，可以被描述为对异性恋规范的酷儿化，那么，将自己从后天习得的神经典型表演习惯中解放出来、允许自己展现神经殊异性的过程，或许可以被描述为对神经规范的酷儿化。



The more I reflected on the process by which I was pushed into the ill-fitting confines of heteronormative gender performance and the process by which I was pushed into the ill-fitting confines of neuronormative performance, the more it became clear that the two processes weren’t merely similar or parallel: they were deeply and thoroughly entwined with one another, with no solid dividing line between them. Ultimately it wasn’t two similar and parallel processes I was looking at, but a single multifaceted process.

我越是反思自己被推入异性恋规范性别表演的狭隘框架的过程，以及被推入神经规范表演的狭隘框架的过程，就越清楚地意识到，这两个过程不仅相似或平行，而是深刻而彻底地交织在一起，彼此之间没有明确的界限。最终，我所看到的并非两个相似且平行的过程，而是一个多层面的单一过程。



If the social imposition of heteronormative performance was inseparably entwined with the social imposition of neuronormative performance, then the process of liberating myself from the confines of heteronormative performance was also inseparably entwined with the process of liberating myself from neuronormative performance. The queering of heteronormativity and the queering of neuronormativity were interconnected at some fundamental level. I couldn’t truly liberate myself from heteronormativity without also liberating myself from neuronormativity, and I couldn’t truly liberate myself from neuronormativity without also liberating myself from heteronormativity.

如果异性恋规范表演的社会强加与神经规范表演的社会强加密不可分地交织在一起，那么我从异性恋规范表演的束缚中解放自己的过程，也与从神经规范表演中解放自己的过程密不可分地交织在一起。对异性恋规范的酷儿化与对神经规范的酷儿化在某种根本层面上相互关联。我无法在不解放自己于神经规范的情况下真正解放自己于异性恋规范，也无法在不解放自己于异性恋规范的情况下真正解放自己于神经规范。




As I contemplated these realizations, the word neuroqueer suggested itself to me almost instantly. I incorporated the word into that paper I was working on, and ever since then I’ve been exploring its potentials as a foundation for creative theory-building and practice.

当我思考这些领悟时，“神经酷儿”这个词几乎立刻浮现在我脑海中。我将这个词融入了当时正在撰写的论文中，自那以后，我一直在探索它作为创造性理论构建与实践基础的潜力。



Beyond Neuroessentialism

超越神经本质主义



The majority of thinkers within the neurodiversity movement and the emerging field of Neurodiversity Studies have thus far tended to view human neurodiversity through an essentialist lens in which each individual is seen as being neurotypical because they were born neurotypical, or neurodivergent because they were born neurodivergent (or because they became neurodivergent due to some event such as trauma or illness that significantly altered their neurocognitive functioning). This essentialist understanding of neurodiversity, which we might describe as neuroessentialism, has admittedly been useful in some respects. Much of the important work of the neurodiversity movement up to the present day has proceeded from the recognition that a great many people are indeed born neurodivergent—meaning that their bodyminds are predisposed to modes of functioning that are incompatible with neuronormative performance—and that attempting to force these people to comply with the standards of neuronormative performance is harmful, unethical, and oppressive. Without this understanding, a neurodiversity movement probably wouldn’t have come into existence.

迄今为止，神经多样性运动及新兴的神经多样性研究领域中的大多数思想家，倾向于通过本质主义的视角看待人类神经多样性。在这种视角下，每个人被视为天生神经典型者或天生神经殊异者（或因创伤、疾病等显著改变神经认知功能的事件而成为神经殊异者）。这种对神经多样性的本质主义理解——我们可称之为"神经本质主义"——诚然在某些方面具有实用性。神经多样性运动至今的重要工作，大多源于这样的认知：确实有大量人群天生神经殊异——这意味着他们的身心系统天生倾向于与神经规范表现不相容的功能模式——而强迫这些人遵守神经规范标准的行为具有危害性、不道德且充满压迫性。若缺乏这种认知，神经多样性运动或许根本不会诞生。



A neuroessentialist lens, however, also tends to impose artificial limitations on our sense of possibility. Here, again, we find parallels and connections between the realm of gender diversity and the realm of neurodiversity. The gender essentialist mindset, which can admit no gender possibilities other than two allegedly innate and immutable “biological sexes,” is inimical to gender creativity and to the realization of the infinite range of gender possibilities. By the same token, an overly neuroessentialist mindset—a mindset which conceives of human neurodiversity as consisting of little more than an assortment of largely innate and immutable “neurotypes” or “types of brains”—is an obstacle to the realization of the infinite range of neurocognitive possibilities, and to the realization of our full potentials for intentional creative queering of our minds.

然而，神经本质主义的视角也往往对我们的可能性感知施加人为限制。在此，我们再次发现性别多样性领域与神经多样性领域之间的平行与关联。性别本质主义思维模式——只承认两种所谓先天且不可改变的"生理性别"，排斥其他性别可能性——与性别创造力及无限性别可能性的实现背道而驰。同理，过度神经本质主义的思维模式——将人类神经多样性简化为一系列先天且不可改变的"神经类型"或"大脑类型"——同样阻碍着无限神经认知可能性的实现，也阻碍着我们充分发挥有意识创造性地重塑心智的潜能。



I’m not saying that it’s not potentially useful for people to recognize themselves as autistic or dyslexic or whatever. When not pathologized or stigmatized, such categories can serve a variety of important purposes—including helping people to better understand themselves, to understand and communicate about their access needs and their experiences, and to connect with and work in solidarity with others who have similar neurocognitive tendencies and needs. What I’m saying here is that we shouldn’t allow our conception of neurodiversity and its potentials to be constrained by such categories, just as we shouldn’t allow our conceptions of gender and sexuality to be constrained by the binaristic categories of male and female, or gay and straight.

我并非否认人们将自己识别为孤独谱系、阅读障碍或其他类别可能具有潜在价值。当这些分类不被病理化或污名化时，它们可以发挥多种重要作用——包括帮助人们更好地理解自己，理解并沟通自身的无障碍需求与经历，以及与具有相似神经认知倾向和需求的他人建立联系并团结协作。我在此强调的是，我们不应让神经多样性及其潜能的认知被这些分类所束缚，正如我们不应让性别与性取向的认知被男女二元或同性恋/异性恋的二元分类所限制一样。



Public discourses on human diversity, including the discourses on gender, sexual orientation, and neurodiversity, occur almost entirely within the framework of identity politics—a framework which is fundamentally essentialist, since it involves sorting people into identity categories which tend to be presented as largely innate and immutable. Those who are accustomed to viewing queerness through this lens are often surprised to learn that the field of Queer Theory tends to reject essentialism and thus to depart radically from the premises of identity politics.

关于人类多样性的公共论述，包括关于性别、性取向和神经多样性的论述，几乎完全在身份政治的框架内展开——这一框架本质上是本质主义的，因为它涉及将人们归入通常被视为先天且不可改变的身份类别。那些习惯于通过这种视角看待酷儿现象的人，往往会惊讶地发现，酷儿理论领域倾向于拒绝本质主义，从而从根本上背离了身份政治的前提。



In conceptualizing gender as being constructed through ongoing socially instilled performances which can be subverted and altered (i.e., queered), Queer Theory frames identity as a fluid byproduct of activity: gender and sexuality are first and foremost things that one does, rather than things that one is, and queer is a verb first and an adjective second. In other words, one is queer not because one was born immutably queer on some sort of essential genetic level, but because one acts in ways which queer heteronormativity (e.g., going outside the boundaries of the binary gender category to which one was assigned at birth, or engaging in non-heteronormative sexual activity).

在将性别概念化为通过持续的社会灌输表演构建而成（这些表演可以被颠覆和改变，即被酷儿化）的过程中，酷儿理论将身份视为活动的流动副产品：性别与性取向首先是人们所做的事情，而非人们所是的本质，而酷儿首先是动词，其次才是形容词。换言之，一个人之所以是酷儿，并非因为其在某种本质基因层面上生来就是不可改变的酷儿，而是因为其以酷儿化异性恋规范的方式行事（例如，超越出生时被指定的二元性别范畴边界，或参与非异性恋规范的性活动）。



This is the case with Neuroqueer Theory as well. While neurodivergent is a category of identity, neuroqueer is first and foremost a verb. Neuroqueering is a practice, or, more accurately, a continually emergent and potentially infinite array of practices—modes of creatively subversive and transformative action in which anyone can choose to engage.

神经酷儿理论亦是如此。虽然神经殊异是一个身份类别，但神经酷儿首先是一个动词。神经酷儿化是一种实践，更准确地说，是一系列持续涌现且可能无限多样的实践——任何人都可以选择参与的创造性颠覆与变革行动模式。



Of course, neuroqueer, like queer, can also function as an identity label. But while a person can be considered neurodivergent simply by virtue of having been born that way, what makes a person neuroqueer is their choice to engage in neuroqueering. One is neuroqueer not because one was born immutably neuroqueer, but because one acts in ways which queer neuronormativity (and remember that a core principle of Neuroqueer Theory is that neuronormativity and heteronormativity are fundamentally entwined with one another, and therefore any significant queering of neuronormativity is also inevitably a queering of heteronormativity).

当然，如同“酷儿”一词，“神经酷儿”也可以作为一种身份标签。然而，一个人可以因天生如此而被视为神经殊异，但成为神经酷儿的关键在于其主动选择参与“神经酷儿化”的行为。一个人之所以是神经酷儿，并非因其天生不可改变地属于神经酷儿，而是因其以酷儿化神经规范的方式行动（请记住，神经酷儿理论的核心原则之一，是神经规范与异性恋规范在根本上相互交织，因此任何对神经规范的重要酷儿化，也必然同时是对异性恋规范的酷儿化）。



Thus, Neuroqueer Theory applies the framework of Queer Theory to the realm of neurodiversity, and expands the scope of Queer Theory to encompass gender, sexuality, and neurodiversity, as well as the intersections of gender and sexuality with neurodiversity. As an extension of Queer Theory, Neuroqueer Theory is an approach to neurodiversity that radically departs from essentialist identity politics and seeks to transcend the constraints of neuroessentialism.

因此，神经酷儿理论将酷儿理论的框架应用于神经多样性领域，并将酷儿理论的范围扩展至涵盖性别、性取向与神经多样性，以及性别、性取向与神经多样性的交叉点。作为酷儿理论的延伸，神经酷儿理论是一种从根本上背离本质主义身份政治、并试图超越神经本质主义束缚的神经多样性研究路径。



My favorite articulation of Queer Theory’s transcendence of the limitations of essentialist identity politics is a single sentence penned in 1997 by queer theorist David M. Halperin. In his book Saint Foucault: Towards a Gay Hagiography, Halperin wrote:

我最喜欢酷儿理论超越本质主义身份政治局限性的表述，是酷儿理论家大卫·M·哈尔佩林在 1997 年写下的一句话。在其著作《圣福柯：迈向同性恋圣徒传》中，哈尔佩林写道：



“Queer,” in any case, does not designate a class of already objectified pathologies or perversions; rather, it describes a horizon of possibility whose precise extent and heterogeneous scope cannot in principle be delimited in advance.

“酷儿”一词无论如何都不指代一类已被物化的病理或变态；相反，它描述了一种可能性的地平线，其确切范围与异质性的广度在原则上无法预先界定。



This post-essentialist articulation of the meaning and potentials of queer also perfectly sums up my conception of the meaning and potentials of neuroqueer. Neuroqueer is not a mere synonym for neurodivergent, or for neurodivergent identity combined with queer identity. Neuroqueer is active subversion of both neuronormativity and heteronormativity. Neuroqueer is intentional noncompliance with the demands of normative performance. Neuroqueer is choosing to actively engage with one’s potentials for neurodivergence and queerness, and the intersections and synergies of those potentials. Neuroqueer is about recognizing the fundamentally entwined nature of cognition, gender, and embodiment, and also about treating cognition, gender, and embodiment as fluid and customizable, and as canvases for ongoing creative experimentation.

这种对酷儿意义与潜力的后本质主义阐述，也完美概括了我对神经酷儿意义与潜力的理解。神经酷儿并非神经殊异或神经殊异身份与酷儿身份结合的简单同义词。神经酷儿是对神经规范性与异性恋规范性的主动颠覆。神经酷儿是对规范性表演要求的有意违抗。神经酷儿是选择主动探索自身神经殊异与酷儿潜质，以及这些潜质相互交织与协同的可能性。神经酷儿既关乎认知、性别与具身性在本质上相互缠绕的特质，也主张将认知、性别与具身性视为流动可塑的载体，以及持续创造性实验的画布。



Neuroqueer transcends essentialist identity politics not only by treating identity as fluid and customizable, but also by being radically inclusive. Neuroqueering is something anyone can potentially do, and there are infinite possible ways to do it and infinite possible ways to be transformed by it. The term neuroqueer points to a horizon of creative possibility with which anyone can choose to engage.

神经酷儿超越了本质主义的身份政治，不仅将身份视为流动且可定制的，还通过彻底的包容性来实现这一点。神经酷儿化是任何人都可能参与的行为，有无数种方式可以实践它，也有无数种方式可以被它改变。这个词指向了一个创造可能性的地平线，任何人都可以选择与之互动。



I want to make it clear that I’m not in any way opposed to the use of the term neuroqueer as an identity label. Because I regard identity as fluid and customizable, and because I regard life as an ongoing process of self-creation, I’m in favor of people freely adopting any identity labels which might be meaningful to them. If identifying as neuroqueer serves in any way to improve your life or aid in your process of creative self-transformation, or even if it just appeals to you aesthetically, then go for it!

我想明确表示，我绝不反对将“神经酷儿”用作身份标签。因为我将身份视为流动且可定制的，并将生活视为持续的自我创造过程，我支持人们自由采用任何对他们有意义的身份标签。如果认同为神经酷儿能在任何方面改善你的生活，或有助于你创造性的自我转变过程，甚至只是它在审美上吸引你，那就大胆去做吧！



The reason I emphasize that neuroqueer is first and foremost a verb, and the reason I focus on neuroqueering as an emergent array of subversive and transformative practices, is that my central priority is the cultivation of human potentials for creativity, well-being, and beautiful weirdness—and our capacity to bring such potentials to realization ultimately depends not on our choice of identity labels but on our choice of practices. But of course, the strategic adoption of a new identity or name or label can itself function as a transformative practice.

我之所以强调神经酷儿首先是一个动词，并聚焦于神经酷儿化作为一系列涌现的颠覆性与变革性实践，是因为我的核心优先事项是培育人类在创造力、福祉与美妙怪异方面的潜能——而实现这些潜能的最终能力并不取决于我们选择的身份标签，而取决于我们选择的实践。当然，策略性地采用新的身份、名称或标签本身也可以成为一种变革性实践。



Performance & Predisposition

表现与倾向



While Neuroqueer Theory aims to transcend the limitations of essentialist identity politics, I also believe that the complete rejection of essentialism is a mistake which throws out the baby with the bathwater. Some prominent thinkers in the field of Queer Theory do reject essentialism completely, taking the position that gender is 100 percent socially constructed and socially instilled. My own position, which informs my conception of Neuroqueer Theory, is that both the essentialist and social constructionist models are overly reductionist when taken entirely on their own. I prefer a more complex hybrid understanding which incorporates elements of both models, and which probably boils down to something like 80 percent social constructionist and 20 percent essentialist. This hybrid understanding is based in the premise that although gender roles and the rules of gender performance are socially constructed and instilled, each individual human does also have their own unique set of more-or-less-innate tendencies and potentials (tendencies and potentials which have nothing whatsoever to do with the shape of a person’s genitals or with so-called “biological sex”).

尽管神经酷儿理论旨在超越本质主义身份政治的局限，但我同样认为完全摒弃本质主义是一种因噎废食的错误。酷儿理论领域的一些著名思想家确实完全拒绝本质主义，坚持性别是百分之百由社会建构和灌输的立场。而我的立场——这一立场也塑造了我对神经酷儿理论的构想——是本质主义模型与社会建构主义模型若各自独立来看都过于简化。我更倾向于一种融合两种模型要素的复合理解，其比例大致可归结为 80%的社会建构与 20%的本质主义。这种复合理解基于以下前提：尽管性别角色与性别表演规则由社会建构和灌输，但每个个体确实也拥有自己独特的、近乎与生俱来的倾向与潜能——这些倾向与潜能与个人生殖器形态或所谓的"生理性别"毫无关联。



The gender essentialist belief that heteronormative gender roles are innate and “natural” is patently absurd. First of all, the prevailing norms of gender role performance vary considerably from culture to culture, place to place, and historical period to historical period, with nearly every culture regarding its own current local norms as the one “natural” way to do gender. And second, if these norms were innate and “natural,” cultures wouldn’t have to put nearly so much effort into instilling and enforcing them.

认为异性恋规范的性别角色是与生俱来且“自然”的性别本质主义信念，显然是荒谬的。首先，不同文化、地域和历史时期的性别角色表现规范差异显著，而几乎每种文化都将其当下的本地规范视为唯一“自然”的性别实践方式。其次，倘若这些规范真是与生俱来且“自然”的，社会根本无需耗费如此巨大的精力去灌输和强制执行它们。



On the other hand, the idea that a person’s gender is entirely instilled by the external social world, with innate qualities and proclivities playing no part whatsoever in the shaping of an individual’s experience and performance of gender, also seems rather implausible. Given the sheer intensity and pervasiveness of the heteronormative gender conditioning to which all of us are subjected from birth, surely few people would grow up to be gay or transgender if they didn’t have some manner of internal disposition that was strong enough to make itself manifest even against the relentless tide of external social pressures.

另一方面，认为人的性别完全由外部社会世界灌输而成，先天特质和倾向在塑造个体性别体验与表现中毫无作用的观点，同样显得不太可信。考虑到我们所有人从出生起就承受着异性恋规范性别规训的强烈渗透，倘若人们没有某种足够强大的内在倾向——强大到能在外部社会压力的无情浪潮中彰显自身——那么很少有人会在成长过程中成为同性恋或跨性别者。



Anyone who’s spent time with babies knows that each one has their own distinct personality from birth. Not a fully-formed personality by any means, but at least an individual style comprised of a unique collection of personal inclinations. These innate inclinations, further shaped and developed through the infant’s interactions with the physical/sensory world, constitute the inner foundation that child psychology pioneer D.W. Winnicott referred to as the True Self. Protean, malleable, and readily shaped by the external world as the young developing bodymind is, the distinctive tendencies, inclinations, and potentials of this core True Self nonetheless exert a significant influence on each individual’s unique development—including a significant influence on how the social inculcation of gender roles is received, integrated, and expressed by that particular individual.

任何与婴儿相处过的人都知道，每个婴儿从出生起就拥有独特的个性。这绝非完全成型的性格，但至少是由一系列独特个人倾向构成的个体风格。这些与生俱来的倾向，通过婴儿与物理/感官世界的互动进一步塑造和发展，构成了儿童心理学先驱 D.W.温尼科特所称的"真实自我"的内在基础。尽管幼年发展中的身心具有可塑性、延展性且易受外部世界塑造，但这一核心真实自我的独特倾向、偏好和潜能仍对每个个体的独特发展产生重大影响——包括深刻影响该个体如何接受、整合并表达社会对性别角色的灌输。



Consider the binary heteronormative masculine and feminine gender role performances that are commonly inculcated by the dominant cultures in the modern world. These gender role performances involve an extensive set of specific norms of embodiment (e.g., distinctive ways of walking, standing, sitting, moving, gesturing, speaking, dressing, engaging with and expressing emotions, doing sex and sexuality, physically interacting with the world and with others). None of these norms are genetically predestined or neurobiologically “hard-wired”; they’re all culturally determined and socially instilled. The individual tendencies and inclinations that constitute the Winnicottian True Self, however, not only contribute at least some measure of unique style to a person’s performance of the norms of their socially assigned and instilled gender role, but also determine how good a fit the assigned gender role and its norms are going to be for that particular person.

考虑一下现代主流文化中普遍灌输的二元异性恋规范的男性与女性性别角色表现。这些性别角色表现涉及一整套具体的身体规范（例如，行走、站立、坐姿、移动、手势、口语表达、着装、情感体验与表达、性行为与性取向、与世界及他人进行身体互动等独特方式）。这些规范中没有一项是基因预先决定或神经生物学上“硬连线”的；它们全部由文化决定并经由社会灌输。然而，构成温尼科特式“真实自体”的个人倾向与偏好，不仅为个体在履行其社会分配并灌输的性别角色规范时增添了至少一定程度的独特风格，还决定了该性别角色及其规范对特定个体的契合程度。



What I’m suggesting here is that although no one is born a straight cisgender heteronormative girl or woman, boy or man, some people are born with a collection of inner tendencies and potentials that are at least somewhat compatible with their local culture’s norms of heterosexual feminine or masculine gender performance—thus enabling them to readily internalize those gender norms, to live within the parameters of those norms, and to come to experience their own socially instilled normative gender performance as “natural.” When we describe someone as cisgender, we’re referring to this condition of relative compatibility between the True Self and the social performance demands associated with their assigned gender.

我在此提出的观点是，虽然没有人天生就是顺性别、异性恋、符合性别规范的女孩或女人、男孩或男人，但有些人天生就具备一系列内在倾向和潜能，这些特质至少在一定程度上与当地文化中异性恋女性或男性性别表现的规范相契合——这使他们能够轻易地内化这些性别规范，在这些规范的参数范围内生活，并逐渐将自己被社会灌输的规范性性别表现体验为"自然的"。当我们称某人为顺性别者时，指的就是其真实自我与被赋予性别的社会表现要求之间相对兼容的状态。



At the other end of the spectrum, we find people in whom the tendencies and inclinations of the True Self are thoroughly incompatible with the norms governing the performance of the gender they were assigned at birth—incompatible to the point where performing their assigned gender causes them serious distress. For some of these people, the ones we refer to as transgender, the socially-constructed binary gender that they weren’t assigned at birth (the so-called “opposite” gender) turns out to be a far better fit than the gender they were initially assigned. For others, neither of the binary gender options offered by the dominant heteronormative culture are a suitable fit.

在光谱的另一端，我们发现有些人真实自我的倾向与出生时被指定的性别规范完全不相容——这种不相容程度甚至到了执行指定性别角色会引发严重痛苦的地步。对于其中被称为跨性别者的人群而言，社会建构的二元性别中未被指定的那个（所谓的"相反"性别）反而比最初被指定的性别更适合他们。而对另一些人来说，主流异性恋规范文化所提供的两种二元性别选项都不适合他们。



Of course, all of this is somewhat of an oversimplification for the sake of brevity; it’s entirely possible to be both transgender and nonbinary, for instance, and not all cultures limit themselves to a strict masculine/feminine binary when it comes to societally-approved gender options. The key point I’m making here is that while no one is born biologically predestined to “naturally” perform a specific gender in accordance with the gender norms of their native society, each individual does have their own particular predispositions which may make the socially-demanded heteronormative performance of their assigned gender viable and relatively intuitive for them, or somewhat less of a good fit, or highly uncomfortable, or downright impossible.

当然，为求简洁，上述描述略有简化；例如，一个人完全可以同时是跨性别者和非二元性别者，且并非所有文化在社会认可的性别选项上都局限于严格的男/女二元划分。此处核心观点在于：虽然没有人天生就注定会"自然地"按照其原生社会的性别规范来表现特定性别，但每个人确实有其独特的先天倾向——这些倾向可能使社会要求的、与其被指派性别相符的异性恋规范表现对他们而言可行且相对直观，也可能不太契合，或令人极度不适，甚至完全无法实现。



In this regard as in so many other regards, the dynamics of neuronormativity mirror and are entwined with the dynamics of heteronormativity. Like heteronormativity, neuronormativity is deeply ingrained in the prevailing culture and in all manner of social conventions, systems, and institutions. Like heteronormativity, neuronormativity is a pervasive social force, comprising a collection of innumerable culturally-constructed norms—norms related to nearly every aspect of embodiment, development, cognition, expression, communication, comportment, conduct, and interaction—which are socially modeled, inculcated, and enforced from birth onward in countless ways. And like heteronormativity, neuronormativity is to a large extent a matter of the ongoing habitual performance of internalized social norms.

在这一方面，如同在许多其他方面一样，神经规范性的动态与异性恋规范性的动态相互映照并交织在一起。与异性恋规范性相似，神经规范性深深植根于主流文化以及各种社会惯例、体系和制度之中。同样地，神经规范性作为一种普遍存在的社会力量，包含无数文化建构的规范——这些规范涉及身体、发展、认知、表达、沟通、举止、行为及互动的几乎每个方面——从出生起便通过无数方式在社会中被塑造、灌输和强化。而如同异性恋规范性，神经规范性在很大程度上也关乎持续习惯性地践行内化的社会规范。



Like heteronormative performance, neuronormative performance is a better fit for some folks than for others. At one end of the spectrum are those whose innate tendencies and inclinations are compatible enough with their local culture’s standards of neuronormative performance that they readily internalize those standards and come to experience their own socially instilled performance of neuronormativity as “natural.” This deep internalization and embodiment of the performance demands of neuronormativity, made possible when there is at least some basic degree of compatibility between those performance demands and the individual’s innate capacities, is what we’re really talking about when we refer to someone as neurotypical.

如同异性恋规范化的表演，神经规范化的表演对某些人而言比其他人更为契合。在光谱的一端，那些天生倾向与当地文化所要求的神经规范化表演标准足够兼容的人，会轻易内化这些标准，并将自身被社会灌输的神经规范化表演体验为"自然"。这种对神经规范化表演要求的深度内化与具身化——当这些表演要求与个体先天能力存在基本程度的兼容性时才有可能实现——正是我们谈论某人属于神经典型者时的真正所指。



At the opposite end of the spectrum are those for whom the performance of neuronormativity is literally impossible—those who are absolutely unable to perform the actions necessary to maintain a neuronormative façade, and unable to suppress visibly non-neuronormative embodiments. In between the neurotypicals and those for whom neuronormative performance is an impossibility are those for whom neuronormativity is to some substantial degree incompatible with their natural tendencies and inclinations, such that neuronormative performance is a bad fit for them, is only partially possible and/or only sometimes possible for them, costs them significant effort, and is ultimately harmful for them to attempt to sustain.

在光谱的另一端，是那些完全无法进行神经规范性表演的人——他们绝对无法执行维持神经规范性表象所需的行动，也无法抑制明显非神经规范性的具身表现。在神经典型者与无法进行神经规范性表演者之间，存在着这样一群人：神经规范性与他们的自然倾向和习性在相当程度上不相容，因此神经规范性表演对他们而言是一种糟糕的适配，只能部分实现或偶尔实现，需要付出巨大努力，且长期维持这种表演最终会对其造成伤害。



Those who view neurodiversity through a neuroessentialist lens have an unfortunate tendency to compare and contrast neurotypicality with innate forms of neurodivergence like autism in a way that implicitly assumes autism and neurotypicality to be equally innate and equally intrinsic to a person’s being. In the less well-informed discourses on neurodiversity that unfold on social media, for instance, one too often sees people speaking of “the neurotypical brain,” as if neurotypicality were a biological destiny that unfolded inevitably from being born with a specific kind of brain.

那些通过神经本质主义视角看待神经多样性的人，往往有一种令人遗憾的倾向，即比较和对比神经典型性与孤独症等先天形式的神经殊异性，这种比较隐含地假设孤独症和神经典型性同样是与生俱来的，同样是一个人存在的内在属性。例如，在社交媒体上那些信息不够充分的神经多样性讨论中，人们常常看到有人谈论“神经典型性大脑”，仿佛神经典型性是一种生物宿命，从出生时拥有特定类型的大脑就必然展开。



On a strictly neurobiological level, there’s not actually such a thing as a “normal brain” or a “neurotypical brain,” any more than there’s such a thing as a  “male brain,” a “heterosexual brain,” or an “American brain.” Neurotypical people aren’t people who all share one distinct type of human brain, they’re people whose compliance with prevailing cultural standards of neuronormative performance gains them the privileges that come with being considered “normal” within the dominant culture. Neurotypicality is more a social phenomenon than a biological one.

严格从神经生物学层面来看，实际上并不存在所谓的“正常大脑”或“神经典型性大脑”，就像不存在“男性大脑”、“异性恋大脑”或“美国人大脑”一样。神经典型性人群并非都共享一种独特的人类大脑类型，而是那些符合主流文化中神经规范性表现标准的人，从而获得了在主流文化中被视为“正常”所带来的特权。神经典型性更多是一种社会现象，而非生物学现象。



As previously noted, some people have more innate capacity than others to adapt to the demands of neuronormative performance. But having that capacity isn’t the same as being innately neurotypical. If we begin from the premise that neurotypicality is performative in the same sense that heteronormative gender roles are performative, then a newborn infant can’t be legitimately considered neurotypical for the same reason a newborn infant can’t be legitimately considered a straight cisgender female or a straight cisgender male: newborn infants are obviously not engaged in enacting acquired habits of performance.

如前所述，有些人在适应神经规范性表现的要求方面天生比其他人更有能力。但拥有这种能力并不等同于天生就是神经典型者。如果我们从这样的前提出发——神经典型性在本质上与异性恋规范的性别角色一样具有表演性——那么新生儿就不能被合理地视为神经典型者，正如新生儿不能被合理地视为顺性别异性恋女性或顺性别异性恋男性：新生儿显然尚未开始展现后天习得的表演习惯。



Infants are adorable messy little bundles of possibility, and which possibilities become realized and embodied over time depends to a large extent on the nature of the actions that a given individual learns to perform. If the innate predispositions of a given infant are fundamentally incompatible with the demands of neuronormative performance, such that a life of comfortably and convincingly performing neuronormativity isn’t within that infant’s scope of future possibilities, then we can legitimately say that the infant is neurodivergent—i.e., it has already diverged from the path of neuronormativity, right at the outset.

婴儿是可爱又混乱的小小可能性包裹，而哪些可能性会随着时间被实现和具身化，很大程度上取决于个体学会执行的行为性质。若某个婴儿的先天倾向与神经典型性表现的要求根本不相容，以至于舒适且令人信服地展现神经典型性的生活不在其未来可能性范围内，那么我们完全可以说这个婴儿是神经殊异的——也就是说，它从一开始就已经偏离了神经典型性的路径。



The reverse, however, doesn’t hold true. If the innate predispositions of a given infant are compatible with the demands of neuronormative performance, such that neurotypicality is within that infant’s scope of future possibilities, that’s not the same as the infant actually being neurotypical yet or being biologically destined for neurotypicality. To say that an infant is innately and “naturally” neurotypical just because it’s capable of acclimating to a life of neuronormative performance makes no more sense than saying that the infant is innately and “naturally” a software engineer just because it would be possible to someday teach it to design software.

然而，反之则不成立。若某婴儿先天禀赋与神经规范表现的要求相符，使其具备未来发展为神经典型者的可能性，这并不等同于该婴儿已然是神经典型者，或生物学上注定成为神经典型者。仅因婴儿能够适应神经规范表现的生活，就断言其天生且"自然"是神经典型者，这与仅因未来可能教会婴儿设计软件，就断言其天生且"自然"是软件工程师同样荒谬。



In other words, it’s possible to be born neurodivergent but it’s not possible to be born neurotypical. Neurotypicality is a socially instilled mode of normative performance, and is no more innate than the performance of a heteronormative gender role. And like heteronormative gender performance, neurotypicality can be queered; one can subvert the performance and liberate the bodymind (and liberate relationships, activities, spaces, and ultimately cultures) from the constraints of normativity. From a neuroqueer perspective, this is excellent news; it means that no one is biologically doomed to a life of being normal.

换言之，人可能生来就是神经殊异者，但不可能生来就是神经典型者。神经典型性是一种社会灌输的规范性表现模式，其先天程度并不比异性恋规范性别角色的表现更高。正如异性恋规范的性别表现可以被酷儿化一样，神经典型性同样可以被酷儿化；人们可以颠覆这种表现，将身心（以及人际关系、活动、空间，最终是文化）从规范性的束缚中解放出来。从神经酷儿视角来看，这是绝佳的消息——这意味着没有人天生注定要过"正常"的生活。



Neuroqueer Theory into Neuroqueer Practice

从神经酷儿理论到神经酷儿实践



Let’s ground this discussion of Neuroqueer Theory in an example of neuroqueer practice. Please note, however, that due to the boundless and heterogeneous scope of neuroqueer possibility, there are innumerable other potential forms of neuroqueer practice that bear no resemblance whatsoever to the example offered here. This example is intended to suggest just one possible avenue of neuroqueer exploration out of a disparate infinitude of potential avenues.

让我们通过一个神经酷儿实践的实例来具体探讨神经酷儿理论。但请注意，由于神经酷儿可能性具有无限且异质性的范畴，此处提供的实例与无数其他潜在形式的神经酷儿实践毫无相似之处。这个例子仅旨在展示神经酷儿探索的某一种可能路径——在浩瀚无垠的潜在路径中，它只是其中一条。



The example I’d like to offer concerns the movement of hands. I choose to focus on hand movement because it’s an example in which the overlap of neuronormativity and heteronormativity is particularly evident, and because it’s the same example I was contemplating and writing about at the precise moment in 2008 when the term neuroqueer first occurred to me.

我想举的例子与手的动作有关。之所以选择手部动作作为焦点，是因为在这个例子中，神经规范性与异性恋规范性的重叠尤为明显，而且这正是 2008 年"神经酷儿"这个术语首次出现在我脑海中时，我正在思考并写作的同一案例。



The policing of bodies and of embodiment is central to both neuronormativity and heteronormativity, and this includes the policing of how people move their hands. The policing of hands has in fact long played a particularly significant role in the enforcement of neuronormative embodiment. Autistic people have an innate proclivity for using their hands to stim; this stimming can take a wide variety of forms which violate the rules of normative performance to varying degrees (e.g., hands flapping, hands dancing in the air like tree branches in the wind, twisty movements of the fingers tracing patterns in space, hands or fingers rubbing together, hands or fingers exploring or stroking or tapping upon surfaces).

对身体的规训与具身化实践，既是神经规范性的核心，也是异性恋规范性的核心，这包括对人们如何移动双手的规训。事实上，对手部的规训长期以来在强制推行神经规范性具身化方面扮演着尤为重要的角色。孤独谱系群体天生倾向于用手进行自我刺激行为；这种自我刺激行为形式多样，在不同程度上违反了规范性表演的规则（例如：双手拍动、双手如风中树枝般在空中舞动、手指扭动在空中勾勒图案、双手或手指相互摩擦、双手或手指探索、抚摸或轻敲表面）。



Applied Behavior Analysis (ABA), an abusive and trauma-inducing form of conversion “therapy” aimed at forcing neurodivergent children into compliance with normative performance, seeks among other things to coerce its young victims into suppressing their capacity to stim. Perpetrators of ABA often focus a great deal—creepily and sometimes downright obsessively—on control of their victims’ hands, and on the suppression of hand-related stimming in particular. The use of the command “Quiet hands!” by ABA practitioners in this context has led to the adoption of the phrase “loud hands” as one of the slogans of autistic liberation (my first published essay on the neurodiversity paradigm, “Throw Away the Master’s Tools,” originally appeared in an anthology of autistic activist writings called Loud Hands). In the war to subjugate neurodivergent bodyminds, and in neuroqueer resistances to that subjugation, our hands have thus become contested territories of particular importance on both the physical and symbolic levels.

应用行为分析（ABA）是一种旨在强迫神经殊异儿童服从规范性表现的虐待性、诱发创伤的转化“疗法”，其目标之一便是胁迫年幼受害者抑制自我刺激能力。ABA 的实施者往往将大量精力——令人不安甚至近乎病态地——集中于控制受害者的双手，尤其着重压制与手部相关的自我刺激行为。在此语境下，ABA 从业者使用的“安静双手！”指令，促使“喧闹双手”成为孤独谱系解放运动的口号之一（我关于神经多样性范式的首篇公开论文《扔掉主人的工具》最初收录于孤独谱系活动家文集《喧闹双手》）。在征服神经殊异身心体的战争，以及神经酷儿对此征服的反抗中，我们的双手由此在物理与象征层面都成为了具有特殊意义的争夺领域。



The entwined nature of neuronormativity and heteronormativity means that the compulsory performance of neurotypicality is never a gender-neutral performance, but instead is strongly tied to the performance of binary heteronormative gender roles. Normative performance of whichever gender one was assigned at birth is central to what it means to be “normal” in the eyes of the present dominant culture. Thus, when the enforcers of normativity demand that a child “act normal,” it’s ultimately a demand to either act like a “normal boy” or like a “normal girl,” whether or not the demand is explicitly phrased that way.

神经规范性与异性恋规范性的交织本质意味着，强制性表演神经典型性从来不是性别中立的表演，而是与二元异性恋规范性性别角色的表演紧密相连。在当今主流文化眼中，按照出生时被指定的性别进行规范性表演，正是"正常"的核心要义。因此，当规范性的执行者要求一个孩子"表现得正常"时，无论这种要求是否明确表述，本质上都是在要求其要么表现得像个"正常男孩"，要么像个"正常女孩"。



Since normative performance is always gendered, deviations from neuronormative embodiment are also inevitably deviations from heteronormative embodiment. Whether a given deviation gets interpreted by the enforcers of normativity as a violation of neuronormativity or as a violation of heteronormativity often depends entirely on context and circumstances. In a context in which a child is known to be autistic (or neurodivergent in some other specific and culturally pathologized way), the child’s non-normative usage of their hands is likely to be pathologized as a “symptom” of their neurodivergence. But in a different context, in which those who are policing the child’s embodiment are unaware of the child’s neurodivergence, the same non-normative hand movements might be flagged as gender violations: children whom adults have labeled as girls might be reprimanded for drumming on the table with their hands or running their fingers vigorously and repeatedly through their hair, on the grounds that such actions are “unladylike”; children whom adults have labeled as boys might be attacked or ridiculed for flapping their hands, on the grounds that such gestures are “gay.”

由于规范性表现总是带有性别色彩，对神经典型性身体表现的偏离也必然是对异性恋规范性身体表现的偏离。某种偏离行为究竟会被规范执行者解读为违反神经典型性规范，还是违反异性恋规范，往往完全取决于具体情境和背景。当某个孩子被确认为孤独谱系（或具有其他被文化病理化的神经殊异特征）时，其非规范性的手部动作很可能被病理化为神经殊异性的"症状"。但在另一种情境中，当监督孩子身体表现的人不了解其神经殊异性时，同样的非规范性手部动作可能被标记为性别违规：被成年人标记为"女孩"的孩子可能因用手敲打桌子或反复用力拨弄头发而受到训斥，理由是这些行为"不像淑女"；被成年人标记为"男孩"的孩子可能因挥手而遭到攻击或嘲笑，理由是这种姿态"像同性恋"。



Thus, there are some autistic people who were forced in childhood to suppress their natural hand movements because those hand movements were flagged as “symptoms of autism” and targeted for elimination by autistiphobic adults, and other autistic people who weren’t recognized as autistic in childhood but were still forced to suppress their hand movements because those hand movements were violations of heteronormativity that got them targeted for homophobic and transphobic abuse by adults and/or peers. And of course, there are many who were targeted on both neuronormative and heteronormative grounds at different times—e.g., autistics who in their youth were abused by adults for moving their hands autistically, and by homophobic peers who read those same hand movements as queer. The professional ABA perpetrator and the homophobic schoolyard bully are ultimately in the same line of work, enforcing the same compulsory normativity from different angles.

因此，有些孤独谱系群体在童年时期被迫抑制自己自然的手部动作，因为这些动作被标记为“孤独症症状”，并成为恐惧孤独症者的成年人试图消除的目标；而另一些未被识别为孤独谱系的孤独谱系群体，在童年时期同样被迫抑制手部动作，因为这些动作违反了异性恋规范，导致他们成为成年人和/或同龄人基于恐同和恐跨性别立场的攻击对象。当然，还有许多人曾在不同时期同时遭受神经规范性和异性恋规范性的双重攻击——例如，那些在青少年时期因孤独谱系式的手部动作被成年人虐待，同时又因这些动作被恐同的同龄人视为酷儿而遭受欺凌的孤独谱系者。职业 ABA 实施者与校园恐同霸凌者本质上从事着同一行当，只是从不同角度强制推行着相同的规范性压迫。



Since distinctively autistic movements of the hands violate the rules of both neuronormative performance and heteronormative performance, to refuse to suppress such movements functions as a simultaneous queering of both neuronormativity and heteronormativity. When an autistic person chooses to allow themselves to follow some or all of the impulses toward non-normative hand movement that spontaneously arise in them, rather than suppressing those impulses in the interest of normative performance, that’s a form of neuroqueering.

由于独特的孤独谱系手部动作同时违反了神经规范性表演和异性恋规范性表演的规则，拒绝抑制此类动作便同时构成了对神经规范性和异性恋规范性的酷儿化。当一位孤独谱系者选择允许自己遵循某些或全部自发产生的非规范性手部动作冲动，而非为了符合规范性表演而压抑这些冲动时，这便是一种神经酷儿化形式。



One can deepen and extend this form of neuroqueering further by actively working to rediscover, explore, reclaim, and cultivate modes of non-normative hand movement which one has been suppressing for so long that the suppression has become ingrained unconscious habit. There’s a growing body of published work, including both personal accounts and scholarly research, on how the suppression of non-normative embodiments for the sake of compliance with standards of neuronormative performance (a compliance toward which the neurodivergent are relentlessly pressured throughout their lives) does profound psychological harm to neurodivergent people and is strongly correlated with depression and suicidality. The dominant culture, in other words, pushes neurodivergent people to prioritize passing for “normal” at the expense of their own well-being, mirroring the way that queer people have traditionally been pressured to stay closeted. In the emerging discourse on this issue, the suppression of non-neuronormative embodiments is commonly referred to as masking, and the reclaiming of those embodiments is referred to as unmasking. So it would be entirely accurate to say that neurodivergent unmasking is a form of neuroqueering (one of the most vital forms, I’d argue).

人们可以通过积极努力去重新发现、探索、重拾并培养那些被长期压抑以致成为根深蒂固无意识习惯的非规范性手部动作模式，从而进一步深化和拓展这种神经殊异化形式。已有越来越多的出版物（包括个人记述和学术研究）指出，为了符合神经规范表现标准（神经殊异者一生都承受着这种顺从标准的无情压力）而压抑非规范性具身表现，会对神经殊异者造成深重的心理伤害，并与抑郁和自杀倾向高度相关。换言之，主流文化迫使神经殊异者以牺牲自身福祉为代价优先追求"正常"伪装，这正如同性恋者传统上被迫隐藏性取向的处境。在围绕该议题的新兴论述中，这种对非神经规范具身表现的压抑通常被称为"伪装"，而重新接纳这些具身表现则被称为"卸下伪装"。 因此，完全可以说神经殊异者的去面具化是一种神经酷儿化（我认为是最关键的形式之一）。



The sort of bodily unmasking I’m talking about here, the reclaiming of previously suppressed ways of moving, can be intense and profoundly transformative. When the suppression has become ingrained unconscious habit (as happens especially when such suppression begins in childhood), it’s maintained in large part by the layers of deep, chronic, unconscious muscular tension which Wilhelm Reich referred to as character armor. Character armor is the bodily component of repression; it serves not only to block the spontaneous performance of various bodily movements and self-expressions, but also to block access to the feelings, yearnings, organismic impulses, and psychological capacities associated with those movements and self-expressions. The process of recovering one’s capacity for spontaneous neuroqueer movement is thus deeply and inseparably entwined with both the process of liberating oneself from the chronic tensions of character armor, and the process of recovering and cultivating modes of self-attunement and embodied expression from which one had previously been cut off by those tensions.

我在此讨论的这种身体层面的去伪装，即重新找回曾被压抑的移动方式，可能是一个强烈且具有深远变革意义的过程。当这种压抑演变为根深蒂固的无意识习惯（尤其在童年时期开始压抑的情况下），它很大程度上由威廉·赖希所称的"性格盔甲"——即深层、慢性、无意识的肌肉紧张层层维持。性格盔甲是压抑在身体层面的体现；它不仅阻碍各种身体动作和自发表达的流畅展现，更阻断了与这些动作和表达相关联的情感、渴望、机体冲动及心理能力的通达。因此，恢复自发神经多元运动能力的过程，与摆脱性格盔甲慢性紧张的解放过程，以及重新获得并培养曾被这些紧张切断的自我调谐与具身表达模式的过程，三者密不可分地交织在一起。



The neuroqueer project of reclaiming specific hand movements and stims that one was forced to suppress in childhood is a doorway to broader vistas of neuroqueer practice: in working to reconnect with those movements, one is also reconnecting with and cultivating one’s attunement to the inner stirrings, inclinations, and impulses from which such movements emerge. The cultivation of this attunement can develop over time into a vastly expanded repertoire of spontaneous self-expression and a greater capacity to creatively reshape ourselves. Neuroqueering at its best is not only a creative defiance and subversion of both neuronormativity and heteronormativity, but also simultaneously a path toward living more authentically and creatively than the strictures of normative performance would allow.

神经酷儿实践中，重新找回童年被迫压抑的特定手部动作与自我刺激行为，是通往更广阔神经酷儿实践图景的门户：在努力重建与这些动作的连接时，人们也在重新连接并培养对催生这些动作的内在悸动、倾向与冲动的感知力。这种感知力的培养会随时间推移，发展成更丰富的自发表达方式，以及更强大的自我重塑创造力。最理想的神经酷儿实践，不仅是对神经规范性与异性恋规范性的创造性反抗与颠覆，更是一条超越规范表演束缚、活出更真实更富创造力人生的路径。



Although I’ve been focusing on autistic hand movements in this discussion, it’s equally applicable to the hand movements of any non-autistic neurodivergent folks who might have natural inclinations toward using their hands in distinctive ways that violate the rules of normative performance (and obviously, it’s also applicable to aspects of embodiment that have little or nothing to do with hands; I’ve just chosen to focus on hand movements as an example). Now here’s a crucial point: it’s also applicable to the hand movements of folks who aren’t innately neurodivergent.

尽管我在本次讨论中聚焦于孤独谱系者的手部动作，但这一观点同样适用于任何非孤独谱系的神经殊异人士——他们可能天生倾向于以独特方式使用双手，从而违背了规范性表演的规则（显然，这也适用于与手部关联甚微或毫无关联的身体表现层面；我仅以手部动作为例进行阐述）。现在关键点在于：这一观点同样适用于那些并非天生神经殊异者的手部动作。



Autistics and other innately neurodivergent folks tend to have strong natural proclivities for modes of embodiment (often including ways of using the hands) that violate the rules of normative performance. But the reverse doesn’t hold true: neurotypical people aren’t born naturally compliant with the rules of normative performance; they’re just people who’ve deeply internalized those rules and are capable of maintaining that performance and experiencing it as natural. This doesn’t mean that a life spent in the embodied performance of neuronormativity is inevitable or truly natural for them, or that such a life is optimal for their well-being.

孤独谱系者及其他天生神经殊异的人群，往往对违反规范表现规则的身体化模式（常包括手部使用方式）有着强烈的自然倾向。但反之并不成立：神经典型者并非天生就能自然遵循规范表现规则；他们只是深度内化了这些规则，能够维持这种表现并将其视为自然状态的人。这并不意味着，对他们而言，终其一生沉浸于神经规范性的身体化表现是不可避免或真正自然的，也不意味着这样的生活最有利于他们的福祉。



For years, in my various public speaking engagements, I’ve talked to audiences about autistic ways of moving and how being able to freely embody the spontaneous dance of stimming is essential to autistic well-being. In the early days of my public speaking career, when I spoke of the harm that results from the suppression of stimming, and the importance of recovering the capacity to stim and defending the right to have “loud hands,” I spoke of these things solely as issues facing the autistic community.

多年来，在我各种公开演讲活动中，我曾向听众讲述孤独谱系者的移动方式，以及能够自由展现刺激行为的自发舞蹈对孤独谱系者福祉的重要性。在我公开演讲生涯的早期，当我谈及抑制刺激行为所造成的伤害，以及恢复刺激能力与捍卫"喧闹双手"权利的重要性时，我仅将这些议题视为孤独谱系社群所面临的问题。



Over time, I started hearing from people who’d been in my audiences at one time or another. They’d contact me to thank me for inspiring them to liberate themselves from the strictures of normative embodiment and reclaim their capacity to stim. They’d tell me that learning to attune to their long-suppressed stimming impulses had expanded their consciousness, sparked interesting changes in their cognitive processes, and helped to restore their joy and vitality and creativity.

随着时间的推移，我开始陆续收到一些曾听过我演讲的人们的来信。他们联系我，感谢我激励他们从规范身体的束缚中解放出来，重新找回自我刺激的能力。他们告诉我，学会倾听自己长期被压抑的自我刺激冲动，拓展了他们的意识，引发了认知过程的有趣变化，并帮助他们重拾快乐、活力与创造力。



What came as a surprise to me was that some of the people who contacted me to tell me these things also told me that they weren’t autistic, and that as far as they knew they hadn’t started out as innately neurodivergent in any way. Instead, inspired by my words on the topic, they’d diverged from normativity of their own accord, through an intentional reclaiming and exploration of ways of moving and engaging with the sensory world that had lain buried under a socially-instilled shell of neurotypicality since their early childhoods. They’d neuroqueered themselves, and their minds and lives were weirder and better for it.

令我惊讶的是，其中一些联系我并分享这些经历的人告诉我，他们并非孤独谱系人士，而且据他们所知，他们天生也并非神经殊异。相反，受我关于这一主题的言论启发，他们主动偏离了规范性，有意识地重新找回并探索那些自童年早期就被社会灌输的神经典型性外壳所掩埋的移动方式以及与感官世界的互动方式。他们实现了自我神经酷儿化，而他们的心智与生活也因此变得更加奇特、更加美好。



All babies and toddlers stim. The people we describe as neurotypical tend to lose touch with the capacity for spontaneous stimmy movement as it becomes buried beneath the socially instilled and internalized performance of normative embodiment. Many autistic or otherwise innately neurodivergent people, on the other hand, tend to remain connected to that capacity to whatever extent they manage to resist being shamed and/or brutalized and/or abusively therapized out of their attunement to it. Either way, though, a unique and beautiful version of the spontaneous organismic dance of stimming abides within each and every human being, no matter how deeply repressed it might be in some cases. With sufficient commitment, a proper spirit of open-minded exploration, and a willingness to let go of normal, anyone can learn to reconnect with that dance and embody it—and that process of reconnection can start with something as simple as experimenting with using one’s hands to stim more.

所有婴儿和幼儿都会进行自我刺激行为。我们通常描述为神经典型的人，往往会逐渐失去自发进行刺激动作的能力，因为这种能力被社会灌输并内化的规范身体表现所掩盖。而许多孤独谱系或天生神经殊异的人，则往往能在一定程度上保持与这种能力的联结，只要他们能够抵抗因这种特质而被羞辱、被粗暴对待或被强制治疗所剥离的处境。无论如何，每个人体内都存留着一种独特而美丽的自发有机体刺激之舞，无论在某些情况下它被压抑得多么深。只要有足够的决心、开放探索的恰当精神，以及放下"正常"的意愿，任何人都能重新学会与这种舞蹈建立联结并体现它——而重新联结的过程，可以从像用手进行更多刺激这样简单的事情开始。



We are embodied psyches, bodyminds. The organization and processes of the psyche are inextricably entwined with the organization and processes of the body in a single complex system and in a continuous dance of mutual shaping. New ways of moving and using the body create new neural pathways and bring new potentials of consciousness into manifestation. To liberate the body from the ingrained habits, tensions, and inhibitions that keep one locked into the performance of normativity, and to reawaken and cultivate the capacity for spontaneous stimming and non-normative self-embodiments, can also serve to help free the mind from the limits of normative perception and cognition.

我们是具身的心灵，是身心合一的存在。心灵的组织与过程，与身体的组织和过程密不可分地交织在一起，构成一个复杂的系统，并在持续的相互塑造之舞中运作。新的身体运动与使用方式会创造新的神经通路，并让意识的新潜能得以显现。将身体从那些使人固守于规范性表演的根深蒂固的习惯、紧张与抑制中解放出来，重新唤醒并培养自发性刺激行为与非规范性自我具身的能力，也有助于将心灵从规范性感知与认知的局限中解放出来。



All queering (including neuroqueering) is inherently transgressive, since by definition it involves subverting, defying, deviating from, and/or fucking with normativity. Neuroqueer Theory is thus in some fundamental way oppositional and defiant by its very nature. At the same time, though, it’s also radically optimistic in its view that with sufficient engagement in neuroqueer practice, anyone can liberate themselves from the strictures of normativity. The already neurodivergent can reconnect with and cultivate previously suppressed or undeveloped capacities, in order to more fully manifest their potentials for beautiful weirdness, and those whom we call neurotypicals are just potential neuroqueer mutant comrades who haven’t yet woken up and figured out how to unzip their normal-person suits.

所有酷儿化（包括神经酷儿化）本质上都具有越界性，因为其定义本身就包含颠覆、反抗、偏离和/或操弄规范性的行为。因此，神经酷儿理论在根本层面上天然具有对抗性与反叛性。但与此同时，它又展现出极端乐观主义——认为只要充分参与神经酷儿实践，任何人都能从规范性的桎梏中解放自我。那些已然神经殊异者能够重新连接并培育曾被压抑或未开发的能力，从而更充分地展现其美丽怪诞的潜能；而那些被我们称为神经典型的人，不过是尚未觉醒、尚未学会如何脱下正常人皮囊的潜在神经酷儿突变同志。



I’ve chosen to build this discussion of neuroqueer practice around a single example, the queering of hand movements. As I noted earlier, however, there are innumerable possible forms of neuroqueering which, apart from constituting some form of subversion of normativity, have little in common with this particular example. One can neuroqueer any aspect of one’s self-embodiment, and one can also neuroqueer art, literature, spaces, systems, fields of academic study, and all manner of other realms of activity.

我选择围绕一个具体例子——手部动作的酷儿化——来展开关于神经酷儿实践的讨论。然而，正如我先前指出的，神经酷儿化存在无数可能的形式，除了构成某种对规范性的颠覆之外，它们与这个特定例子几乎没有共同之处。人们可以对自己身体体现的任何方面进行神经酷儿化，也可以对艺术、文学、空间、系统、学术研究领域以及各种其他活动领域进行神经酷儿化。



Neuroqueering on an individual level, in the form of creative bodily enactments that subvert the norms of normative performance and disrupt internalized habits of normative embodiment, serves to materialize previously unrealized neurocognitive and creative potentials. With this awakening of new neuroqueer creative capacities comes an increased capacity to participate in the neuroqueering of cultural spaces and cultural practices: the ongoing co-creation of social environments that support the creative participation of neuroqueer bodyminds and encourage further embodied exploration of neuroqueer performance and neuroqueer possibilities. This sort of ongoing interplay between the neuroqueering of individual bodyminds and the neuroqueering of cultural spaces is the key to collective liberation from compulsory normativity.

在个体层面，神经酷儿化通过创造性的身体实践，颠覆规范性表演的常规，瓦解内化的规范身体习惯，从而将此前未实现的神经认知与创造潜能具象化。随着这种新型神经酷儿创造力的觉醒，参与文化空间与文化实践神经酷儿化的能力也随之增强：即持续共创支持神经酷儿身心创造性参与的社会环境，鼓励对神经酷儿表演与神经酷儿可能性进行更深入的身体探索。这种个体身心神经酷儿化与文化空间神经酷儿化之间的持续互动，正是集体摆脱强制性规范束缚的关键。



Neuronormativity and heteronormativity, in essence, are systems of artificial restriction on human potential. By their very nature, they limit our possibilities. To neuroqueer is to refuse to be constrained by those limits. Wherever restrictive conventions of compulsory neuronormativity and heteronormativity exist, there also exists the potential to open new vistas of creative possibility by queering those conventions in some way or another. The possible forms and horizons of neuroqueer practice are effectively infinite; the amount of space outside of a closet, after all, is always infinitely greater than the amount of space inside the closet.

神经规范性与异性恋规范性，本质上都是对人类潜能的系统性人为限制。它们天然地束缚着我们的可能性。神经酷儿化意味着拒绝被这些界限所禁锢。只要强制性神经规范与异性规范的限制性惯例存在，就存在通过某种方式酷儿化这些惯例、从而开辟创造性可能性的新视野的潜力。神经酷儿实践的可能形式与边界实际上是无限的——毕竟，衣柜外的空间永远比衣柜内的空间广阔得多。

Acknowledgements

致谢



This book wouldn’t be what it is without the support of my beloved fellow members of the Autonomous Press collective: B. Martin Allen, Casandra Johns, Andrew M. Reichart, Phil Smith, and Azzia Walker. In particular, Casandra is responsible for making the book look as good as it does, and Andrew went above and beyond in swiftly guiding it through the publication process.

没有自主出版社集体中我挚爱的同伴们——B. 马丁·艾伦、卡桑德拉·约翰斯、安德鲁·M·赖卡特、菲尔·史密斯和阿齐娅·沃克——的支持，这本书就不会是现在这个样子。特别要感谢卡桑德拉，是她让这本书呈现出如此精美的外观；而安德鲁则不遗余力地迅速引导它完成了出版流程。



Azzia Walker, the love of my life, supported and encouraged my writing every step of the way, and also kept me alive by making sure that I occasionally stepped away from the computer for exercise and snuggles.

阿齐娅·沃克，我生命中的挚爱，在我写作的每一步都给予我支持和鼓励，并且通过确保我偶尔离开电脑去锻炼和拥抱，让我得以保持活力。



Kris Brandenburger taught me how to use the medium of the essay to explore and communicate my thoughts, back when she was one of my teachers in my undergrad years. Later, as chair of the undergraduate Psychology program at California Institute of Integral Studies, Kris hired me to teach the Neurodiversity Studies course for which I was inspired to create this book as an introductory text.

克里斯·布兰登堡在我本科时期曾是我的老师，她教会了我如何运用散文这一媒介来探索和表达我的思想。后来，作为加州整合研究学院心理学本科项目的主任，克里斯聘请我教授神经多样性研究课程，正是为了这门课，我萌生了创作这本书作为入门教材的灵感。



Some of the ideas in the newer pieces were originally stirred up in my mind by two interviews conducted with me in 2020: a written interview conducted by Dora M. Raymaker (published under the title “Toward a Neuroqueer Future” in the journal Autism in Adulthood in 2021) and a livestreamed video interview conducted by Chloe Farahar and Harry Thompson of Aucademy.

新作中的一些想法最初源于 2020 年对我进行的两次访谈：一次是 Dora M. Raymaker 进行的书面访谈（2021 年以《迈向神经酷儿未来》为题发表在《成人孤独症》期刊上），另一次是 Aucademy 的 Chloe Farahar 与 Harry Thompson 进行的直播视频访谈。



My students at California Institute of Integral Studies have asked me countless intriguing questions over the past decade, and many of the thoughts that ended up in the book were thoughts I first articulated in answer to those questions.

过去十年间，我在加州整合研究学院的学生们提出了无数引人深思的问题，书中许多观点正是我最初回答这些问题时阐述的思考。



And finally, Ian J. Grand was the professor and mentor in whose graduate Psychodynamics course I was first inspired to coin the term neuroqueer. Ian’s passed on now to whatever lies beyond this world, but my writing process is still informed by the habit of trying to express each idea in a way that he would have enjoyed reading.

最后要感谢 Ian J. Grand 教授与导师，正是在他研究生课程《心理动力学》中，我首次受到启发创造了"神经酷儿"这个术语。伊恩现已离世，前往彼岸世界，但我的写作仍延续着这样的习惯：努力以他会乐于阅读的方式表达每个观点。

Nick_ebook-4










What’s in This Book, and How It Came to Be

这本书里有什么，以及它是如何诞生的



When I first got involved in online autistic communities back in 2003, the word neurodiversity had already been around for a little while. Very few non-autistic folks had heard of it yet, but autistic rights activists were having some exciting conversations about the word’s implications. Over the next dozen years or so, through my participation in these conversations and through my published writings, I had the honor of contributing in some small way to the emergence of a new cultural paradigm. I took to calling it the neurodiversity paradigm, a name which has caught on in some circles.

2003 年，当我初次涉足线上孤独谱系社群时，“神经多样性”这个词已经存在了一段时间。当时，非孤独谱系人士中鲜有人听说过这个词，但孤独谱系权利活动家们正围绕这个词的含义展开令人振奋的讨论。在接下来的十多年里，通过参与这些讨论以及发表文章，我有幸为一种新兴文化范式的形成贡献了绵薄之力。我将这种范式称为“神经多样性范式”，这个名称在某些圈子里已经流行开来。



While the myriad conversations that shaped the neurodiversity paradigm were unfolding, I finished my undergraduate degree and then my master’s degree, and began my doctoral studies. In the papers I wrote for my grad school classes, I explored the phenomenon of neurodiversity and the ways it interconnected with other phenomena like embodiment and gender. In one of those papers, in 2008, I coined the term neuroqueer, which became central to my work and eventually became meaningful to a surprising number of other people, too.

在塑造神经多样性范式的无数对话展开的同时，我完成了本科学业和硕士学位，并开始了博士研究。在研究生课程所写的论文中，我探讨了神经多样性现象及其与具身性、性别等其他现象的相互关联。在 2008 年的一篇论文中，我创造了“神经酷儿”一词，这个词后来成为我工作的核心，并意外地对许多其他人产生了意义。



In 2013 I created the website Neurocosmopolitanism as a public repository for my short essays on autism and the neurodiversity paradigm. Some of those essays ended up having a lasting influence on neurodiversity-related discourse and on the emergent field of Neurodiversity Studies. By the Fall of 2016 I’d drifted away from producing such essays, to focus on finishing my doctoral dissertation and then on writing speculative fiction, comics, and the occasional academic book chapter. I left the essays sitting on the Neurocosmopolitanism site until I replaced that whole site with my current site, Neuroqueer. For several years now, fans of my online writings—a wildly diverse bunch ranging from widely-published scholars to queer neurodivergent teens—have been reaching out to ask me when the heck I’m going to put my work on neurodiversity and neuroqueerness into a book. And, hey, look, I’ve finally gone and done it.

2013 年，我创建了 Neurocosmopolitanism 网站，作为我关于孤独谱系和神经多样性范式短文的公共资料库。其中一些文章最终对神经多样性相关论述以及新兴的神经多样性研究领域产生了持久影响。到 2016 年秋季，我逐渐停止撰写这类文章，转而专注于完成博士论文，随后开始创作思辨小说、漫画，偶尔撰写学术书籍章节。这些文章一直保留在 Neurocosmopolitanism 网站上，直到我用现网站 Neuroqueer 完全取代了它。多年来，我网络文章的读者群——从著作颇丰的学者到酷儿神经殊异青少年，形形色色——不断联系我，询问我究竟何时会将关于神经多样性和神经酷儿的研究集结成书。瞧，我终于做到了。



The various short chapters that make up this book come in three different flavors: old stuff (most of which was written between 2012 and 2016 and appeared on the Neurocosmopolitanism site at one time or another), new commentary on the old stuff, and brand new essays written for this book in the Summer of 2021. I couldn’t resist making the occasional edit to some of the older material. Where the wording of a piece in this book differs from another version that appears elsewhere, the version in this book should be regarded as the definitive one for purposes of citation.

构成此书的各篇短章分为三种类型：旧作（多数写于 2012 至 2016 年间，曾陆续发表于 Neurocosmopolitanism 网站）、对旧作的新评注，以及 2021 年夏季专为此书撰写的新篇。我忍不住对部分旧作做了零星修订。若本书中某篇的措辞与其他版本存在差异，引用时请以本书版本为准。



The material in this book doesn’t appear in the order in which I wrote it. Instead, I’ve arranged the chapters in an order intended to make the book as coherent as possible. At the beginning of each piece, though, you’ll find a note that mentions what year the piece was originally written. Where something I say in a newer piece seems to contradict something I say in an older piece, the newer piece takes precedence and should be considered a better representation of my present understanding. I’ve learned and grown a great deal over the past decade, and my views have evolved and mutated. By the time you read this book, they’ll probably have mutated even further.

本书中的材料并非按我写作的时间顺序排列。相反，我特意将各章节编排成尽可能连贯的序列。不过，每篇文章开头都会注明其最初写作的年份。若新作中的某些表述与旧作存在矛盾，应以新作为准，视作我当前理解的更准确体现。过去十年间，我经历了大量学习与成长，观点也随之演变与蜕变。当你读到这本书时，这些观点或许已进一步演化。



The book is divided into three parts:

全书分为三个部分：



Part I, The Neurodiversity Paradigm, introduces the neurodiversity paradigm and some of the key concepts associated with it. This part begins with two of my older and more widely-cited pieces, “Throw Away the Master’s Tools: Liberating Ourselves from the Pathology Paradigm” and “Neurodiversity: Some Basic Terms & Definitions” (plus some history and new commentary on those pieces), and then moves on to new material on neurodiversity, the nature of neurotypicality and neurodivergence, the social model of disability, and neurocosmopolitanism.

第一部分：神经多样性范式，介绍了神经多样性范式及其相关的一些关键概念。本部分以我两篇较早且被广泛引用的文章《扔掉主人的工具：将我们从病理学范式中解放出来》和《神经多样性：一些基本术语与定义》（并附有这些文章的背景历史与最新评注）开篇，随后转向关于神经多样性、神经典型性与神经殊异性的本质、残障的社会模型以及神经世界主义的新内容。



Part II, Autistic Empowerment, consists of pieces that are specifically focused on autism. Most of the material in Part II was written between 2012 and 2017, but there’s also some newer stuff.

第二部分：孤独谱系赋权，收录了专门聚焦孤独谱系的文章。本部分大部分内容写于 2012 年至 2017 年间，但也包含一些较新的作品。



Part III, Postnormal Possibilities, consists of my 2015 piece “Neuroqueer: An Introduction,” some new commentary on that piece, and a new in-depth discussion of Neuroqueer Theory.

第三部分：后常态可能性，收录了我 2015 年的文章《神经酷儿：导论》、对该文的新评注，以及关于神经酷儿理论的深入新探讨。



I hope you’ll find something, somewhere in all this, that expands your perspective and your sense of possibility.

希望你能在本书的某个角落找到一些内容，拓宽你的视野与对可能性的感知。



Nick Walker

尼克·沃克



Summer 2021

2021 年夏季



Berkeley, CA

加利福尼亚州伯克利
