Nick_ebook-5










PART I:

THE NEURODIVERSITY PARADIGM

第一部分：神经多样性范式



“Homogeneity lacks genius.”

"同质化缺乏天才。"



Edgar Morin

埃德加·莫兰







---


Nick_ebook-6










The Story Behind “Throw Away the Master’s Tools”

“扔掉大师的工具”背后的故事



Back in the early 1990s, a growing number of autistic folks began connecting with one another through the internet and co-creating autistic community, autistic culture, and an autistic rights movement. The autistic rights movement emerged in response to the fact that autism-related discourse and praxis is dominated by what I’ve termed a pathology paradigm, in which autism is framed as a form of medical pathology—a “disorder” or “condition”—and the fact that this pathology paradigm consistently results in autistic people being stigmatized, dehumanized, abused, harmed, and traumatized by professionals and often by their own families.

早在 20 世纪 90 年代初，越来越多的孤独谱系群体开始通过互联网相互联系，共同创建孤独谱系社群、孤独谱系文化以及孤独谱系权利运动。这场孤独谱系权利运动的兴起，源于一个事实：与孤独谱系相关的论述和实践被我所称的“病理学范式”所主导——在这种范式中，孤独谱系被框定为一种医学病理，即一种“障碍”或“状况”——而这一病理学范式持续导致孤独谱系群体遭受专业人士乃至其家人的污名化、非人化、虐待、伤害和精神创伤。



If we look at the ways in which different historically oppressed groups are oppressed, we can see that the particulars are different for each group but that there are recurring patterns. For instance, the stereotypes projected onto two different groups might be vastly different, but there are consistent patterns in the way that stereotypes get propagated and in the role that stereotyping plays in dehumanizing and disenfranchising members of an oppressed group. An understanding developed among autistic activists that autistics were an oppressed minority group whose oppression in some ways follows similar patterns to those experienced by other historically oppressed groups.

如果我们审视历史上不同受压迫群体的受压迫方式，就会发现每个群体的具体情况各不相同，但存在反复出现的模式。例如，投射到两个不同群体上的刻板印象可能截然不同，但刻板印象的传播方式，以及刻板印象在非人化和剥夺受压迫群体成员权利方面所起的作用，却存在一致的规律。孤独谱系活动家们逐渐形成了一种共识：孤独谱系群体是一个受压迫的少数群体，其受压迫方式在某些方面与其他历史上受压迫群体所经历的压迫模式相似。



As discussions of these matters unfolded within autistic spaces, new vocabularies had to emerge in order to express new ways of thinking about things. A new conceptual framework was slowly beginning to emerge, and by the late 1990s a crucial piece of this framework’s vocabulary had been provided by the emergence of the term neurodiversity. Implicit in this juicy new word was an idea that the discourse in the autistic community had been groping its way toward all along: the idea that just as humanity is ethnically diverse and diverse in terms of gender and myriad other qualities, humanity is also neurocognitively diverse. Just as there are ethnic minority groups and gender minority groups, there are neurocognitive minority groups, and that’s what autistic people are.

随着这些讨论在孤独谱系群体内部展开，新的词汇必须应运而生，以表达看待事物的新方式。一种新的概念框架开始缓慢浮现，到 20 世纪 90 年代末，该框架词汇中的一个关键部分已由"神经多样性"这一术语的出现所提供。这个充满活力的新词隐含着一个理念，正是孤独谱系群体的话语体系一直摸索前行的方向：正如人类在种族、性别以及无数其他特质上具有多样性一样，人类在神经认知层面同样具有多样性。正如存在少数族裔群体和性别少数群体一样，也存在神经认知少数群体，而孤独谱系群体正是这样的群体。



New terms and concepts didn’t propagate quite as quickly in those days before the advent of massive social media platforms. In 2003, when I first stepped into the world of online autistic discourse, the term neurodiversity had caught on within some autistic activist circles but was far from widespread. Even those who’d known the word for a few years were still in the early stages of working to grasp and articulate its implications. No one had even coined the obvious corollary term neurominority yet; I ended up coining that one myself, in 2004, because it was useful for talking about the sort of things I was trying to talk about at the time (which I suppose is the reason most new words get coined).

在那个大型社交媒体平台尚未兴起的年代，新术语和概念的传播速度远不及今日。2003 年，当我初次踏入线上孤独谱系群体的话语圈时，"神经多样性"一词虽已在部分孤独谱系活动家群体中流行开来，却远未普及。即便是那些已接触该词汇数年的人，也仍处于理解并阐述其内涵的早期阶段。当时甚至尚未有人提出"神经少数群体"这一显而易见的衍生术语——最终是我在 2004 年创造了这个词，因为它恰好适用于阐述我当时试图探讨的议题（想来这正是多数新词诞生的缘由）。



The dominant cultural perspective on autism and autistic lives, and the perspective that was developing among those autistic thinkers and activists who were exploring the concept of neurodiversity and its implications, were based in fundamentally different sets of implicit values, goals, and understandings of reality—in other words, in different paradigms. By 2010, I’d started referring to these two contrasting paradigms as the pathology paradigm and the neurodiversity paradigm—and in the ongoing conversations within what was now being called the Neurodiversity Movement, I’d begun attempting to articulate the nature of these two paradigms and the core distinctions between them.

关于孤独症及孤独谱系人群的主流文化视角，与那些探索神经多样性概念及其影响的孤独谱系思想家及活动家们正在形成的视角，植根于截然不同的隐性价值观、目标及对现实的理解——换言之，即不同的范式。到 2010 年，我开始将这两种对立的范式分别称为病理范式与神经多样性范式——在如今被称为神经多样性运动的持续对话中，我已开始尝试阐明这两种范式的本质及其核心差异。



In 2011, I was invited to contribute to a new book of autistic activist writings. It wasn’t the first anthology featuring autistic voices (for example, Aquamarine Blue 5, collecting personal accounts of being autistic in college, came out in 2002, and Ask and Tell, an early book on self-advocacy skills for autistics, came out in 2004), but it was the first book focused specifically on radical autistic activist voices—the first book in which all of the authors were at least to some degree on board with the emerging neurodiversity paradigm, and were openly and strongly critical of various aspects of the pathology paradigm.

2011 年，我受邀为一本新的孤独谱系活动家文集撰稿。这并非首部收录孤独谱系声音的选集（例如 2002 年出版的《海蓝宝石 5 号》收录了孤独谱系人士的大学生活自述，2004 年出版的《问与说》则是早期关于孤独谱系自我倡导技能的著作），但这是第一本专门聚焦激进孤独谱系活动家声音的书籍——所有作者至少在一定程度上认同新兴的神经多样性范式，并公开强烈批判病理范式的各个方面。



I offered to contribute what I felt was most needed in the discourse at the time: an essay which would define the pathology paradigm, introduce and define the neurodiversity paradigm, and discuss what it meant to make the shift from the pathology paradigm to the neurodiversity paradigm and why such a shift was essential to autistic well-being. I’d been addressing these topics for a while in online discussions, but I’d never before tried to put it all together into a single cohesive piece that aimed to introduce these ideas to new readers in an accessible way.

我提议贡献一篇当时我认为最需要的文章：一篇界定病理范式、介绍并定义神经多样性范式、探讨从病理范式转向神经多样性的意义，以及为何这种转变对孤独谱系福祉至关重要的论文。此前我已在线上讨论中多次涉及这些主题，但从未尝试将其整合成一篇连贯的文章，以通俗易懂的方式向新读者介绍这些理念。



I called the resulting essay “Throw Away the Master’s Tools: Liberating Ourselves from the Pathology Paradigm,” and it was my first of writing on autism and the neurodiversity paradigm to be published. That anthology for which I wrote it was published in early 2012, under the title Loud Hands: Autistic People, Speaking. It was a groundbreaking book when it came out, though the discourse has advanced so much since then that it’s now only of interest for historical purposes.

我将这篇论文命名为《抛弃主人的工具：从病理学范式中解放自我》，这是我首次公开发表关于孤独谱系与神经多样性范式的作品。这篇论文收录的文集于 2012 年初出版，书名是《响亮的手：孤独谱系群体，口语者》。该书问世时堪称开创性著作，不过此后相关论述已取得长足发展，如今它仅具有历史研究价值。



When I created the Neurocosmopolitanism website in 2013, one of the first things I posted on it was a heavily revised version of “Throw Away the Master’s Tools.” The revisions were badly needed; some of my writing in the original Loud Hands version was embarrassingly clunky. The version that went up on the website (and can now be found on my Neuroqueer site) is only about half as clunky, and that’s the version that’s reprinted here.

2013 年创建神经世界主义网站时，我上传的首批内容中就包括大幅修订版的《抛弃主人的工具》。这些修订实属必要——原版《响亮的手》中某些表述笨拙得令人汗颜。网站版本（现可在我创建的神经酷儿网站查阅）的笨拙程度仅剩原版的一半，本书收录的正是这个修订版本。



This piece was originally written for an autistic audience, so it’s specifically addressed to autistic readers and focused on what the shift from the pathology paradigm to the neurodiversity paradigm means in the context of the discourse on autism. Nonetheless, it serves as a good 101-level introduction to the neurodiversity paradigm for anyone, and readers over the past decade have found it a relatively easy matter to extrapolate from my autism-related examples and apply my analysis to the discourses on dyslexia, ADHD, and other pathologized neurocognitive styles.

本文最初是为孤独谱系读者撰写的，因此专门面向孤独谱系读者，聚焦于从病理范式向神经多样性范式转变对孤独谱系话语体系的意义。尽管如此，它仍可作为任何人了解神经多样性范式的入门级优质读物。过去十年间，读者们发现，从我的孤独谱系相关案例中推导出普遍规律，并将我的分析应用于阅读障碍、注意力缺陷多动障碍及其他被病理化的神经认知风格的话语体系，是相对容易的事情。



“Throw Away the Master’s Tools” remains one of the more significant things I’ve written, in terms of its long-term influence on the discourse. It’s been widely cited in academic works, and translated into Spanish, French, Portuguese, Russian, and Czech. The conceptions of the pathology paradigm and the neurodiversity paradigm originally articulated in this piece are now integral to the fields of Neurodiversity Studies and Critical Autism Studies, fields which didn’t exist yet when I wrote the thing. So much can happen in the blink of a decade.

《抛弃主人的工具》一文至今仍是我最具影响力的作品之一，其长期影响贯穿整个话语体系。该文被学术著作广泛引用，并已译成西班牙语、法语、葡萄牙语、俄语和捷克语。文中首次阐明的病理范式与神经多样性范式概念，如今已成为神经多样性研究与批判性孤独谱系研究领域的核心基石——而在我撰写此文时，这些学科领域尚未诞生。十年弹指间，沧海已桑田。







---


Nick_ebook-7










Throw Away the Master’s Tools:

Liberating Ourselves from the

Pathology Paradigm

抛弃主人的工具：从病理范式中解放自我



When it comes to human neurodiversity, the dominant paradigm in the world today is what I refer to as the pathology paradigm. The long-term well-being and empowerment of autistics and members of other neurocognitive minority groups hinges upon our ability to create a paradigm shift—a shift from the pathology paradigm to the neurodiversity paradigm. Such a shift must happen internally, within the consciousness of individuals, and must also be propagated in the cultures in which we live.

在人类神经多样性问题上，当今世界的主流范式是我所称的病理范式。自闭症患者及其他神经认知少数群体的长期福祉与赋权，取决于我们能否实现范式转换——从病理范式转向神经多样性范式。这种转换必须发生在个体意识内部，同时也要在我们所生活的文化中传播开来。



So what does all that fancy talk mean? What are these paradigms of which I speak, and what does it mean to  make a “shift” from one paradigm to another? This piece is an attempt to explain that, in plain language that I hope will make these concepts easily accessible.

这些花哨的术语究竟意味着什么？我所说的这些范式是什么？从一个范式"转换"到另一个范式又意味着什么？本文试图用通俗易懂的语言解释这些概念，希望能让它们变得易于理解。



What’s a Paradigm, and What’s a Paradigm Shift?

什么是范式？什么是范式转换？



Even if you haven’t encountered it in an academic context, you’ve probably heard the term paradigm before, because it’s annoyingly overused by corporate marketers to describe any new development they’re trying to get people excited about: A new paradigm in wireless technology! A new paradigm in sales hyperbole!

即使你从未在学术语境中接触过“范式”这个词，也可能听过它——因为企业营销人员总爱滥用这个词，用来描述任何他们想让人兴奋的新发展：无线技术的新范式！销售夸张手法的新范式！



As a great Spanish diplomat once put it, I do not think it means what they think it means.

正如一位伟大的西班牙外交官所言，我认为这个词的意思并非他们所以为的那样。



A paradigm is not just an idea or a method. A paradigm is a set of fundamental assumptions or principles, a mindset or frame of reference that shapes how one thinks about and talks about a given subject. A paradigm shapes the ways in which one interprets information, and determines what sort of questions one asks and how one asks them. A paradigm is a lens through which one views reality.

范式不仅仅是一个想法或方法。它是一套基本假设或原则，是一种思维模式或参考框架，塑造了人们如何思考和谈论某个特定主题。范式决定了人们解读信息的方式，并影响人们提出什么样的问题以及如何提问。范式是观察现实的透镜。



Perhaps the most simple and well-known example of a paradigm shift comes from the history of astronomy: the shift from the geocentric paradigm (which assumes that the Sun and planets revolve around Earth) to the heliocentric paradigm (Earth and several other planets revolve around the Sun). At the time this shift began, many generations of astronomers had already recorded extensive observations of the movements of planets. But now all their measurements meant something different. All the information had to be reinterpreted from an entirely new perspective. It wasn’t just that questions had new answers—the questions themselves were different. Questions like “What is the path of Mercury’s orbit around Earth?” went from seeming important to being outright nonsense, while other questions, that had never been asked because they would have seemed like nonsense under the old paradigm, suddenly became meaningful.

也许范式转换最简明且广为人知的例子来自天文学史：从地心说范式（认为太阳和行星围绕地球运转）转向日心说范式（地球与其他行星围绕太阳运转）。当这一转变开始时，已有数代天文学家记录了大量行星运动观测数据。但此刻，他们所有的测量结果都获得了全新含义。所有信息都必须从全新的视角重新解读。不仅是问题有了新答案——连问题本身都发生了改变。诸如"水星绕地球运行的轨道是怎样的？"这类问题，从看似重要沦为彻底荒谬，而另一些在旧范式下因显得荒诞而从未被提出的问题，突然变得意义非凡。



That’s a true paradigm shift: a shift in our fundamental assumptions; a radical shift in perspective that requires us to redefine our terms, recalibrate our language, rephrase our questions, reinterpret our data, and completely rethink our basic concepts and approaches.

这才是真正的范式转换：根本性假设的转变；视角的彻底革新，要求我们重新定义术语、校准语言、重构问题、重新诠释数据，并彻底反思基本概念与方法。



The Pathology Paradigm

病理学范式



A paradigm can often be boiled down to a few basic, general principles, although those principles tend to be far-reaching in their implications and consequences. The principles of a widely dominant sociocultural paradigm like the pathology paradigm usually take the form of assumptions—that is, they’re so widely taken-for-granted that most people never consciously reflect upon them or articulate them (and sometimes it can be a disturbing revelation to hear them plainly articulated). The pathology paradigm ultimately boils down to just two fundamental assumptions:

一个范式通常可以归结为几个基本的一般性原则，尽管这些原则往往具有深远的影响和后果。像病理学范式这样广泛主导的社会文化范式，其原则通常以假设的形式存在——也就是说，它们被广泛视为理所当然，以至于大多数人从未有意识地反思或明确表达它们（有时，当这些假设被直白地阐述出来时，可能会带来令人不安的启示）。病理学范式最终可归结为两个基本假设：




There is one “right,” “normal,” or “healthy” way for human brains and human minds to be configured and to function (or one relatively narrow “normal” range into which the configuration and functioning of human brains and minds ought to fall).

人类大脑和心智的构造与运作存在一种“正确”、“正常”或“健康”的方式（或者说，存在一个相对狭窄的“正常”范围，人类大脑和心智的构造与运作应当落在这个范围内）。



If your neurological configuration and functioning (and, as a result, your ways of thinking and behaving) diverge substantially from the dominant standard of  “normal,” then there is Something Wrong With You.

如果你的神经构造和运作（以及由此产生的思维和行为方式）与主流的“正常”标准存在显著差异，那么你就有问题。




It is these two assumptions that define the pathology paradigm. Different groups and individuals build upon these assumptions in very different ways, with varying degrees of rationality, absurdity, fearfulness, or compassion—but as long as they share those two basic assumptions, they’re still operating within the pathology paradigm (just as ancient Mayan astronomers and 13th Century Islamic astronomers had vastly different conceptions of the cosmos, yet both operated within the geocentric paradigm).

正是这两个假设定义了病理学范式。不同群体和个人以截然不同的方式在这些假设基础上展开思考，其理性程度、荒谬性、恐惧感或同理心各有差异——但只要他们共享这两个基本假设，就仍然在病理学范式内运作（正如古玛雅天文学家和 13 世纪伊斯兰天文学家对宇宙有着截然不同的认知，却都遵循着地心说范式）。



The psychiatric establishment that classifies autism as a “disorder”; the “autism charity” that calls autism a “global health crisis”; autism researchers who keep coming up with new theories of “causation”; scientifically illiterate wing nuts who believe that autism is some form of “poisoning”; anyone who speaks of autism using medicalized language like “symptom,” “treatment,” or “epidemic”; the mother who thinks that the best way to help her autistic child is to subject him to Behaviorist “interventions” intended to train him to act like a “normal” child; the “inspiring” autistic celebrity who advises other autistics that the secret to success is to try harder to conform to the social demands of non-autistics… all of these groups and individuals are operating within the pathology paradigm, regardless of their intentions or how much they might disagree with one another on various points.

将孤独症归类为“障碍”的精神医学机构；将孤独症称为“全球健康危机”的“孤独症慈善组织”；不断提出新“病因”理论的孤独症研究人员；缺乏科学素养、认为孤独症是某种“中毒”的偏执狂；任何使用“症状”“治疗”或“流行病”等医学化语言谈论孤独症的人；认为帮助孤独症孩子的最佳方式是让其接受行为主义“干预”、训练其表现得像“正常”孩子的母亲；以及那些“鼓舞人心”的孤独症名人，建议其他孤独症患者成功的秘诀是更努力地迎合非孤独症者的社交要求……所有这些群体和个人，无论其意图如何，也无论他们在各种问题上存在多大分歧，都运行在病理学范式之内。



The Neurodiversity Paradigm

神经多样性范式



Here’s how I’d articulate the fundamental principles of the neurodiversity paradigm:

以下是我对神经多样性范式基本原则的阐述：




Neurodiversity—the diversity among minds—is a natural, healthy, and valuable form of human diversity.

神经多样性——即心智的多样性——是人类多样性中一种自然、健康且有价值的形式。



There is no “normal” or “right” style of human mind, any more than there is one “normal” or “right” ethnicity, gender, or culture.

不存在所谓"正常"或"正确"的人类心智模式，正如不存在单一"正常"或"正确"的种族、性别或文化。



The social dynamics that manifest in regard to neurodiversity are similar to the social dynamics that manifest in regard to other forms of human diversity (e.g., diversity of race, culture, gender, or sexual orientation). These dynamics include the dynamics of social power relations—the dynamics of social inequality, privilege, and oppression—as well as the dynamics by which diversity, when embraced, acts as a source of creative potential within a group or society.

围绕神经多样性所呈现的社会动态，与围绕其他形式人类多样性（如种族、文化、性别或性取向的多样性）所呈现的社会动态相似。这些动态既包括社会权力关系的动态——即社会不平等、特权和压迫的动态——也包括当多样性被接纳时，它作为群体或社会中创造性潜力源泉的动态。




The Master’s Tools Will Never Dismantle the Master’s House

主人的工具永远拆不掉主人的房子



At an international feminist conference in 1979, the poet Audre Lorde delivered a speech entitled “The Master’s Tools Will Never Dismantle the Master’s House.” In that speech, Lorde, a Black lesbian from a working-class immigrant family, castigated her almost entirely white and affluent audience for remaining rooted in, and continuing to propagate, the fundamental dynamics of the patriarchy: hierarchy, exclusion, racism, classism, homophobia, obliviousness to privilege, failure to embrace diversity. Lorde recognized sexism as being part of a broader, deeply-rooted paradigm that dealt with all forms of difference by establishing hierarchies of dominance, and she saw that genuine, widespread liberation was impossible as long as feminists continued to operate within this paradigm.

1979 年，在一场国际女性主义会议上，诗人奥德丽·洛德发表了题为《主人的工具永远拆不掉主人的房子》的演讲。作为出身工薪阶层移民家庭的黑人女同性恋者，洛德在演讲中严厉谴责了几乎全是白人中产阶级的听众——她们固守并持续传播着父权制的基本运作模式：等级制度、排他性、种族主义、阶级歧视、恐同倾向、对特权的漠视、对多元性的抗拒。洛德认识到，性别歧视是更广泛、根深蒂固的范式的一部分，这种范式通过建立支配等级来应对所有形式的差异。她看到，只要女性主义者继续在这个范式内运作，真正的、广泛的解放就不可能实现。



“What does it mean,” Lorde said, “when the tools of a racist patriarchy are used to examine the fruits of that same patriarchy? It means that only the most narrow perimeters of change are possible and allowable. […] For the master’s tools will never dismantle the master’s house. They may allow us temporarily to beat him at his own game, but they will never enable us to bring about genuine change.”

“当种族主义父权制的工具被用来审视同一父权制的产物时，”洛德说道，“这意味着什么？这意味着只有最狭隘的变革边界才是可能且被允许的。[……]因为主人的工具永远拆不掉主人的房子。它们或许能让我们暂时在主人的游戏里击败他，但永远无法让我们带来真正的改变。”



The master’s tools will never dismantle the master’s house. To work within a system, to play by its rules, inevitably reinforces that system, whether or not that’s what you intend. Not only do the master’s tools never serve to dismantle the master’s house, but any time you try to use the master’s tools for anything, you somehow end up building another extension of that darned house.

主人的工具永远无法拆毁主人的房子。在一个系统内运作、遵循其规则行事，无论你是否有意，都必然强化这个系统。主人的工具不仅无法拆毁主人的房子，而且每当你试图用这些工具做任何事时，最终都会为那座该死的房子添砖加瓦。



Lorde’s warning applies equally well, today, to the autistic community and our fight for empowerment. The assumption that there is Something Wrong With Us is inherently disempowering, and that assumption is absolutely intrinsic to the pathology paradigm. So the “tools” of the pathology paradigm (by which I mean all strategies, goals, or ways of speaking or thinking that explicitly or implicitly buy into the pathology paradigm’s assumptions) will never empower us in the long run. Genuine, lasting, widespread empowerment for autistics can only be attained through making and propagating the shift from the pathology paradigm to the neurodiversity paradigm. We must throw away the master’s tools.

如今，洛德的警示同样适用于孤独谱系群体及其争取赋权的斗争。认为"我们有问题"的假设本质上就是剥夺我们的力量，而这种假设恰恰是病理范式的核心。因此，病理范式的"工具"（我指的是所有明确或隐含地认同病理范式假设的策略、目标、言说或思维方式）从长远来看永远无法赋予我们力量。孤独谱系群体真正、持久、广泛的赋权，只能通过推动从病理范式向神经多样性范式的转变来实现。我们必须抛弃主人的工具。



The Language of Pathology vs. the Language of Diversity

病理学的语言 vs. 多样性的语言



Because the pathology paradigm has been dominant for some time, many people, even many who claim to advocate for the empowerment of autistic people, still habitually use language that’s based in the assumptions of that paradigm. The shift from the pathology paradigm to the neurodiversity paradigm calls for a radical shift in language, because the appropriate language for discussing medical problems is quite different from the appropriate language for discussing diversity. The issue of “person-first language” is a good basic example to start with.

由于病理学范式长期占据主导地位，许多人——甚至包括许多自称支持孤独谱系群体赋权的人——仍习惯性地使用基于该范式假设的语言。从病理学范式向神经多样性范式的转变，要求我们在语言上进行根本性变革，因为讨论医学问题与讨论多样性问题所需的恰当语言截然不同。“以人为本的语言”这一议题便是一个很好的基础范例。



If a person has a medical condition, we might say that “she has cancer,” or she’s “a person with allergies,” or “she suffers from ulcers.” But when a person is a member of a historically marginalized group, we don’t talk about their identity as though it were a disease. We say “she’s Black,” or “she’s a lesbian.” We recognize that it would be outrageously inappropriate—and likely to mark us as ignorant or bigoted—if we were to refer to a Black person as “having negroism” or being a “person with negroism,” or if we were to say that someone “suffers from homosexuality.”

若某人患有医学病症，我们可能会说“她得了癌症”，或她是“过敏症患者”，或“她饱受溃疡之苦”。但当一个人属于历史上被边缘化的群体时，我们不会将其身份当作疾病来谈论。我们会说“她是黑人”，或“她是女同性恋”。我们深知，若将黑人称为“患有黑人症”或“黑人症患者”，或说某人“饱受同性恋之苦”，将是极其不当的——这很可能暴露我们的无知或偏见。



So if we use phrases like “person with autism,” or “she has autism,” or “families affected by autism,” we’re using the language of the pathology paradigm—language that implicitly accepts and reinforces the assumption that autism is intrinsically a problem, a Something-Wrong-With-You. In the language of the neurodiversity paradigm, on the other hand, we speak of neurodiversity in the same way we would speak of ethnic or sexual diversity, and we speak of autistics in the same way we would speak of any other social minority group: I am autistic. I am an autistic. I am an autistic person. There are autistic people in my family.

因此，如果我们使用诸如“患有孤独症的人”、“她有孤独症”或“受孤独症影响的家庭”这类表述，我们就是在使用病理范式的语言——这种语言隐含着并强化了“孤独症本质上是一种问题、一种‘你身上出了什么毛病’”的假设。而另一方面，在神经多样性的语言中，我们谈论神经多样性的方式，就如同谈论种族或性取向多样性一样；我们谈论孤独谱系群体的方式，也如同谈论任何其他社会少数群体一样：我是孤独谱系者。我是一名孤独谱系者。我是一位孤独谱系人士。我的家人中有孤独谱系者。



These linguistic distinctions might seem trivial, but our language plays a key role in shaping our thoughts, our perceptions, our cultures, and our realities. In the long run, the sort of language that’s used to talk about autistics has enormous influence on how society treats us, and on the messages we internalize about ourselves. To describe ourselves in language that reinforces the pathology paradigm is to use the master’s tools, in Audre Lorde’s metaphor, and thus to imprison ourselves more deeply in the master’s house.

这些语言上的区别看似微不足道，但我们的语言在塑造思想、认知、文化和现实方面起着关键作用。从长远来看，用来谈论孤独谱系群体的语言，对社会如何对待我们、以及我们如何内化关于自我的信息，有着巨大的影响。用强化病理范式的语言来描述自己，借用奥德丽·洛德的比喻，就是使用主人的工具，从而更深地将自己囚禁在主人的房子里。



I Don’t Believe in Normal People

我不相信有“正常人”



The concept of a “normal brain” or a “normal person” has no more objective scientific validity—and serves no better purpose—than the concept of a “master race.” Of all the master’s tools (i.e., the dynamics, language, and conceptual frameworks that create and maintain social inequities), the most powerful and insidious is the concept of “normal people.” In the context of human diversity (ethnic, cultural, sexual, neurological, or any other sort), to treat one particular group as the “normal” or default group inevitably serves to privilege that group and to marginalize those who don’t belong to that group.

"正常大脑"或"正常人"的概念，与"优等种族"的概念一样，既缺乏客观的科学依据，也毫无裨益。在所有"主人的工具"（即制造并维持社会不平等的动态机制、语言和概念框架）中，最强大且最阴险的莫过于"正常人"这一概念。在人类多样性（包括种族、文化、性取向、神经类型或其他任何方面）的语境中，将某一特定群体视为"正常"或默认群体，必然会使该群体享有特权，并边缘化那些不属于该群体的人。



The dubious assumption that there’s such a thing as a “normal person” lies at the core of the pathology paradigm. The neurodiversity paradigm, on the other hand, does not recognize “normal” as a valid concept when it comes to human diversity.

"存在所谓'正常人'"这一可疑假设，正是病理范式的核心。而神经多样性范式则截然不同，它不承认在人类多样性问题上"正常"是一个有效的概念。



Most reasonably well-educated people these days already recognize that the concept of “normal” is absurd and meaningless in the context of racial, ethnic, or cultural diversity. The Han Chinese constitute the single largest ethnic group in the world, but it would be ridiculous to claim that this makes Han Chinese the “natural” or “default” human ethnicity. The fact that a randomly-selected human is statistically far more likely to be Han Chinese than Irish does not make a Han Chinese more “normal” than an Irishman (whatever that would even mean).

如今，大多数受过良好教育的人已经认识到，在种族、民族或文化多样性的语境下，“正常”这一概念是荒谬且毫无意义的。汉族是世界上最大的单一族群，但若因此声称汉族是“天然”或“默认”的人类族群，则显得荒唐可笑。统计上随机选出一个汉族人的概率远高于爱尔兰人，但这并不意味着汉族比爱尔兰人更“正常”（无论这种说法究竟有何含义）。



The most insidious sort of social inequality, the most difficult sort of privilege to challenge, occurs when a dominant group is so deeply established as the “normal” or “default” group that it has no specific name, no label. The members of such a group are simply thought of as “normal people,” “healthy people,” or just “people”—with the implication that those who aren’t members of that group represent deviations from that which is normal and natural, rather than equally natural and legitimate manifestations of human diversity.

最阴险的社会不平等、最难挑战的特权，往往出现在某个主导群体已根深蒂固地成为“正常”或“默认”群体，以至于它没有特定名称、没有标签之时。这类群体的成员通常被简单视为“正常人”、“健康人”或仅仅是“人”——言下之意，那些不属于该群体的人，代表了对正常与自然的偏离，而非人类多样性中同样自然且合理的表现。



For instance, consider the connotations of the statement “Gay people want the same rights as heterosexuals,” versus the connotations of the statement “Gay people want the same rights as normal people.” Simply by substituting the word normal for heterosexual, the second statement implicitly accepts and reinforces heterosexual privilege, and relegates gays to an inferior, “abnormal” status.

例如，比较“同性恋者希望获得与异性恋者相同的权利”与“同性恋者希望获得与正常人相同的权利”这两句话的隐含意义。仅仅将“异性恋者”替换为“正常人”，第二句话便默认并强化了异性恋特权，将同性恋者贬低为低等、“不正常”的群体。



Now imagine if terms like heterosexual and straight didn’t exist at all. That would put gay rights activists in the position of having to say things like “We want the same rights as normal people”—language that would reinforce their marginal, “abnormal” status and thus undermine their struggle. They’d be stuck using the master’s tools. If terms like heterosexual and straight didn’t exist, it would be necessary for gay rights activists to invent them.

现在设想一下，如果“异性恋”或“直人”这类词汇根本不存在，同性恋权益倡导者将不得不说出“我们希望获得与正常人相同的权利”这样的话——这种语言会强化他们边缘化、“不正常”的地位，从而削弱他们的抗争。他们将被困在“主人的工具”中。如果“异性恋”或“直人”这类词汇不存在，同性恋权益倡导者就必须创造它们。



This is why an essential early step in the neurodiversity movement was the coining of the term neurotypical. Neurotypical is to autistic as straight is to gay. The existence of the word neurotypical makes it possible to have conversations about topics like neurotypical privilege. Neurotypical is a word that allows us to talk about members of the dominant neurological group without implicitly reinforcing that group’s privileged position (and our own marginalization) by referring to them as “normal.” The word normal, used to privilege one sort of human over others, is one of the master’s tools, but the word neurotypical is one of our tools—a tool that we can use instead of the master’s tool; a tool that can help us to dismantle the master’s house.

这正是神经多样性运动中一个关键早期步骤——创造“神经典型”（neurotypical）这一术语的原因。神经典型之于孤独谱系，正如异性恋之于同性恋。“神经典型”一词的存在，使我们能够讨论诸如神经典型特权之类的话题。这个词让我们得以指代主导性神经群体的成员，而无需通过称其为“正常”来暗中强化该群体的特权地位（以及我们自身的边缘化）。用“正常”一词来赋予某一类人凌驾于他人之上的特权，是“主人的工具”；但“神经典型”却是我们的工具之一——一个我们可以用来替代“主人工具”的工具；一个能帮助我们拆毁“主人之屋”的工具。



The Vocabulary of Neurodiversity

神经多样性的词汇体系



The word neurotypical is an essential piece of the new vocabulary of neurodiversity that’s beginning to emerge—that needs to emerge, if we are to free ourselves of the disempowering language of the pathology paradigm, and if we are to successfully propagate the neurodiversity paradigm in our own thinking and in the sphere of public discourse.

“神经典型”一词，是正在浮现的神经多样性新词汇体系中的关键组成部分——如果我们想摆脱病理学范式中令人丧失力量的旧语言，如果我们想在自己的思维和公共话语领域成功传播神经多样性范式，那么这套新词汇体系就必须出现。



The word neurodiversity itself is of course the most essential piece of this new vocabulary. The essence of the entire paradigm—the understanding of neurological variation as a natural form of human diversity, subject to the same societal dynamics as other forms of diversity—is packed into that one word.

“神经多样性”这个词本身自然是这套新词汇中最核心的组成部分。整个范式的精髓——将神经变异视为人类多样性的一种自然形式，并与其他形式的多样性一样受制于相同的社会动态——都凝聚在这个词中。



Another useful word is neurominority. Neurotypicals are the majority; autistic people and dyslexic people are examples of neurominorities. I’d like to see the term neurominority come into more widespread usage, because there’s a need for it; there are a lot of topics in the discourse on neurodiversity that are much easier to talk about when one has a good, non-pathologizing word for referring to the various groups of people who aren’t neurotypical.

另一个有用的词是“神经少数群体”。神经典型者是多数群体；孤独谱系群体和阅读障碍者则是神经少数群体的例子。我希望“神经少数群体”这个术语能得到更广泛的使用，因为确实存在这样的需求；在关于神经多样性的讨论中，当人们有一个恰当且非病理化的词汇来指代那些不属于神经典型者的各类群体时，许多话题会更容易探讨。



Terms like neurodiversity, neurotypical, and neurominority allow us to talk and think about neurodiversity in ways that don’t implicitly pathologize neurominority individuals. As we cultivate autistic community and interact with other neurominority communities, and as we continue to generate writing and discussion on issues of relevance to us, more new language will emerge. Already, we’ve generated terms like stim and loud hands to describe important aspects of the autistic experience. And in my own academic work, my studies of cross-cultural competence (the ability to interact and communicate skillfully with people from multiple cultures) have led me to begin using the term neurocosmopolitanism, which I hope will catch on widely.

像神经多样性、神经典型、神经少数这类术语，让我们能够以不隐含病理化神经少数个体的方式谈论和思考神经多样性。随着我们培育孤独谱系社群、与其他神经少数群体互动，并持续撰写和讨论与我们相关议题，更多新语言将会涌现。我们已经创造了诸如"自我刺激行为"和"响亮双手"等术语来描述孤独谱系体验的重要方面。在我个人的学术研究中，对跨文化能力（与来自多元文化背景的人进行娴熟互动沟通的能力）的研究，促使我开始使用"神经世界主义"这一术语，希望它能被广泛接受。



It’s also my hope that the terms neurodiversity paradigm and pathology paradigm will catch on and come into widespread usage. In the interest of clarity, it’s useful to make the distinction between neurodiversity (the phenomenon of human neurological diversity) and the neurodiversity paradigm (the understanding of neurodiversity as a natural form of human diversity, subject to the same societal dynamics as other forms of diversity). And having a name for the pathology paradigm makes that paradigm much easier to discuss, recognize, challenge, and deconstruct—and eventually dismantle.

我也希望"神经多样性范式"和"病理学范式"这两个术语能够流行并广泛使用。为了清晰起见，区分"神经多样性"（人类神经多样性的现象）和"神经多样性范式"（将神经多样性理解为人类多样性的一种自然形式，与其他形式的多样性一样受制于相同的社会动态）是很有用的。而为病理学范式命名，则使该范式更容易被讨论、识别、挑战和解构——并最终被瓦解。



Words are tools. And as we recognize that the master’s tools will never dismantle the master’s house, we are creating our own tools, which can help us not only to dismantle the master’s house, but to build a new house in which we can live better, more empowered lives.

词语是工具。当我们认识到主人的工具永远无法拆毁主人的房屋时，我们正在创造自己的工具——这些工具不仅能帮助我们拆毁主人的房屋，还能建造一栋让我们生活得更好、更有力量的新居所。



Outposts in Your Head

你脑海中的前哨站



It breaks my heart when so many of the autistic people I meet speak of themselves and think of themselves in the language of the pathology paradigm, and when I see how this disempowers them and keeps them feeling bad about themselves. They’ve spent their lives listening to the toxic messages spread by proponents of the pathology paradigm, and they’ve accepted and internalized those messages and now endlessly repeat them in their own heads.

当我遇到许多孤独谱系群体成员用病理学范式的语言来描述和看待自己时，看到这种思维方式如何削弱他们的力量、让他们持续自我否定，这让我心碎不已。他们一生都在倾听病理学范式倡导者散播的有毒信息，接受并内化了这些信息，如今这些话语在他们脑海中无休止地循环播放。



When we recognize that the struggles of neurominorities largely follow the same dynamics as the struggles of other sorts of minority groups, we recognize this self-pathologizing talk as a manifestation of a problem that has plagued members of many minority groups—a phenomenon called internalized oppression.

当我们认识到神经少数群体的挣扎与其他少数群体面临的困境遵循着相似的动态规律时，就会明白这种自我病理化的言谈正是困扰许多少数群体成员的问题表现——这种现象被称为"内化压迫"。



A contemporary of Audre Lorde’s, the feminist journalist Sally Kempton, had this to say about internalized oppression: “It’s hard to fight an enemy who has outposts in your head.”

与奥德丽·洛德同时代的女性主义记者莎莉·肯普顿曾这样描述内化压迫："与一个在你脑海中设有前哨的敌人作战，实在艰难。"



The task of liberating ourselves from the master’s house begins with dismantling the parts of that house that have been built within our own heads. And that process begins with throwing away the master’s tools so that we stop inadvertently building up the very thing we’re trying to dismantle.

从主人的房子里解放自己的任务，始于拆除我们脑海中已建成的那些部分。而这个过程，要从扔掉主人的工具开始，这样我们才不会在无意中加固我们试图拆除的东西。



Throwing Away the Master’s Tools

扔掉主人的工具



Once we recognize that the foundation of the pathology paradigm—the fictive concept of “normal people”—is a fundamental element of the master’s toolkit, it becomes a lot easier to identify and rid ourselves of the master’s tools. All we need to do is take careful stock of our words, concepts, thoughts, beliefs, and worries, and see whether they still make sense if we throw out the concept of “normal,” the concept that there’s one “right” way for people’s brains and minds to function.

一旦我们认识到病理学范式的根基——虚构的“正常人”概念——是主人工具箱中的基本元素，识别并摆脱主人的工具就变得容易得多。我们只需仔细审视自己的言语、概念、思想、信念和忧虑，看看如果抛弃“正常”这一概念——即认为人们的大脑和心智只有一种“正确”运作方式——这些是否还能成立。



Once we’ve thrown away the concept of “normal,” neurotypicals are just members of a majority—not healthier or more “right” than the rest of us, just more common. And autistics are a minority group, no more intrinsically “disordered” than any ethnic minority. When we realize that “normal” is just something a bunch of people made up, when we recognize it as one of the master’s tools and toss it out the window, the idea of autism as a “disorder” goes out the window right along with it. Disordered compared to what state of order, exactly, if we refuse to buy into the idea that there’s one particular “normal” order to which all minds should conform?

一旦我们抛弃了“正常”这个概念，神经典型者不过是多数群体——并不比我们其他人更健康或更“正确”，只是更常见而已。而孤独谱系者是一个少数群体，其内在的“失调”程度并不比任何少数族裔更本质。当我们意识到“正常”不过是某些人编造出来的东西，当我们将其视为统治者的工具之一并扔出窗外时，孤独症是“障碍”的观念也会随之消失。如果我们拒绝接受所有心智都应遵循某种特定“正常”秩序的观点，那么所谓“失调”究竟是相对于何种秩序状态而言的呢？



Without the fictive reference point of “normal,” functioning labels—“high-functioning autism” and “low-functioning autism”—are also revealed to be absurd fictions. “High-functioning” or “low-functioning” compared to what? Who gets to decide what the proper “function” of any individual human should be?

没有了“正常”这个虚构的参照点，功能标签——“高功能孤独症”和“低功能孤独症”——也暴露为荒谬的虚构。“高功能”或“低功能”是相对于什么而言？谁有权决定任何个体人类应有的“功能”是什么？



In the pathology paradigm, the neurotypical mind is enthroned as the “normal” ideal against which all other types of minds are measured. “Low-functioning” really means “far from passing for neurotypical, far from being able to do the things that neurotypicals think people should do, and far from being able to thrive in a society created by and for neurotypicals.” “High-functioning” means “closer to passing for neurotypical.” To describe yourself as “high-functioning” is to use the master’s tools, to wall yourself up in the master’s house—a house in which neurotypicals are the ideal standard against which you should be measured, a house in which neurotypicals are always at the top, and in which “higher” means “more like them.”

在病理学范式中，神经典型心智被奉为衡量所有其他心智类型的"正常"标准。"低功能"实际上意味着"远未达到神经典型标准，远不能完成神经典型者认为人们应该做的事情，远不能在由神经典型者创建并为其服务的社会中茁壮成长"。"高功能"则意味着"更接近神经典型标准"。用"高功能"描述自己，就是在使用主人的工具，将自己禁锢在主人的房子里——在这所房子里，神经典型者是衡量你的理想标准，他们永远处于顶端，而"更高"意味着"更像他们"。



If we start from the assumption that neurotypicals are “normal,” and autistics are “disordered,” then poor connections between neurotypicals and autistics inevitably get blamed on some “defect” or “deficit” in autistics. If an autistic person can’t understand a neurotypical, it’s because autistics have empathy deficits and impaired communication skills; if a neurotypical can’t understand an autistic person, it’s because autistics have empathy deficits and poor communication skills. All the frictions and failures of connection between the two groups, and all the difficulties autistics run into in neurotypical society, all get blamed on autism. But when our vision is no longer clouded by the illusion of “normal,” we can recognize this double standard for what it is, recognize it as just another manifestation of the sort of privilege and power that dominant majorities so often wield over minorities of any sort.

如果我们从“神经典型者是‘正常的’，而孤独谱系者是‘失调的’”这一假设出发，那么神经典型者与孤独谱系者之间的不良连接，就不可避免地会被归咎于孤独谱系者身上的某种“缺陷”或“不足”。如果一个孤独谱系者无法理解神经典型者，那是因为孤独谱系者存在共情缺陷和沟通能力受损；如果一个神经典型者无法理解孤独谱系者，那也是因为孤独谱系者存在共情缺陷和沟通能力差。两个群体之间所有的摩擦与连接失败，以及孤独谱系者在神经典型者社会中遇到的所有困难，统统被归咎于孤独谱系。然而，当我们的视野不再被“正常”的幻象所蒙蔽时，我们就能认清这种双重标准的本质，认识到它不过是主流多数群体对任何少数群体所施加的特权与权力的另一种表现形式。



Life Beyond the Pathology Paradigm

超越病理学范式的生活



A paradigm shift, as you may recall, requires that all data be reinterpreted through the lens of the new paradigm. If you reject the fundamental premises of the pathology paradigm, and accept the premises of the neurodiversity paradigm, then it turns out that you don’t have a disorder after all. And it turns out that maybe you function exactly as you ought to function, and that you just live in a society that isn’t yet sufficiently enlightened to effectively accommodate and integrate people who function like you. And that maybe the troubles in your life have not been the result of any inherent wrongness in you. And that your true potential is unknown and is yours to explore. And that maybe you are, in fact, a thing of beauty.

范式转变，正如你可能记得的，要求所有数据都要通过新范式的视角重新解读。如果你拒绝病理范式的基本前提，接受神经多样性范式的前提，那么结果就是你根本没有障碍。而且结果可能是，你的运作方式恰恰就是你应该运作的方式，你只是生活在一个尚未足够开明、无法有效容纳和整合像你这样运作的人的社会里。也许你生活中的困扰并非源于你内在的任何错误。你的真正潜力是未知的，并且属于你自己去探索。也许，事实上，你本身就是一种美好的存在。







---


Nick_ebook-8










Comments on “Throw Away the Master’s Tools”

对“扔掉主人的工具”的评论



Re-reading “Throw Away the Master’s Tools” in the Summer of 2021, as I put this book together, I was pleasantly surprised at how much of it still holds up reasonably well, a decade after I wrote the original draft.

在 2021 年夏天重新阅读《扔掉主人的工具》时，我惊喜地发现，距离我写下初稿已过去十年，这篇文章的大部分内容依然经得起推敲。



One thing that I feel is worth emphasizing here is that the pathology paradigm and the neurodiversity paradigm are as fundamentally incompatible as, say, homophobia and the gay rights movement, or misogyny and feminism. In terms of discourse, research, and policy, the pathology paradigm asks, in essence, “What do we do about the problem of these people not being normal,” while the neurodiversity paradigm asks, “What do we do about the problem of these people being oppressed, marginalized, and/or poorly served and poorly accommodated by the prevailing culture?”

这里值得强调的一点是，病理范式与神经多样性范式从根本上互不相容，就像恐同与同性恋权利运动、厌女与女权主义一样。在话语、研究和政策层面，病理范式本质上问的是：“我们该如何解决这些人不够正常的问题？”而神经多样性范式问的是：“我们该如何解决这些人受到压迫、边缘化，以及/或在主流文化中得不到良好服务与安置的问题？”



•



It’s also worth noting that the growing popularity of the term neurodiversity has led to its widespread appropriation as a buzzword by a lot of individuals and organizations who don’t understand its implications and are still very much thinking and operating within the pathology paradigm. It’s far too common these days to see some website or article that uses the word neurodiversity and then proceeds to talk about autism and/or other forms of neurodivergence in highly pathologizing ways—for example, referring to them as “conditions,” promoting the old pathology paradigm stereotypes and canards, or rating autistic people as “high-functioning” or “low-functioning” based on how close they come to passing for neurotypical. So it’s important to remember that mere adoption of terminology isn’t the same as actually making a meaningful shift in mindset. It’s important to keep thinking critically about how neurodiversity-related terms are being used (or misused) in a given context, and whether the underlying premises involved are the premises of the neurodiversity paradigm or of the pathology paradigm.

同样值得注意的是，“神经多样性”这一术语日益流行，导致许多个人和组织将其广泛挪用为流行词汇，但他们并不理解其内涵，思维和行动仍深陷病理学范式。如今常见某些网站或文章使用“神经多样性”一词后，却以高度病理化的方式谈论孤独谱系和/或其他形式的神经殊异性——例如将其称为“病症”，宣扬旧病理学范式的刻板印象与谬论，或根据孤独谱系群体接近神经典型者的程度将其划分为“高功能”或“低功能”。因此必须谨记：单纯采用术语并不等同于真正实现思维模式的转变。关键在于持续批判性思考：在特定语境中，与神经多样性相关的术语是如何被使用（或滥用）的？其背后的前提究竟是神经多样性范式还是病理学范式？



•



Toward the end of “Throw Away the Master’s Tools,” I discussed the pathology paradigm terms “high-functioning” and “low-functioning”—terms which assume that neurotypicality represents the “highest” human ideal, and which rate autistic human beings as “higher” or “lower” based on how well they conform to dominant social norms of neurotypical performance. Contemplating this part of the essay now, I’d like to propose that instead of rating human beings as “high-functioning” or “low-functioning,” we apply the terms “high-functioning” and “low-functioning” to societies, rating the functioning of a society according to the degree to which it succeeds in supporting and furthering the well-being of all of its members—and the degree to which it can accommodate and integrate diversity, and employ diversity as a creative resource, without attempting to reduce or eliminate it and without establishing hierarchies of dominance and oppression.

在《扔掉主人的工具》一文接近尾声时，我讨论了病理学范式中的术语“高功能”和“低功能”——这些术语假定神经典型性代表了人类的“最高”理想，并根据孤独谱系个体在多大程度上符合神经典型表现的主流社会规范，将其评为“更高”或“更低”。如今重读这部分内容，我想提议：与其将人类个体评为“高功能”或“低功能”，不如将这些术语应用于社会本身——根据社会在多大程度上成功支持并促进所有成员的福祉，以及它在多大程度上能够容纳和整合多样性、将多样性作为创造性资源加以运用（而非试图减少或消除多样性，也非建立支配与压迫的等级制度），来评判社会的功能水平。



•



Another thing I wrote toward the end of “Throw Away the Master’s Tools” was this:

我在《扔掉主人的工具》结尾处还写了这样一段话：



If we start from the assumption that neurotypicals are “normal,” and autistics are “disordered,” then poor connections between neurotypicals and Autistics inevitably get blamed on some “defect” or “deficit” in autistics. If an autistic person can’t understand a neurotypical, it’s because autistics have empathy deficits and impaired communication skills; if a neurotypical can’t understand an autistic person, it’s because autistics have empathy deficits and poor communication skills. All the frictions and failures of connection between the two groups, and all the difficulties autistics run into in neurotypical society, all get blamed on autism. But when our vision is no longer clouded by the illusion of “normal,” we can recognize this double standard for what it is, recognize it as just another manifestation of the sort of privilege and power that dominant majorities so often wield over minorities of any sort.

如果我们从“神经典型者是‘正常的’，而孤独谱系者是‘失调的’”这一假设出发，那么神经典型者与孤独谱系者之间的不良连接，就不可避免地会被归咎于孤独谱系者的某种“缺陷”或“不足”。如果孤独谱系者无法理解神经典型者，那是因为孤独谱系者缺乏共情能力、沟通能力受损；如果神经典型者无法理解孤独谱系者，那还是因为孤独谱系者缺乏共情能力、沟通能力不佳。两个群体之间所有的摩擦与连接失败，以及孤独谱系者在神经典型者社会中遭遇的所有困难，统统被归咎于孤独谱系。然而，当我们的视野不再被“正常”的幻象所遮蔽时，我们就能认清这种双重标准的本质，认识到它不过是优势多数群体对任何少数群体惯常施加的那种特权与权力的又一种表现形式。



It’s worth noting here that right around the time I wrote the original version of “Throw Away the Master’s Tools,” my fellow autistic scholar Damian Milton began writing academic articles focused on the particular phenomenon I described in the above paragraph—the fact that it’s harder for people to understand each other when their respective modes of experience and cognition differ significantly, and under the pathology paradigm this mutual gap of understanding is blamed entirely on alleged autistic deficits rather than treated as a mutual communication challenge to be worked on reciprocally. Milton dubbed this double standard the Double Empathy Problem, and it’s a phenomenon that’s now widely recognized and discussed in the field of Critical Autism Studies.

值得注意的是，大约在我撰写《扔掉大师的工具》初稿的同时，同为孤独谱系学者的达米安·米尔顿开始撰写学术文章，聚焦于我在上文描述的特殊现象——当人们的经验与认知模式存在显著差异时，彼此理解会变得更为困难；而在病理学范式下，这种相互理解的鸿沟被完全归咎于所谓的孤独谱系缺陷，而非被视为需要双方共同应对的沟通挑战。米尔顿将这种双重标准称为"双向同理心问题"，这一现象如今在批判性孤独谱系研究领域已得到广泛认可与讨论。



•



Two other things it occurred to me to comment upon and expand upon further as I re-read “Throw Away the Master’s Tools” were the definition of neurodiversity and the definition of neurotypical. But those comments ended up long enough that I turned them into their own separate chapters, “Defining Neurodiversity” and “Defining Neurotypicality & Neurodivergence,” which appear a little bit later in this book.

重读《扔掉大师的工具》时，我还想到另外两个值得进一步评论和扩展的内容：神经多样性的定义，以及神经典型者的定义。但这些评论篇幅过长，最终被我单独成章，即《定义神经多样性》与《定义神经典型性与神经殊异性》，稍后将在本书中呈现。







---


Nick_ebook-9










Neurodiversity: Some Basic Terms & Definitions

神经多样性：基本术语与定义



I originally wrote this piece for the Neurocosmopolitanism website in September of 2014, and these days it lives on the Neuroqueer site. There’s not much story behind this one to tell, beyond what’s already stated in the opening paragraphs of the piece itself: I created it as a public service because I saw a lot of confused people using neurodiversity-related terms incorrectly. So far, of all the pieces I’ve written, this is the one that’s been most frequently cited in other people’s writing—academic and otherwise—and most frequently linked to online.

我最初于 2014 年 9 月为 Neurocosmopolitanism 网站撰写此文，如今它已收录于 Neuroqueer 网站。这篇文章背后的故事并不多，除了开篇段落已提及的内容：我将其作为公共服务创作，是因为看到许多人误用与神经多样性相关的术语。迄今为止，在我所有作品中，这是被他人（无论是学术著作还是其他类型写作）引用最多、在线链接最频繁的一篇。



New paradigms often require a bit of new language, and this is certainly the case with the neurodiversity paradigm. I see many people—scholars, journalists, bloggers, internet commenters, and even people who identify as neurodiversity activists—get confused about the terminology around neurodiversity. Their misunderstanding and incorrect usage of certain terms often results in poor and clumsy communication of their message, and propagation of further confusion (including other confused people imitating their errors). At the very least, incorrect use of terminology can make a writer or speaker appear ignorant, or an unreliable source of information, in the eyes of those who do understand the meanings of the terms.

新范式往往需要一些新语言，神经多样性范式正是如此。我看到许多人——学者、记者、博主、网络评论者，甚至自认为是神经多样性活动家的人——对神经多样性相关术语感到困惑。他们对某些术语的误解和错误使用，往往导致信息传达粗糙笨拙，并进一步引发混乱（包括其他困惑者模仿他们的错误）。至少，在那些真正理解术语含义的人看来，术语使用不当会让作者或发言者显得无知，或成为不可靠的信息来源。



For those of us who seek to propagate and build upon the neurodiversity paradigm—especially those of us who are producing writing on neurodiversity—it’s vital that we maintain some basic clarity and consistency of language, for the sake of effective communication among ourselves and with our broader audiences. Clarity of language supports clarity of understanding.

对于我们这些致力于传播和发展神经多样性范式的人——尤其是那些撰写神经多样性相关文章的人——为了在彼此之间以及与更广泛的受众之间进行有效沟通，保持语言的基本清晰度和一致性至关重要。语言的清晰有助于理解的清晰。



And, as I increasingly find myself in the position of reviewing other people’s writing on neurodiversity—grading student papers, reviewing book submissions or submissions to journals, consulting on various projects, or even just deciding which pieces of writing I’m willing to recommend to people—I’m getting tired of running into the same basic errors over and over.

而且，随着我越来越多地审阅他人关于神经多样性的文章——批改学生论文、审阅书籍投稿或期刊投稿、为各种项目提供咨询，甚至只是决定哪些文章我愿意推荐给别人——我厌倦了反复遇到同样基本错误的情况。



So, as a public service, I’ve created this list of a few key neurodiversity-related terms, their meanings and proper usage, and the ways in which I most commonly see them misused.

因此，作为一项公共服务，我列出了这份与神经多样性相关的关键术语清单，包括它们的含义、正确用法，以及我最常见到的误用方式。



NEURODIVERSITY

神经多样性



What It Means:

含义：



Neurodiversity is the diversity of human minds, the infinite variation in neurocognitive functioning within our species.

神经多样性是人类心智的多样性，是我们这个物种在神经认知功能上的无限变异。



What It Doesn’t Mean:

它并不意味着：



Neurodiversity is a biological fact. It’s not a perspective, an approach, a belief, a political position, or a paradigm. That’s the neurodiversity paradigm (see below), not neurodiversity itself.

神经多样性是一个生物学事实。它不是一种视角、方法、信念、政治立场或范式。那是神经多样性范式（见下文），而非神经多样性本身。



Neurodiversity is not a political or social activist movement. That’s the Neurodiversity Movement (see below), not neurodiversity itself.

神经多样性不是政治或社会活动运动。那是神经多样性运动（见下文），而非神经多样性本身。



Neurodiversity is not a trait that any individual possesses or can possess. When an individual or group of individuals diverges from the dominant societal standards of “normal” neurocognitive functioning, they don’t “have neurodiversity,” they’re neurodivergent (see below).

神经多样性并非任何个体所拥有或可能拥有的特质。当个体或群体偏离主流社会对“正常”神经认知功能的标准时，他们并非“拥有神经多样性”，而是属于神经殊异（见下文）。



Example of Correct Usage:

正确用法示例：



“Our school offers multiple learning strategies to accommodate the neurodiversity of our student body.”

“我校提供多种学习策略，以适应学生群体的神经多样性。”



Examples of Incorrect Usage:

错误用法示例：



“Neurodiversity claims that…”

“神经多样性声称……”



This writer is actually trying to talk about either the neurodiversity paradigm or the Neurodiversity Movement. Neurodiversity, as a biological characteristic of the species, can’t “claim” anything, any more than variations in human skin pigmentation can “claim” something.

这位作者实际上是想讨论神经多样性范式或神经多样性运动。神经多样性作为物种的一种生物特征，本身无法“声称”任何事情，就像人类肤色的差异无法“声称”什么一样。



“Neurodiversity is a load of nonsense.”

“神经多样性纯属一派胡言。”



Really? So human brains and minds don’t differ from one another? There’s an awful lot of scientific evidence that shows quite plainly that there’s considerable variation among human brains. And if we all thought alike, the world would be a very different place indeed. The person who wrote this sentence was probably trying to object to the neurodiversity paradigm and/or the positions of the Neurodiversity Movement, and has ended up sounding rather silly as a result of failing to distinguish between these things and the phenomenon of neurodiversity itself.

真的吗？那么人类的大脑和思维之间就不存在差异吗？大量科学证据明确表明，人类大脑之间存在相当大的差异。如果我们都想法一致，世界将会截然不同。写下这句话的人很可能是在反对神经多样性范式和/或神经多样性运动的立场，但由于未能区分这些概念与神经多样性现象本身，最终显得相当荒谬。



“My neurodiversity makes it hard for me to cope with school.”

“我的神经多样性让我很难应对学校生活。”

The correct word here would be neurodivergence, rather than neurodiversity. An individual, by definition, cannot be “diverse” or “have diversity.”

这里正确的词应该是神经殊异性，而非神经多样性。从定义上讲，个体不可能“具有多样性”或“拥有多样性”。



“Autism and dyslexia are forms of neurodiversity.”

“孤独症和阅读障碍是神经多样性的表现形式。”



Nope. Nope, nope, nope. There’s no such thing as a “form of neurodiversity.” Autism and dyslexia are forms of neurodivergence.

不对。完全不对。根本不存在所谓的“神经多样性的表现形式”。孤独症和阅读障碍是神经殊异性的表现形式。



NEURODIVERSITY PARADIGM

神经多样性范式



What It Means:

其含义：



The neurodiversity paradigm is a specific perspective on neurodiversity—a perspective or approach that boils down to these fundamental principles:

神经多样性范式是对神经多样性的一种特定视角——一种可归结为以下基本原则的视角或方法：




Neurodiversity is a natural and valuable form of human diversity.

神经多样性是人类多样性中一种自然且有价值的形式。



The idea that there is one “normal” or “healthy” type of brain or mind, or one “right” style of neurocognitive functioning, is a culturally constructed fiction, no more valid (and no more conducive to a healthy society or to the overall well-being of humanity) than the idea that there is one “normal” or “right” ethnicity, gender, or culture.

认为存在一种"正常"或"健康"的大脑或心智类型，或一种"正确"的神经认知功能模式，这本身就是一种文化建构的虚构，其合理性（以及对健康社会或人类整体福祉的促进作用）并不比认为存在一种"正常"或"正确"的种族、性别或文化更高明。



The social dynamics that manifest in regard to neurodiversity are similar to the social dynamics that manifest in regard to other forms of human diversity (e.g., diversity of ethnicity, gender, or culture). These dynamics include the dynamics of social power inequalities, and also the dynamics by which diversity, when embraced, acts as a source of creative potential.

神经多样性所呈现的社会动态，与人类其他形式的多样性（如种族、性别或文化的多样性）所呈现的社会动态相似。这些动态既包括社会权力不平等的运作机制，也包括多样性在被接纳时如何成为创造性潜能源泉的运作机制。




What It Doesn’t Mean:

它不意味着什么：



The neurodiversity paradigm provides a philosophical foundation for the activism of the Neurodiversity Movement, but the two aren’t the same. For instance, there are people working on developing inclusive education strategies based on the neurodiversity paradigm, who don’t identify as social justice activists or as part of the Neurodiversity Movement.

神经多样性范式为神经多样性运动的社会行动提供了哲学基础，但两者并不等同。例如，有些基于神经多样性范式开发包容性教育策略的人，并不自认为是社会正义活动家或神经多样性运动的一部分。



Example of Correct Usage:

正确用法示例：



“Those who have embraced the neurodiversity paradigm, and who truly understand it, do not use pathologizing terms like ‘disorder’ to describe neurocognitive variants like autism.”

“那些接受并真正理解神经多样性范式的人，不会使用‘障碍’这类病理化术语来描述孤独谱系等神经认知变异。”



NEURODIVERSITY MOVEMENT

神经多样性运动



What It Means:

其含义：



The Neurodiversity Movement is a social justice movement that seeks civil rights, equality, respect, and full societal inclusion for the neurodivergent.

神经多样性运动是一场社会正义运动，旨在为神经殊异群体争取公民权利、平等、尊重以及全面的社会包容。



What It Doesn’t Mean:

它并不意味着：



The Neurodiversity Movement is not a single group or organization, is not run by any single group or organization, and has no leader. Like most civil rights movements, the Neurodiversity Movement is made up of a great many individuals, some of them organized into groups of one sort or another. These individuals and groups are quite diverse in their viewpoints, goals, concerns, political positions, affiliations, methods of activism, and interpretations of the neurodiversity paradigm.

神经多样性运动并非由某个单一团体或组织主导，也不存在任何领导者。与大多数民权运动类似，它由众多个体组成，其中部分人自发形成各类团体。这些个体和团体在观点、目标、关切、政治立场、所属组织、行动方式以及对神经多样性范式的理解上，呈现出显著的多样性。



The Neurodiversity Movement began within the Autism Rights Movement, and there is still a great deal of overlap between the two movements. But the Neurodiversity Movement and the Autism Rights Movement are not one and the same. The most significant distinction between the two is that the Neurodiversity Movement seeks to be inclusive of all neurominorities, not just autistics. Also, there some who advocate for the rights of autistics but who cannot rightly be considered part of the Neurodiversity Movement because they still consider autism to be a medical pathology or “disorder,” a view at odds with the neurodiversity paradigm.

神经多样性运动起源于孤独症权利运动，两者至今仍有大量重叠。但神经多样性运动与孤独症权利运动并非同一回事。两者最显著的区别在于，神经多样性运动力求包容所有神经少数群体，而不仅限于孤独症人士。此外，有些人为孤独症人士争取权利，却不能被真正视为神经多样性运动的一部分，因为他们仍将孤独症视为医学病理或"障碍"，这种观点与神经多样性范式相悖。



NEURODIVERGENT and NEURODIVERGENCE

神经殊异与神经殊异性



What It Means:

含义：



Neurodivergent, sometimes abbreviated as ND, means having a mind that functions in ways which diverge significantly from the dominant societal standards of “normal.”

神经殊异（有时缩写为 ND）指心智运作方式与主流社会"正常"标准存在显著差异的状态。



Neurodivergent is quite a broad term. Neurodivergence (the state of being neurodivergent) can be largely or entirely genetic and innate, or it can be largely or entirely produced by brain-altering experience, or some combination of the two. Autism and dyslexia are examples of innate forms of neurodivergence, while alterations in brain functioning caused by such things as trauma, long-term meditation practice, or heavy usage of psychedelic drugs are examples of forms of neurodivergence produced through experience.

神经殊异是一个相当宽泛的术语。神经殊异性（即处于神经殊异状态）可能很大程度上或完全由遗传和先天因素决定，也可能很大程度上或完全由改变大脑的经历所产生，或是两者的某种结合。孤独症和阅读障碍属于先天形式的神经殊异，而由创伤、长期冥想练习或大量使用迷幻药物等因素导致的大脑功能改变，则是通过经历产生的神经殊异形式。



A person whose neurocognitive functioning diverges from dominant societal norms in multiple ways—for instance, a person who is autistic, dyslexic, and epileptic—can be described as multiply neurodivergent.

一个人的神经认知功能在多个方面偏离主流社会规范——例如，一个同时患有孤独症、阅读障碍和癫痫的人——可以被描述为多重神经殊异。



Some forms of innate or largely innate neurodivergence, like autism, are intrinsic and pervasive factors in an individual’s psyche, personality, and fundamental way of relating to the world. The neurodiversity paradigm rejects the pathologizing of such forms of neurodivergence, and the Neurodiversity Movement opposes attempts to get rid of them.

某些先天或基本先天的神经殊异形式，如孤独症，是个体心理、人格以及与世界互动基本方式中内在且普遍存在的因素。神经多样性范式拒绝将此类神经殊异形式病理化，而神经多样性运动则反对试图消除它们的做法。



Other forms of neurodivergence, like epilepsy or the effects of traumatic brain injuries, could be removed from an individual without erasing fundamental aspects of the individual’s selfhood, and in many cases the individual would be happy to be rid of such forms of neurodivergence. The neurodiversity paradigm does not reject the pathologizing of these forms of neurodivergence, and the Neurodiversity Movement does not object to consensual attempts to cure them (but still most definitely objects to discrimination against people who have them).

其他形式的神经殊异性，例如癫痫或创伤性脑损伤的后遗症，可以在不抹除个体自我本质核心的情况下被移除，而且在许多情况下，个体也乐于摆脱这类神经殊异性。神经多样性范式并不排斥将这些形式的神经殊异性病理化，神经多样性运动也不反对在自愿前提下尝试治愈它们（但依然坚决反对歧视患有这些神经殊异性的人）。



Thus, neurodivergence is not intrinsically positive or negative, desirable or undesirable—it all depends on what sort of neurodivergence one is talking about.

因此，神经殊异性本身并无内在的积极或消极、可取或不可取之分——这完全取决于具体讨论的是哪种神经殊异性。



The terms neurodivergent and neurodivergence were coined in the year 2000 by Kassiane Asasumasu, a multiply neurodivergent neurodiversity activist.

“神经殊异”和“神经殊异性”这两个术语由凯西恩·阿萨苏玛苏于 2000 年创造，她本人是一位多重神经殊异的神经多样性活动家。



What It Doesn’t Mean:

它并不意味着：



Neurodivergent is not a synonym for autistic. There are countless possible ways to be neurodivergent, and being autistic is only one of those ways. There are myriad ways of being neurodivergent that have no resemblance or connection to autism whatsoever. Never, ever use neurodivergent as a euphemism for autistic. If you mean that someone is autistic, say they’re autistic. It’s not a dirty word.

神经殊异并非孤独谱系的同义词。成为神经殊异的方式有无数种可能，而孤独谱系只是其中一种。存在无数种与孤独症毫无相似或关联的神经殊异方式。永远不要用"神经殊异"作为"孤独谱系"的委婉说法。如果你想说某人是孤独谱系，就直接说他们是孤独谱系。这不是什么脏话。



Examples of Correct Usage:

正确用法示例：



“Our school aims to be inclusive of students who are Autistic, dyslexic, or otherwise neurodivergent, though there are some types of neurodivergence that we’re still seeking ways to accommodate.”

"我们学校旨在包容孤独谱系、阅读障碍或其他神经殊异的学生，尽管对于某些类型的神经殊异性，我们仍在寻求更好的适应方式。"



“This group is for people who identify as both queer and ND (neurodivergent).”

"这个小组面向那些同时认同自己为酷儿和 ND（神经殊异）的人。"



NEUROTYPICAL, or NT

神经典型者，或 NT



What It Means:

含义：



Neurotypical, often abbreviated as NT, means having a style of neurocognitive functioning that falls within the dominant societal standards of “normal.”

神经典型者（常缩写为 NT）指神经认知功能模式符合社会主流"正常"标准的人。



Neurotypical can be used as either an adjective (“He’s neurotypical”) or a noun (“He’s a neurotypical”).

"神经典型者"既可作形容词（"他是神经典型者"），也可作名词（"他是个神经典型者"）。



Neurotypical is the opposite of neurodivergent. Neurotypicality is the way-of-being from which neurodivergent people diverge. Neurotypical bears the same sort of relationship to neurodivergent that straight bears to queer.

神经典型是神经殊异的对立面。神经典型性是一种存在方式，神经殊异者正是从这种存在方式中偏离出来。神经典型与神经殊异的关系，类似于直人与酷儿的关系。



What It Doesn’t Mean:

它并不意味着：



Neurotypical is not synonymous with non-autistic.

神经典型并非非孤独谱系者的同义词。



Neurotypical is the opposite of neurodivergent, not the opposite of autistic. Autism is only one of many forms of neurodivergence, so there are many, many people who are neither neurotypical nor autistic. Using neurotypical to mean non-autistic is like using “white” to mean “not black.”

神经典型是神经殊异的对立面，而非孤独谱系的对立面。孤独谱系只是神经殊异性的众多形式之一，因此有许许多多的人既非神经典型也非孤独谱系。用神经典型来指代非孤独谱系者，就像用"白人"来指代"非黑人"一样。



Also, neurotypical is not a derogatory word, and has no intrinsic negative connotation. Of course, sometimes people use the word in the context of criticizing the behavior of neurotypicals, but that doesn’t make it an intrinsically negative word. A lot of people criticize the behavior of men, too, but that doesn’t make “man” an intrinsically derogatory word.

此外，神经典型并非贬义词，本身也不含负面含义。当然，有时人们会在批评神经典型者行为时使用这个词，但这并不使其成为本质上的负面词汇。就像很多人也会批评男性的行为，但"男人"这个词本身并非贬义词。



Examples of Correct Usage:

正确用法示例：



“If the primary language of the society in which you were born is well-suited to the purpose of describing your sensory experiences, your needs, and your thought processes, you may have neurotypical privilege.”

"如果你出生社会的主流语言能很好地描述你的感官体验、需求和思维过程，那么你可能享有神经典型特权。"



“My sister is NT, but after growing up with an Autistic father and brother, she’s quite at ease with other people’s neurodivergence.”

"我姐姐是神经典型者，但在与孤独谱系的父亲和弟弟一起成长后，她对他人的神经殊异性表现得相当从容。"



Example of Incorrect Usage:

错误用法示例：



“Is your daughter Autistic or neurotypical?”

“你的女儿是孤独谱系还是神经典型？”



This isn’t a well-worded question because there are other possibilities. The daughter in question might be non-autistic, but might also not qualify as neurotypical—she might, for instance, be dyslexic or have Down Syndrome.

这个问题措辞不当，因为还存在其他可能性。所提及的女儿可能并非孤独谱系，但也未必符合神经典型的定义——例如，她可能患有阅读障碍或唐氏综合征。



NEUROMINORITY

神经少数群体



What It Means:

含义：



A neurominority is a population of neurodivergent people about whom all of the following are true:

神经少数群体是指符合以下所有条件的神经殊异人群：




They all share a similar form of neurodivergence.

他们共享相似的神经殊异性形式。



The form of neurodivergence they share is one of those forms that is largely innate and that is inseparable from who they are, constituting an intrinsic and pervasive factor in their psyches, personalities, and fundamental ways of relating to the world.

他们所共享的神经殊异性形式在很大程度上是与生俱来的，且与其身份密不可分，构成了其心理、人格及与世界互动基本方式中固有且普遍的要素。



The form of neurodivergence they share is one to which the neurotypical majority tends to respond with some degree of prejudice, misunderstanding, discrimination, and/or oppression (generally facilitated by classifying that form of neurodivergence as a medical pathology).

他们所共有的神经殊异形式，往往会引起神经典型多数群体一定程度的偏见、误解、歧视和/或压迫（通常通过将这种神经殊异形式归类为医学病理来促成）。




Some examples of neurominority groups include autistic people, dyslexic people, and people with Down Syndrome.

神经少数群体的例子包括孤独谱系群体、阅读障碍者以及唐氏综合征患者。



It’s also possible to be neurodivergent without being a member of a neurominority group. Examples include people with acquired traumatic brain injuries, and people who have altered their own neurocognitive functioning through extensive use of psychedelic drugs.

一个人也可能在没有成为神经少数群体成员的情况下具有神经殊异性。例如，后天获得性脑损伤患者，以及通过大量使用迷幻药物改变自身神经认知功能的人。



The word neurominority can function as either a noun (as in, “autistics are a neurominority”) or an adjective (as in, “autistics are a neurominority group”).

“神经少数群体”一词既可作名词（如“孤独谱系群体是一个神经少数群体”），也可作形容词（如“孤独谱系群体是一个神经少数群体”）。



NEURODIVERSE

神经多元



What It Means:

含义：



A group of people is neurodiverse if one or more members of the group differ substantially from other members, in terms of their neurocognitive functioning.

如果一个群体中有一个或多个成员在神经认知功能方面与其他成员存在显著差异，那么这个群体就是神经多元的。



Or, to phrase it another way, a neurodiverse group is a group in which multiple neurocognitive styles are represented.

或者换种说法，神经多元群体是指包含多种神经认知风格的群体。



Thus, a family, the faculty or student body of a school, the population of a town, or the cast of characters of a TV show would be neurodiverse if some members had different neurocognitive styles from other members—for instance, if some members were neurotypical while others were autistic.

因此，一个家庭、一所学校的教职员工或学生群体、一个城镇的人口，或一部电视剧的角色阵容，如果其中一些成员拥有与其他成员不同的神经认知风格——例如，有些成员是神经典型者，而另一些是孤独谱系者——那么他们就是神经多元的。



What It Doesn’t Mean:

它并不意味着：



Many people mistakenly use neurodiverse where the correct word would be neurodivergent. Of all the errors that people make in writing and speaking about neurodiversity, the misuse of neurodiverse to mean neurodivergent is by far the most common.

许多人错误地使用“神经多元”一词，而正确的说法应该是“神经殊异”。在所有关于神经多样性的写作和口语表达中，将“神经多元”误用为“神经殊异”是最常见的错误。



There is no such thing as a “neurodiverse individual.” The correct term is “neurodivergent individual.” An individual can diverge, but an individual cannot be diverse.

不存在所谓的“神经多元个体”。正确的术语是“神经殊异个体”。个体可以存在殊异，但个体不能是多元的。



Neurodiverse does not mean “non-neurotypical.” The opposite of neurotypical is neurodivergent, not neurodiverse. Neurodiverse cannot be used to mean “non-neurotypical,” because neurotypical people, like all other human beings, are part of the spectrum of human neurodiversity. The opposite of neurodiverse would be neurohomogenous (meaning “composed of people who are all neurocognitively similar to one another”).

“神经多元”并不意味着“非神经典型”。神经典型的反义词是神经殊异，而非神经多元。神经多元不能用来指代“非神经典型”，因为神经典型人群与其他所有人一样，都是人类神经多样性光谱的一部分。神经多元的反义词应是神经同质（意为“由神经认知特征相似的人组成”）。



To refer to neurominority groups or neurodivergent individuals as “neurodiverse” is incorrect grammatically, because diverse doesn’t mean different from the majority, it means made up of multiple different types. So an individual can never be diverse, by definition. And a group where everyone is neurodivergent in more or less the same way (e.g., a group composed entirely of autistic people) wouldn’t be “neurodiverse,” either.

将神经少数群体或神经殊异个体称为“神经多元”在语法上是不正确的，因为“多元”并非指“与多数不同”，而是指“由多种不同类型组成”。因此，从定义上讲，个体永远不能是“多元”的。同样，一个由神经认知特征大致相同的神经殊异者组成的群体（例如完全由孤独谱系群体构成的群体）也不能被称为“神经多元”。



The only appropriate and grammatically correct use of the term neurodiverse is when it’s used to describe a group of people whose members differ neurocognitively from each other. In other words, a classroom where everyone is autistic is not neurodiverse, but a classroom where some students are neurotypical and some aren’t is neurodiverse.

“神经多元”一词唯一恰当且语法正确的用法，是用于描述其成员在神经认知上彼此存在差异的群体。换言之，一个所有学生都是孤独谱系的教室并非神经多元，但一个既有神经典型学生、也有非神经典型学生的教室才是神经多元的。



Humanity is neurodiverse, just as humanity is racially, ethnically, and culturally diverse. By definition, no human being falls outside of the spectrum of human neurodiversity, just as no human being falls outside of the spectrum of human racial, ethnic, and cultural diversity.

人类是神经多元的，正如人类在种族、民族和文化上也是多元的。从定义上来说，没有人能脱离人类神经多元的范畴，正如没有人能脱离人类种族、民族和文化的多元范畴一样。



In addition to being incorrect, it’s also oppressive to misuse the word “diverse” to mean “minority,” because this misuse of “diverse” is based in the intrinsically oppressive assumption that there’s a default “normal” way of being and that “diversity” is about adding non-normative individuals into the “normal” default environment. This is the assumption that allows tokenization to pass for “diversity” in corporations, schools, and other social institutions.

将“多元”误用为“少数群体”不仅不正确，而且具有压迫性。因为这种对“多元”的误用基于一种本质上的压迫性假设——即存在一种默认的“正常”存在方式，而“多元”只是将非规范个体添加到“正常”的默认环境中。正是这种假设，让企业、学校及其他社会机构得以用象征性的点缀来冒充“多元”。



We can see this same oppressive misuse of the word “diverse” in the discourse of racists who use the term “diverse” as a euphemism for “non-white.” This usage seeks to twist the definition of the word “diverse” to mean “not part of the privileged in-group.” Again, that’s not what the word means, and misusing it in that particular way serves to reinforce a racist mindset in which white people are seen as intrinsically separate from the rest of humanity, rather than as just another part of the spectrum of human ethnic diversity.

我们可以看到，在种族主义者的言论中同样存在对“多元”一词的压迫性滥用——他们将“多元”用作“非白人”的委婉说法。这种用法试图扭曲“多元”的定义，使其意指“不属于特权内群体”。再次强调，这并非该词的本义，而如此滥用恰恰强化了种族主义思维模式：将白人视为本质上与人类其他群体割裂的存在，而非人类种族多样性光谱中的普通一环。



It is the same with the misuse of the term neurodiverse to mean “non-neurotypical.” To describe an autistic, dyslexic, or otherwise neurodivergent person as a “neurodiverse individual” is not merely an incorrect usage of the word “diverse”—it also serves to reinforce an ableist mindset in which neurotypical people are seen as intrinsically separate from the rest of humanity, rather than as just another part of the spectrum of human neurodiversity.

对“神经多元”一词的滥用同样如此——将其曲解为“非神经典型”。将孤独谱系、阅读障碍或其他神经殊异个体描述为“神经多元个体”，不仅是对“多元”一词的错误使用，更强化了能力主义思维模式：将神经典型人群视为本质上与人类其他群体割裂的存在，而非人类神经多样性光谱中的普通一环。



In summary, then: misusing the term neurodiverse to mean neurodivergent (i.e., non-neurotypical) is not only plain old bad grammar, it also subtly reinforces ableism and undercuts the fundamental tenets of the neurodiversity paradigm. I hope this explanation will help people to avoid this particular error in the future—and, when possible, to correct such misuse where they encounter it.

总之，将“神经多元”误用为“神经殊异”（即非神经典型）不仅是一种糟糕的语法错误，还会微妙地强化能力主义，并削弱神经多样性范式的基本原则。我希望这一解释能帮助人们未来避免这一特定错误——并在可能的情况下，纠正他们遇到的此类误用。



Examples of Correct Usage:

正确用法示例：



“We humans are a neurodiverse species.”

“我们人类是一个神经多元的物种。”



“We employ a wide variety of creative teaching strategies to accommodate the many different learning styles represented in our highly neurodiverse student body.”

“我们采用多种多样的创造性教学策略，以适应高度神经多元的学生群体中呈现的众多不同学习风格。”



“My neurodiverse family includes three neurotypicals, two autistics, and one person who’s both ADHD and dyslexic.”

“我的神经多元家庭包括三位神经典型者、两位自闭症人士，以及一位兼具多动症和阅读障碍的成员。”



“I think every single member of their board of directors is neurotypical. An organization that supposedly serves the needs of neurominority children should have a more neurodiverse board.”

“我认为他们董事会的每一位成员都是神经典型者。一个理应服务于神经少数群体儿童需求的组织，其董事会应该更加神经多元。”



Examples of Incorrect Usage:

错误用法示例：



“This group welcomes autistics and other neurodiverse people.”

“这个团体欢迎自闭症人士及其他神经多元者。”

It’s nice to be welcomed, but there’s no such thing as a “neurodiverse person.” the correct phrase here would be “autistics and other neurodivergent people.”

受到欢迎固然好，但根本不存在所谓的“神经多元人士”。正确的说法应该是“自闭症者及其他神经殊异人士”。



“This group is open to both neurotypicals and the neurodiverse.”

“本团体对神经典型者及神经多元人士均开放。”

No, no, no. “The neurodiverse?” Seriously? What does that even mean? The spectrum of neurodiversity encompasses the entire human species, so one can’t label any subset of the human species as “the neurodiverse.” And neurotypicals are part of the spectrum of human neurodiversity, so it makes no sense to say “neurotypicals and the neurodiverse,” as if those were two separate things. The correct way to say this would be, “This group is open to both neurotypicals and the neurodivergent.”

不，不，不。“神经多元人士”？认真的吗？这到底是什么意思？神经多样性的谱系涵盖整个人类物种，因此不能将人类中的任何子集标记为“神经多元人士”。而且神经典型者也属于人类神经多样性的谱系，所以将“神经典型者与神经多元人士”说成是两回事毫无意义。正确的说法应该是：“本团体对神经典型者及神经殊异人士均开放。”



I hope this list of definitions will help to foster greater clarity and understanding, and more accurate writing, when it comes to the terminology around neurodiversity. I encourage readers to share, cite, or quote from this piece, anywhere it might be useful. If you’re writing up submission guidelines for neurodiversity-related writings, for a journal, anthology, conference, or other project, feel free to draw upon this piece in creating your guidelines. If you encounter a journalist who’s doing a piece on a neurodiversity-related topic, or a group of college students who are writing about neurodiversity, please share this piece with them. And please feel free to use this piece as a resource in any situation in which there’s confusion about what any of these terms mean.

我希望这份定义清单能有助于在涉及神经多样性相关术语时，促进更清晰的理解和更准确的写作。我鼓励读者在任何可能有用之处分享、引用或摘录本文。如果你正在为期刊、文集、会议或其他项目撰写神经多样性相关文章的投稿指南，欢迎参考本文来制定你的指南。如果你遇到正在撰写神经多样性相关报道的记者，或一群正在撰写神经多样性相关文章的大学生，请将本文分享给他们。在任何对这些术语含义存在困惑的情况下，请随意将本文作为参考资源使用。
